"1211"	"a vast shout and came pouring down like a deluge to smother me"
"1212"	"with blessings and gratitude; and Clarence was not the last of"
"1213"	"the wash, to be sure."
"1214"	"CHAPTER VII"
"1215"	"MERLIN’S TOWER"
"1216"	"Inasmuch as I was now the second personage in the Kingdom, as far"
"1217"	"as political power and authority were concerned, much was made"
"1218"	"of me.  My raiment was of silks and velvets and cloth of gold,"
"1219"	"and by consequence was very showy, also uncomfortable.  But habit"
"1220"	"would soon reconcile me to my clothes; I was aware of that.  I was"
"1221"	"given the choicest suite of apartments in the castle, after"
"1222"	"the king’s.  They were aglow with loud-colored silken hangings,"
"1223"	"but the stone floors had nothing but rushes on them for a carpet,"
"1224"	"and they were misfit rushes at that, being not all of one breed."
"1225"	"As for conveniences, properly speaking, there weren’t any.  I mean"
"1226"	"_little_ conveniences; it is the little conveniences that make"
"1227"	"the real comfort of life.  The big oaken chairs, graced with rude"
"1228"	"carvings, were well enough, but that was the stopping place."
"1229"	"There was no soap, no matches, no looking-glass--except a metal"
"1230"	"one, about as powerful as a pail of water.  And not a chromo."
"1231"	"I had been used to chromos for years, and I saw now that without"
"1232"	"my suspecting it a passion for art had got worked into the fabric"
"1233"	"of my being, and was become a part of me.  It made me homesick"
"1234"	"to look around over this proud and gaudy but heartless barrenness"
"1235"	"and remember that in our house in East Hartford, all unpretending"
"1236"	"as it was, you couldn’t go into a room but you would find an"
"1237"	"insurance-chromo, or at least a three-color God-Bless-Our-Home"
"1238"	"over the door; and in the parlor we had nine.  But here, even in"
"1239"	"my grand room of state, there wasn’t anything in the nature of"
"1240"	"a picture except a thing the size of a bedquilt, which was either"
"1241"	"woven or knitted (it had darned places in it), and nothing in it"
"1242"	"was the right color or the right shape; and as for proportions,"
"1243"	"even Raphael himself couldn’t have botched them more formidably,"
"1244"	"after all his practice on those nightmares they call his “celebrated"
"1245"	"Hampton Court cartoons.”  Raphael was a bird.  We had several"
"1246"	"of his chromos; one was his “Miraculous Draught of Fishes,” where"
"1247"	"he puts in a miracle of his own--puts three men into a canoe which"
"1248"	"wouldn’t have held a dog without upsetting.  I always admired"
"1249"	"to study R.’s art, it was so fresh and unconventional."
"1250"	"There wasn’t even a bell or a speaking-tube in the castle.  I had"
"1251"	"a great many servants, and those that were on duty lolled in the"
"1252"	"anteroom; and when I wanted one of them I had to go and call for him."
"1253"	"There was no gas, there were no candles; a bronze dish half full"
"1254"	"of boarding-house butter with a blazing rag floating in it was"
"1255"	"the thing that produced what was regarded as light.  A lot of"
"1256"	"these hung along the walls and modified the dark, just toned it"
"1257"	"down enough to make it dismal.  If you went out at night, your"
"1258"	"servants carried torches.  There were no books, pens, paper or"
"1259"	"ink, and no glass in the openings they believed to be windows."
"1260"	"It is a little thing--glass is--until it is absent, then it becomes"
"1261"	"a big thing.  But perhaps the worst of all was, that there wasn’t"
"1262"	"any sugar, coffee, tea, or tobacco.  I saw that I was just another"
"1263"	"Robinson Crusoe cast away on an uninhabited island, with no society"
"1264"	"but some more or less tame animals, and if I wanted to make life"
"1265"	"bearable I must do as he did--invent, contrive, create, reorganize"
"1266"	"things; set brain and hand to work, and keep them busy.  Well,"
"1267"	"that was in my line."
"1268"	"One thing troubled me along at first--the immense interest which"
"1269"	"people took in me.  Apparently the whole nation wanted a look"
"1270"	"at me.  It soon transpired that the eclipse had scared the British"
"1271"	"world almost to death; that while it lasted the whole country,"
"1272"	"from one end to the other, was in a pitiable state of panic, and"
"1273"	"the churches, hermitages, and monkeries overflowed with praying"
"1274"	"and weeping poor creatures who thought the end of the world was"
"1275"	"come.  Then had followed the news that the producer of this awful"
"1276"	"event was a stranger, a mighty magician at Arthur’s court; that he"
"1277"	"could have blown out the sun like a candle, and was just going"
"1278"	"to do it when his mercy was purchased, and he then dissolved"
"1279"	"his enchantments, and was now recognized and honored as the man"
"1280"	"who had by his unaided might saved the globe from destruction and"
"1281"	"its peoples from extinction.  Now if you consider that everybody"
"1282"	"believed that, and not only believed it, but never even dreamed"
"1283"	"of doubting it, you will easily understand that there was not"
"1284"	"a person in all Britain that would not have walked fifty miles"
"1285"	"to get a sight of me.  Of course I was all the talk--all other"
"1286"	"subjects were dropped; even the king became suddenly a person of"
"1287"	"minor interest and notoriety.  Within twenty-four hours the"
"1288"	"delegations began to arrive, and from that time onward for a fortnight"
"1289"	"they kept coming.  The village was crowded, and all the countryside."
"1290"	"I had to go out a dozen times a day and show myself to these"
"1291"	"reverent and awe-stricken multitudes.  It came to be a great burden,"
"1292"	"as to time and trouble, but of course it was at the same time"
"1293"	"compensatingly agreeable to be so celebrated and such a center"
"1294"	"of homage.  It turned Brer Merlin green with envy and spite, which"
"1295"	"was a great satisfaction to me.  But there was one thing I couldn’t"
"1296"	"understand--nobody had asked for an autograph.  I spoke to Clarence"
"1297"	"about it.  By George!  I had to explain to him what it was.  Then"
"1298"	"he said nobody in the country could read or write but a few dozen"
"1299"	"priests.  Land! think of that."
"1300"	"There was another thing that troubled me a little.  Those multitudes"
"1301"	"presently began to agitate for another miracle.  That was natural."
"1302"	"To be able to carry back to their far homes the boast that they"
"1303"	"had seen the man who could command the sun, riding in the heavens,"
"1304"	"and be obeyed, would make them great in the eyes of their neighbors,"
"1305"	"and envied by them all; but to be able to also say they had seen"
"1306"	"him work a miracle themselves--why, people would come a distance"
"1307"	"to see _them_.  The pressure got to be pretty strong.  There was"
"1308"	"going to be an eclipse of the moon, and I knew the date and hour,"
"1309"	"but it was too far away.  Two years.  I would have given a good"
"1310"	"deal for license to hurry it up and use it now when there was"
"1311"	"a big market for it.  It seemed a great pity to have it wasted so,"
"1312"	"and come lagging along at a time when a body wouldn’t have any"
"1313"	"use for it, as like as not.  If it had been booked for only a month"
"1314"	"away, I could have sold it short; but, as matters stood, I couldn’t"
"1315"	"seem to cipher out any way to make it do me any good, so I gave up"
"1316"	"trying.  Next, Clarence found that old Merlin was making himself"
"1317"	"busy on the sly among those people.  He was spreading a report that"
"1318"	"I was a humbug, and that the reason I didn’t accommodate the people"
"1319"	"with a miracle was because I couldn’t.  I saw that I must do"
"1320"	"something.  I presently thought out a plan."
"1321"	"By my authority as executive I threw Merlin into prison--the same"
"1322"	"cell I had occupied myself.  Then I gave public notice by herald"
"1323"	"and trumpet that I should be busy with affairs of state for"
"1324"	"a fortnight, but about the end of that time I would take a moment’s"
"1325"	"leisure and blow up Merlin’s stone tower by fires from heaven;"
"1326"	"in the meantime, whoso listened to evil reports about me, let him"
"1327"	"beware.  Furthermore, I would perform but this one miracle at"
"1328"	"this time, and no more; if it failed to satisfy and any murmured,"
"1329"	"I would turn the murmurers into horses, and make them useful."
"1330"	"Quiet ensued."
"1331"	"I took Clarence into my confidence, to a certain degree, and we"
"1332"	"went to work privately.  I told him that this was a sort of miracle"
"1333"	"that required a trifle of preparation, and that it would be sudden"
"1334"	"death to ever talk about these preparations to anybody.  That made"
"1335"	"his mouth safe enough.  Clandestinely we made a few bushels of"
"1336"	"first-rate blasting powder, and I superintended my armorers while"
"1337"	"they constructed a lightning-rod and some wires.  This old stone"
"1338"	"tower was very massive--and rather ruinous, too, for it was Roman,"
"1339"	"and four hundred years old.  Yes, and handsome, after a rude"
"1340"	"fashion, and clothed with ivy from base to summit, as with a shirt"
"1341"	"of scale mail.  It stood on a lonely eminence, in good view from"
"1342"	"the castle, and about half a mile away."
"1343"	"Working by night, we stowed the powder in the tower--dug stones"
"1344"	"out, on the inside, and buried the powder in the walls themselves,"
"1345"	"which were fifteen feet thick at the base.  We put in a peck"
"1346"	"at a time, in a dozen places.  We could have blown up the Tower"
"1347"	"of London with these charges.  When the thirteenth night was come"
"1348"	"we put up our lightning-rod, bedded it in one of the batches of"
"1349"	"powder, and ran wires from it to the other batches.  Everybody"
"1350"	"had shunned that locality from the day of my proclamation, but"
"1351"	"on the morning of the fourteenth I thought best to warn the people,"
"1352"	"through the heralds, to keep clear away--a quarter of a mile away."
"1353"	"Then added, by command, that at some time during the twenty-four"
"1354"	"hours I would consummate the miracle, but would first give a brief"
"1355"	"notice; by flags on the castle towers if in the daytime, by"
"1356"	"torch-baskets in the same places if at night."
"1357"	"Thunder-showers had been tolerably frequent of late, and I was"
"1358"	"not much afraid of a failure; still, I shouldn’t have cared for"
"1359"	"a delay of a day or two; I should have explained that I was busy"
"1360"	"with affairs of state yet, and the people must wait."
"1361"	"Of course, we had a blazing sunny day--almost the first one without"
"1362"	"a cloud for three weeks; things always happen so.  I kept secluded,"
"1363"	"and watched the weather.  Clarence dropped in from time to time"
"1364"	"and said the public excitement was growing and growing all the"
"1365"	"time, and the whole country filling up with human masses as far"
"1366"	"as one could see from the battlements.  At last the wind sprang up"
"1367"	"and a cloud appeared--in the right quarter, too, and just at"
"1368"	"nightfall.  For a little while I watched that distant cloud spread"
"1369"	"and blacken, then I judged it was time for me to appear.  I ordered"
"1370"	"the torch-baskets to be lit, and Merlin liberated and sent to me."
"1371"	"A quarter of an hour later I ascended the parapet and there found"
"1372"	"the king and the court assembled and gazing off in the darkness"
"1373"	"toward Merlin’s Tower.  Already the darkness was so heavy that"
"1374"	"one could not see far; these people and the old turrets, being"
"1375"	"partly in deep shadow and partly in the red glow from the great"
"1376"	"torch-baskets overhead, made a good deal of a picture."
"1377"	"Merlin arrived in a gloomy mood.  I said:"
"1378"	"“You wanted to burn me alive when I had not done you any harm,"
"1379"	"and latterly you have been trying to injure my professional"
"1380"	"reputation.  Therefore I am going to call down fire and blow up"
"1381"	"your tower, but it is only fair to give you a chance; now if you"
"1382"	"think you can break my enchantments and ward off the fires, step"
"1383"	"to the bat, it’s your innings.”"
"1384"	"“I can, fair sir, and I will. Doubt it not.”"
"1385"	"He drew an imaginary circle on the stones of the roof, and burnt"
"1386"	"a pinch of powder in it, which sent up a small cloud of aromatic"
"1387"	"smoke, whereat everybody fell back and began to cross themselves"
"1388"	"and get uncomfortable.  Then he began to mutter and make passes"
"1389"	"in the air with his hands.  He worked himself up slowly and"
"1390"	"gradually into a sort of frenzy, and got to thrashing around with"
"1391"	"his arms like the sails of a windmill.  By this time the storm had"
"1392"	"about reached us; the gusts of wind were flaring the torches and"
"1393"	"making the shadows swash about, the first heavy drops of rain"
"1394"	"were falling, the world abroad was black as pitch, the lightning"
"1395"	"began to wink fitfully.  Of course, my rod would be loading itself"
"1396"	"now.  In fact, things were imminent. So I said:"
"1397"	"“You have had time enough.  I have given you every advantage,"
"1398"	"and not interfered.  It is plain your magic is weak. It is only"
"1399"	"fair that I begin now.”"
"1400"	"I made about three passes in the air, and then there was an awful"
"1401"	"crash and that old tower leaped into the sky in chunks, along"
"1402"	"with a vast volcanic fountain of fire that turned night to noonday,"
"1403"	"and showed a thousand acres of human beings groveling on the ground"
"1404"	"in a general collapse of consternation.  Well, it rained mortar and"
"1405"	"masonry the rest of the week.  This was the report; but probably"
"1406"	"the facts would have modified it."
"1407"	"It was an effective miracle.  The great bothersome temporary"
"1408"	"population vanished.  There were a good many thousand tracks"
"1409"	"in the mud the next morning, but they were all outward bound."
"1410"	"If I had advertised another miracle I couldn’t have raised an"
"1411"	"audience with a sheriff."
"1412"	"Merlin’s stock was flat.  The king wanted to stop his wages; he"
"1413"	"even wanted to banish him, but I interfered.  I said he would be"
"1414"	"useful to work the weather, and attend to small matters like that,"
"1415"	"and I would give him a lift now and then when his poor little"
"1416"	"parlor-magic soured on him.  There wasn’t a rag of his tower left,"
"1417"	"but I had the government rebuild it for him, and advised him"
"1418"	"to take boarders; but he was too high-toned for that.  And as for"
"1419"	"being grateful, he never even said thank you.  He was a rather"
"1420"	"hard lot, take him how you might; but then you couldn’t fairly"
"1421"	"expect a man to be sweet that had been set back so."
"1422"	"CHAPTER VIII"
"1423"	"THE BOSS"
"1424"	"To be vested with enormous authority is a fine thing; but to have"
"1425"	"the on-looking world consent to it is a finer.  The tower episode"
"1426"	"solidified my power, and made it impregnable.  If any were perchance"
"1427"	"disposed to be jealous and critical before that, they experienced"
"1428"	"a change of heart, now.  There was not any one in the kingdom"
"1429"	"who would have considered it good judgment to meddle with my matters."
"1430"	"I was fast getting adjusted to my situation and circumstances."
"1431"	"For a time, I used to wake up, mornings, and smile at my “dream,”"
"1432"	" and listen for the Colt’s factory whistle; but that sort of thing"
"1433"	"played itself out, gradually, and at last I was fully able to realize"
"1434"	"that I was actually living in the sixth century, and in Arthur’s"
"1435"	"court, not a lunatic asylum.  After that, I was just as much"
"1436"	"at home in that century as I could have been in any other; and"
"1437"	"as for preference, I wouldn’t have traded it for the twentieth."
"1438"	"Look at the opportunities here for a man of knowledge, brains,"
"1439"	"pluck, and enterprise to sail in and grow up with the country."
"1440"	"The grandest field that ever was; and all my own; not a competitor;"
"1441"	"not a man who wasn’t a baby to me in acquirements and capacities;"
"1442"	"whereas, what would I amount to in the twentieth century?  I should"
"1443"	"be foreman of a factory, that is about all; and could drag a seine"
"1444"	"down street any day and catch a hundred better men than myself."
"1445"	"What a jump I had made!  I couldn’t keep from thinking about it,"
"1446"	"and contemplating it, just as one does who has struck oil.  There"
"1447"	"was nothing back of me that could approach it, unless it might be"
"1448"	"Joseph’s case; and Joseph’s only approached it, it didn’t equal"
"1449"	"it, quite.  For it stands to reason that as Joseph’s splendid"
"1450"	"financial ingenuities advantaged nobody but the king, the general"
"1451"	"public must have regarded him with a good deal of disfavor, whereas"
"1452"	"I had done my entire public a kindness in sparing the sun, and was"
"1453"	"popular by reason of it."
"1454"	"I was no shadow of a king; I was the substance; the king himself"
"1455"	"was the shadow.  My power was colossal; and it was not a mere"
"1456"	"name, as such things have generally been, it was the genuine"
"1457"	"article.  I stood here, at the very spring and source of the second"
"1458"	"great period of the world’s history; and could see the trickling"
"1459"	"stream of that history gather and deepen and broaden, and roll"
"1460"	"its mighty tides down the far centuries; and I could note the"
"1461"	"upspringing of adventurers like myself in the shelter of its long"
"1462"	"array of thrones: De Montforts, Gavestons, Mortimers, Villierses;"
"1463"	"the war-making, campaign-directing wantons of France, and Charles"
"1464"	"the Second’s scepter-wielding drabs; but nowhere in the procession"
"1465"	"was my full-sized fellow visible.  I was a Unique; and glad to know"
"1466"	"that that fact could not be dislodged or challenged for thirteen"
"1467"	"centuries and a half, for sure.  Yes, in power I was equal to"
"1468"	"the king.  At the same time there was another power that was"
"1469"	"a trifle stronger than both of us put together.  That was the Church."
"1470"	"I do not wish to disguise that fact.  I couldn’t, if I wanted to."
"1471"	"But never mind about that, now; it will show up, in its proper"
"1472"	"place, later on.  It didn’t cause me any trouble in the beginning"
"1473"	"--at least any of consequence."
"1474"	"Well, it was a curious country, and full of interest.  And the"
"1475"	"people!  They were the quaintest and simplest and trustingest race;"
"1476"	"why, they were nothing but rabbits.  It was pitiful for a person"
"1477"	"born in a wholesome free atmosphere to listen to their humble"
"1478"	"and hearty outpourings of loyalty toward their king and Church"
"1479"	"and nobility; as if they had any more occasion to love and honor"
"1480"	"king and Church and noble than a slave has to love and honor"
"1481"	"the lash, or a dog has to love and honor the stranger that kicks him!"
"1482"	"Why, dear me, _any_ kind of royalty, howsoever modified, _any_ kind"
"1483"	"of aristocracy, howsoever pruned, is rightly an insult; but if you"
"1484"	"are born and brought up under that sort of arrangement you probably"
"1485"	"never find it out for yourself, and don’t believe it when somebody"
"1486"	"else tells you.  It is enough to make a body ashamed of his race"
"1487"	"to think of the sort of froth that has always occupied its thrones"
"1488"	"without shadow of right or reason, and the seventh-rate people"
"1489"	"that have always figured as its aristocracies--a company of monarchs"
"1490"	"and nobles who, as a rule, would have achieved only poverty and"
"1491"	"obscurity if left, like their betters, to their own exertions."
"1492"	"The most of King Arthur’s British nation were slaves, pure and"
"1493"	"simple, and bore that name, and wore the iron collar on their"
"1494"	"necks; and the rest were slaves in fact, but without the name;"
"1495"	"they imagined themselves men and freemen, and called themselves"
"1496"	"so.  The truth was, the nation as a body was in the world for one"
"1497"	"object, and one only: to grovel before king and Church and noble;"
"1498"	"to slave for them, sweat blood for them, starve that they might"
"1499"	"be fed, work that they might play, drink misery to the dregs that"
"1500"	"they might be happy, go naked that they might wear silks and"
"1501"	"jewels, pay taxes that they might be spared from paying them,"
"1502"	"be familiar all their lives with the degrading language and postures"
"1503"	"of adulation that they might walk in pride and think themselves"
"1504"	"the gods of this world.  And for all this, the thanks they got were"
"1505"	"cuffs and contempt; and so poor-spirited were they that they took"
"1506"	"even this sort of attention as an honor."
"1507"	"Inherited ideas are a curious thing, and interesting to observe"
"1508"	"and examine.  I had mine, the king and his people had theirs."
"1509"	"In both cases they flowed in ruts worn deep by time and habit,"
"1510"	"and the man who should have proposed to divert them by reason"
"1511"	"and argument would have had a long contract on his hands.  For"
"1512"	"instance, those people had inherited the idea that all men without"
"1513"	"title and a long pedigree, whether they had great natural gifts"
"1514"	"and acquirements or hadn’t, were creatures of no more consideration"
"1515"	"than so many animals, bugs, insects; whereas I had inherited the idea"
"1516"	"that human daws who can consent to masquerade in the peacock-shams"
"1517"	"of inherited dignities and unearned titles, are of no good but"
"1518"	"to be laughed at.  The way I was looked upon was odd, but it was"
"1519"	"natural.  You know how the keeper and the public regard the elephant"
"1520"	"in the menagerie: well, that is the idea.  They are full of"
"1521"	"admiration of his vast bulk and his prodigious strength; they"
"1522"	"speak with pride of the fact that he can do a hundred marvels"
"1523"	"which are far and away beyond their own powers; and they speak"
"1524"	"with the same pride of the fact that in his wrath he is able"
"1525"	"to drive a thousand men before him.  But does that make him one"
"1526"	"of _them_?  No; the raggedest tramp in the pit would smile at"
"1527"	"the idea.  He couldn’t comprehend it; couldn’t take it in; couldn’t"
"1528"	"in any remote way conceive of it.  Well, to the king, the nobles,"
"1529"	"and all the nation, down to the very slaves and tramps, I was"
"1530"	"just that kind of an elephant, and nothing more.  I was admired,"
"1531"	"also feared; but it was as an animal is admired and feared."
"1532"	"The animal is not reverenced, neither was I; I was not even"
"1533"	"respected.  I had no pedigree, no inherited title; so in the king’s"
"1534"	"and nobles’ eyes I was mere dirt; the people regarded me with"
"1535"	"wonder and awe, but there was no reverence mixed with it; through"
"1536"	"the force of inherited ideas they were not able to conceive of"
"1537"	"anything being entitled to that except pedigree and lordship."
"1538"	"There you see the hand of that awful power, the Roman Catholic"
"1539"	"Church.  In two or three little centuries it had converted a nation"
"1540"	"of men to a nation of worms.  Before the day of the Church’s"
"1541"	"supremacy in the world, men were men, and held their heads up,"
"1542"	"and had a man’s pride and spirit and independence; and what"
"1543"	"of greatness and position a person got, he got mainly by achievement,"
"1544"	"not by birth.  But then the Church came to the front, with an axe"
"1545"	"to grind; and she was wise, subtle, and knew more than one way"
"1546"	"to skin a cat--or a nation; she invented “divine right of kings,”"
"1547"	" and propped it all around, brick by brick, with the Beatitudes"
"1548"	"--wrenching them from their good purpose to make them fortify"
"1549"	"an evil one; she preached (to the commoner) humility, obedience"
"1550"	"to superiors, the beauty of self-sacrifice; she preached (to the"
"1551"	"commoner) meekness under insult; preached (still to the commoner,"
"1552"	"always to the commoner) patience, meanness of spirit, non-resistance"
"1553"	"under oppression; and she introduced heritable ranks and"
"1554"	"aristocracies, and taught all the Christian populations of the earth"
"1555"	"to bow down to them and worship them.  Even down to my birth-century"
"1556"	"that poison was still in the blood of Christendom, and the best"
"1557"	"of English commoners was still content to see his inferiors"
"1558"	"impudently continuing to hold a number of positions, such as"
"1559"	"lordships and the throne, to which the grotesque laws of his country"
"1560"	"did not allow him to aspire; in fact, he was not merely contented"
"1561"	"with this strange condition of things, he was even able to persuade"
"1562"	"himself that he was proud of it.  It seems to show that there isn’t"
"1563"	"anything you can’t stand, if you are only born and bred to it."
"1564"	"Of course that taint, that reverence for rank and title, had been"
"1565"	"in our American blood, too--I know that; but when I left America"
"1566"	"it had disappeared--at least to all intents and purposes.  The"
"1567"	"remnant of it was restricted to the dudes and dudesses.  When"
"1568"	"a disease has worked its way down to that level, it may fairly"
"1569"	"be said to be out of the system."
"1570"	"But to return to my anomalous position in King Arthur’s kingdom."
"1571"	"Here I was, a giant among pigmies, a man among children, a master"
"1572"	"intelligence among intellectual moles: by all rational measurement"
"1573"	"the one and only actually great man in that whole British world;"
"1574"	"and yet there and then, just as in the remote England of my"
"1575"	"birth-time, the sheep-witted earl who could claim long descent"
"1576"	"from a king’s leman, acquired at second-hand from the slums of"
"1577"	"London, was a better man than I was.  Such a personage was fawned"
"1578"	"upon in Arthur’s realm and reverently looked up to by everybody,"
"1579"	"even though his dispositions were as mean as his intelligence,"
"1580"	"and his morals as base as his lineage.  There were times when"
"1581"	"_he_ could sit down in the king’s presence, but I couldn’t.  I could"
"1582"	"have got a title easily enough, and that would have raised me"
"1583"	"a large step in everybody’s eyes; even in the king’s, the giver"
"1584"	"of it.  But I didn’t ask for it; and I declined it when it was"
"1585"	"offered.  I couldn’t have enjoyed such a thing with my notions;"
"1586"	"and it wouldn’t have been fair, anyway, because as far back as"
"1587"	"I could go, our tribe had always been short of the bar sinister."
"1588"	"I couldn’t have felt really and satisfactorily fine and proud"
"1589"	"and set-up over any title except one that should come from the nation"
"1590"	"itself, the only legitimate source; and such an one I hoped to win;"
"1591"	"and in the course of years of honest and honorable endeavor, I did"
"1592"	"win it and did wear it with a high and clean pride.  This title"
"1593"	"fell casually from the lips of a blacksmith, one day, in a village,"
"1594"	"was caught up as a happy thought and tossed from mouth to mouth"
"1595"	"with a laugh and an affirmative vote; in ten days it had swept"
"1596"	"the kingdom, and was become as familiar as the king’s name.  I was"
"1597"	"never known by any other designation afterward, whether in the"
"1598"	"nation’s talk or in grave debate upon matters of state at the"
"1599"	"council-board of the sovereign.  This title, translated into modern"
"1600"	"speech, would be THE BOSS.  Elected by the nation.  That suited me."
"1601"	"And it was a pretty high title.  There were very few THE’S, and"
"1602"	"I was one of them.  If you spoke of the duke, or the earl, or"
"1603"	"the bishop, how could anybody tell which one you meant?  But if"
"1604"	"you spoke of The King or The Queen or The Boss, it was different."
"1605"	"Well, I liked the king, and as king I respected him--respected"
"1606"	"the office; at least respected it as much as I was capable of"
"1607"	"respecting any unearned supremacy; but as MEN I looked down upon"
"1608"	"him and his nobles--privately.  And he and they liked me, and"
"1609"	"respected my office; but as an animal, without birth or sham title,"
"1610"	"they looked down upon me--and were not particularly private about it,"
"1611"	"either.  I didn’t charge for my opinion about them, and they didn’t"
"1612"	"charge for their opinion about me: the account was square, the"
"1613"	"books balanced, everybody was satisfied."
"1614"	"CHAPTER IX"
"1615"	"THE TOURNAMENT"
"1616"	"They were always having grand tournaments there at Camelot; and"
"1617"	"very stirring and picturesque and ridiculous human bull-fights"
"1618"	"they were, too, but just a little wearisome to the practical mind."
"1619"	"However, I was generally on hand--for two reasons: a man must"
"1620"	"not hold himself aloof from the things which his friends and his"
"1621"	"community have at heart if he would be liked--especially as"
"1622"	"a statesman; and both as business man and statesman I wanted"
"1623"	"to study the tournament and see if I couldn’t invent an improvement"
"1624"	"on it.  That reminds me to remark, in passing, that the very first"
"1625"	"official thing I did, in my administration--and it was on the very"
"1626"	"first day of it, too--was to start a patent office; for I knew"
"1627"	"that a country without a patent office and good patent laws was"
"1628"	"just a crab, and couldn’t travel any way but sideways or backways."
"1629"	"Things ran along, a tournament nearly every week; and now and then"
"1630"	"the boys used to want me to take a hand--I mean Sir Launcelot and"
"1631"	"the rest--but I said I would by and by; no hurry yet, and too much"
"1632"	"government machinery to oil up and set to rights and start a-going."
"1633"	"We had one tournament which was continued from day to day during"
"1634"	"more than a week, and as many as five hundred knights took part"
"1635"	"in it, from first to last.  They were weeks gathering.  They came"
"1636"	"on horseback from everywhere; from the very ends of the country,"
"1637"	"and even from beyond the sea; and many brought ladies, and all"
"1638"	"brought squires and troops of servants.  It was a most gaudy and"
"1639"	"gorgeous crowd, as to costumery, and very characteristic of the"
"1640"	"country and the time, in the way of high animal spirits, innocent"
"1641"	"indecencies of language, and happy-hearted indifference to morals."
"1642"	"It was fight or look on, all day and every day; and sing, gamble,"
"1643"	"dance, carouse half the night every night.  They had a most noble"
"1644"	"good time.  You never saw such people.  Those banks of beautiful"
"1645"	"ladies, shining in their barbaric splendors, would see a knight"
"1646"	"sprawl from his horse in the lists with a lanceshaft the thickness"
"1647"	"of your ankle clean through him and the blood spouting, and instead"
"1648"	"of fainting they would clap their hands and crowd each other for a"
"1649"	"better view; only sometimes one would dive into her handkerchief,"
"1650"	"and look ostentatiously broken-hearted, and then you could lay"
"1651"	"two to one that there was a scandal there somewhere and she was"
"1652"	"afraid the public hadn’t found it out."
"1653"	"The noise at night would have been annoying to me ordinarily, but"
"1654"	"I didn’t mind it in the present circumstances, because it kept me"
"1655"	"from hearing the quacks detaching legs and arms from the day’s"
"1656"	"cripples.  They ruined an uncommon good old cross-cut saw for me,"
"1657"	"and broke the saw-buck, too, but I let it pass.  And as for my"
"1658"	"axe--well, I made up my mind that the next time I lent an axe"
"1659"	"to a surgeon I would pick my century."
"1660"	"I not only watched this tournament from day to day, but detailed"
"1661"	"an intelligent priest from my Department of Public Morals and"
"1662"	"Agriculture, and ordered him to report it; for it was my purpose"
"1663"	"by and by, when I should have gotten the people along far enough,"
"1664"	"to start a newspaper.  The first thing you want in a new country,"
"1665"	"is a patent office; then work up your school system; and after that,"
"1666"	"out with your paper.  A newspaper has its faults, and plenty of them,"
"1667"	"but no matter, it’s hark from the tomb for a dead nation, and don’t"
"1668"	"you forget it.  You can’t resurrect a dead nation without it; there"
"1669"	"isn’t any way.  So I wanted to sample things, and be finding out"
"1670"	"what sort of reporter-material I might be able to rake together out"
"1671"	"of the sixth century when I should come to need it."
"1672"	"Well, the priest did very well, considering.  He got in all"
"1673"	"the details, and that is a good thing in a local item: you see,"
"1674"	"he had kept books for the undertaker-department of his church"
"1675"	"when he was younger, and there, you know, the money’s in the details;"
"1676"	"the more details, the more swag: bearers, mutes, candles, prayers"
"1677"	"--everything counts; and if the bereaved don’t buy prayers enough"
"1678"	"you mark up your candles with a forked pencil, and your bill"
"1679"	"shows up all right.  And he had a good knack at getting in the"
"1680"	"complimentary thing here and there about a knight that was likely"
"1681"	"to advertise--no, I mean a knight that had influence; and he also"
"1682"	"had a neat gift of exaggeration, for in his time he had kept door"
"1683"	"for a pious hermit who lived in a sty and worked miracles."
"1684"	"Of course this novice’s report lacked whoop and crash and lurid"
"1685"	"description, and therefore wanted the true ring; but its antique"
"1686"	"wording was quaint and sweet and simple, and full of the fragrances"
"1687"	"and flavors of the time, and these little merits made up in a measure"
"1688"	"for its more important lacks.  Here is an extract from it:"
"1689"	"  Then Sir Brian de les Isles and Grummore Grummorsum,"
"1690"	"  knights of the castle, encountered with Sir Aglovale and"
"1691"	"  Sir Tor, and Sir Tor smote down Sir Grummore Grummorsum"
"1692"	"  to the earth.  Then came Sir Carados of the dolorous"
"1693"	"  tower, and Sir Turquine, knights of the castle, and"
"1694"	"  there encountered with them Sir Percivale de Galis"
"1695"	"  and Sir Lamorak de Galis, that were two brethren, and"
"1696"	"  there encountered Sir Percivale with Sir Carados, and"
"1697"	"  either brake their spears unto their hands, and then"
"1698"	"  Sir Turquine with Sir Lamorak, and either of them smote"
"1699"	"  down other, horse and all, to the earth, and either"
"1700"	"  parties rescued other and horsed them again.  And Sir"
"1701"	"  Arnold, and Sir Gauter, knights of the castle,"
"1702"	"  encountered with Sir Brandiles and Sir Kay, and these"
"1703"	"  four knights encountered mightily, and brake their"
"1704"	"  spears to their hands.  Then came Sir Pertolope from"
"1705"	"  the castle, and there encountered with him Sir Lionel,"
"1706"	"  and there Sir Pertolope the green knight smote down Sir"
"1707"	"  Lionel, brother to Sir Launcelot.  All this was marked"
"1708"	"  by noble heralds, who bare him best, and their names."
"1709"	"  Then Sir Bleobaris brake his spear upon Sir Gareth,"
"1710"	"  but of that stroke Sir Bleobaris fell to the earth."
"1711"	"  When Sir Galihodin saw that, he bad Sir Gareth keep him,"
"1712"	"  and Sir Gareth smote him to the earth.  Then Sir Galihud"
"1713"	"  gat a spear to avenge his brother, and in the same wise"
"1714"	"  Sir Gareth served him, and Sir Dinadan and his brother"
"1715"	"  La Cote Male Taile, and Sir Sagramore le Disirous, and"
"1716"	"  Sir Dodinas le Savage; all these he bare down with one"
"1717"	"  spear.  When King Aswisance of Ireland saw Sir Gareth"
"1718"	"  fare so he marvelled what he might be, that one time"
"1719"	"  seemed green, and another time, at his again coming,"
"1720"	"  he seemed blue.  And thus at every course that he rode"
"1721"	"  to and fro he changed his color, so that there might"
"1722"	"  neither king nor knight have ready cognizance of him."
"1723"	"  Then Sir Agwisance the King of Ireland encountered"
"1724"	"  with Sir Gareth, and there Sir Gareth smote him from"
"1725"	"  his horse, saddle and all.  And then came King Carados"
"1726"	"  of Scotland, and Sir Gareth smote him down horse and"
"1727"	"  man.  And in the same wise he served King Uriens of the"
"1728"	"  land of Gore.  And then there came in Sir Bagdemagus,"
"1729"	"  and Sir Gareth smote him down horse and man to the"
"1730"	"  earth.  And Bagdemagus’s son Meliganus brake a spear"
"1731"	"  upon Sir Gareth mightily and knightly.  And then Sir"
"1732"	"  Galahault the noble prince cried on high, Knight with"
"1733"	"  the many colors, well hast thou justed; now make thee"
"1734"	"  ready that I may just with thee.  Sir Gareth heard him,"
"1735"	"  and he gat a great spear, and so they encountered"
"1736"	"  together, and there the prince brake his spear; but Sir"
"1737"	"  Gareth smote him upon the left side of the helm, that"
"1738"	"  he reeled here and there, and he had fallen down had not"
"1739"	"  his men recovered him.  Truly, said King Arthur, that"
"1740"	"  knight with the many colors is a good knight.  Wherefore"
"1741"	"  the king called unto him Sir Launcelot, and prayed him"
"1742"	"  to encounter with that knight.  Sir, said Launcelot, I"
"1743"	"  may as well find in my heart for to forbear him at"
"1744"	"  this time, for he hath had travail enough this day, and"
"1745"	"  when a good knight doth so well upon some day, it is"
"1746"	"  no good knight’s part to let him of his worship, and,"
"1747"	"  namely, when he seeth a knight hath done so great"
"1748"	"  labour; for peradventure, said Sir Launcelot, his"
"1749"	"  quarrel is here this day, and peradventure he is best"
"1750"	"  beloved with this lady of all that be here, for I see"
"1751"	"  well he paineth himself and enforceth him to do great"
"1752"	"  deeds, and therefore, said Sir Launcelot, as for me,"
"1753"	"  this day he shall have the honour; though it lay in my"
"1754"	"  power to put him from it, I would not."
"1755"	"There was an unpleasant little episode that day, which for reasons"
"1756"	"of state I struck out of my priest’s report.  You will have noticed"
"1757"	"that Garry was doing some great fighting in the engagement.  When"
"1758"	"I say Garry I mean Sir Gareth.  Garry was my private pet name"
"1759"	"for him; it suggests that I had a deep affection for him, and that"
"1760"	"was the case.  But it was a private pet name only, and never spoken"
"1761"	"aloud to any one, much less to him; being a noble, he would not"
"1762"	"have endured a familiarity like that from me.  Well, to proceed:"
"1763"	"I sat in the private box set apart for me as the king’s minister."
"1764"	"While Sir Dinadan was waiting for his turn to enter the lists,"
"1765"	"he came in there and sat down and began to talk; for he was always"
"1766"	"making up to me, because I was a stranger and he liked to have"
"1767"	"a fresh market for his jokes, the most of them having reached that"
"1768"	"stage of wear where the teller has to do the laughing himself while"
"1769"	"the other person looks sick.  I had always responded to his efforts"
"1770"	"as well as I could, and felt a very deep and real kindness for him,"
"1771"	"too, for the reason that if by malice of fate he knew the one"
"1772"	"particular anecdote which I had heard oftenest and had most hated"
"1773"	"and most loathed all my life, he had at least spared it me.  It was"
"1774"	"one which I had heard attributed to every humorous person who"
"1775"	"had ever stood on American soil, from Columbus down to Artemus Ward."
"1776"	"It was about a humorous lecturer who flooded an ignorant audience"
"1777"	"with the killingest jokes for an hour and never got a laugh; and"
"1778"	"then when he was leaving, some gray simpletons wrung him gratefully"
"1779"	"by the hand and said it had been the funniest thing they had ever"
"1780"	"heard, and “it was all they could do to keep from laughin’ right"
"1781"	"out in meetin’.”  That anecdote never saw the day that it was"
"1782"	"worth the telling; and yet I had sat under the telling of it"
"1783"	"hundreds and thousands and millions and billions of times, and"
"1784"	"cried and cursed all the way through.  Then who can hope to know"
"1785"	"what my feelings were, to hear this armor-plated ass start in on"
"1786"	"it again, in the murky twilight of tradition, before the dawn of"
"1787"	"history, while even Lactantius might be referred to as “the late"
"1788"	"Lactantius,” and the Crusades wouldn’t be born for five hundred"
"1789"	"years yet?  Just as he finished, the call-boy came; so, haw-hawing"
"1790"	"like a demon, he went rattling and clanking out like a crate of"
"1791"	"loose castings, and I knew nothing more.  It was some minutes"
"1792"	"before I came to, and then I opened my eyes just in time to see"
"1793"	"Sir Gareth fetch him an awful welt, and I unconsciously out with"
"1794"	"the prayer, “I hope to gracious he’s killed!”  But by ill-luck,"
"1795"	"before I had got half through with the words, Sir Gareth crashed"
"1796"	"into Sir Sagramor le Desirous and sent him thundering over his"
"1797"	"horse’s crupper, and Sir Sagramor caught my remark and thought"
"1798"	"I meant it for _him_."
"1799"	"Well, whenever one of those people got a thing into his head,"
"1800"	"there was no getting it out again.  I knew that, so I saved my"
"1801"	"breath, and offered no explanations.  As soon as Sir Sagramor"
"1802"	"got well, he notified me that there was a little account to settle"
"1803"	"between us, and he named a day three or four years in the future;"
"1804"	"place of settlement, the lists where the offense had been given."
"1805"	"I said I would be ready when he got back.  You see, he was going"
"1806"	"for the Holy Grail.  The boys all took a flier at the Holy Grail"
"1807"	"now and then.  It was a several years’ cruise.  They always put in"
"1808"	"the long absence snooping around, in the most conscientious way,"
"1809"	"though none of them had any idea where the Holy Grail really was,"
"1810"	"and I don’t think any of them actually expected to find it, or"
"1811"	"would have known what to do with it if he _had_ run across it."
"1812"	"You see, it was just the Northwest Passage of that day, as you may"
"1813"	"say; that was all.  Every year expeditions went out holy grailing,"
"1814"	"and next year relief expeditions went out to hunt for _them_.  There"
"1815"	"was worlds of reputation in it, but no money.  Why, they actually"
"1816"	"wanted _me_ to put in!  Well, I should smile."
"1817"	"CHAPTER X"
"1818"	"BEGINNINGS OF CIVILIZATION"
"1819"	"The Round Table soon heard of the challenge, and of course it was"
"1820"	"a good deal discussed, for such things interested the boys."
"1821"	"The king thought I ought now to set forth in quest of adventures,"
"1822"	"so that I might gain renown and be the more worthy to meet"
"1823"	"Sir Sagramor when the several years should have rolled away."
"1824"	"I excused myself for the present; I said it would take me three"
"1825"	"or four years yet to get things well fixed up and going smoothly;"
"1826"	"then I should be ready; all the chances were that at the end of"
"1827"	"that time Sir Sagramor would still be out grailing, so no valuable"
"1828"	"time would be lost by the postponement; I should then have been"
"1829"	"in office six or seven years, and I believed my system and machinery"
"1830"	"would be so well developed that I could take a holiday without"
"1831"	"its working any harm."
"1832"	"I was pretty well satisfied with what I had already accomplished."
"1833"	"In various quiet nooks and corners I had the beginnings of all"
"1834"	"sorts of industries under way--nuclei of future vast factories,"
"1835"	"the iron and steel missionaries of my future civilization.  In these"
"1836"	"were gathered together the brightest young minds I could find,"
"1837"	"and I kept agents out raking the country for more, all the time."
"1838"	"I was training a crowd of ignorant folk into experts--experts"
"1839"	"in every sort of handiwork and scientific calling.  These nurseries"
"1840"	"of mine went smoothly and privately along undisturbed in their"
"1841"	"obscure country retreats, for nobody was allowed to come into their"
"1842"	"precincts without a special permit--for I was afraid of the Church."
"1843"	"I had started a teacher-factory and a lot of Sunday-schools the"
"1844"	"first thing; as a result, I now had an admirable system of graded"
"1845"	"schools in full blast in those places, and also a complete variety"
"1846"	"of Protestant congregations all in a prosperous and growing"
"1847"	"condition.  Everybody could be any kind of a Christian he wanted"
"1848"	"to; there was perfect freedom in that matter.  But I confined public"
"1849"	"religious teaching to the churches and the Sunday-schools, permitting"
"1850"	"nothing of it in my other educational buildings.  I could have"
"1851"	"given my own sect the preference and made everybody a Presbyterian"
"1852"	"without any trouble, but that would have been to affront a law"
"1853"	"of human nature: spiritual wants and instincts are as various in"
"1854"	"the human family as are physical appetites, complexions, and"
"1855"	"features, and a man is only at his best, morally, when he is"
"1856"	"equipped with the religious garment whose color and shape and"
"1857"	"size most nicely accommodate themselves to the spiritual complexion,"
"1858"	"angularities, and stature of the individual who wears it; and,"
"1859"	"besides, I was afraid of a united Church; it makes a mighty power,"
"1860"	"the mightiest conceivable, and then when it by and by gets into"
"1861"	"selfish hands, as it is always bound to do, it means death to"
"1862"	"human liberty and paralysis to human thought."
"1863"	"All mines were royal property, and there were a good many of them."
"1864"	"They had formerly been worked as savages always work mines--holes"
"1865"	"grubbed in the earth and the mineral brought up in sacks of hide by"
"1866"	"hand, at the rate of a ton a day; but I had begun to put the mining"
"1867"	"on a scientific basis as early as I could."
"1868"	"Yes, I had made pretty handsome progress when Sir Sagramor’s"
"1869"	"challenge struck me."
"1870"	"Four years rolled by--and then!  Well, you would never imagine"
"1871"	"it in the world.  Unlimited power is the ideal thing when it is in"
"1872"	"safe hands.  The despotism of heaven is the one absolutely perfect"
"1873"	"government.  An earthly despotism would be the absolutely perfect"
"1874"	"earthly government, if the conditions were the same, namely, the"
"1875"	"despot the perfectest individual of the human race, and his lease"
"1876"	"of life perpetual.  But as a perishable perfect man must die, and"
"1877"	"leave his despotism in the hands of an imperfect successor, an"
"1878"	"earthly despotism is not merely a bad form of government, it is"
"1879"	"the worst form that is possible."
"1880"	"My works showed what a despot could do with the resources of"
"1881"	"a kingdom at his command.  Unsuspected by this dark land, I had"
"1882"	"the civilization of the nineteenth century booming under its very"
"1883"	"nose!  It was fenced away from the public view, but there it was,"
"1884"	"a gigantic and unassailable fact--and to be heard from, yet, if"
"1885"	"I lived and had luck.  There it was, as sure a fact and as substantial"
"1886"	"a fact as any serene volcano, standing innocent with its smokeless"
"1887"	"summit in the blue sky and giving no sign of the rising hell in its"
"1888"	"bowels.  My schools and churches were children four years before;"
"1889"	"they were grown-up now; my shops of that day were vast factories"
"1890"	"now; where I had a dozen trained men then, I had a thousand now;"
"1891"	"where I had one brilliant expert then, I had fifty now.  I stood"
"1892"	"with my hand on the cock, so to speak, ready to turn it on and"
"1893"	"flood the midnight world with light at any moment.  But I was not"
"1894"	"going to do the thing in that sudden way.  It was not my policy."
"1895"	"The people could not have stood it; and, moreover, I should have"
"1896"	"had the Established Roman Catholic Church on my back in a minute."
"1897"	"No, I had been going cautiously all the while.  I had had confidential"
"1898"	"agents trickling through the country some time, whose office was"
"1899"	"to undermine knighthood by imperceptible degrees, and to gnaw"
"1900"	"a little at this and that and the other superstition, and so prepare"
"1901"	"the way gradually for a better order of things.  I was turning on"
"1902"	"my light one-candle-power at a time, and meant to continue to do so."
"1903"	"I had scattered some branch schools secretly about the kingdom,"
"1904"	"and they were doing very well.  I meant to work this racket more"
"1905"	"and more, as time wore on, if nothing occurred to frighten me."
"1906"	"One of my deepest secrets was my West Point--my military academy."
"1907"	"I kept that most jealously out of sight; and I did the same with my"
"1908"	"naval academy which I had established at a remote seaport.  Both"
"1909"	"were prospering to my satisfaction."
"1910"	"Clarence was twenty-two now, and was my head executive, my right"
"1911"	"hand.  He was a darling; he was equal to anything; there wasn’t"
"1912"	"anything he couldn’t turn his hand to.  Of late I had been training"
"1913"	"him for journalism, for the time seemed about right for a start"
"1914"	"in the newspaper line; nothing big, but just a small weekly for"
"1915"	"experimental circulation in my civilization-nurseries.  He took"
"1916"	"to it like a duck; there was an editor concealed in him, sure."
"1917"	"Already he had doubled himself in one way; he talked sixth century"
"1918"	"and wrote nineteenth.  His journalistic style was climbing,"
"1919"	"steadily; it was already up to the back settlement Alabama mark,"
"1920"	"and couldn’t be told from the editorial output of that region"
"1921"	"either by matter or flavor."
"1922"	"We had another large departure on hand, too.  This was a telegraph"
"1923"	"and a telephone; our first venture in this line.  These wires were"
"1924"	"for private service only, as yet, and must be kept private until"
"1925"	"a riper day should come.  We had a gang of men on the road, working"
"1926"	"mainly by night.  They were stringing ground wires; we were afraid"
"1927"	"to put up poles, for they would attract too much inquiry.  Ground"
"1928"	"wires were good enough, in both instances, for my wires were"
"1929"	"protected by an insulation of my own invention which was perfect."
"1930"	"My men had orders to strike across country, avoiding roads, and"
"1931"	"establishing connection with any considerable towns whose lights"
"1932"	"betrayed their presence, and leaving experts in charge. Nobody"
"1933"	"could tell you how to find any place in the kingdom, for nobody"
"1934"	"ever went intentionally to any place, but only struck it by"
"1935"	"accident in his wanderings, and then generally left it without"
"1936"	"thinking to inquire what its name was.  At one time and another"
"1937"	"we had sent out topographical expeditions to survey and map the"
"1938"	"kingdom, but the priests had always interfered and raised trouble."
"1939"	"So we had given the thing up, for the present; it would be poor"
"1940"	"wisdom to antagonize the Church."
"1941"	"As for the general condition of the country, it was as it had been"
"1942"	"when I arrived in it, to all intents and purposes.  I had made"
"1943"	"changes, but they were necessarily slight, and they were not"
"1944"	"noticeable.  Thus far, I had not even meddled with taxation,"
"1945"	"outside of the taxes which provided the royal revenues.  I had"
"1946"	"systematized those, and put the service on an effective and"
"1947"	"righteous basis.  As a result, these revenues were already quadrupled,"
"1948"	"and yet the burden was so much more equably distributed than"
"1949"	"before, that all the kingdom felt a sense of relief, and the praises"
"1950"	"of my administration were hearty and general."
"1951"	"Personally, I struck an interruption, now, but I did not mind it,"
"1952"	"it could not have happened at a better time.  Earlier it could"
"1953"	"have annoyed me, but now everything was in good hands and swimming"
"1954"	"right along.  The king had reminded me several times, of late, that"
"1955"	"the postponement I had asked for, four years before, had about"
"1956"	"run out now.  It was a hint that I ought to be starting out to seek"
"1957"	"adventures and get up a reputation of a size to make me worthy"
"1958"	"of the honor of breaking a lance with Sir Sagramor, who was still"
"1959"	"out grailing, but was being hunted for by various relief expeditions,"
"1960"	"and might be found any year, now.  So you see I was expecting"
"1961"	"this interruption; it did not take me by surprise."
"1962"	"CHAPTER XI"
"1963"	"THE YANKEE IN SEARCH OF ADVENTURES"
"1964"	"There never was such a country for wandering liars; and they were"
"1965"	"of both sexes.  Hardly a month went by without one of these tramps"
"1966"	"arriving; and generally loaded with a tale about some princess or"
"1967"	"other wanting help to get her out of some far-away castle where"
"1968"	"she was held in captivity by a lawless scoundrel, usually a giant."
"1969"	"Now you would think that the first thing the king would do after"
"1970"	"listening to such a novelette from an entire stranger, would be"
"1971"	"to ask for credentials--yes, and a pointer or two as to locality"
"1972"	"of castle, best route to it, and so on.  But nobody ever thought"
"1973"	"of so simple and common-sense a thing at that.  No, everybody"
"1974"	"swallowed these people’s lies whole, and never asked a question"
"1975"	"of any sort or about anything.  Well, one day when I was not"
"1976"	"around, one of these people came along--it was a she one, this"
"1977"	"time--and told a tale of the usual pattern.  Her mistress was"
"1978"	"a captive in a vast and gloomy castle, along with forty-four other"
"1979"	"young and beautiful girls, pretty much all of them princesses;"
"1980"	"they had been languishing in that cruel captivity for twenty-six"
"1981"	"years; the masters of the castle were three stupendous brothers,"
"1982"	"each with four arms and one eye--the eye in the center of the"
"1983"	"forehead, and as big as a fruit.  Sort of fruit not mentioned;"
"1984"	"their usual slovenliness in statistics."
"1985"	"Would you believe it?  The king and the whole Round Table were"
"1986"	"in raptures over this preposterous opportunity for adventure."
"1987"	"Every knight of the Table jumped for the chance, and begged for it;"
"1988"	"but to their vexation and chagrin the king conferred it upon me,"
"1989"	"who had not asked for it at all."
"1990"	"By an effort, I contained my joy when Clarence brought me the news."
"1991"	"But he--he could not contain his.  His mouth gushed delight and"
"1992"	"gratitude in a steady discharge--delight in my good fortune,"
"1993"	"gratitude to the king for this splendid mark of his favor for me."
"1994"	"He could keep neither his legs nor his body still, but pirouetted"
"1995"	"about the place in an airy ecstasy of happiness."
"1996"	"On my side, I could have cursed the kindness that conferred upon"
"1997"	"me this benefaction, but I kept my vexation under the surface"
"1998"	"for policy’s sake, and did what I could to let on to be glad."
"1999"	"Indeed, I _said_ I was glad.  And in a way it was true; I was as"
"2000"	"glad as a person is when he is scalped."
"2001"	"Well, one must make the best of things, and not waste time with"
"2002"	"useless fretting, but get down to business and see what can be"
"2003"	"done.  In all lies there is wheat among the chaff; I must get at"
"2004"	"the wheat in this case: so I sent for the girl and she came.  She"
"2005"	"was a comely enough creature, and soft and modest, but, if signs"
"2006"	"went for anything, she didn’t know as much as a lady’s watch.  I said:"
"2007"	"“My dear, have you been questioned as to particulars?”"
"2008"	"She said she hadn’t."
"2009"	"“Well, I didn’t expect you had, but I thought I would ask, to make"
"2010"	"sure; it’s the way I’ve been raised.  Now you mustn’t take it"
"2011"	"unkindly if I remind you that as we don’t know you, we must go"
"2012"	"a little slow.  You may be all right, of course, and we’ll hope"
"2013"	"that you are; but to take it for granted isn’t business.  _You_"
"2014"	"understand that.  I’m obliged to ask you a few questions; just"
"2015"	"answer up fair and square, and don’t be afraid.  Where do you"
"2016"	"live, when you are at home?”"
"2017"	"“In the land of Moder, fair sir.”"
"2018"	"“Land of Moder.  I don’t remember hearing of it before."
"2019"	"Parents living?”"
"2020"	"“As to that, I know not if they be yet on live, sith it is many"
"2021"	"years that I have lain shut up in the castle.”"
"2022"	"“Your name, please?”"
"2023"	"“I hight the Demoiselle Alisande la Carteloise, an it please you.”"
"2024"	"“Do you know anybody here who can identify you?”"
"2025"	"“That were not likely, fair lord, I being come hither now for"
"2026"	"the first time.”"
"2027"	"“Have you brought any letters--any documents--any proofs that"
"2028"	"you are trustworthy and truthful?”"
"2029"	"“Of a surety, no; and wherefore should I?  Have I not a tongue,"
"2030"	"and cannot I say all that myself?”"
"2031"	"“But _your_ saying it, you know, and somebody else’s saying it,"
"2032"	"is different.”"
"2033"	"“Different?  How might that be?  I fear me I do not understand.”"
"2034"	"“Don’t _understand_?  Land of--why, you see--you see--why, great Scott,"
"2035"	"can’t you understand a little thing like that?  Can’t you understand"
"2036"	"the difference between your--_why_ do you look so innocent and idiotic!”"
"2037"	"“I?  In truth I know not, but an it were the will of God.”"
"2038"	"“Yes, yes, I reckon that’s about the size of it.  Don’t mind my"
"2039"	"seeming excited; I’m not.  Let us change the subject.  Now as"
"2040"	"to this castle, with forty-five princesses in it, and three ogres"
"2041"	"at the head of it, tell me--where is this harem?”"
"2042"	"“Harem?”"
"2043"	"“The _castle_, you understand; where is the castle?”"
"2044"	"“Oh, as to that, it is great, and strong, and well beseen, and"
"2045"	"lieth in a far country.  Yes, it is many leagues.”"
"2046"	"“_How_ many?”"
"2047"	"“Ah, fair sir, it were woundily hard to tell, they are so many,"
"2048"	"and do so lap the one upon the other, and being made all in the"
"2049"	"same image and tincted with the same color, one may not know"
"2050"	"the one league from its fellow, nor how to count them except"
"2051"	"they be taken apart, and ye wit well it were God’s work to do"
"2052"	"that, being not within man’s capacity; for ye will note--”"
"2053"	"“Hold on, hold on, never mind about the distance; _whereabouts_"
"2054"	"does the castle lie?  What’s the direction from here?”"
"2055"	"“Ah, please you sir, it hath no direction from here; by reason"
"2056"	"that the road lieth not straight, but turneth evermore; wherefore"
"2057"	"the direction of its place abideth not, but is some time under"
"2058"	"the one sky and anon under another, whereso if ye be minded that"
"2059"	"it is in the east, and wend thitherward, ye shall observe that"
"2060"	"the way of the road doth yet again turn upon itself by the space"
"2061"	"of half a circle, and this marvel happing again and yet again and"
"2062"	"still again, it will grieve you that you had thought by vanities"
"2063"	"of the mind to thwart and bring to naught the will of Him that"
"2064"	"giveth not a castle a direction from a place except it pleaseth"
"2065"	"Him, and if it please Him not, will the rather that even all castles"
"2066"	"and all directions thereunto vanish out of the earth, leaving the"
"2067"	"places wherein they tarried desolate and vacant, so warning His"
"2068"	"creatures that where He will He will, and where He will not He--”"
"2069"	"“Oh, that’s all right, that’s all right, give us a rest; never mind"
"2070"	"about the direction, _hang_ the direction--I beg pardon, I beg"
"2071"	"a thousand pardons, I am not well to-day; pay no attention when"
"2072"	"I soliloquize, it is an old habit, an old, bad habit, and hard"
"2073"	"to get rid of when one’s digestion is all disordered with eating"
"2074"	"food that was raised forever and ever before he was born; good"
"2075"	"land! a man can’t keep his functions regular on spring chickens"
"2076"	"thirteen hundred years old.  But come--never mind about that;"
"2077"	"let’s--have you got such a thing as a map of that region about"
"2078"	"you?  Now a good map--”"
"2079"	"“Is it peradventure that manner of thing which of late the unbelievers"
"2080"	"have brought from over the great seas, which, being boiled in oil,"
"2081"	"and an onion and salt added thereto, doth--”"
"2082"	"“What, a map?  What are you talking about?  Don’t you know what"
"2083"	"a map is?  There, there, never mind, don’t explain, I hate"
"2084"	"explanations; they fog a thing up so that you can’t tell anything"
"2085"	"about it.  Run along, dear; good-day; show her the way, Clarence.”"
"2086"	"Oh, well, it was reasonably plain, now, why these donkeys didn’t"
"2087"	"prospect these liars for details.  It may be that this girl had"
"2088"	"a fact in her somewhere, but I don’t believe you could have sluiced"
"2089"	"it out with a hydraulic; nor got it with the earlier forms of"
"2090"	"blasting, even; it was a case for dynamite.  Why, she was a perfect"
"2091"	"ass; and yet the king and his knights had listened to her as if"
"2092"	"she had been a leaf out of the gospel.  It kind of sizes up the"
"2093"	"whole party.  And think of the simple ways of this court: this"
"2094"	"wandering wench hadn’t any more trouble to get access to the king"
"2095"	"in his palace than she would have had to get into the poorhouse"
"2096"	"in my day and country.  In fact, he was glad to see her, glad"
"2097"	"to hear her tale; with that adventure of hers to offer, she was"
"2098"	"as welcome as a corpse is to a coroner."
"2099"	"Just as I was ending-up these reflections, Clarence came back."
"2100"	"I remarked upon the barren result of my efforts with the girl;"
"2101"	"hadn’t got hold of a single point that could help me to find"
"2102"	"the castle.  The youth looked a little surprised, or puzzled,"
"2103"	"or something, and intimated that he had been wondering to himself"
"2104"	"what I had wanted to ask the girl all those questions for."
"2105"	"“Why, great guns,” I said, “don’t I want to find the castle?  And"
"2106"	"how else would I go about it?”"
"2107"	"“La, sweet your worship, one may lightly answer that, I ween."
"2108"	"She will go with thee.  They always do.  She will ride with thee.”"
"2109"	"“Ride with me?  Nonsense!”"
"2110"	"“But of a truth she will.  She will ride with thee.  Thou shalt see.”"
"2111"	"“What?  She browse around the hills and scour the woods with me"
"2112"	"--alone--and I as good as engaged to be married?  Why, it’s scandalous."
"2113"	"Think how it would look.”"
"2114"	"My, the dear face that rose before me!  The boy was eager to know"
"2115"	"all about this tender matter.  I swore him to secrecy and then"
"2116"	"whispered her name--“Puss Flanagan.”  He looked disappointed,"
"2117"	"and said he didn’t remember the countess.  How natural it was for"
"2118"	"the little courtier to give her a rank.  He asked me where she lived."
"2119"	"“In East Har--” I came to myself and stopped, a little confused;"
"2120"	"then I said, “Never mind, now; I’ll tell you some time.”"
"2121"	"And might he see her?  Would I let him see her some day?"
"2122"	"It was but a little thing to promise--thirteen hundred years"
"2123"	"or so--and he so eager; so I said Yes.  But I sighed; I couldn’t"
"2124"	"help it.  And yet there was no sense in sighing, for she wasn’t"
"2125"	"born yet.  But that is the way we are made: we don’t reason,"
"2126"	"where we feel; we just feel."
"2127"	"My expedition was all the talk that day and that night, and the"
"2128"	"boys were very good to me, and made much of me, and seemed to have"
"2129"	"forgotten their vexation and disappointment, and come to be as"
"2130"	"anxious for me to hive those ogres and set those ripe old virgins"
"2131"	"loose as if it were themselves that had the contract.  Well, they"
"2132"	"_were_ good children--but just children, that is all.  And they"
"2133"	"gave me no end of points about how to scout for giants, and how"
"2134"	"to scoop them in; and they told me all sorts of charms against"
"2135"	"enchantments, and gave me salves and other rubbish to put on my"
"2136"	"wounds.  But it never occurred to one of them to reflect that if"
"2137"	"I was such a wonderful necromancer as I was pretending to be,"
"2138"	"I ought not to need salves or instructions, or charms against"
"2139"	"enchantments, and, least of all, arms and armor, on a foray of any"
"2140"	"kind--even against fire-spouting dragons, and devils hot from"
"2141"	"perdition, let alone such poor adversaries as these I was after,"
"2142"	"these commonplace ogres of the back settlements."
"2143"	"I was to have an early breakfast, and start at dawn, for that was"
"2144"	"the usual way; but I had the demon’s own time with my armor,"
"2145"	"and this delayed me a little.  It is troublesome to get into, and"
"2146"	"there is so much detail.  First you wrap a layer or two of blanket"
"2147"	"around your body, for a sort of cushion and to keep off the cold"
"2148"	"iron; then you put on your sleeves and shirt of chain mail--these"
"2149"	"are made of small steel links woven together, and they form a fabric"
"2150"	"so flexible that if you toss your shirt onto the floor, it slumps"
"2151"	"into a pile like a peck of wet fish-net; it is very heavy and"
"2152"	"is nearly the uncomfortablest material in the world for a night"
"2153"	"shirt, yet plenty used it for that--tax collectors, and reformers,"
"2154"	"and one-horse kings with a defective title, and those sorts of"
"2155"	"people; then you put on your shoes--flat-boats roofed over with"
"2156"	"interleaving bands of steel--and screw your clumsy spurs into"
"2157"	"the heels.  Next you buckle your greaves on your legs, and your"
"2158"	"cuisses on your thighs; then come your backplate and your breastplate,"
"2159"	"and you begin to feel crowded; then you hitch onto the breastplate"
"2160"	"the half-petticoat of broad overlapping bands of steel which hangs"
"2161"	"down in front but is scolloped out behind so you can sit down,"
"2162"	"and isn’t any real improvement on an inverted coal scuttle, either"
"2163"	"for looks or for wear, or to wipe your hands on; next you belt"
"2164"	"on your sword; then you put your stove-pipe joints onto your arms,"
"2165"	"your iron gauntlets onto your hands, your iron rat-trap onto your"
"2166"	"head, with a rag of steel web hitched onto it to hang over the back"
"2167"	"of your neck--and there you are, snug as a candle in a candle-mould."
"2168"	"This is no time to dance.  Well, a man that is packed away like"
"2169"	"that is a nut that isn’t worth the cracking, there is so little of"
"2170"	"the meat, when you get down to it, by comparison with the shell."
"2171"	"The boys helped me, or I never could have got in.  Just as we"
"2172"	"finished, Sir Bedivere happened in, and I saw that as like as not"
"2173"	"I hadn’t chosen the most convenient outfit for a long trip.  How"
"2174"	"stately he looked; and tall and broad and grand.  He had on his"
"2175"	"head a conical steel casque that only came down to his ears, and"
"2176"	"for visor had only a narrow steel bar that extended down to his"
"2177"	"upper lip and protected his nose; and all the rest of him, from"
"2178"	"neck to heel, was flexible chain mail, trousers and all.  But"
"2179"	"pretty much all of him was hidden under his outside garment, which"
"2180"	"of course was of chain mail, as I said, and hung straight from his"
"2181"	"shoulders to his ankles; and from his middle to the bottom, both"
"2182"	"before and behind, was divided, so that he could ride and let the"
"2183"	"skirts hang down on each side.  He was going grailing, and it was"
"2184"	"just the outfit for it, too.  I would have given a good deal for"
"2185"	"that ulster, but it was too late now to be fooling around.  The sun"
"2186"	"was just up, the king and the court were all on hand to see me off"
"2187"	"and wish me luck; so it wouldn’t be etiquette for me to tarry."
"2188"	"You don’t get on your horse yourself; no, if you tried it you"
"2189"	"would get disappointed.  They carry you out, just as they carry"
"2190"	"a sun-struck man to the drug store, and put you on, and help get"
"2191"	"you to rights, and fix your feet in the stirrups; and all the while"
"2192"	"you do feel so strange and stuffy and like somebody else--like"
"2193"	"somebody that has been married on a sudden, or struck by lightning,"
"2194"	"or something like that, and hasn’t quite fetched around yet, and"
"2195"	"is sort of numb, and can’t just get his bearings.  Then they"
"2196"	"stood up the mast they called a spear, in its socket by my left"
"2197"	"foot, and I gripped it with my hand; lastly they hung my shield"
"2198"	"around my neck, and I was all complete and ready to up anchor"
"2199"	"and get to sea.  Everybody was as good to me as they could be,"
"2200"	"and a maid of honor gave me the stirrup-cup her own self.  There was"
"2201"	"nothing more to do now, but for that damsel to get up behind me on"
"2202"	"a pillion, which she did, and put an arm or so around me to hold on."
"2203"	"And so we started, and everybody gave us a goodbye and waved their"
"2204"	"handkerchiefs or helmets.  And everybody we met, going down the hill"
"2205"	"and through the village was respectful to us, except some shabby"
"2206"	"little boys on the outskirts.  They said:"
"2207"	"“Oh, what a guy!”  And hove clods at us."
"2208"	"In my experience boys are the same in all ages.  They don’t respect"
"2209"	"anything, they don’t care for anything or anybody.  They say"
"2210"	"“Go up, baldhead” to the prophet going his unoffending way in"
"2211"	"the gray of antiquity; they sass me in the holy gloom of the"
"2212"	"Middle Ages; and I had seen them act the same way in Buchanan’s"
"2213"	"administration; I remember, because I was there and helped.  The"
"2214"	"prophet had his bears and settled with his boys; and I wanted"
"2215"	"to get down and settle with mine, but it wouldn’t answer, because"
"2216"	"I couldn’t have got up again.  I hate a country without a derrick."
"2217"	"CHAPTER XII"
"2218"	"SLOW TORTURE"
"2219"	"Straight off, we were in the country.  It was most lovely and"
"2220"	"pleasant in those sylvan solitudes in the early cool morning"
"2221"	"in the first freshness of autumn.  From hilltops we saw fair"
"2222"	"green valleys lying spread out below, with streams winding through"
"2223"	"them, and island groves of trees here and there, and huge lonely"
"2224"	"oaks scattered about and casting black blots of shade; and beyond"
"2225"	"the valleys we saw the ranges of hills, blue with haze, stretching"
"2226"	"away in billowy perspective to the horizon, with at wide intervals"
"2227"	"a dim fleck of white or gray on a wave-summit, which we knew was"
"2228"	"a castle.  We crossed broad natural lawns sparkling with dew,"
"2229"	"and we moved like spirits, the cushioned turf giving out no sound"
"2230"	"of footfall; we dreamed along through glades in a mist of green"
"2231"	"light that got its tint from the sun-drenched roof of leaves"
"2232"	"overhead, and by our feet the clearest and coldest of runlets"
"2233"	"went frisking and gossiping over its reefs and making a sort of"
"2234"	"whispering music, comfortable to hear; and at times we left the"
"2235"	"world behind and entered into the solemn great deeps and rich"
"2236"	"gloom of the forest, where furtive wild things whisked and scurried"
"2237"	"by and were gone before you could even get your eye on the place"
"2238"	"where the noise was; and where only the earliest birds were turning"
"2239"	"out and getting to business with a song here and a quarrel yonder"
"2240"	"and a mysterious far-off hammering and drumming for worms on"
"2241"	"a tree trunk away somewhere in the impenetrable remotenesses of"
"2242"	"the woods.  And by and by out we would swing again into the glare."
"2243"	"About the third or fourth or fifth time that we swung out into"
"2244"	"the glare--it was along there somewhere, a couple of hours or so"
"2245"	"after sun-up--it wasn’t as pleasant as it had been.  It was"
"2246"	"beginning to get hot.  This was quite noticeable.  We had a very"
"2247"	"long pull, after that, without any shade.  Now it is curious how"
"2248"	"progressively little frets grow and multiply after they once get"
"2249"	"a start.  Things which I didn’t mind at all, at first, I began"
"2250"	"to mind now--and more and more, too, all the time.  The first"
"2251"	"ten or fifteen times I wanted my handkerchief I didn’t seem to care;"
"2252"	"I got along, and said never mind, it isn’t any matter, and dropped"
"2253"	"it out of my mind.  But now it was different; I wanted it all"
"2254"	"the time; it was nag, nag, nag, right along, and no rest; I couldn’t"
"2255"	"get it out of my mind; and so at last I lost my temper and said"
"2256"	"hang a man that would make a suit of armor without any pockets"
"2257"	"in it.  You see I had my handkerchief in my helmet; and some other"
"2258"	"things; but it was that kind of a helmet that you can’t take off"
"2259"	"by yourself.  That hadn’t occurred to me when I put it there;"
"2260"	"and in fact I didn’t know it.  I supposed it would be particularly"
"2261"	"convenient there.  And so now, the thought of its being there,"
"2262"	"so handy and close by, and yet not get-at-able, made it all the"
"2263"	"worse and the harder to bear.  Yes, the thing that you can’t get"
"2264"	"is the thing that you want, mainly; every one has noticed that."
"2265"	"Well, it took my mind off from everything else; took it clear off,"
"2266"	"and centered it in my helmet; and mile after mile, there it stayed,"
"2267"	"imagining the handkerchief, picturing the handkerchief; and it"
"2268"	"was bitter and aggravating to have the salt sweat keep trickling"
"2269"	"down into my eyes, and I couldn’t get at it.  It seems like a little"
"2270"	"thing, on paper, but it was not a little thing at all; it was"
"2271"	"the most real kind of misery.  I would not say it if it was not so."
"2272"	"I made up my mind that I would carry along a reticule next time,"
"2273"	"let it look how it might, and people say what they would.  Of course"
"2274"	"these iron dudes of the Round Table would think it was scandalous,"
"2275"	"and maybe raise Sheol about it, but as for me, give me comfort"
"2276"	"first, and style afterwards.  So we jogged along, and now and then"
"2277"	"we struck a stretch of dust, and it would tumble up in clouds and"
"2278"	"get into my nose and make me sneeze and cry; and of course I said"
"2279"	"things I oughtn’t to have said, I don’t deny that.  I am not"
"2280"	"better than others."
"2281"	"We couldn’t seem to meet anybody in this lonesome Britain, not"
"2282"	"even an ogre; and, in the mood I was in then, it was well for"
"2283"	"the ogre; that is, an ogre with a handkerchief.  Most knights"
"2284"	"would have thought of nothing but getting his armor; but so I got"
"2285"	"his bandanna, he could keep his hardware, for all of me."
"2286"	"Meantime, it was getting hotter and hotter in there.  You see,"
"2287"	"the sun was beating down and warming up the iron more and more"
"2288"	"all the time.  Well, when you are hot, that way, every little thing"
"2289"	"irritates you.  When I trotted, I rattled like a crate of dishes,"
"2290"	"and that annoyed me; and moreover I couldn’t seem to stand that"
"2291"	"shield slatting and banging, now about my breast, now around my"
"2292"	"back; and if I dropped into a walk my joints creaked and screeched"
"2293"	"in that wearisome way that a wheelbarrow does, and as we didn’t"
"2294"	"create any breeze at that gait, I was like to get fried in that"
"2295"	"stove; and besides, the quieter you went the heavier the iron"
"2296"	"settled down on you and the more and more tons you seemed to weigh"
"2297"	"every minute.  And you had to be always changing hands, and passing"
"2298"	"your spear over to the other foot, it got so irksome for one hand"
"2299"	"to hold it long at a time."
"2300"	"Well, you know, when you perspire that way, in rivers, there comes"
"2301"	"a time when you--when you--well, when you itch.  You are inside,"
"2302"	"your hands are outside; so there you are; nothing but iron between."
"2303"	"It is not a light thing, let it sound as it may.  First it is one"
"2304"	"place; then another; then some more; and it goes on spreading and"
"2305"	"spreading, and at last the territory is all occupied, and nobody"
"2306"	"can imagine what you feel like, nor how unpleasant it is.  And"
"2307"	"when it had got to the worst, and it seemed to me that I could"
"2308"	"not stand anything more, a fly got in through the bars and settled"
"2309"	"on my nose, and the bars were stuck and wouldn’t work, and I"
"2310"	"couldn’t get the visor up; and I could only shake my head, which"
"2311"	"was baking hot by this time, and the fly--well, you know how a fly"
"2312"	"acts when he has got a certainty--he only minded the shaking enough"
"2313"	"to change from nose to lip, and lip to ear, and buzz and buzz"
"2314"	"all around in there, and keep on lighting and biting, in a way"
"2315"	"that a person, already so distressed as I was, simply could not"
"2316"	"stand.  So I gave in, and got Alisande to unship the helmet and"
"2317"	"relieve me of it.  Then she emptied the conveniences out of it"
"2318"	"and fetched it full of water, and I drank and then stood up, and"
"2319"	"she poured the rest down inside the armor. One cannot think how"
"2320"	"refreshing it was.  She continued to fetch and pour until I was"
"2321"	"well soaked and thoroughly comfortable."
"2322"	"It was good to have a rest--and peace.  But nothing is quite"
"2323"	"perfect in this life, at any time.  I had made a pipe a while back,"
"2324"	"and also some pretty fair tobacco; not the real thing, but what"
"2325"	"some of the Indians use: the inside bark of the willow, dried."
"2326"	"These comforts had been in the helmet, and now I had them again,"
"2327"	"but no matches."
"2328"	"Gradually, as the time wore along, one annoying fact was borne in"
"2329"	"upon my understanding--that we were weather-bound.  An armed novice"
"2330"	"cannot mount his horse without help and plenty of it.  Sandy was"
"2331"	"not enough; not enough for me, anyway.  We had to wait until"
"2332"	"somebody should come along.  Waiting, in silence, would have been"
"2333"	"agreeable enough, for I was full of matter for reflection, and"
"2334"	"wanted to give it a chance to work.  I wanted to try and think out"
"2335"	"how it was that rational or even half-rational men could ever"
"2336"	"have learned to wear armor, considering its inconveniences; and"
"2337"	"how they had managed to keep up such a fashion for generations"
"2338"	"when it was plain that what I had suffered to-day they had had"
"2339"	"to suffer all the days of their lives.  I wanted to think that out;"
