"2340"	"and moreover I wanted to think out some way to reform this evil"
"2341"	"and persuade the people to let the foolish fashion die out; but"
"2342"	"thinking was out of the question in the circumstances.  You couldn’t"
"2343"	"think, where Sandy was."
"2344"	"She was a quite biddable creature and good-hearted, but she had"
"2345"	"a flow of talk that was as steady as a mill, and made your head"
"2346"	"sore like the drays and wagons in a city.  If she had had a cork"
"2347"	"she would have been a comfort.  But you can’t cork that kind;"
"2348"	"they would die.  Her clack was going all day, and you would think"
"2349"	"something would surely happen to her works, by and by; but no,"
"2350"	"they never got out of order; and she never had to slack up for"
"2351"	"words.  She could grind, and pump, and churn, and buzz by the week,"
"2352"	"and never stop to oil up or blow out.  And yet the result was just"
"2353"	"nothing but wind.  She never had any ideas, any more than a fog"
"2354"	"has.  She was a perfect blatherskite; I mean for jaw, jaw, jaw,"
"2355"	"talk, talk, talk, jabber, jabber, jabber; but just as good as she"
"2356"	"could be.  I hadn’t minded her mill that morning, on account of"
"2357"	"having that hornets’ nest of other troubles; but more than once"
"2358"	"in the afternoon I had to say:"
"2359"	"“Take a rest, child; the way you are using up all the domestic air,"
"2360"	"the kingdom will have to go to importing it by to-morrow, and it’s"
"2361"	"a low enough treasury without that.”"
"2362"	"CHAPTER XIII"
"2363"	"FREEMEN"
"2364"	"Yes, it is strange how little a while at a time a person can be"
"2365"	"contented.  Only a little while back, when I was riding and"
"2366"	"suffering, what a heaven this peace, this rest, this sweet serenity"
"2367"	"in this secluded shady nook by this purling stream would have"
"2368"	"seemed, where I could keep perfectly comfortable all the time"
"2369"	"by pouring a dipper of water into my armor now and then; yet"
"2370"	"already I was getting dissatisfied; partly because I could not"
"2371"	"light my pipe--for, although I had long ago started a match factory,"
"2372"	"I had forgotten to bring matches with me--and partly because we"
"2373"	"had nothing to eat.  Here was another illustration of the childlike"
"2374"	"improvidence of this age and people.  A man in armor always trusted"
"2375"	"to chance for his food on a journey, and would have been scandalized"
"2376"	"at the idea of hanging a basket of sandwiches on his spear.  There"
"2377"	"was probably not a knight of all the Round Table combination who"
"2378"	"would not rather have died than been caught carrying such a thing"
"2379"	"as that on his flagstaff.  And yet there could not be anything more"
"2380"	"sensible.  It had been my intention to smuggle a couple of sandwiches"
"2381"	"into my helmet, but I was interrupted in the act, and had to make"
"2382"	"an excuse and lay them aside, and a dog got them."
"2383"	"Night approached, and with it a storm.  The darkness came on fast."
"2384"	"We must camp, of course.  I found a good shelter for the demoiselle"
"2385"	"under a rock, and went off and found another for myself.  But"
"2386"	"I was obliged to remain in my armor, because I could not get it off"
"2387"	"by myself and yet could not allow Alisande to help, because it"
"2388"	"would have seemed so like undressing before folk.  It would not"
"2389"	"have amounted to that in reality, because I had clothes on"
"2390"	"underneath; but the prejudices of one’s breeding are not gotten"
"2391"	"rid of just at a jump, and I knew that when it came to stripping"
"2392"	"off that bob-tailed iron petticoat I should be embarrassed."
"2393"	"With the storm came a change of weather; and the stronger the wind"
"2394"	"blew, and the wilder the rain lashed around, the colder and colder"
"2395"	"it got.  Pretty soon, various kinds of bugs and ants and worms"
"2396"	"and things began to flock in out of the wet and crawl down inside"
"2397"	"my armor to get warm; and while some of them behaved well enough,"
"2398"	"and snuggled up amongst my clothes and got quiet, the majority"
"2399"	"were of a restless, uncomfortable sort, and never stayed still,"
"2400"	"but went on prowling and hunting for they did not know what;"
"2401"	"especially the ants, which went tickling along in wearisome"
"2402"	"procession from one end of me to the other by the hour, and are"
"2403"	"a kind of creatures which I never wish to sleep with again."
"2404"	"It would be my advice to persons situated in this way, to not roll"
"2405"	"or thrash around, because this excites the interest of all the"
"2406"	"different sorts of animals and makes every last one of them want"
"2407"	"to turn out and see what is going on, and this makes things worse"
"2408"	"than they were before, and of course makes you objurgate harder,"
"2409"	"too, if you can.  Still, if one did not roll and thrash around"
"2410"	"he would die; so perhaps it is as well to do one way as the other;"
"2411"	"there is no real choice.  Even after I was frozen solid I could"
"2412"	"still distinguish that tickling, just as a corpse does when he is"
"2413"	"taking electric treatment.  I said I would never wear armor"
"2414"	"after this trip."
"2415"	"All those trying hours whilst I was frozen and yet was in a living"
"2416"	"fire, as you may say, on account of that swarm of crawlers, that"
"2417"	"same unanswerable question kept circling and circling through my"
"2418"	"tired head: How do people stand this miserable armor?  How have"
"2419"	"they managed to stand it all these generations?  How can they sleep"
"2420"	"at night for dreading the tortures of next day?"
"2421"	"When the morning came at last, I was in a bad enough plight: seedy,"
"2422"	"drowsy, fagged, from want of sleep; weary from thrashing around,"
"2423"	"famished from long fasting; pining for a bath, and to get rid of"
"2424"	"the animals; and crippled with rheumatism.  And how had it fared"
"2425"	"with the nobly born, the titled aristocrat, the Demoiselle Alisande"
"2426"	"la Carteloise?  Why, she was as fresh as a squirrel; she had slept"
"2427"	"like the dead; and as for a bath, probably neither she nor any"
"2428"	"other noble in the land had ever had one, and so she was not"
"2429"	"missing it.  Measured by modern standards, they were merely modified"
"2430"	"savages, those people.  This noble lady showed no impatience to get"
"2431"	"to breakfast--and that smacks of the savage, too.  On their journeys"
"2432"	"those Britons were used to long fasts, and knew how to bear them;"
"2433"	"and also how to freight up against probable fasts before starting,"
"2434"	"after the style of the Indian and the anaconda.  As like as not,"
"2435"	"Sandy was loaded for a three-day stretch."
"2436"	"We were off before sunrise, Sandy riding and I limping along"
"2437"	"behind.  In half an hour we came upon a group of ragged poor"
"2438"	"creatures who had assembled to mend the thing which was regarded"
"2439"	"as a road.  They were as humble as animals to me; and when I"
"2440"	"proposed to breakfast with them, they were so flattered, so"
"2441"	"overwhelmed by this extraordinary condescension of mine that"
"2442"	"at first they were not able to believe that I was in earnest."
"2443"	"My lady put up her scornful lip and withdrew to one side; she said"
"2444"	"in their hearing that she would as soon think of eating with the"
"2445"	"other cattle--a remark which embarrassed these poor devils merely"
"2446"	"because it referred to them, and not because it insulted or offended"
"2447"	"them, for it didn’t.  And yet they were not slaves, not chattels."
"2448"	"By a sarcasm of law and phrase they were freemen.  Seven-tenths"
"2449"	"of the free population of the country were of just their class and"
"2450"	"degree: small “independent” farmers, artisans, etc.; which is"
"2451"	"to say, they were the nation, the actual Nation; they were about"
"2452"	"all of it that was useful, or worth saving, or really respect-worthy,"
"2453"	"and to subtract them would have been to subtract the Nation and"
"2454"	"leave behind some dregs, some refuse, in the shape of a king,"
"2455"	"nobility and gentry, idle, unproductive, acquainted mainly with"
"2456"	"the arts of wasting and destroying, and of no sort of use or value"
"2457"	"in any rationally constructed world.  And yet, by ingenious"
"2458"	"contrivance, this gilded minority, instead of being in the tail"
"2459"	"of the procession where it belonged, was marching head up and"
"2460"	"banners flying, at the other end of it; had elected itself to be"
"2461"	"the Nation, and these innumerable clams had permitted it so long"
"2462"	"that they had come at last to accept it as a truth; and not only"
"2463"	"that, but to believe it right and as it should be.  The priests"
"2464"	"had told their fathers and themselves that this ironical state"
"2465"	"of things was ordained of God; and so, not reflecting upon how"
"2466"	"unlike God it would be to amuse himself with sarcasms, and especially"
"2467"	"such poor transparent ones as this, they had dropped the matter"
"2468"	"there and become respectfully quiet."
"2469"	"The talk of these meek people had a strange enough sound in"
"2470"	"a formerly American ear.  They were freemen, but they could not"
"2471"	"leave the estates of their lord or their bishop without his"
"2472"	"permission; they could not prepare their own bread, but must have"
"2473"	"their corn ground and their bread baked at his mill and his bakery,"
"2474"	"and pay roundly for the same; they could not sell a piece of their"
"2475"	"own property without paying him a handsome percentage of the"
"2476"	"proceeds, nor buy a piece of somebody else’s without remembering"
"2477"	"him in cash for the privilege; they had to harvest his grain for him"
"2478"	"gratis, and be ready to come at a moment’s notice, leaving their"
"2479"	"own crop to destruction by the threatened storm; they had to let"
"2480"	"him plant fruit trees in their fields, and then keep their indignation"
"2481"	"to themselves when his heedless fruit-gatherers trampled the grain"
"2482"	"around the trees; they had to smother their anger when his hunting"
"2483"	"parties galloped through their fields laying waste the result of"
"2484"	"their patient toil; they were not allowed to keep doves themselves,"
"2485"	"and when the swarms from my lord’s dovecote settled on their crops"
"2486"	"they must not lose their temper and kill a bird, for awful would"
"2487"	"the penalty be; when the harvest was at last gathered, then came"
"2488"	"the procession of robbers to levy their blackmail upon it: first"
"2489"	"the Church carted off its fat tenth, then the king’s commissioner"
"2490"	"took his twentieth, then my lord’s people made a mighty inroad"
"2491"	"upon the remainder; after which, the skinned freeman had liberty"
"2492"	"to bestow the remnant in his barn, in case it was worth the trouble;"
"2493"	"there were taxes, and taxes, and taxes, and more taxes, and taxes"
"2494"	"again, and yet other taxes--upon this free and independent pauper,"
"2495"	"but none upon his lord the baron or the bishop, none upon the"
"2496"	"wasteful nobility or the all-devouring Church; if the baron would"
"2497"	"sleep unvexed, the freeman must sit up all night after his day’s"
"2498"	"work and whip the ponds to keep the frogs quiet; if the freeman’s"
"2499"	"daughter--but no, that last infamy of monarchical government is"
"2500"	"unprintable; and finally, if the freeman, grown desperate with his"
"2501"	"tortures, found his life unendurable under such conditions, and"
"2502"	"sacrificed it and fled to death for mercy and refuge, the gentle"
"2503"	"Church condemned him to eternal fire, the gentle law buried him"
"2504"	"at midnight at the cross-roads with a stake through his back,"
"2505"	"and his master the baron or the bishop confiscated all his property"
"2506"	"and turned his widow and his orphans out of doors."
"2507"	"And here were these freemen assembled in the early morning to work"
"2508"	"on their lord the bishop’s road three days each--gratis; every"
"2509"	"head of a family, and every son of a family, three days each,"
"2510"	"gratis, and a day or so added for their servants.  Why, it was"
"2511"	"like reading about France and the French, before the ever memorable"
"2512"	"and blessed Revolution, which swept a thousand years of such"
"2513"	"villany away in one swift tidal-wave of blood--one: a settlement"
"2514"	"of that hoary debt in the proportion of half a drop of blood for"
"2515"	"each hogshead of it that had been pressed by slow tortures out of"
"2516"	"that people in the weary stretch of ten centuries of wrong and"
"2517"	"shame and misery the like of which was not to be mated but in hell."
"2518"	"There were two “Reigns of Terror,” if we would but remember it"
"2519"	"and consider it; the one wrought murder in hot passion, the other"
"2520"	"in heartless cold blood; the one lasted mere months, the other had"
"2521"	"lasted a thousand years; the one inflicted death upon ten thousand"
"2522"	"persons, the other upon a hundred millions; but our shudders are"
"2523"	"all for the “horrors” of the minor Terror, the momentary Terror,"
"2524"	"so to speak; whereas, what is the horror of swift death by the axe,"
"2525"	"compared with lifelong death from hunger, cold, insult, cruelty,"
"2526"	"and heart-break?  What is swift death by lightning compared with"
"2527"	"death by slow fire at the stake?  A city cemetery could contain the"
"2528"	"coffins filled by that brief Terror which we have all been so"
"2529"	"diligently taught to shiver at and mourn over; but all France could"
"2530"	"hardly contain the coffins filled by that older and real Terror"
"2531"	"--that unspeakably bitter and awful Terror which none of us has"
"2532"	"been taught to see in its vastness or pity as it deserves."
"2533"	"These poor ostensible freemen who were sharing their breakfast"
"2534"	"and their talk with me, were as full of humble reverence for their"
"2535"	"king and Church and nobility as their worst enemy could desire."
"2536"	"There was something pitifully ludicrous about it.  I asked them"
"2537"	"if they supposed a nation of people ever existed, who, with a free"
"2538"	"vote in every man’s hand, would elect that a single family and its"
"2539"	"descendants should reign over it forever, whether gifted or boobies,"
"2540"	"to the exclusion of all other families--including the voter’s; and"
"2541"	"would also elect that a certain hundred families should be raised"
"2542"	"to dizzy summits of rank, and clothed on with offensive transmissible"
"2543"	"glories and privileges to the exclusion of the rest of the nation’s"
"2544"	"families--_including his own_."
"2545"	"They all looked unhit, and said they didn’t know; that they had"
"2546"	"never thought about it before, and it hadn’t ever occurred to them"
"2547"	"that a nation could be so situated that every man _could_ have"
"2548"	"a say in the government.  I said I had seen one--and that it would"
"2549"	"last until it had an Established Church.  Again they were all"
"2550"	"unhit--at first.  But presently one man looked up and asked me"
"2551"	"to state that proposition again; and state it slowly, so it could"
"2552"	"soak into his understanding.  I did it; and after a little he had"
"2553"	"the idea, and he brought his fist down and said _he_ didn’t believe"
"2554"	"a nation where every man had a vote would voluntarily get down"
"2555"	"in the mud and dirt in any such way; and that to steal from a nation"
"2556"	"its will and preference must be a crime and the first of all crimes."
"2557"	"I said to myself:"
"2558"	"“This one’s a man.  If I were backed by enough of his sort, I would"
"2559"	"make a strike for the welfare of this country, and try to prove"
"2560"	"myself its loyalest citizen by making a wholesome change in its"
"2561"	"system of government.”"
"2562"	"You see my kind of loyalty was loyalty to one’s country, not to"
"2563"	"its institutions or its office-holders.  The country is the real"
"2564"	"thing, the substantial thing, the eternal thing; it is the thing"
"2565"	"to watch over, and care for, and be loyal to; institutions are"
"2566"	"extraneous, they are its mere clothing, and clothing can wear out,"
"2567"	"become ragged, cease to be comfortable, cease to protect the body"
"2568"	"from winter, disease, and death.  To be loyal to rags, to shout"
"2569"	"for rags, to worship rags, to die for rags--that is a loyalty"
"2570"	"of unreason, it is pure animal; it belongs to monarchy, was invented"
"2571"	"by monarchy; let monarchy keep it.  I was from Connecticut, whose"
"2572"	"Constitution declares “that all political power is inherent in"
"2573"	"the people, and all free governments are founded on their authority"
"2574"	"and instituted for their benefit; and that they have _at all times_"
"2575"	"an undeniable and indefeasible right to _alter their form of"
"2576"	"government_ in such a manner as they may think expedient.”"
"2577"	"Under that gospel, the citizen who thinks he sees that the"
"2578"	"commonwealth’s political clothes are worn out, and yet holds his"
"2579"	"peace and does not agitate for a new suit, is disloyal; he is"
"2580"	"a traitor.  That he may be the only one who thinks he sees this"
"2581"	"decay, does not excuse him; it is his duty to agitate anyway, and"
"2582"	"it is the duty of the others to vote him down if they do not see"
"2583"	"the matter as he does."
"2584"	"And now here I was, in a country where a right to say how the"
"2585"	"country should be governed was restricted to six persons in each"
"2586"	"thousand of its population.  For the nine hundred and ninety-four"
"2587"	"to express dissatisfaction with the regnant system and propose"
"2588"	"to change it, would have made the whole six shudder as one man,"
"2589"	"it would have been so disloyal, so dishonorable, such putrid black"
"2590"	"treason.  So to speak, I was become a stockholder in a corporation"
"2591"	"where nine hundred and ninety-four of the members furnished all"
"2592"	"the money and did all the work, and the other six elected themselves"
"2593"	"a permanent board of direction and took all the dividends.  It seemed"
"2594"	"to me that what the nine hundred and ninety-four dupes needed was"
"2595"	"a new deal.  The thing that would have best suited the circus side"
"2596"	"of my nature would have been to resign the Boss-ship and get up"
"2597"	"an insurrection and turn it into a revolution; but I knew that the"
"2598"	"Jack Cade or the Wat Tyler who tries such a thing without first"
"2599"	"educating his materials up to revolution grade is almost absolutely"
"2600"	"certain to get left.  I had never been accustomed to getting left,"
"2601"	"even if I do say it myself.  Wherefore, the “deal” which had been"
"2602"	"for some time working into shape in my mind was of a quite different"
"2603"	"pattern from the Cade-Tyler sort."
"2604"	"So I did not talk blood and insurrection to that man there who sat"
"2605"	"munching black bread with that abused and mistaught herd of human"
"2606"	"sheep, but took him aside and talked matter of another sort to him."
"2607"	"After I had finished, I got him to lend me a little ink from his"
"2608"	"veins; and with this and a sliver I wrote on a piece of bark--"
"2609"	"   Put him in the Man-factory--"
"2610"	"and gave it to him, and said:"
"2611"	"“Take it to the palace at Camelot and give it into the hands of"
"2612"	"Amyas le Poulet, whom I call Clarence, and he will understand.”"
"2613"	"“He is a priest, then,” said the man, and some of the enthusiasm"
"2614"	"went out of his face."
"2615"	"“How--a priest?  Didn’t I tell you that no chattel of the Church,"
"2616"	"no bond-slave of pope or bishop can enter my Man-Factory?  Didn’t"
"2617"	"I tell you that _you_ couldn’t enter unless your religion, whatever"
"2618"	"it might be, was your own free property?”"
"2619"	"“Marry, it is so, and for that I was glad; wherefore it liked me not,"
"2620"	"and bred in me a cold doubt, to hear of this priest being there.”"
"2621"	"“But he isn’t a priest, I tell you.”"
"2622"	"The man looked far from satisfied.  He said:"
"2623"	"“He is not a priest, and yet can read?”"
"2624"	"“He is not a priest and yet can read--yes, and write, too, for that"
"2625"	"matter.  I taught him myself.” The man’s face cleared.  “And it is"
"2626"	"the first thing that you yourself will be taught in that Factory--”"
"2627"	"“I?  I would give blood out of my heart to know that art.  Why,"
"2628"	"I will be your slave, your--”"
"2629"	"“No you won’t, you won’t be anybody’s slave.  Take your family"
"2630"	"and go along.  Your lord the bishop will confiscate your small"
"2631"	"property, but no matter.  Clarence will fix you all right.”"
"2632"	"CHAPTER XIV"
"2633"	"“DEFEND THEE, LORD”"
"2634"	"I paid three pennies for my breakfast, and a most extravagant"
"2635"	"price it was, too, seeing that one could have breakfasted a dozen"
"2636"	"persons for that money; but I was feeling good by this time, and"
"2637"	"I had always been a kind of spendthrift anyway; and then these"
"2638"	"people had wanted to give me the food for nothing, scant as"
"2639"	"their provision was, and so it was a grateful pleasure to emphasize"
"2640"	"my appreciation and sincere thankfulness with a good big financial"
"2641"	"lift where the money would do so much more good than it would"
"2642"	"in my helmet, where, these pennies being made of iron and not"
"2643"	"stinted in weight, my half-dollar’s worth was a good deal of a"
"2644"	"burden to me.  I spent money rather too freely in those days,"
"2645"	"it is true; but one reason for it was that I hadn’t got the"
"2646"	"proportions of things entirely adjusted, even yet, after so long"
"2647"	"a sojourn in Britain--hadn’t got along to where I was able to"
"2648"	"absolutely realize that a penny in Arthur’s land and a couple of"
"2649"	"dollars in Connecticut were about one and the same thing: just"
"2650"	"twins, as you may say, in purchasing power.  If my start from"
"2651"	"Camelot could have been delayed a very few days I could have paid"
"2652"	"these people in beautiful new coins from our own mint, and that"
"2653"	"would have pleased me; and them, too, not less.  I had adopted"
"2654"	"the American values exclusively.  In a week or two now, cents,"
"2655"	"nickels, dimes, quarters, and half-dollars, and also a trifle of"
"2656"	"gold, would be trickling in thin but steady streams all through"
"2657"	"the commercial veins of the kingdom, and I looked to see this"
"2658"	"new blood freshen up its life."
"2659"	"The farmers were bound to throw in something, to sort of offset"
"2660"	"my liberality, whether I would or no; so I let them give me a flint"
"2661"	"and steel; and as soon as they had comfortably bestowed Sandy"
"2662"	"and me on our horse, I lit my pipe.  When the first blast of smoke"
"2663"	"shot out through the bars of my helmet, all those people broke"
"2664"	"for the woods, and Sandy went over backwards and struck the ground"
"2665"	"with a dull thud.  They thought I was one of those fire-belching"
"2666"	"dragons they had heard so much about from knights and other"
"2667"	"professional liars.  I had infinite trouble to persuade those people"
"2668"	"to venture back within explaining distance.  Then I told them that"
"2669"	"this was only a bit of enchantment which would work harm to none"
"2670"	"but my enemies.  And I promised, with my hand on my heart, that"
"2671"	"if all who felt no enmity toward me would come forward and pass"
"2672"	"before me they should see that only those who remained behind would"
"2673"	"be struck dead.  The procession moved with a good deal of promptness."
"2674"	"There were no casualties to report, for nobody had curiosity enough"
"2675"	"to remain behind to see what would happen."
"2676"	"I lost some time, now, for these big children, their fears gone,"
"2677"	"became so ravished with wonder over my awe-compelling fireworks"
"2678"	"that I had to stay there and smoke a couple of pipes out before"
"2679"	"they would let me go.  Still the delay was not wholly unproductive,"
"2680"	"for it took all that time to get Sandy thoroughly wonted to the new"
"2681"	"thing, she being so close to it, you know.  It plugged up her"
"2682"	"conversation mill, too, for a considerable while, and that was"
"2683"	"a gain.  But above all other benefits accruing, I had learned"
"2684"	"something.  I was ready for any giant or any ogre that might come"
"2685"	"along, now."
"2686"	"We tarried with a holy hermit, that night, and my opportunity"
"2687"	"came about the middle of the next afternoon.  We were crossing"
"2688"	"a vast meadow by way of short-cut, and I was musing absently,"
"2689"	"hearing nothing, seeing nothing, when Sandy suddenly interrupted"
"2690"	"a remark which she had begun that morning, with the cry:"
"2691"	"“Defend thee, lord!--peril of life is toward!”"
"2692"	"And she slipped down from the horse and ran a little way and stood."
"2693"	"I looked up and saw, far off in the shade of a tree, half a dozen"
"2694"	"armed knights and their squires; and straightway there was bustle"
"2695"	"among them and tightening of saddle-girths for the mount.  My pipe"
"2696"	"was ready and would have been lit, if I had not been lost in"
"2697"	"thinking about how to banish oppression from this land and restore"
"2698"	"to all its people their stolen rights and manhood without disobliging"
"2699"	"anybody.  I lit up at once, and by the time I had got a good head"
"2700"	"of reserved steam on, here they came.  All together, too; none of"
"2701"	"those chivalrous magnanimities which one reads so much about"
"2702"	"--one courtly rascal at a time, and the rest standing by to see fair"
"2703"	"play.  No, they came in a body, they came with a whirr and a rush,"
"2704"	"they came like a volley from a battery; came with heads low down,"
"2705"	"plumes streaming out behind, lances advanced at a level.  It was"
"2706"	"a handsome sight, a beautiful sight--for a man up a tree.  I laid"
"2707"	"my lance in rest and waited, with my heart beating, till the iron"
"2708"	"wave was just ready to break over me, then spouted a column of"
"2709"	"white smoke through the bars of my helmet.  You should have seen"
"2710"	"the wave go to pieces and scatter!  This was a finer sight than"
"2711"	"the other one."
"2712"	"But these people stopped, two or three hundred yards away, and"
"2713"	"this troubled me.  My satisfaction collapsed, and fear came;"
"2714"	"I judged I was a lost man.  But Sandy was radiant; and was going"
"2715"	"to be eloquent--but I stopped her, and told her my magic had"
"2716"	"miscarried, somehow or other, and she must mount, with all despatch,"
"2717"	"and we must ride for life.  No, she wouldn’t.  She said that my"
"2718"	"enchantment had disabled those knights; they were not riding on,"
"2719"	"because they couldn’t; wait, they would drop out of their saddles"
"2720"	"presently, and we would get their horses and harness.  I could not"
"2721"	"deceive such trusting simplicity, so I said it was a mistake; that"
"2722"	"when my fireworks killed at all, they killed instantly; no, the men"
"2723"	"would not die, there was something wrong about my apparatus,"
"2724"	"I couldn’t tell what; but we must hurry and get away, for those"
"2725"	"people would attack us again, in a minute.  Sandy laughed, and said:"
"2726"	"“Lack-a-day, sir, they be not of that breed!  Sir Launcelot will"
"2727"	"give battle to dragons, and will abide by them, and will assail"
"2728"	"them again, and yet again, and still again, until he do conquer"
"2729"	"and destroy them; and so likewise will Sir Pellinore and Sir Aglovale"
"2730"	"and Sir Carados, and mayhap others, but there be none else that"
"2731"	"will venture it, let the idle say what the idle will.  And, la,"
"2732"	"as to yonder base rufflers, think ye they have not their fill,"
"2733"	"but yet desire more?”"
"2734"	"“Well, then, what are they waiting for?  Why don’t they leave?"
"2735"	"Nobody’s hindering.  Good land, I’m willing to let bygones be"
"2736"	"bygones, I’m sure.”"
"2737"	"“Leave, is it?  Oh, give thyself easement as to that.  They dream"
"2738"	"not of it, no, not they.  They wait to yield them.”"
"2739"	"“Come--really, is that ‘sooth’--as you people say?  If they want to,"
"2740"	"why don’t they?”"
"2741"	"“It would like them much; but an ye wot how dragons are esteemed,"
"2742"	"ye would not hold them blamable. They fear to come.”"
"2743"	"“Well, then, suppose I go to them instead, and--”"
"2744"	"“Ah, wit ye well they would not abide your coming.  I will go.”"
"2745"	"And she did.  She was a handy person to have along on a raid."
"2746"	"I would have considered this a doubtful errand, myself.  I presently"
"2747"	"saw the knights riding away, and Sandy coming back.  That was"
"2748"	"a relief.  I judged she had somehow failed to get the first innings"
"2749"	"--I mean in the conversation; otherwise the interview wouldn’t have"
"2750"	"been so short.  But it turned out that she had managed the business"
"2751"	"well; in fact, admirably.  She said that when she told those people"
"2752"	"I was The Boss, it hit them where they lived: “smote them sore"
"2753"	"with fear and dread” was her word; and then they were ready to"
"2754"	"put up with anything she might require.  So she swore them to appear"
"2755"	"at Arthur’s court within two days and yield them, with horse and"
"2756"	"harness, and be my knights henceforth, and subject to my command."
"2757"	"How much better she managed that thing than I should have done"
"2758"	"it myself!  She was a daisy."
"2759"	"CHAPTER XV"
"2760"	"SANDY’S TALE"
"2761"	"“And so I’m proprietor of some knights,” said I, as we rode off."
"2762"	"“Who would ever have supposed that I should live to list up assets"
"2763"	"of that sort.  I shan’t know what to do with them; unless I raffle"
"2764"	"them off.  How many of them are there, Sandy?”"
"2765"	"“Seven, please you, sir, and their squires.”"
"2766"	"“It is a good haul.  Who are they?  Where do they hang out?”"
"2767"	"“Where do they hang out?”"
"2768"	"“Yes, where do they live?”"
"2769"	"“Ah, I understood thee not.  That will I tell eftsoons.”  Then she"
"2770"	"said musingly, and softly, turning the words daintily over her"
"2771"	"tongue: “Hang they out--hang they out--where hang--where do they"
"2772"	"hang out; eh, right so; where do they hang out.  Of a truth the"
"2773"	"phrase hath a fair and winsome grace, and is prettily worded"
"2774"	"withal.  I will repeat it anon and anon in mine idlesse, whereby"
"2775"	"I may peradventure learn it.  Where do they hang out.  Even so!"
"2776"	"already it falleth trippingly from my tongue, and forasmuch as--”"
"2777"	"“Don’t forget the cowboys, Sandy.”"
"2778"	"“Cowboys?”"
"2779"	"“Yes; the knights, you know: You were going to tell me about them."
"2780"	"A while back, you remember.  Figuratively speaking, game’s called.”"
"2781"	"“Game--”"
"2782"	"“Yes, yes, yes!  Go to the bat.  I mean, get to work on your"
"2783"	"statistics, and don’t burn so much kindling getting your fire"
"2784"	"started.  Tell me about the knights.”"
"2785"	"“I will well, and lightly will begin.  So they two departed and"
"2786"	"rode into a great forest.  And--”"
"2787"	"“Great Scott!”"
"2788"	"You see, I recognized my mistake at once.  I had set her works"
"2789"	"a-going; it was my own fault; she would be thirty days getting down"
"2790"	"to those facts.  And she generally began without a preface and"
"2791"	"finished without a result.  If you interrupted her she would either"
"2792"	"go right along without noticing, or answer with a couple of words,"
"2793"	"and go back and say the sentence over again.  So, interruptions"
"2794"	"only did harm; and yet I had to interrupt, and interrupt pretty"
"2795"	"frequently, too, in order to save my life; a person would die if"
"2796"	"he let her monotony drip on him right along all day."
"2797"	"“Great Scott!” I said in my distress.  She went right back and"
"2798"	"began over again:"
"2799"	"“So they two departed and rode into a great forest.  And--”"
"2800"	"“_Which_ two?”"
"2801"	"“Sir Gawaine and Sir Uwaine.  And so they came to an abbey of monks,"
"2802"	"and there were well lodged.  So on the morn they heard their masses"
"2803"	"in the abbey, and so they rode forth till they came to a great"
"2804"	"forest; then was Sir Gawaine ware in a valley by a turret, of"
"2805"	"twelve fair damsels, and two knights armed on great horses, and"
"2806"	"the damsels went to and fro by a tree.  And then was Sir Gawaine"
"2807"	"ware how there hung a white shield on that tree, and ever as the"

"2809"	"the shield--”"

"2811"	"I wouldn’t believe it.  But I’ve seen it, and I can just see those"

"2972"	"“And so they rode and came into a deep valley full of stones,"

"3000"	"Fifteen!  Break--my heart! oh, my lost darling!  Just her age"

"3008"	"She got three dollars a week, but she was worth it."
"3009"	"I could not follow Alisande’s further explanation of who our"
"3010"	"captured knights were, now--I mean in case she should ever get"

"3019"	"The sun was now setting.  It was about three in the afternoon when"
"3020"	"Alisande had begun to tell me who the cowboys were; so she had made"
"3021"	"pretty good progress with it--for her.  She would arrive some time"

"3023"	"We were approaching a castle which stood on high ground; a huge,"
"3024"	"strong, venerable structure, whose gray towers and battlements were"
"3025"	"charmingly draped with ivy, and whose whole majestic mass was"
"3026"	"drenched with splendors flung from the sinking sun.  It was the"
"3027"	"largest castle we had seen, and so I thought it might be the one"
"3028"	"we were after, but Sandy said no.  She did not know who owned it;"
"3029"	"she said she had passed it without calling, when she went down"

"3031"	"CHAPTER XVI"
"3032"	"MORGAN LE FAY"
"3033"	"If knights errant were to be believed, not all castles were desirable"
"3034"	"places to seek hospitality in.  As a matter of fact, knights errant"
"3035"	"were _not_ persons to be believed--that is, measured by modern"
"3036"	"standards of veracity; yet, measured by the standards of their own"
"3037"	"time, and scaled accordingly, you got the truth.  It was very"
"3038"	"simple: you discounted a statement ninety-seven per cent; the rest"
"3039"	"was fact.  Now after making this allowance, the truth remained"
"3040"	"that if I could find out something about a castle before ringing"
"3041"	"the door-bell--I mean hailing the warders--it was the sensible"
"3042"	"thing to do.  So I was pleased when I saw in the distance a horseman"
"3043"	"making the bottom turn of the road that wound down from this castle."
"3044"	"As we approached each other, I saw that he wore a plumed helmet,"
"3045"	"and seemed to be otherwise clothed in steel, but bore a curious"
"3046"	"addition also--a stiff square garment like a herald’s tabard."
"3047"	"However, I had to smile at my own forgetfulness when I got nearer"
"3048"	"and read this sign on his tabard:"
"3049"	"  “Persimmon’s Soap -- All the Prime-Donna Use It.”"
"3050"	"That was a little idea of my own, and had several wholesome purposes"
"3051"	"in view toward the civilizing and uplifting of this nation.  In the"
"3052"	"first place, it was a furtive, underhand blow at this nonsense"
"3053"	"of knight errantry, though nobody suspected that but me.  I had"
"3054"	"started a number of these people out--the bravest knights I could"
"3055"	"get--each sandwiched between bulletin-boards bearing one device"
"3056"	"or another, and I judged that by and by when they got to be numerous"
"3057"	"enough they would begin to look ridiculous; and then, even the"
"3058"	"steel-clad ass that _hadn’t_ any board would himself begin to look"
"3059"	"ridiculous because he was out of the fashion."
"3060"	"Secondly, these missionaries would gradually, and without creating"
"3061"	"suspicion or exciting alarm, introduce a rudimentary cleanliness"
"3062"	"among the nobility, and from them it would work down to the people,"
"3063"	"if the priests could be kept quiet.  This would undermine the Church."
"3064"	"I mean would be a step toward that.  Next, education--next, freedom"
"3065"	"--and then she would begin to crumble.  It being my conviction that"
"3066"	"any Established Church is an established crime, an established"
"3067"	"slave-pen, I had no scruples, but was willing to assail it in"
"3068"	"any way or with any weapon that promised to hurt it.  Why, in my"
"3069"	"own former day--in remote centuries not yet stirring in the womb"
"3070"	"of time--there were old Englishmen who imagined that they had been"
"3071"	"born in a free country: a “free” country with the Corporation Act"
"3072"	"and the Test still in force in it--timbers propped against men’s"
"3073"	"liberties and dishonored consciences to shore up an Established"
"3074"	"Anachronism with."
"3075"	"My missionaries were taught to spell out the gilt signs on their"
"3076"	"tabards--the showy gilding was a neat idea, I could have got the"
"3077"	"king to wear a bulletin-board for the sake of that barbaric"
"3078"	"splendor--they were to spell out these signs and then explain to"
"3079"	"the lords and ladies what soap was; and if the lords and ladies"
"3080"	"were afraid of it, get them to try it on a dog.  The missionary’s"
"3081"	"next move was to get the family together and try it on himself;"
"3082"	"he was to stop at no experiment, however desperate, that could"
"3083"	"convince the nobility that soap was harmless; if any final doubt"
"3084"	"remained, he must catch a hermit--the woods were full of them;"
"3085"	"saints they called themselves, and saints they were believed to be."
"3086"	"They were unspeakably holy, and worked miracles, and everybody"
"3087"	"stood in awe of them.  If a hermit could survive a wash, and that"
"3088"	"failed to convince a duke, give him up, let him alone."
"3089"	"Whenever my missionaries overcame a knight errant on the road"
"3090"	"they washed him, and when he got well they swore him to go and"
"3091"	"get a bulletin-board and disseminate soap and civilization the rest"
"3092"	"of his days.  As a consequence the workers in the field were"
"3093"	"increasing by degrees, and the reform was steadily spreading."
"3094"	"My soap factory felt the strain early.  At first I had only two"
"3095"	"hands; but before I had left home I was already employing fifteen,"
"3096"	"and running night and day; and the atmospheric result was getting"
"3097"	"so pronounced that the king went sort of fainting and gasping"
"3098"	"around and said he did not believe he could stand it much longer,"
"3099"	"and Sir Launcelot got so that he did hardly anything but walk up"
"3100"	"and down the roof and swear, although I told him it was worse up"
"3101"	"there than anywhere else, but he said he wanted plenty of air; and"
"3102"	"he was always complaining that a palace was no place for a soap"
"3103"	"factory anyway, and said if a man was to start one in his house"
"3104"	"he would be damned if he wouldn’t strangle him.  There were ladies"
"3105"	"present, too, but much these people ever cared for that; they would"
"3106"	"swear before children, if the wind was their way when the factory"
"3107"	"was going."
"3108"	"This missionary knight’s name was La Cote Male Taile, and he said"
"3109"	"that this castle was the abode of Morgan le Fay, sister of"
"3110"	"King Arthur, and wife of King Uriens, monarch of a realm about"
"3111"	"as big as the District of Columbia--you could stand in the middle"
"3112"	"of it and throw bricks into the next kingdom.  “Kings” and “Kingdoms”"
"3113"	" were as thick in Britain as they had been in little Palestine in"
"3114"	"Joshua’s time, when people had to sleep with their knees pulled up"
"3115"	"because they couldn’t stretch out without a passport."
"3116"	"La Cote was much depressed, for he had scored here the worst"
"3117"	"failure of his campaign.  He had not worked off a cake; yet he had"
"3118"	"tried all the tricks of the trade, even to the washing of a hermit;"
"3119"	"but the hermit died.  This was, indeed, a bad failure, for this"
"3120"	"animal would now be dubbed a martyr, and would take his place"
"3121"	"among the saints of the Roman calendar.  Thus made he his moan,"
"3122"	"this poor Sir La Cote Male Taile, and sorrowed passing sore.  And"
"3123"	"so my heart bled for him, and I was moved to comfort and stay him."
"3124"	"Wherefore I said:"
"3125"	"“Forbear to grieve, fair knight, for this is not a defeat.  We have"
"3126"	"brains, you and I; and for such as have brains there are no defeats,"
"3127"	"but only victories.  Observe how we will turn this seeming disaster"
"3128"	"into an advertisement; an advertisement for our soap; and the"
"3129"	"biggest one, to draw, that was ever thought of; an advertisement"
"3130"	"that will transform that Mount Washington defeat into a Matterhorn"
"3131"	"victory.  We will put on your bulletin-board, ‘_Patronized by the"
"3132"	"elect_.’  How does that strike you?”"
"3133"	"“Verily, it is wonderly bethought!”"
"3134"	"“Well, a body is bound to admit that for just a modest little"
"3135"	"one-line ad, it’s a corker.”"
"3136"	"So the poor colporteur’s griefs vanished away.  He was a brave"
"3137"	"fellow, and had done mighty feats of arms in his time.  His chief"
"3138"	"celebrity rested upon the events of an excursion like this one"
"3139"	"of mine, which he had once made with a damsel named Maledisant,"
"3140"	"who was as handy with her tongue as was Sandy, though in a different"
"3141"	"way, for her tongue churned forth only railings and insult, whereas"
"3142"	"Sandy’s music was of a kindlier sort.  I knew his story well, and so"
"3143"	"I knew how to interpret the compassion that was in his face when he"
"3144"	"bade me farewell.  He supposed I was having a bitter hard time of it."
"3145"	"Sandy and I discussed his story, as we rode along, and she said"
"3146"	"that La Cote’s bad luck had begun with the very beginning of that"
"3147"	"trip; for the king’s fool had overthrown him on the first day,"
"3148"	"and in such cases it was customary for the girl to desert to the"
"3149"	"conqueror, but Maledisant didn’t do it; and also persisted afterward"
"3150"	"in sticking to him, after all his defeats.  But, said I, suppose"
"3151"	"the victor should decline to accept his spoil?  She said that that"
"3152"	"wouldn’t answer--he must.  He couldn’t decline; it wouldn’t be"
"3153"	"regular.  I made a note of that.  If Sandy’s music got to be too"
"3154"	"burdensome, some time, I would let a knight defeat me, on the chance"
"3155"	"that she would desert to him."
"3156"	"In due time we were challenged by the warders, from the castle"
"3157"	"walls, and after a parley admitted.  I have nothing pleasant to"
"3158"	"tell about that visit.  But it was not a disappointment, for I knew"
"3159"	"Mrs. le Fay by reputation, and was not expecting anything pleasant."
"3160"	"She was held in awe by the whole realm, for she had made everybody"
"3161"	"believe she was a great sorceress.  All her ways were wicked, all"
"3162"	"her instincts devilish.  She was loaded to the eyelids with cold"
"3163"	"malice.  All her history was black with crime; and among her crimes"
"3164"	"murder was common.  I was most curious to see her; as curious as"
"3165"	"I could have been to see Satan.  To my surprise she was beautiful;"
"3166"	"black thoughts had failed to make her expression repulsive, age"
"3167"	"had failed to wrinkle her satin skin or mar its bloomy freshness."
"3168"	"She could have passed for old Uriens’ granddaughter, she could"
"3169"	"have been mistaken for sister to her own son."
"3170"	"As soon as we were fairly within the castle gates we were ordered"
"3171"	"into her presence.  King Uriens was there, a kind-faced old man"
"3172"	"with a subdued look; and also the son, Sir Uwaine le Blanchemains,"
"3173"	"in whom I was, of course, interested on account of the tradition"
"3174"	"that he had once done battle with thirty knights, and also on"
"3175"	"account of his trip with Sir Gawaine and Sir Marhaus, which Sandy"
"3176"	"had been aging me with.  But Morgan was the main attraction, the"
"3177"	"conspicuous personality here; she was head chief of this household,"
"3178"	"that was plain.  She caused us to be seated, and then she began,"
"3179"	"with all manner of pretty graces and graciousnesses, to ask me"
"3180"	"questions.  Dear me, it was like a bird or a flute, or something,"
"3181"	"talking.  I felt persuaded that this woman must have been"
"3182"	"misrepresented, lied about.  She trilled along, and trilled along,"
"3183"	"and presently a handsome young page, clothed like the rainbow, and"
"3184"	"as easy and undulatory of movement as a wave, came with something"
"3185"	"on a golden salver, and, kneeling to present it to her, overdid"
"3186"	"his graces and lost his balance, and so fell lightly against her"
"3187"	"knee.  She slipped a dirk into him in as matter-of-course a way as"
"3188"	"another person would have harpooned a rat!"
"3189"	"Poor child! he slumped to the floor, twisted his silken limbs in"
"3190"	"one great straining contortion of pain, and was dead.  Out of the"
"3191"	"old king was wrung an involuntary “O-h!” of compassion.  The look"
"3192"	"he got, made him cut it suddenly short and not put any more hyphens"
"3193"	"in it.  Sir Uwaine, at a sign from his mother, went to the anteroom"
"3194"	"and called some servants, and meanwhile madame went rippling sweetly"
"3195"	"along with her talk."
"3196"	"I saw that she was a good housekeeper, for while she talked she"
"3197"	"kept a corner of her eye on the servants to see that they made"
"3198"	"no balks in handling the body and getting it out; when they came"
"3199"	"with fresh clean towels, she sent back for the other kind; and"
"3200"	"when they had finished wiping the floor and were going, she indicated"
"3201"	"a crimson fleck the size of a tear which their duller eyes had"
"3202"	"overlooked.  It was plain to me that La Cote Male Taile had failed"
"3203"	"to see the mistress of the house.  Often, how louder and clearer"
"3204"	"than any tongue, does dumb circumstantial evidence speak."
"3205"	"Morgan le Fay rippled along as musically as ever.  Marvelous woman."
"3206"	"And what a glance she had: when it fell in reproof upon those"
"3207"	"servants, they shrunk and quailed as timid people do when the"
"3208"	"lightning flashes out of a cloud.  I could have got the habit"
"3209"	"myself.  It was the same with that poor old Brer Uriens; he was"
"3210"	"always on the ragged edge of apprehension; she could not even turn"
"3211"	"toward him but he winced."
"3212"	"In the midst of the talk I let drop a complimentary word about"
"3213"	"King Arthur, forgetting for the moment how this woman hated her"
"3214"	"brother.  That one little compliment was enough.  She clouded up"
"3215"	"like storm; she called for her guards, and said:"
"3216"	"“Hale me these varlets to the dungeons.”"
"3217"	"That struck cold on my ears, for her dungeons had a reputation."
"3218"	"Nothing occurred to me to say--or do.  But not so with Sandy."
"3219"	"As the guard laid a hand upon me, she piped up with the tranquilest"
"3220"	"confidence, and said:"
"3221"	"“God’s wounds, dost thou covet destruction, thou maniac?  It is"
"3222"	"The Boss!”"
"3223"	"Now what a happy idea that was!--and so simple; yet it would never"
"3224"	"have occurred to me.  I was born modest; not all over, but in spots;"
"3225"	"and this was one of the spots."
"3226"	"The effect upon madame was electrical.  It cleared her countenance"
"3227"	"and brought back her smiles and all her persuasive graces and"
"3228"	"blandishments; but nevertheless she was not able to entirely cover up"
"3229"	"with them the fact that she was in a ghastly fright. She said:"
"3230"	"“La, but do list to thine handmaid! as if one gifted with powers"
"3231"	"like to mine might say the thing which I have said unto one who"
"3232"	"has vanquished Merlin, and not be jesting.  By mine enchantments"
"3233"	"I foresaw your coming, and by them I knew you when you entered"
"3234"	"here.  I did but play this little jest with hope to surprise you"
"3235"	"into some display of your art, as not doubting you would blast"
"3236"	"the guards with occult fires, consuming them to ashes on the spot,"
"3237"	"a marvel much beyond mine own ability, yet one which I have long"
"3238"	"been childishly curious to see.”"
"3239"	"The guards were less curious, and got out as soon as they got permission."
"3240"	"CHAPTER XVII"
"3241"	"A ROYAL BANQUET"
"3242"	"Madame, seeing me pacific and unresentful, no doubt judged that"
"3243"	"I was deceived by her excuse; for her fright dissolved away, and"
"3244"	"she was soon so importunate to have me give an exhibition and kill"
"3245"	"somebody, that the thing grew to be embarrassing.  However, to my"
"3246"	"relief she was presently interrupted by the call to prayers.  I will"
"3247"	"say this much for the nobility: that, tyrannical, murderous,"
"3248"	"rapacious, and morally rotten as they were, they were deeply and"
"3249"	"enthusiastically religious.  Nothing could divert them from the"
"3250"	"regular and faithful performance of the pieties enjoined by the"
"3251"	"Church.  More than once I had seen a noble who had gotten his"
"3252"	"enemy at a disadvantage, stop to pray before cutting his throat;"
"3253"	"more than once I had seen a noble, after ambushing and despatching"
"3254"	"his enemy, retire to the nearest wayside shrine and humbly give"
"3255"	"thanks, without even waiting to rob the body.  There was to be"
"3256"	"nothing finer or sweeter in the life of even Benvenuto Cellini,"
"3257"	"that rough-hewn saint, ten centuries later.  All the nobles of"
"3258"	"Britain, with their families, attended divine service morning and"
"3259"	"night daily, in their private chapels, and even the worst of them"
"3260"	"had family worship five or six times a day besides.  The credit"
"3261"	"of this belonged entirely to the Church.  Although I was no friend"
"3262"	"to that Catholic Church, I was obliged to admit this.  And often,"
"3263"	"in spite of me, I found myself saying, “What would this country"
"3264"	"be without the Church?”"
"3265"	"After prayers we had dinner in a great banqueting hall which was"
"3266"	"lighted by hundreds of grease-jets, and everything was as fine and"
"3267"	"lavish and rudely splendid as might become the royal degree of the"
"3268"	"hosts.  At the head of the hall, on a dais, was the table of the"
"3269"	"king, queen, and their son, Prince Uwaine.  Stretching down the hall"
"3270"	"from this, was the general table, on the floor.  At this, above"
"3271"	"the salt, sat the visiting nobles and the grown members of their"
"3272"	"families, of both sexes,--the resident Court, in effect--sixty-one"
"3273"	"persons; below the salt sat minor officers of the household, with"
"3274"	"their principal subordinates: altogether a hundred and eighteen"
"3275"	"persons sitting, and about as many liveried servants standing"
"3276"	"behind their chairs, or serving in one capacity or another.  It was"
"3277"	"a very fine show.  In a gallery a band with cymbals, horns, harps,"
"3278"	"and other horrors, opened the proceedings with what seemed to be"
"3279"	"the crude first-draft or original agony of the wail known to later"
"3280"	"centuries as “In the Sweet Bye and Bye.”  It was new, and ought"
"3281"	"to have been rehearsed a little more.  For some reason or other"
"3282"	"the queen had the composer hanged, after dinner."
"3283"	"After this music, the priest who stood behind the royal table said"
"3284"	"a noble long grace in ostensible Latin.  Then the battalion of"
"3285"	"waiters broke away from their posts, and darted, rushed, flew,"
"3286"	"fetched and carried, and the mighty feeding began; no words"
"3287"	"anywhere, but absorbing attention to business.  The rows of chops"
"3288"	"opened and shut in vast unison, and the sound of it was like to"
"3289"	"the muffled burr of subterranean machinery."
"3290"	"The havoc continued an hour and a half, and unimaginable was the"
"3291"	"destruction of substantials.  Of the chief feature of the feast"
"3292"	"--the huge wild boar that lay stretched out so portly and imposing"
"3293"	"at the start--nothing was left but the semblance of a hoop-skirt;"
"3294"	"and he was but the type and symbol of what had happened to all"
"3295"	"the other dishes."
"3296"	"With the pastries and so on, the heavy drinking began--and the talk."
"3297"	"Gallon after gallon of wine and mead disappeared, and everybody"
"3298"	"got comfortable, then happy, then sparklingly joyous--both sexes,"
"3299"	"--and by and by pretty noisy.  Men told anecdotes that were terrific"
"3300"	"to hear, but nobody blushed; and when the nub was sprung, the"
"3301"	"assemblage let go with a horse-laugh that shook the fortress."
"3302"	"Ladies answered back with historiettes that would almost have made"
"3303"	"Queen Margaret of Navarre or even the great Elizabeth of England"
"3304"	"hide behind a handkerchief, but nobody hid here, but only laughed"
"3305"	"--howled, you may say.  In pretty much all of these dreadful stories,"
"3306"	"ecclesiastics were the hardy heroes, but that didn’t worry the"
"3307"	"chaplain any, he had his laugh with the rest; more than that, upon"
"3308"	"invitation he roared out a song which was of as daring a sort as"
"3309"	"any that was sung that night."
"3310"	"By midnight everybody was fagged out, and sore with laughing; and,"
"3311"	"as a rule, drunk: some weepingly, some affectionately, some"
"3312"	"hilariously, some quarrelsomely, some dead and under the table."
"3313"	"Of the ladies, the worst spectacle was a lovely young duchess, whose"
"3314"	"wedding-eve this was; and indeed she was a spectacle, sure enough."
"3315"	"Just as she was she could have sat in advance for the portrait of the"
"3316"	"young daughter of the Regent d’Orleans, at the famous dinner whence"
"3317"	"she was carried, foul-mouthed, intoxicated, and helpless, to her bed,"
"3318"	"in the lost and lamented days of the Ancient Regime."
"3319"	"Suddenly, even while the priest was lifting his hands, and all"
"3320"	"conscious heads were bowed in reverent expectation of the coming"
"3321"	"blessing, there appeared under the arch of the far-off door at"
"3322"	"the bottom of the hall an old and bent and white-haired lady,"
"3323"	"leaning upon a crutch-stick; and she lifted the stick and pointed it"
"3324"	"toward the queen and cried out:"
"3325"	"“The wrath and curse of God fall upon you, woman without pity,"
"3326"	"who have slain mine innocent grandchild and made desolate this"
"3327"	"old heart that had nor chick, nor friend nor stay nor comfort in"
"3328"	"all this world but him!”"
"3329"	"Everybody crossed himself in a grisly fright, for a curse was an"
"3330"	"awful thing to those people; but the queen rose up majestic, with"
"3331"	"the death-light in her eye, and flung back this ruthless command:"
"3332"	"“Lay hands on her!  To the stake with her!”"
"3333"	"The guards left their posts to obey.  It was a shame; it was a"
"3334"	"cruel thing to see.  What could be done?  Sandy gave me a look;"
"3335"	"I knew she had another inspiration.  I said:"
"3336"	"“Do what you choose.”"
"3337"	"She was up and facing toward the queen in a moment.  She indicated"
"3338"	"me, and said:"
"3339"	"“Madame, _he_ saith this may not be.  Recall the commandment, or he"
"3340"	"will dissolve the castle and it shall vanish away like the instable"
"3341"	"fabric of a dream!”"
"3342"	"Confound it, what a crazy contract to pledge a person to!  What if"
"3343"	"the queen--"
"3344"	"But my consternation subsided there, and my panic passed off;"
"3345"	"for the queen, all in a collapse, made no show of resistance but"
"3346"	"gave a countermanding sign and sunk into her seat.  When she reached"
"3347"	"it she was sober.  So were many of the others.  The assemblage rose,"
"3348"	"whiffed ceremony to the winds, and rushed for the door like a mob;"
"3349"	"overturning chairs, smashing crockery, tugging, struggling,"
"3350"	"shouldering, crowding--anything to get out before I should change"
"3351"	"my mind and puff the castle into the measureless dim vacancies of"
"3352"	"space.  Well, well, well, they _were_ a superstitious lot.  It is"
"3353"	"all a body can do to conceive of it."
"3354"	"The poor queen was so scared and humbled that she was even afraid"
"3355"	"to hang the composer without first consulting me.  I was very sorry"
"3356"	"for her--indeed, any one would have been, for she was really"
"3357"	"suffering; so I was willing to do anything that was reasonable, and"
"3358"	"had no desire to carry things to wanton extremities.  I therefore"
"3359"	"considered the matter thoughtfully, and ended by having the"
"3360"	"musicians ordered into our presence to play that Sweet Bye and"
"3361"	"Bye again, which they did.  Then I saw that she was right, and"
"3362"	"gave her permission to hang the whole band.  This little relaxation"
"3363"	"of sternness had a good effect upon the queen.  A statesman gains"
"3364"	"little by the arbitrary exercise of iron-clad authority upon all"
"3365"	"occasions that offer, for this wounds the just pride of his"
"3366"	"subordinates, and thus tends to undermine his strength.  A little"
"3367"	"concession, now and then, where it can do no harm, is the wiser policy."
"3368"	"Now that the queen was at ease in her mind once more, and measurably"
"3369"	"happy, her wine naturally began to assert itself again, and it got"
"3370"	"a little the start of her.  I mean it set her music going--her silver"
"3371"	"bell of a tongue.  Dear me, she was a master talker.  It would not"
"3372"	"become me to suggest that it was pretty late and that I was a tired"
"3373"	"man and very sleepy.  I wished I had gone off to bed when I had"
"3374"	"the chance.  Now I must stick it out; there was no other way.  So"
"3375"	"she tinkled along and along, in the otherwise profound and ghostly"
"3376"	"hush of the sleeping castle, until by and by there came, as if"
"3377"	"from deep down under us, a far-away sound, as of a muffled shriek"
"3378"	"--with an expression of agony about it that made my flesh crawl."
"3379"	"The queen stopped, and her eyes lighted with pleasure; she tilted"
"3380"	"her graceful head as a bird does when it listens.  The sound bored"
"3381"	"its way up through the stillness again."
"3382"	"“What is it?” I said."
"3383"	"“It is truly a stubborn soul, and endureth long.  It is many hours now.”"
"3384"	"“Endureth what?”"
"3385"	"“The rack.  Come--ye shall see a blithe sight.  An he yield not"
"3386"	"his secret now, ye shall see him torn asunder.”"
"3387"	"What a silky smooth hellion she was; and so composed and serene,"
"3388"	"when the cords all down my legs were hurting in sympathy with that"
"3389"	"man’s pain.  Conducted by mailed guards bearing flaring torches,"
"3390"	"we tramped along echoing corridors, and down stone stairways dank"
"3391"	"and dripping, and smelling of mould and ages of imprisoned night"
"3392"	"--a chill, uncanny journey and a long one, and not made the shorter"
"3393"	"or the cheerier by the sorceress’s talk, which was about this"
"3394"	"sufferer and his crime.  He had been accused by an anonymous"
"3395"	"informer, of having killed a stag in the royal preserves.  I said:"
"3396"	"“Anonymous testimony isn’t just the right thing, your Highness."
"3397"	"It were fairer to confront the accused with the accuser.”"
"3398"	"“I had not thought of that, it being but of small consequence."
"3399"	"But an I would, I could not, for that the accuser came masked by"
"3400"	"night, and told the forester, and straightway got him hence again,"
"3401"	"and so the forester knoweth him not.”"
"3402"	"“Then is this Unknown the only person who saw the stag killed?”"
"3403"	"“Marry, _no_ man _saw_ the killing, but this Unknown saw this hardy"
"3404"	"wretch near to the spot where the stag lay, and came with right"
"3405"	"loyal zeal and betrayed him to the forester.”"
"3406"	"“So the Unknown was near the dead stag, too?  Isn’t it just possible"
"3407"	"that he did the killing himself?  His loyal zeal--in a mask--looks"
"3408"	"just a shade suspicious.  But what is your highness’s idea for"
"3409"	"racking the prisoner?  Where is the profit?”"
"3410"	"“He will not confess, else; and then were his soul lost.  For his"
"3411"	"crime his life is forfeited by the law--and of a surety will I see"
"3412"	"that he payeth it!--but it were peril to my own soul to let him"
"3413"	"die unconfessed and unabsolved.  Nay, I were a fool to fling me"
"3414"	"into hell for _his_ accommodation.”"
"3415"	"“But, your Highness, suppose he has nothing to confess?”"
"3416"	"“As to that, we shall see, anon.  An I rack him to death and he"
"3417"	"confess not, it will peradventure show that he had indeed naught"
"3418"	"to confess--ye will grant that that is sooth?  Then shall I not be"
"3419"	"damned for an unconfessed man that had naught to confess"
"3420"	"--wherefore, I shall be safe.”"
"3421"	"It was the stubborn unreasoning of the time.  It was useless to"
"3422"	"argue with her.  Arguments have no chance against petrified"
"3423"	"training; they wear it as little as the waves wear a cliff.  And"
"3424"	"her training was everybody’s.  The brightest intellect in the land"
"3425"	"would not have been able to see that her position was defective."
"3426"	"As we entered the rack-cell I caught a picture that will not go"
"3427"	"from me; I wish it would.  A native young giant of thirty or"
"3428"	"thereabouts lay stretched upon the frame on his back, with his"
"3429"	"wrists and ankles tied to ropes which led over windlasses at either"
"3430"	"end.  There was no color in him; his features were contorted and"
"3431"	"set, and sweat-drops stood upon his forehead.  A priest bent over"
"3432"	"him on each side; the executioner stood by; guards were on duty;"
"3433"	"smoking torches stood in sockets along the walls; in a corner"
"3434"	"crouched a poor young creature, her face drawn with anguish,"
"3435"	"a half-wild and hunted look in her eyes, and in her lap lay a little"
"3436"	"child asleep.  Just as we stepped across the threshold the"
"3437"	"executioner gave his machine a slight turn, which wrung a cry"
"3438"	"from both the prisoner and the woman; but I shouted, and the"
"3439"	"executioner released the strain without waiting to see who spoke."
"3440"	"I could not let this horror go on; it would have killed me to"
"3441"	"see it.  I asked the queen to let me clear the place and speak"
"3442"	"to the prisoner privately; and when she was going to object I spoke"
"3443"	"in a low voice and said I did not want to make a scene before"
"3444"	"her servants, but I must have my way; for I was King Arthur’s"
"3445"	"representative, and was speaking in his name.  She saw she had"
"3446"	"to yield.  I asked her to indorse me to these people, and then"
"3447"	"leave me.  It was not pleasant for her, but she took the pill;"
"3448"	"and even went further than I was meaning to require.  I only wanted"
"3449"	"the backing of her own authority; but she said:"
"3450"	"“Ye will do in all things as this lord shall command.  It is The Boss.”"
"3451"	"It was certainly a good word to conjure with: you could see it"
"3452"	"by the squirming of these rats.  The queen’s guards fell into line,"
"3453"	"and she and they marched away, with their torch-bearers, and woke"
"3454"	"the echoes of the cavernous tunnels with the measured beat of their"
"3455"	"retreating footfalls.  I had the prisoner taken from the rack and"
"3456"	"placed upon his bed, and medicaments applied to his hurts, and"
"3457"	"wine given him to drink.  The woman crept near and looked on,"
"3458"	"eagerly, lovingly, but timorously,--like one who fears a repulse;"
"3459"	"indeed, she tried furtively to touch the man’s forehead, and jumped"
"3460"	"back, the picture of fright, when I turned unconsciously toward"
"3461"	"her.  It was pitiful to see."
"3462"	"“Lord,” I said, “stroke him, lass, if you want to.  Do anything"
"3463"	"you’re a mind to; don’t mind me.”"
"3464"	"Why, her eyes were as grateful as an animal’s, when you do it"
"3465"	"a kindness that it understands.  The baby was out of her way and"
"3466"	"she had her cheek against the man’s in a minute and her hands"
"3467"	"fondling his hair, and her happy tears running down.  The man"
"3468"	"revived and caressed his wife with his eyes, which was all he"
"3469"	"could do.  I judged I might clear the den, now, and I did; cleared"
"3470"	"it of all but the family and myself.  Then I said:"
"3471"	"“Now, my friend, tell me your side of this matter; I know"
"3472"	"the other side.”"
"3473"	"The man moved his head in sign of refusal.  But the woman looked"
"3474"	"pleased--as it seemed to me--pleased with my suggestion.  I went on--"
"3475"	"“You know of me?”"
"3476"	"“Yes.  All do, in Arthur’s realms.”"
"3477"	"“If my reputation has come to you right and straight, you should"
"3478"	"not be afraid to speak.”"
"3479"	"The woman broke in, eagerly:"
"3480"	"“Ah, fair my lord, do thou persuade him!  Thou canst an thou wilt."
"3481"	"Ah, he suffereth so; and it is for me--for _me_!  And how can I bear it?"
"3482"	"I would I might see him die--a sweet, swift death; oh, my Hugo,"
"3483"	"I cannot bear this one!”"
"3484"	"And she fell to sobbing and grovelling about my feet, and still"
"3485"	"imploring.  Imploring what?  The man’s death?  I could not quite"
"3486"	"get the bearings of the thing.  But Hugo interrupted her and said:"
"3487"	"“Peace!  Ye wit not what ye ask.  Shall I starve whom I love,"
"3488"	"to win a gentle death?  I wend thou knewest me better.”"
"3489"	"“Well,” I said, “I can’t quite make this out.  It is a puzzle.  Now--”"
"3490"	"“Ah, dear my lord, an ye will but persuade him!  Consider how"
"3491"	"these his tortures wound me!  Oh, and he will not speak!--whereas,"
"3492"	"the healing, the solace that lie in a blessed swift death--”"
"3493"	"“What _are_ you maundering about?  He’s going out from here a free"
"3494"	"man and whole--he’s not going to die.”"
"3495"	"The man’s white face lit up, and the woman flung herself at me"
"3496"	"in a most surprising explosion of joy, and cried out:"
"3497"	"“He is saved!--for it is the king’s word by the mouth of the king’s"
"3498"	"servant--Arthur, the king whose word is gold!”"
"3499"	"“Well, then you do believe I can be trusted, after all.  Why"
"3500"	"didn’t you before?”"
"3501"	"“Who doubted?  Not I, indeed; and not she.”"
"3502"	"“Well, why wouldn’t you tell me your story, then?”"
"3503"	"“Ye had made no promise; else had it been otherwise.”"
"3504"	"“I see, I see....  And yet I believe I don’t quite see, after all."
"3505"	"You stood the torture and refused to confess; which shows plain"
"3506"	"enough to even the dullest understanding that you had nothing"
"3507"	"to confess--”"
"3508"	"“I, my lord?  How so?  It was I that killed the deer!”"
"3509"	"“You _did_?  Oh, dear, this is the most mixed-up business that ever--”"
"3510"	"“Dear lord, I begged him on my knees to confess, but--”"
"3511"	"“You _did_!  It gets thicker and thicker.  What did you want him"
"3512"	"to do that for?”"
"3513"	"“Sith it would bring him a quick death and save him all this"
"3514"	"cruel pain.”"
"3515"	"“Well--yes, there is reason in that.  But _he_ didn’t want the"
"3516"	"quick death.”"
"3517"	"“He?  Why, of a surety he _did_.”"
"3518"	"“Well, then, why in the world _didn’t_ he confess?”"
"3519"	"“Ah, sweet sir, and leave my wife and chick without bread and shelter?”"
"3520"	"“Oh, heart of gold, now I see it!  The bitter law takes the convicted"
"3521"	"man’s estate and beggars his widow and his orphans.  They could"
"3522"	"torture you to death, but without conviction or confession they"
"3523"	"could not rob your wife and baby.  You stood by them like a man;"
"3524"	"and _you_--true wife and the woman that you are--you would have"
"3525"	"bought him release from torture at cost to yourself of slow"
"3526"	"starvation and death--well, it humbles a body to think what your"
"3527"	"sex can do when it comes to self-sacrifice.  I’ll book you both"
"3528"	"for my colony; you’ll like it there; it’s a Factory where I’m going"
"3529"	"to turn groping and grubbing automata into _men_.”"
"3530"	"CHAPTER XVIII"
"3531"	"IN THE QUEEN’S DUNGEONS"
"3532"	"Well, I arranged all that; and I had the man sent to his home."
"3533"	"I had a great desire to rack the executioner; not because he was"
"3534"	"a good, painstaking and paingiving official,--for surely it was"
"3535"	"not to his discredit that he performed his functions well--but to"
"3536"	"pay him back for wantonly cuffing and otherwise distressing that"
"3537"	"young woman.  The priests told me about this, and were generously"
"3538"	"hot to have him punished.  Something of this disagreeable sort"
"3539"	"was turning up every now and then.  I mean, episodes that showed"
"3540"	"that not all priests were frauds and self-seekers, but that many,"
"3541"	"even the great majority, of these that were down on the ground"
"3542"	"among the common people, were sincere and right-hearted, and"
"3543"	"devoted to the alleviation of human troubles and sufferings."
"3544"	"Well, it was a thing which could not be helped, so I seldom fretted"
"3545"	"about it, and never many minutes at a time; it has never been my"
"3546"	"way to bother much about things which you can’t cure.  But I did"
"3547"	"not like it, for it was just the sort of thing to keep people"
"3548"	"reconciled to an Established Church.  We _must_ have a religion"
"3549"	"--it goes without saying--but my idea is, to have it cut up into"
"3550"	"forty free sects, so that they will police each other, as had been"
"3551"	"the case in the United States in my time.  Concentration of power"
"3552"	"in a political machine is bad; and an Established Church is"
"3553"	"only a political machine; it was invented for that; it is nursed,"
"3554"	"cradled, preserved for that; it is an enemy to human liberty, and"
"3555"	"does no good which it could not better do in a split-up and scattered"
"3556"	"condition.  That wasn’t law; it wasn’t gospel: it was only"
"3557"	"an opinion--my opinion, and I was only a man, one man: so it wasn’t"
"3558"	"worth any more than the pope’s--or any less, for that matter."
"3559"	"Well, I couldn’t rack the executioner, neither would I overlook"
"3560"	"the just complaint of the priests.  The man must be punished"
"3561"	"somehow or other, so I degraded him from his office and made him"
"3562"	"leader of the band--the new one that was to be started.  He begged"
"3563"	"hard, and said he couldn’t play--a plausible excuse, but too thin;"
"3564"	"there wasn’t a musician in the country that could."
"3565"	"The queen was a good deal outraged, next morning when she found"
"3566"	"she was going to have neither Hugo’s life nor his property.  But"
"3567"	"I told her she must bear this cross; that while by law and custom"
"3568"	"she certainly was entitled to both the man’s life and his property,"
"3569"	"there were extenuating circumstances, and so in Arthur the king’s"
"3570"	"name I had pardoned him.  The deer was ravaging the man’s fields,"
"3571"	"and he had killed it in sudden passion, and not for gain; and he"
"3572"	"had carried it into the royal forest in the hope that that might make"
"3573"	"detection of the misdoer impossible.  Confound her, I couldn’t"
"3574"	"make her see that sudden passion is an extenuating circumstance"
"3575"	"in the killing of venison--or of a person--so I gave it up and let"
"3576"	"her sulk it out.  I _did_ think I was going to make her see it by"
"3577"	"remarking that her own sudden passion in the case of the page"
"3578"	"modified that crime."
"3579"	"“Crime!” she exclaimed.  “How thou talkest!  Crime, forsooth!"
"3580"	"Man, I am going to _pay_ for him!”"
"3581"	"Oh, it was no use to waste sense on her.  Training--training is"
"3582"	"everything; training is all there is _to_ a person.  We speak of"
"3583"	"nature; it is folly; there is no such thing as nature; what we"
"3584"	"call by that misleading name is merely heredity and training."
"3585"	"We have no thoughts of our own, no opinions of our own; they are"
"3586"	"transmitted to us, trained into us.  All that is original in us,"
"3587"	"and therefore fairly creditable or discreditable to us, can be"
"3588"	"covered up and hidden by the point of a cambric needle, all the"
"3589"	"rest being atoms contributed by, and inherited from, a procession"
"3590"	"of ancestors that stretches back a billion years to the Adam-clam"
"3591"	"or grasshopper or monkey from whom our race has been so tediously"
"3592"	"and ostentatiously and unprofitably developed.  And as for me,"
"3593"	"all that I think about in this plodding sad pilgrimage, this"
"3594"	"pathetic drift between the eternities, is to look out and humbly"
"3595"	"live a pure and high and blameless life, and save that one"
"3596"	"microscopic atom in me that is truly _me_: the rest may land in"
"3597"	"Sheol and welcome for all I care."
"3598"	"No, confound her, her intellect was good, she had brains enough,"
"3599"	"but her training made her an ass--that is, from a many-centuries-later"
"3600"	"point of view.  To kill the page was no crime--it was her right;"
"3601"	"and upon her right she stood, serenely and unconscious of offense."
"3602"	"She was a result of generations of training in the unexamined and"
"3603"	"unassailed belief that the law which permitted her to kill a subject"
"3604"	"when she chose was a perfectly right and righteous one."
"3605"	"Well, we must give even Satan his due.  She deserved a compliment"
"3606"	"for one thing; and I tried to pay it, but the words stuck in my"
"3607"	"throat.  She had a right to kill the boy, but she was in no wise"
"3608"	"obliged to pay for him.  That was law for some other people, but"
"3609"	"not for her.  She knew quite well that she was doing a large and"
"3610"	"generous thing to pay for that lad, and that I ought in common"
"3611"	"fairness to come out with something handsome about it, but I"
"3612"	"couldn’t--my mouth refused.  I couldn’t help seeing, in my fancy,"
"3613"	"that poor old grandma with the broken heart, and that fair young"
"3614"	"creature lying butchered, his little silken pomps and vanities"
"3615"	"laced with his golden blood.  How could she _pay_ for him!  _Whom_"
"3616"	"could she pay?  And so, well knowing that this woman, trained"
"3617"	"as she had been, deserved praise, even adulation, I was yet not"
"3618"	"able to utter it, trained as I had been.  The best I could do was"
"3619"	"to fish up a compliment from outside, so to speak--and the pity"
"3620"	"of it was, that it was true:"
"3621"	"“Madame, your people will adore you for this.”"
"3622"	"Quite true, but I meant to hang her for it some day if I lived."
"3623"	"Some of those laws were too bad, altogether too bad.  A master"
"3624"	"might kill his slave for nothing--for mere spite, malice, or"
"3625"	"to pass the time--just as we have seen that the crowned head could"
"3626"	"do it with _his_ slave, that is to say, anybody.  A gentleman could"
"3627"	"kill a free commoner, and pay for him--cash or garden-truck."
"3628"	"A noble could kill a noble without expense, as far as the law was"
"3629"	"concerned, but reprisals in kind were to be expected.  _Any_body"
"3630"	"could kill _some_body, except the commoner and the slave; these had"
"3631"	"no privileges.  If they killed, it was murder, and the law wouldn’t"
"3632"	"stand murder.  It made short work of the experimenter--and of"
"3633"	"his family, too, if he murdered somebody who belonged up among"
"3634"	"the ornamental ranks.  If a commoner gave a noble even so much"
"3635"	"as a Damiens-scratch which didn’t kill or even hurt, he got Damiens’"
"3636"	"dose for it just the same; they pulled him to rags and tatters"
"3637"	"with horses, and all the world came to see the show, and crack"
"3638"	"jokes, and have a good time; and some of the performances of the"
"3639"	"best people present were as tough, and as properly unprintable,"
"3640"	"as any that have been printed by the pleasant Casanova in his"
"3641"	"chapter about the dismemberment of Louis XV’s poor awkward enemy."
"3642"	"I had had enough of this grisly place by this time, and wanted"
"3643"	"to leave, but I couldn’t, because I had something on my mind that"
"3644"	"my conscience kept prodding me about, and wouldn’t let me forget."
"3645"	"If I had the remaking of man, he wouldn’t have any conscience."
"3646"	"It is one of the most disagreeable things connected with a person;"
"3647"	"and although it certainly does a great deal of good, it cannot"
"3648"	"be said to pay, in the long run; it would be much better to have"
"3649"	"less good and more comfort.  Still, this is only my opinion, and"
"3650"	"I am only one man; others, with less experience, may think"
"3651"	"differently.  They have a right to their view.  I only stand"
"3652"	"to this: I have noticed my conscience for many years, and I know"
"3653"	"it is more trouble and bother to me than anything else I started"
"3654"	"with.  I suppose that in the beginning I prized it, because we"
"3655"	"prize anything that is ours; and yet how foolish it was to think so."
"3656"	"If we look at it in another way, we see how absurd it is: if I had"
"3657"	"an anvil in me would I prize it?  Of course not.  And yet when you"
"3658"	"come to think, there is no real difference between a conscience"
"3659"	"and an anvil--I mean for comfort.  I have noticed it a thousand"
"3660"	"times.  And you could dissolve an anvil with acids, when you"
"3661"	"couldn’t stand it any longer; but there isn’t any way that you can"
"3662"	"work off a conscience--at least so it will stay worked off; not"
"3663"	"that I know of, anyway."
"3664"	"There was something I wanted to do before leaving, but it was"
"3665"	"a disagreeable matter, and I hated to go at it.  Well, it bothered"
"3666"	"me all the morning.  I could have mentioned it to the old king,"
"3667"	"but what would be the use?--he was but an extinct volcano; he had"
"3668"	"been active in his time, but his fire was out, this good while,"
"3669"	"he was only a stately ash-pile now; gentle enough, and kindly"
"3670"	"enough for my purpose, without doubt, but not usable.  He was"
"3671"	"nothing, this so-called king: the queen was the only power there."
"3672"	"And she was a Vesuvius.  As a favor, she might consent to warm"
"3673"	"a flock of sparrows for you, but then she might take that very"
"3674"	"opportunity to turn herself loose and bury a city.  However,"
"3675"	"I reflected that as often as any other way, when you are expecting"
"3676"	"the worst, you get something that is not so bad, after all."
"3677"	"So I braced up and placed my matter before her royal Highness."
"3678"	"I said I had been having a general jail-delivery at Camelot and"
"3679"	"among neighboring castles, and with her permission I would like"
"3680"	"to examine her collection, her bric-a-brac--that is to say, her"
"3681"	"prisoners.  She resisted; but I was expecting that.  But she finally"
"3682"	"consented.  I was expecting that, too, but not so soon.  That about"
"3683"	"ended my discomfort.  She called her guards and torches, and"
"3684"	"we went down into the dungeons.  These were down under the castle’s"
"3685"	"foundations, and mainly were small cells hollowed out of the living"
"3686"	"rock.  Some of these cells had no light at all.  In one of them was"
"3687"	"a woman, in foul rags, who sat on the ground, and would not answer"
"3688"	"a question or speak a word, but only looked up at us once or twice,"
