"3689"	"through a cobweb of tangled hair, as if to see what casual thing"
"3690"	"it might be that was disturbing with sound and light the meaningless"
"3691"	"dull dream that was become her life; after that, she sat bowed,"
"3692"	"with her dirt-caked fingers idly interlocked in her lap, and gave"
"3693"	"no further sign.  This poor rack of bones was a woman of middle"
"3694"	"age, apparently; but only apparently; she had been there nine"
"3695"	"years, and was eighteen when she entered.  She was a commoner,"
"3696"	"and had been sent here on her bridal night by Sir Breuse Sance Pite,"
"3697"	"a neighboring lord whose vassal her father was, and to which said"
"3698"	"lord she had refused what has since been called le droit du"
"3699"	"seigneur, and, moreover, had opposed violence to violence and spilt"
"3700"	"half a gill of his almost sacred blood.  The young husband had"
"3701"	"interfered at that point, believing the bride’s life in danger,"
"3702"	"and had flung the noble out into the midst of the humble and"
"3703"	"trembling wedding guests, in the parlor, and left him there"
"3704"	"astonished at this strange treatment, and implacably embittered"
"3705"	"against both bride and groom.  The said lord being cramped for"
"3706"	"dungeon-room had asked the queen to accommodate his two criminals,"
"3707"	"and here in her bastile they had been ever since; hither, indeed,"
"3708"	"they had come before their crime was an hour old, and had never"
"3709"	"seen each other since.  Here they were, kenneled like toads in the"
"3710"	"same rock; they had passed nine pitch dark years within fifty feet"
"3711"	"of each other, yet neither knew whether the other was alive or not."
"3712"	"All the first years, their only question had been--asked with"
"3713"	"beseechings and tears that might have moved stones, in time,"
"3714"	"perhaps, but hearts are not stones: “Is he alive?”  “Is she alive?”"
"3715"	" But they had never got an answer; and at last that question was"
"3716"	"not asked any more--or any other."
"3717"	"I wanted to see the man, after hearing all this.  He was thirty-four"
"3718"	"years old, and looked sixty.  He sat upon a squared block of"
"3719"	"stone, with his head bent down, his forearms resting on his knees,"
"3720"	"his long hair hanging like a fringe before his face, and he was"
"3721"	"muttering to himself.  He raised his chin and looked us slowly"
"3722"	"over, in a listless dull way, blinking with the distress of the"
"3723"	"torchlight, then dropped his head and fell to muttering again"
"3724"	"and took no further notice of us.  There were some pathetically"
"3725"	"suggestive dumb witnesses present.  On his wrists and ankles were"
"3726"	"cicatrices, old smooth scars, and fastened to the stone on which"
"3727"	"he sat was a chain with manacles and fetters attached; but this"
"3728"	"apparatus lay idle on the ground, and was thick with rust.  Chains"
"3729"	"cease to be needed after the spirit has gone out of a prisoner."
"3730"	"I could not rouse the man; so I said we would take him to her,"
"3731"	"and see--to the bride who was the fairest thing in the earth to him,"
"3732"	"once--roses, pearls, and dew made flesh, for him; a wonder-work,"
"3733"	"the master-work of nature: with eyes like no other eyes, and voice"
"3734"	"like no other voice, and a freshness, and lithe young grace, and"
"3735"	"beauty, that belonged properly to the creatures of dreams--as he"
"3736"	"thought--and to no other.  The sight of her would set his stagnant"
"3737"	"blood leaping; the sight of her--"
"3738"	"But it was a disappointment.  They sat together on the ground and"
"3739"	"looked dimly wondering into each other’s faces a while, with a"
"3740"	"sort of weak animal curiosity; then forgot each other’s presence,"
"3741"	"and dropped their eyes, and you saw that they were away again and"
"3742"	"wandering in some far land of dreams and shadows that we know"
"3743"	"nothing about."
"3744"	"I had them taken out and sent to their friends.  The queen did not"
"3745"	"like it much.  Not that she felt any personal interest in the matter,"
"3746"	"but she thought it disrespectful to Sir Breuse Sance Pite.  However,"
"3747"	"I assured her that if he found he couldn’t stand it I would fix him"
"3748"	"so that he could."
"3749"	"I set forty-seven prisoners loose out of those awful rat-holes,"
"3750"	"and left only one in captivity.  He was a lord, and had killed"
"3751"	"another lord, a sort of kinsman of the queen.  That other lord"
"3752"	"had ambushed him to assassinate him, but this fellow had got the"
"3753"	"best of him and cut his throat.  However, it was not for that that"
"3754"	"I left him jailed, but for maliciously destroying the only public"
"3755"	"well in one of his wretched villages.  The queen was bound to hang"
"3756"	"him for killing her kinsman, but I would not allow it: it was no"
"3757"	"crime to kill an assassin.  But I said I was willing to let her"
"3758"	"hang him for destroying the well; so she concluded to put up with"
"3759"	"that, as it was better than nothing."
"3760"	"Dear me, for what trifling offenses the most of those forty-seven"
"3761"	"men and women were shut up there!  Indeed, some were there for"
"3762"	"no distinct offense at all, but only to gratify somebody’s spite;"
"3763"	"and not always the queen’s by any means, but a friend’s.  The newest"
"3764"	"prisoner’s crime was a mere remark which he had made.  He said"
"3765"	"he believed that men were about all alike, and one man as good"
"3766"	"as another, barring clothes.  He said he believed that if you were"
"3767"	"to strip the nation naked and send a stranger through the crowd, he"
"3768"	"couldn’t tell the king from a quack doctor, nor a duke from a hotel"
"3769"	"clerk.  Apparently here was a man whose brains had not been reduced"
"3770"	"to an ineffectual mush by idiotic training.  I set him loose and"
"3771"	"sent him to the Factory."
"3772"	"Some of the cells carved in the living rock were just behind the"
"3773"	"face of the precipice, and in each of these an arrow-slit had been"
"3774"	"pierced outward to the daylight, and so the captive had a thin"
"3775"	"ray from the blessed sun for his comfort.  The case of one of"
"3776"	"these poor fellows was particularly hard.  From his dusky swallow’s"
"3777"	"hole high up in that vast wall of native rock he could peer out"
"3778"	"through the arrow-slit and see his own home off yonder in the"
"3779"	"valley; and for twenty-two years he had watched it, with heartache"
"3780"	"and longing, through that crack.  He could see the lights shine"
"3781"	"there at night, and in the daytime he could see figures go in and"
"3782"	"come out--his wife and children, some of them, no doubt, though"
"3783"	"he could not make out at that distance.  In the course of years"
"3784"	"he noted festivities there, and tried to rejoice, and wondered"
"3785"	"if they were weddings or what they might be.  And he noted funerals;"
"3786"	"and they wrung his heart.  He could make out the coffin, but he"
"3787"	"could not determine its size, and so could not tell whether it was"
"3788"	"wife or child.  He could see the procession form, with priests"
"3789"	"and mourners, and move solemnly away, bearing the secret with"
"3790"	"them.  He had left behind him five children and a wife; and in"
"3791"	"nineteen years he had seen five funerals issue, and none of them"
"3792"	"humble enough in pomp to denote a servant.  So he had lost five"
"3793"	"of his treasures; there must still be one remaining--one now"
"3794"	"infinitely, unspeakably precious,--but _which_ one? wife, or child?"
"3795"	"That was the question that tortured him, by night and by day,"
"3796"	"asleep and awake.  Well, to have an interest, of some sort, and"
"3797"	"half a ray of light, when you are in a dungeon, is a great support"
"3798"	"to the body and preserver of the intellect.  This man was in pretty"
"3799"	"good condition yet.  By the time he had finished telling me his"
"3800"	"distressful tale, I was in the same state of mind that you would"
"3801"	"have been in yourself, if you have got average human curiosity;"
"3802"	"that is to say, I was as burning up as he was to find out which"
"3803"	"member of the family it was that was left.  So I took him over"
"3804"	"home myself; and an amazing kind of a surprise party it was, too"
"3805"	"--typhoons and cyclones of frantic joy, and whole Niagaras of happy"
"3806"	"tears; and by George! we found the aforetime young matron graying"
"3807"	"toward the imminent verge of her half century, and the babies all"
"3808"	"men and women, and some of them married and experimenting familywise"
"3809"	"themselves--for not a soul of the tribe was dead!  Conceive of the"
"3810"	"ingenious devilishness of that queen: she had a special hatred for"
"3811"	"this prisoner, and she had _invented_ all those funerals herself,"
"3812"	"to scorch his heart with; and the sublimest stroke of genius of"
"3813"	"the whole thing was leaving the family-invoice a funeral _short_,"
"3814"	"so as to let him wear his poor old soul out guessing."
"3815"	"But for me, he never would have got out.  Morgan le Fay hated him"
"3816"	"with her whole heart, and she never would have softened toward him."
"3817"	"And yet his crime was committed more in thoughtlessness than"
"3818"	"deliberate depravity.  He had said she had red hair.  Well, she"
"3819"	"had; but that was no way to speak of it.  When red-headed people"
"3820"	"are above a certain social grade their hair is auburn."
"3821"	"Consider it: among these forty-seven captives there were five"
"3822"	"whose names, offenses, and dates of incarceration were no longer"
"3823"	"known!  One woman and four men--all bent, and wrinkled, and"
"3824"	"mind-extinguished patriarchs.  They themselves had long ago forgotten"
"3825"	"these details; at any rate they had mere vague theories about them,"
"3826"	"nothing definite and nothing that they repeated twice in the same"
"3827"	"way.  The succession of priests whose office it had been to pray"
"3828"	"daily with the captives and remind them that God had put them"
"3829"	"there, for some wise purpose or other, and teach them that patience,"
"3830"	"humbleness, and submission to oppression was what He loved to see"
"3831"	"in parties of a subordinate rank, had traditions about these poor"
"3832"	"old human ruins, but nothing more.  These traditions went but"
"3833"	"little way, for they concerned the length of the incarceration only,"
"3834"	"and not the names of the offenses.  And even by the help of"
"3835"	"tradition the only thing that could be proven was that none of"
"3836"	"the five had seen daylight for thirty-five years: how much longer"
"3837"	"this privation has lasted was not guessable.  The king and the queen"
"3838"	"knew nothing about these poor creatures, except that they were"
"3839"	"heirlooms, assets inherited, along with the throne, from the former"
"3840"	"firm.  Nothing of their history had been transmitted with their"
"3841"	"persons, and so the inheriting owners had considered them of no"
"3842"	"value, and had felt no interest in them.  I said to the queen:"
"3843"	"“Then why in the world didn’t you set them free?”"
"3844"	"The question was a puzzler.  She didn’t know _why_ she hadn’t, the"
"3845"	"thing had never come up in her mind.  So here she was, forecasting"
"3846"	"the veritable history of future prisoners of the Castle d’If,"
"3847"	"without knowing it.  It seemed plain to me now, that with her"
"3848"	"training, those inherited prisoners were merely property--nothing"
"3849"	"more, nothing less.  Well, when we inherit property, it does not"
"3850"	"occur to us to throw it away, even when we do not value it."
"3851"	"When I brought my procession of human bats up into the open world"
"3852"	"and the glare of the afternoon sun--previously blindfolding them,"
"3853"	"in charity for eyes so long untortured by light--they were a"
"3854"	"spectacle to look at.  Skeletons, scarecrows, goblins, pathetic"
"3855"	"frights, every one; legitimatest possible children of Monarchy"
"3856"	"by the Grace of God and the Established Church.  I muttered absently:"
"3857"	"“I _wish_ I could photograph them!”"
"3858"	"You have seen that kind of people who will never let on that they"
"3859"	"don’t know the meaning of a new big word.  The more ignorant they"
"3860"	"are, the more pitifully certain they are to pretend you haven’t"
"3861"	"shot over their heads.  The queen was just one of that sort, and"
"3862"	"was always making the stupidest blunders by reason of it.  She"
"3863"	"hesitated a moment; then her face brightened up with sudden"
"3864"	"comprehension, and she said she would do it for me."
"3865"	"I thought to myself: She? why what can she know about photography?"
"3866"	"But it was a poor time to be thinking.  When I looked around, she"
"3867"	"was moving on the procession with an axe!"
"3868"	"Well, she certainly was a curious one, was Morgan le Fay.  I have"
"3869"	"seen a good many kinds of women in my time, but she laid over them"
"3870"	"all for variety.  And how sharply characteristic of her this episode"
"3871"	"was.  She had no more idea than a horse of how to photograph"
"3872"	"a procession; but being in doubt, it was just like her to try"
"3873"	"to do it with an axe."
"3874"	"CHAPTER XIX"
"3875"	"KNIGHT-ERRANTRY AS A TRADE"
"3876"	"Sandy and I were on the road again, next morning, bright and early."
"3877"	"It was so good to open up one’s lungs and take in whole luscious"
"3878"	"barrels-ful of the blessed God’s untainted, dew-fashioned,"
"3879"	"woodland-scented air once more, after suffocating body and mind for two"
"3880"	"days and nights in the moral and physical stenches of that intolerable"
"3881"	"old buzzard-roost!  I mean, for me: of course the place was all"
"3882"	"right and agreeable enough for Sandy, for she had been used to"
"3883"	"high life all her days."
"3884"	"Poor girl, her jaws had had a wearisome rest now for a while,"
"3885"	"and I was expecting to get the consequences.  I was right; but she"
"3886"	"had stood by me most helpfully in the castle, and had mightily"
"3887"	"supported and reinforced me with gigantic foolishnesses which were"
"3888"	"worth more for the occasion than wisdoms double their size; so"
"3889"	"I thought she had earned a right to work her mill for a while,"
"3890"	"if she wanted to, and I felt not a pang when she started it up:"
"3891"	"“Now turn we unto Sir Marhaus that rode with the damsel of thirty"
"3892"	"winter of age southward--”"
"3893"	"“Are you going to see if you can work up another half-stretch on"
"3894"	"the trail of the cowboys, Sandy?”"
"3895"	"“Even so, fair my lord.”"
"3896"	"“Go ahead, then.  I won’t interrupt this time, if I can help it."
"3897"	"Begin over again; start fair, and shake out all your reefs, and"
"3898"	"I will load my pipe and give good attention.”"
"3899"	"“Now turn we unto Sir Marhaus that rode with the damsel of thirty"
"3900"	"winter of age southward.  And so they came into a deep forest,"
"3901"	"and by fortune they were nighted, and rode along in a deep way,"
"3902"	"and at the last they came into a courtelage where abode the duke"
"3903"	"of South Marches, and there they asked harbour.  And on the morn"
"3904"	"the duke sent unto Sir Marhaus, and bad him make him ready.  And"
"3905"	"so Sir Marhaus arose and armed him, and there was a mass sung"
"3906"	"afore him, and he brake his fast, and so mounted on horseback in"
"3907"	"the court of the castle, there they should do the battle.  So there"
"3908"	"was the duke already on horseback, clean armed, and his six sons"
"3909"	"by him, and every each had a spear in his hand, and so they"
"3910"	"encountered, whereas the duke and his two sons brake their spears"
"3911"	"upon him, but Sir Marhaus held up his spear and touched none of"
"3912"	"them.  Then came the four sons by couples, and two of them brake"
"3913"	"their spears, and so did the other two.  And all this while"
"3914"	"Sir Marhaus touched them not.  Then Sir Marhaus ran to the duke,"
"3915"	"and smote him with his spear that horse and man fell to the earth."
"3916"	"And so he served his sons.  And then Sir Marhaus alight down, and"
"3917"	"bad the duke yield him or else he would slay him.  And then some"
"3918"	"of his sons recovered, and would have set upon Sir Marhaus.  Then"
"3919"	"Sir Marhaus said to the duke, Cease thy sons, or else I will do"
"3920"	"the uttermost to you all.  When the duke saw he might not escape"
"3921"	"the death, he cried to his sons, and charged them to yield them"
"3922"	"to Sir Marhaus.  And they kneeled all down and put the pommels"
"3923"	"of their swords to the knight, and so he received them.  And then"
"3924"	"they holp up their father, and so by their common assent promised"
"3925"	"unto Sir Marhaus never to be foes unto King Arthur, and thereupon"
"3926"	"at Whitsuntide after, to come he and his sons, and put them in"
"3927"	"the king’s grace.*"
"3928"	"[*Footnote: The story is borrowed, language and all, from the"
"3929"	"Morte d’Arthur.--M.T.]"
"3930"	"“Even so standeth the history, fair Sir Boss.  Now ye shall wit"
"3931"	"that that very duke and his six sons are they whom but few days"
"3932"	"past you also did overcome and send to Arthur’s court!”"
"3933"	"“Why, Sandy, you can’t mean it!”"
"3934"	"“An I speak not sooth, let it be the worse for me.”"
"3935"	"“Well, well, well,--now who would ever have thought it?  One"
"3936"	"whole duke and six dukelets; why, Sandy, it was an elegant haul."
"3937"	"Knight-errantry is a most chuckle-headed trade, and it is tedious"
"3938"	"hard work, too, but I begin to see that there _is_ money in it,"
"3939"	"after all, if you have luck.  Not that I would ever engage in it"
"3940"	"as a business, for I wouldn’t.  No sound and legitimate business"
"3941"	"can be established on a basis of speculation.  A successful whirl"
"3942"	"in the knight-errantry line--now what is it when you blow away"
"3943"	"the nonsense and come down to the cold facts?  It’s just a corner"
"3944"	"in pork, that’s all, and you can’t make anything else out of it."
"3945"	"You’re rich--yes,--suddenly rich--for about a day, maybe a week;"
"3946"	"then somebody corners the market on _you_, and down goes your"
"3947"	"bucket-shop; ain’t that so, Sandy?”"
"3948"	"“Whethersoever it be that my mind miscarrieth, bewraying simple"
"3949"	"language in such sort that the words do seem to come endlong"
"3950"	"and overthwart--”"
"3951"	"“There’s no use in beating about the bush and trying to get around"
"3952"	"it that way, Sandy, it’s _so_, just as I say.  I _know_ it’s so.  And,"
"3953"	"moreover, when you come right down to the bedrock, knight-errantry"
"3954"	"is _worse_ than pork; for whatever happens, the pork’s left, and"
"3955"	"so somebody’s benefited anyway; but when the market breaks, in a"
"3956"	"knight-errantry whirl, and every knight in the pool passes in his"
"3957"	"checks, what have you got for assets?  Just a rubbish-pile of"
"3958"	"battered corpses and a barrel or two of busted hardware.  Can you"
"3959"	"call _those_ assets?  Give me pork, every time.  Am I right?”"
"3960"	"“Ah, peradventure my head being distraught by the manifold matters"
"3961"	"whereunto the confusions of these but late adventured haps and"
"3962"	"fortunings whereby not I alone nor you alone, but every each of us,"
"3963"	"meseemeth--”"
"3964"	"“No, it’s not your head, Sandy.  Your head’s all right, as far as"
"3965"	"it goes, but you don’t know business; that’s where the trouble"
"3966"	"is.  It unfits you to argue about business, and you’re wrong"
"3967"	"to be always trying.  However, that aside, it was a good haul,"
"3968"	"anyway, and will breed a handsome crop of reputation in Arthur’s"
"3969"	"court.  And speaking of the cowboys, what a curious country this"
"3970"	"is for women and men that never get old.  Now there’s Morgan le Fay,"
"3971"	"as fresh and young as a Vassar pullet, to all appearances, and"
"3972"	"here is this old duke of the South Marches still slashing away with"
"3973"	"sword and lance at his time of life, after raising such a family"
"3974"	"as he has raised.  As I understand it, Sir Gawaine killed seven"
"3975"	"of his sons, and still he had six left for Sir Marhaus and me to"
"3976"	"take into camp.  And then there was that damsel of sixty winter"
"3977"	"of age still excursioning around in her frosty bloom--How old"
"3978"	"are you, Sandy?”"
"3979"	"It was the first time I ever struck a still place in her.  The mill"
"3980"	"had shut down for repairs, or something."
"3981"	"CHAPTER XX"
"3982"	"THE OGRE’S CASTLE"
"3983"	"Between six and nine we made ten miles, which was plenty for a"
"3984"	"horse carrying triple--man, woman, and armor; then we stopped"
"3985"	"for a long nooning under some trees by a limpid brook."
"3986"	"Right so came by and by a knight riding; and as he drew near he"
"3987"	"made dolorous moan, and by the words of it I perceived that he"
"3988"	"was cursing and swearing; yet nevertheless was I glad of his"
"3989"	"coming, for that I saw he bore a bulletin-board whereon in letters"
"3990"	"all of shining gold was writ:"
"3991"	"    “USE PETERSON’S PROPHYLACTIC TOOTH-BRUSH--ALL THE GO.”"
"3992"	"I was glad of his coming, for even by this token I knew him for"
"3993"	"knight of mine.  It was Sir Madok de la Montaine, a burly great"
"3994"	"fellow whose chief distinction was that he had come within an ace"
"3995"	"of sending Sir Launcelot down over his horse-tail once.  He was"
"3996"	"never long in a stranger’s presence without finding some pretext"
"3997"	"or other to let out that great fact.  But there was another fact"
"3998"	"of nearly the same size, which he never pushed upon anybody unasked,"
"3999"	"and yet never withheld when asked: that was, that the reason he"
"4000"	"didn’t quite succeed was, that he was interrupted and sent down"
"4001"	"over horse-tail himself.  This innocent vast lubber did not see"
"4002"	"any particular difference between the two facts.  I liked him,"
"4003"	"for he was earnest in his work, and very valuable.  And he was so"
"4004"	"fine to look at, with his broad mailed shoulders, and the grand"
"4005"	"leonine set of his plumed head, and his big shield with its quaint"
"4006"	"device of a gauntleted hand clutching a prophylactic tooth-brush,"
"4007"	"with motto: “Try Noyoudont.”  This was a tooth-wash that I was"
"4008"	"introducing."
"4009"	"He was aweary, he said, and indeed he looked it; but he would not"
"4010"	"alight.  He said he was after the stove-polish man; and with this"
"4011"	"he broke out cursing and swearing anew.  The bulletin-boarder"
"4012"	"referred to was Sir Ossaise of Surluse, a brave knight, and of"
"4013"	"considerable celebrity on account of his having tried conclusions"
"4014"	"in a tournament once, with no less a Mogul than Sir Gaheris"
"4015"	"himself--although not successfully.  He was of a light and laughing"
"4016"	"disposition, and to him nothing in this world was serious.  It was"
"4017"	"for this reason that I had chosen him to work up a stove-polish"
"4018"	"sentiment.  There were no stoves yet, and so there could be nothing"
"4019"	"serious about stove-polish.  All that the agent needed to do was"
"4020"	"to deftly and by degrees prepare the public for the great change,"
"4021"	"and have them established in predilections toward neatness against"
"4022"	"the time when the stove should appear upon the stage."
"4023"	"Sir Madok was very bitter, and brake out anew with cursings.  He"
"4024"	"said he had cursed his soul to rags; and yet he would not get down"
"4025"	"from his horse, neither would he take any rest, or listen to any"
"4026"	"comfort, until he should have found Sir Ossaise and settled this"
"4027"	"account.  It appeared, by what I could piece together of the"
"4028"	"unprofane fragments of his statement, that he had chanced upon"
"4029"	"Sir Ossaise at dawn of the morning, and been told that if he would"
"4030"	"make a short cut across the fields and swamps and broken hills and"
"4031"	"glades, he could head off a company of travelers who would be rare"
"4032"	"customers for prophylactics and tooth-wash.  With characteristic"
"4033"	"zeal Sir Madok had plunged away at once upon this quest, and after"
"4034"	"three hours of awful crosslot riding had overhauled his game.  And"
"4035"	"behold, it was the five patriarchs that had been released from the"
"4036"	"dungeons the evening before!  Poor old creatures, it was all of"
"4037"	"twenty years since any one of them had known what it was to be"
"4038"	"equipped with any remaining snag or remnant of a tooth."
"4039"	"“Blank-blank-blank him,” said Sir Madok, “an I do not stove-polish"
"4040"	"him an I may find him, leave it to me; for never no knight that"
"4041"	"hight Ossaise or aught else may do me this disservice and bide"
"4042"	"on live, an I may find him, the which I have thereunto sworn a"
"4043"	"great oath this day.”"
"4044"	"And with these words and others, he lightly took his spear and"
"4045"	"gat him thence.  In the middle of the afternoon we came upon one"
"4046"	"of those very patriarchs ourselves, in the edge of a poor village."
"4047"	"He was basking in the love of relatives and friends whom he had not"
"4048"	"seen for fifty years; and about him and caressing him were also"
"4049"	"descendants of his own body whom he had never seen at all till now;"
"4050"	"but to him these were all strangers, his memory was gone, his mind"
"4051"	"was stagnant.  It seemed incredible that a man could outlast half"
"4052"	"a century shut up in a dark hole like a rat, but here were his old"
"4053"	"wife and some old comrades to testify to it.  They could remember"
"4054"	"him as he was in the freshness and strength of his young manhood,"
"4055"	"when he kissed his child and delivered it to its mother’s hands"
"4056"	"and went away into that long oblivion.  The people at the castle"
"4057"	"could not tell within half a generation the length of time the man"
"4058"	"had been shut up there for his unrecorded and forgotten offense;"
"4059"	"but this old wife knew; and so did her old child, who stood there"
"4060"	"among her married sons and daughters trying to realize a father"
"4061"	"who had been to her a name, a thought, a formless image, a tradition,"
"4062"	"all her life, and now was suddenly concreted into actual flesh"
"4063"	"and blood and set before her face."
"4064"	"It was a curious situation; yet it is not on that account that"
"4065"	"I have made room for it here, but on account of a thing which"
"4066"	"seemed to me still more curious.  To wit, that this dreadful matter"
"4067"	"brought from these downtrodden people no outburst of rage against"
"4068"	"these oppressors.  They had been heritors and subjects of cruelty"
"4069"	"and outrage so long that nothing could have startled them but"
"4070"	"a kindness.  Yes, here was a curious revelation, indeed, of the"
"4071"	"depth to which this people had been sunk in slavery.  Their entire"
"4072"	"being was reduced to a monotonous dead level of patience, resignation,"
"4073"	"dumb uncomplaining acceptance of whatever might befall them in"
"4074"	"this life.  Their very imagination was dead.  When you can say"
"4075"	"that of a man, he has struck bottom, I reckon; there is no lower"
"4076"	"deep for him."
"4077"	"I rather wished I had gone some other road.  This was not the sort"
"4078"	"of experience for a statesman to encounter who was planning out"
"4079"	"a peaceful revolution in his mind.  For it could not help bringing"
"4080"	"up the unget-aroundable fact that, all gentle cant and philosophizing"
"4081"	"to the contrary notwithstanding, no people in the world ever did"
"4082"	"achieve their freedom by goody-goody talk and moral suasion:"
"4083"	"it being immutable law that all revolutions that will succeed must"
"4084"	"_begin_ in blood, whatever may answer afterward.  If history teaches"
"4085"	"anything, it teaches that.  What this folk needed, then, was a"
"4086"	"Reign of Terror and a guillotine, and I was the wrong man for them."
"4087"	"Two days later, toward noon, Sandy began to show signs of excitement"
"4088"	"and feverish expectancy.  She said we were approaching the ogre’s"
"4089"	"castle.  I was surprised into an uncomfortable shock.  The object"
"4090"	"of our quest had gradually dropped out of my mind; this sudden"
"4091"	"resurrection of it made it seem quite a real and startling thing"
"4092"	"for a moment, and roused up in me a smart interest.  Sandy’s"
"4093"	"excitement increased every moment; and so did mine, for that sort"
"4094"	"of thing is catching.  My heart got to thumping.  You can’t reason"
"4095"	"with your heart; it has its own laws, and thumps about things which"
"4096"	"the intellect scorns.  Presently, when Sandy slid from the horse,"
"4097"	"motioned me to stop, and went creeping stealthily, with her head"
"4098"	"bent nearly to her knees, toward a row of bushes that bordered"
"4099"	"a declivity, the thumpings grew stronger and quicker.  And they"
"4100"	"kept it up while she was gaining her ambush and getting her glimpse"
"4101"	"over the declivity; and also while I was creeping to her side on"
"4102"	"my knees.  Her eyes were burning now, as she pointed with her"
"4103"	"finger, and said in a panting whisper:"
"4104"	"“The castle!  The castle!  Lo, where it looms!”"
"4105"	"What a welcome disappointment I experienced!  I said:"
"4106"	"“Castle?  It is nothing but a pigsty; a pigsty with a wattled"
"4107"	"fence around it.”"
"4108"	"She looked surprised and distressed.  The animation faded out of"
"4109"	"her face; and during many moments she was lost in thought and"
"4110"	"silent.  Then:"
"4111"	"“It was not enchanted aforetime,” she said in a musing fashion,"
"4112"	"as if to herself.  “And how strange is this marvel, and how awful"
"4113"	"--that to the one perception it is enchanted and dight in a base"
"4114"	"and shameful aspect; yet to the perception of the other it is not"
"4115"	"enchanted, hath suffered no change, but stands firm and stately"
"4116"	"still, girt with its moat and waving its banners in the blue air"
"4117"	"from its towers.  And God shield us, how it pricks the heart to"
"4118"	"see again these gracious captives, and the sorrow deepened in their"
"4119"	"sweet faces!  We have tarried along, and are to blame.”"
"4120"	"I saw my cue.  The castle was enchanted to _me_, not to her. It would"
"4121"	"be wasted time to try to argue her out of her delusion, it couldn’t"
"4122"	"be done; I must just humor it.  So I said:"
"4123"	"“This is a common case--the enchanting of a thing to one eye and"
"4124"	"leaving it in its proper form to another.  You have heard of it"
"4125"	"before, Sandy, though you haven’t happened to experience it."
"4126"	"But no harm is done.  In fact, it is lucky the way it is.  If these"
"4127"	"ladies were hogs to everybody and to themselves, it would be"
"4128"	"necessary to break the enchantment, and that might be impossible"
"4129"	"if one failed to find out the particular process of the enchantment."
"4130"	"And hazardous, too; for in attempting a disenchantment without the"
"4131"	"true key, you are liable to err, and turn your hogs into dogs,"
"4132"	"and the dogs into cats, the cats into rats, and so on, and end by"
"4133"	"reducing your materials to nothing finally, or to an odorless gas"
"4134"	"which you can’t follow--which, of course, amounts to the same"
"4135"	"thing.  But here, by good luck, no one’s eyes but mine are under"
"4136"	"the enchantment, and so it is of no consequence to dissolve it."
"4137"	"These ladies remain ladies to you, and to themselves, and to"
"4138"	"everybody else; and at the same time they will suffer in no way"
"4139"	"from my delusion, for when I know that an ostensible hog is a"
"4140"	"lady, that is enough for me, I know how to treat her.”"
"4141"	"“Thanks, oh, sweet my lord, thou talkest like an angel.  And I know"
"4142"	"that thou wilt deliver them, for that thou art minded to great"
"4143"	"deeds and art as strong a knight of your hands and as brave to will"
"4144"	"and to do, as any that is on live.”"
"4145"	"“I will not leave a princess in the sty, Sandy.  Are those three"
"4146"	"yonder that to my disordered eyes are starveling swine-herds--”"
"4147"	"“The ogres, Are _they_ changed also?  It is most wonderful.  Now"
"4148"	"am I fearful; for how canst thou strike with sure aim when five of"
"4149"	"their nine cubits of stature are to thee invisible?  Ah, go warily,"
"4150"	"fair sir; this is a mightier emprise than I wend.”"
"4151"	"“You be easy, Sandy.  All I need to know is, how _much_ of an ogre"
"4152"	"is invisible; then I know how to locate his vitals.  Don’t you be"
"4153"	"afraid, I will make short work of these bunco-steerers.  Stay"
"4154"	"where you are.”"
"4155"	"I left Sandy kneeling there, corpse-faced but plucky and hopeful,"
"4156"	"and rode down to the pigsty, and struck up a trade with the"
"4157"	"swine-herds.  I won their gratitude by buying out all the hogs"
"4158"	"at the lump sum of sixteen pennies, which was rather above latest"
"4159"	"quotations.  I was just in time; for the Church, the lord of the"
"4160"	"manor, and the rest of the tax-gatherers would have been along"
"4161"	"next day and swept off pretty much all the stock, leaving the"
"4162"	"swine-herds very short of hogs and Sandy out of princesses.  But"
"4163"	"now the tax people could be paid in cash, and there would be"
"4164"	"a stake left besides.  One of the men had ten children; and he"
"4165"	"said that last year when a priest came and of his ten pigs took"
"4166"	"the fattest one for tithes, the wife burst out upon him, and offered"
"4167"	"him a child and said:"
"4168"	"“Thou beast without bowels of mercy, why leave me my child, yet"
"4169"	"rob me of the wherewithal to feed it?”"
"4170"	"How curious.  The same thing had happened in the Wales of my day,"
"4171"	"under this same old Established Church, which was supposed by many"
"4172"	"to have changed its nature when it changed its disguise."
"4173"	"I sent the three men away, and then opened the sty gate and beckoned"
"4174"	"Sandy to come--which she did; and not leisurely, but with the rush"
"4175"	"of a prairie fire.  And when I saw her fling herself upon those"
"4176"	"hogs, with tears of joy running down her cheeks, and strain them"
"4177"	"to her heart, and kiss them, and caress them, and call them"
"4178"	"reverently by grand princely names, I was ashamed of her, ashamed"
"4179"	"of the human race."
"4180"	"We had to drive those hogs home--ten miles; and no ladies were"
"4181"	"ever more fickle-minded or contrary.  They would stay in no road,"
"4182"	"no path; they broke out through the brush on all sides, and flowed"
"4183"	"away in all directions, over rocks, and hills, and the roughest"
"4184"	"places they could find.  And they must not be struck, or roughly"
"4185"	"accosted; Sandy could not bear to see them treated in ways unbecoming"
"4186"	"their rank.  The troublesomest old sow of the lot had to be called"
"4187"	"my Lady, and your Highness, like the rest.  It is annoying and"
"4188"	"difficult to scour around after hogs, in armor.  There was one"
"4189"	"small countess, with an iron ring in her snout and hardly any hair"
"4190"	"on her back, that was the devil for perversity.  She gave me a race"
"4191"	"of an hour, over all sorts of country, and then we were right where"
"4192"	"we had started from, having made not a rod of real progress."
"4193"	"I seized her at last by the tail, and brought her along squealing."
"4194"	"When I overtook Sandy she was horrified, and said it was in the"
"4195"	"last degree indelicate to drag a countess by her train."
"4196"	"We got the hogs home just at dark--most of them.  The princess"
"4197"	"Nerovens de Morganore was missing, and two of her ladies in waiting:"
"4198"	"namely, Miss Angela Bohun, and the Demoiselle Elaine Courtemains,"
"4199"	"the former of these two being a young black sow with a white star"
"4200"	"in her forehead, and the latter a brown one with thin legs and a"
"4201"	"slight limp in the forward shank on the starboard side--a couple"
"4202"	"of the tryingest blisters to drive that I ever saw.  Also among"
"4203"	"the missing were several mere baronesses--and I wanted them to"
"4204"	"stay missing; but no, all that sausage-meat had to be found; so"
"4205"	"servants were sent out with torches to scour the woods and hills"
"4206"	"to that end."
"4207"	"Of course, the whole drove was housed in the house, and, great"
"4208"	"guns!--well, I never saw anything like it.  Nor ever heard anything"
"4209"	"like it.  And never smelt anything like it.  It was like an"
"4210"	"insurrection in a gasometer."
"4211"	"CHAPTER XXI"
"4212"	"THE PILGRIMS"
"4213"	"When I did get to bed at last I was unspeakably tired; the stretching"
"4214"	"out, and the relaxing of the long-tense muscles, how luxurious,"
"4215"	"how delicious! but that was as far as I could get--sleep was out of"
"4216"	"the question for the present.  The ripping and tearing and squealing"
"4217"	"of the nobility up and down the halls and corridors was pandemonium"
"4218"	"come again, and kept me broad awake.  Being awake, my thoughts"
"4219"	"were busy, of course; and mainly they busied themselves with Sandy’s"
"4220"	"curious delusion.  Here she was, as sane a person as the kingdom"
"4221"	"could produce; and yet, from my point of view she was acting like"
"4222"	"a crazy woman.  My land, the power of training! of influence!"
"4223"	"of education!  It can bring a body up to believe anything.  I had"
"4224"	"to put myself in Sandy’s place to realize that she was not a"
"4225"	"lunatic.  Yes, and put her in mine, to demonstrate how easy it is"
"4226"	"to seem a lunatic to a person who has not been taught as you have"
"4227"	"been taught.  If I had told Sandy I had seen a wagon, uninfluenced"
"4228"	"by enchantment, spin along fifty miles an hour; had seen a man,"
"4229"	"unequipped with magic powers, get into a basket and soar out of"
"4230"	"sight among the clouds; and had listened, without any necromancer’s"
"4231"	"help, to the conversation of a person who was several hundred miles"
"4232"	"away, Sandy would not merely have supposed me to be crazy, she"
"4233"	"would have thought she knew it.  Everybody around her believed in"
"4234"	"enchantments; nobody had any doubts; to doubt that a castle could"
"4235"	"be turned into a sty, and its occupants into hogs, would have been"
"4236"	"the same as my doubting among Connecticut people the actuality"
"4237"	"of the telephone and its wonders,--and in both cases would be"
"4238"	"absolute proof of a diseased mind, an unsettled reason.  Yes, Sandy"
"4239"	"was sane; that must be admitted.  If I also would be sane--to Sandy"
"4240"	"--I must keep my superstitions about unenchanted and unmiraculous"
"4241"	"locomotives, balloons, and telephones, to myself.  Also, I believed"
"4242"	"that the world was not flat, and hadn’t pillars under it to support"
"4243"	"it, nor a canopy over it to turn off a universe of water that"
"4244"	"occupied all space above; but as I was the only person in the kingdom"
"4245"	"afflicted with such impious and criminal opinions, I recognized"
"4246"	"that it would be good wisdom to keep quiet about this matter, too,"
"4247"	"if I did not wish to be suddenly shunned and forsaken by everybody"
"4248"	"as a madman."
"4249"	"The next morning Sandy assembled the swine in the dining-room and"
"4250"	"gave them their breakfast, waiting upon them personally and"
"4251"	"manifesting in every way the deep reverence which the natives of"
"4252"	"her island, ancient and modern, have always felt for rank, let its"
"4253"	"outward casket and the mental and moral contents be what they may."
"4254"	"I could have eaten with the hogs if I had had birth approaching my"
"4255"	"lofty official rank; but I hadn’t, and so accepted the unavoidable"
"4256"	"slight and made no complaint.  Sandy and I had our breakfast at"
"4257"	"the second table.  The family were not at home.  I said:"
"4258"	"“How many are in the family, Sandy, and where do they keep themselves?”"
"4259"	"“Family?”"
"4260"	"“Yes.”"
"4261"	"“Which family, good my lord?”"
"4262"	"“Why, this family; your own family.”"
"4263"	"“Sooth to say, I understand you not.  I have no family.”"
"4264"	"“No family?  Why, Sandy, isn’t this your home?”"
"4265"	"“Now how indeed might that be?  I have no home.”"
"4266"	"“Well, then, whose house is this?”"
"4267"	"“Ah, wit you well I would tell you an I knew myself.”"
"4268"	"“Come--you don’t even know these people?  Then who invited us here?”"
"4269"	"“None invited us.  We but came; that is all.”"
"4270"	"“Why, woman, this is a most extraordinary performance.  The"
"4271"	"effrontery of it is beyond admiration.  We blandly march into"
"4272"	"a man’s house, and cram it full of the only really valuable nobility"
"4273"	"the sun has yet discovered in the earth, and then it turns out"
"4274"	"that we don’t even know the man’s name.  How did you ever venture"
"4275"	"to take this extravagant liberty?  I supposed, of course, it was"
"4276"	"your home.  What will the man say?”"
"4277"	"“What will he say?  Forsooth what can he say but give thanks?”"
"4278"	"“Thanks for what?”"
"4279"	"Her face was filled with a puzzled surprise:"
"4280"	"“Verily, thou troublest mine understanding with strange words."
"4281"	"Do ye dream that one of his estate is like to have the honor twice"
"4282"	"in his life to entertain company such as we have brought to grace"
"4283"	"his house withal?”"
"4284"	"“Well, no--when you come to that.  No, it’s an even bet that this"
"4285"	"is the first time he has had a treat like this.”"
"4286"	"“Then let him be thankful, and manifest the same by grateful speech"
"4287"	"and due humility; he were a dog, else, and the heir and ancestor"
"4288"	"of dogs.”"
"4289"	"To my mind, the situation was uncomfortable.  It might become more so."
"4290"	"It might be a good idea to muster the hogs and move on.  So I said:"
"4291"	"“The day is wasting, Sandy.  It is time to get the nobility together"
"4292"	"and be moving.”"
"4293"	"“Wherefore, fair sir and Boss?”"
"4294"	"“We want to take them to their home, don’t we?”"
"4295"	"“La, but list to him!  They be of all the regions of the earth!"
"4296"	"Each must hie to her own home; wend you we might do all these"
"4297"	"journeys in one so brief life as He hath appointed that created"
"4298"	"life, and thereto death likewise with help of Adam, who by sin"
"4299"	"done through persuasion of his helpmeet, she being wrought upon"
"4300"	"and bewrayed by the beguilements of the great enemy of man, that"
"4301"	"serpent hight Satan, aforetime consecrated and set apart unto that"
"4302"	"evil work by overmastering spite and envy begotten in his heart"
"4303"	"through fell ambitions that did blight and mildew a nature erst"
"4304"	"so white and pure whenso it hove with the shining multitudes"
"4305"	"its brethren-born in glade and shade of that fair heaven wherein"
"4306"	"all such as native be to that rich estate and--”"
"4307"	"“Great Scott!”"
"4308"	"“My lord?”"
"4309"	"“Well, you know we haven’t got time for this sort of thing.  Don’t"
"4310"	"you see, we could distribute these people around the earth in less"
"4311"	"time than it is going to take you to explain that we can’t.  We"
"4312"	"mustn’t talk now, we must act.  You want to be careful; you mustn’t"
"4313"	"let your mill get the start of you that way, at a time like this."
"4314"	"To business now--and sharp’s the word.  Who is to take the"
"4315"	"aristocracy home?”"
"4316"	"“Even their friends.  These will come for them from the far parts"
"4317"	"of the earth.”"
"4318"	"This was lightning from a clear sky, for unexpectedness; and the"
"4319"	"relief of it was like pardon to a prisoner.  She would remain to"
"4320"	"deliver the goods, of course."
"4321"	"“Well, then, Sandy, as our enterprise is handsomely and successfully"
"4322"	"ended, I will go home and report; and if ever another one--”"
"4323"	"“I also am ready; I will go with thee.”"
"4324"	"This was recalling the pardon."
"4325"	"“How?  You will go with me?  Why should you?”"
"4326"	"“Will I be traitor to my knight, dost think?  That were dishonor."
"4327"	"I may not part from thee until in knightly encounter in the field"
"4328"	"some overmatching champion shall fairly win and fairly wear me."
"4329"	"I were to blame an I thought that that might ever hap.”"
"4330"	"“Elected for the long term,” I sighed to myself.  “I may as well"
"4331"	"make the best of it.”  So then I spoke up and said:"
"4332"	"“All right; let us make a start.”"
"4333"	"While she was gone to cry her farewells over the pork, I gave that"
"4334"	"whole peerage away to the servants.  And I asked them to take"
"4335"	"a duster and dust around a little where the nobilities had mainly"
"4336"	"lodged and promenaded; but they considered that that would be"
"4337"	"hardly worth while, and would moreover be a rather grave departure"
"4338"	"from custom, and therefore likely to make talk.  A departure from"
"4339"	"custom--that settled it; it was a nation capable of committing any"
"4340"	"crime but that.  The servants said they would follow the fashion,"
"4341"	"a fashion grown sacred through immemorial observance; they would"
"4342"	"scatter fresh rushes in all the rooms and halls, and then the"
"4343"	"evidence of the aristocratic visitation would be no longer visible."
"4344"	"It was a kind of satire on Nature: it was the scientific method,"
"4345"	"the geologic method; it deposited the history of the family in"
"4346"	"a stratified record; and the antiquary could dig through it and"
"4347"	"tell by the remains of each period what changes of diet the family"
"4348"	"had introduced successively for a hundred years."
"4349"	"The first thing we struck that day was a procession of pilgrims."
"4350"	"It was not going our way, but we joined it, nevertheless; for it"
"4351"	"was hourly being borne in upon me now, that if I would govern"
"4352"	"this country wisely, I must be posted in the details of its life,"
"4353"	"and not at second hand, but by personal observation and scrutiny."
"4354"	"This company of pilgrims resembled Chaucer’s in this: that it"
"4355"	"had in it a sample of about all the upper occupations and professions"
"4356"	"the country could show, and a corresponding variety of costume."
"4357"	"There were young men and old men, young women and old women,"
"4358"	"lively folk and grave folk.  They rode upon mules and horses, and"
"4359"	"there was not a side-saddle in the party; for this specialty was"
"4360"	"to remain unknown in England for nine hundred years yet."
"4361"	"It was a pleasant, friendly, sociable herd; pious, happy, merry and"
"4362"	"full of unconscious coarsenesses and innocent indecencies.  What"
"4363"	"they regarded as the merry tale went the continual round and caused"
"4364"	"no more embarrassment than it would have caused in the best English"
"4365"	"society twelve centuries later.  Practical jokes worthy of the"
"4366"	"English wits of the first quarter of the far-off nineteenth century"
"4367"	"were sprung here and there and yonder along the line, and compelled"
"4368"	"the delightedest applause; and sometimes when a bright remark was"
"4369"	"made at one end of the procession and started on its travels toward"
"4370"	"the other, you could note its progress all the way by the sparkling"
"4371"	"spray of laughter it threw off from its bows as it plowed along;"
"4372"	"and also by the blushes of the mules in its wake."
"4373"	"Sandy knew the goal and purpose of this pilgrimage, and she posted"
"4374"	"me.  She said:"
"4375"	"“They journey to the Valley of Holiness, for to be blessed of the"
"4376"	"godly hermits and drink of the miraculous waters and be cleansed"
"4377"	"from sin.”"
"4378"	"“Where is this watering place?”"
"4379"	"“It lieth a two-day journey hence, by the borders of the land that"
"4380"	"hight the Cuckoo Kingdom.”"
"4381"	"“Tell me about it.  Is it a celebrated place?”"
"4382"	"“Oh, of a truth, yes.  There be none more so.  Of old time there"
"4383"	"lived there an abbot and his monks.  Belike were none in the world"
"4384"	"more holy than these; for they gave themselves to study of pious"
"4385"	"books, and spoke not the one to the other, or indeed to any, and"
"4386"	"ate decayed herbs and naught thereto, and slept hard, and prayed"
"4387"	"much, and washed never; also they wore the same garment until it"
"4388"	"fell from their bodies through age and decay.  Right so came they"
"4389"	"to be known of all the world by reason of these holy austerities,"
"4390"	"and visited by rich and poor, and reverenced.”"
"4391"	"“Proceed.”"
"4392"	"“But always there was lack of water there.  Whereas, upon a time,"
"4393"	"the holy abbot prayed, and for answer a great stream of clear"
"4394"	"water burst forth by miracle in a desert place.  Now were the"
"4395"	"fickle monks tempted of the Fiend, and they wrought with their"
"4396"	"abbot unceasingly by beggings and beseechings that he would construct"
"4397"	"a bath; and when he was become aweary and might not resist more,"
"4398"	"he said have ye your will, then, and granted that they asked."
"4399"	"Now mark thou what ‘tis to forsake the ways of purity the which"
"4400"	"He loveth, and wanton with such as be worldly and an offense."
"4401"	"These monks did enter into the bath and come thence washed as"
"4402"	"white as snow; and lo, in that moment His sign appeared, in"
"4403"	"miraculous rebuke! for His insulted waters ceased to flow, and"
"4404"	"utterly vanished away.”"
"4405"	"“They fared mildly, Sandy, considering how that kind of crime"
"4406"	"is regarded in this country.”"
"4407"	"“Belike; but it was their first sin; and they had been of perfect"
"4408"	"life for long, and differing in naught from the angels.  Prayers,"
"4409"	"tears, torturings of the flesh, all was vain to beguile that water"
"4410"	"to flow again.  Even processions; even burnt-offerings; even votive"
"4411"	"candles to the Virgin, did fail every each of them; and all in"
"4412"	"the land did marvel.”"
"4413"	"“How odd to find that even this industry has its financial panics,"
"4414"	"and at times sees its assignats and greenbacks languish to zero,"
"4415"	"and everything come to a standstill.  Go on, Sandy.”"
"4416"	"“And so upon a time, after year and day, the good abbot made humble"
"4417"	"surrender and destroyed the bath.  And behold, His anger was in that"
"4418"	"moment appeased, and the waters gushed richly forth again, and even"
"4419"	"unto this day they have not ceased to flow in that generous measure.”"
"4420"	"“Then I take it nobody has washed since.”"
"4421"	"“He that would essay it could have his halter free; yes, and"
"4422"	"swiftly would he need it, too.”"
"4423"	"“The community has prospered since?”"
"4424"	"“Even from that very day.  The fame of the miracle went abroad"
"4425"	"into all lands.  From every land came monks to join; they came"
"4426"	"even as the fishes come, in shoals; and the monastery added building"
"4427"	"to building, and yet others to these, and so spread wide its arms"
"4428"	"and took them in.  And nuns came, also; and more again, and yet"
"4429"	"more; and built over against the monastery on the yon side of the"
"4430"	"vale, and added building to building, until mighty was that nunnery."
"4431"	"And these were friendly unto those, and they joined their loving"
"4432"	"labors together, and together they built a fair great foundling"
"4433"	"asylum midway of the valley between.”"
"4434"	"“You spoke of some hermits, Sandy.”"
"4435"	"“These have gathered there from the ends of the earth.  A hermit"
"4436"	"thriveth best where there be multitudes of pilgrims.  Ye shall not"
"4437"	"find no hermit of no sort wanting.  If any shall mention a hermit"
"4438"	"of a kind he thinketh new and not to be found but in some far"
"4439"	"strange land, let him but scratch among the holes and caves and"
"4440"	"swamps that line that Valley of Holiness, and whatsoever be his"
"4441"	"breed, it skills not, he shall find a sample of it there.”"
"4442"	"I closed up alongside of a burly fellow with a fat good-humored"
"4443"	"face, purposing to make myself agreeable and pick up some further"
"4444"	"crumbs of fact; but I had hardly more than scraped acquaintance"
"4445"	"with him when he began eagerly and awkwardly to lead up, in the"
"4446"	"immemorial way, to that same old anecdote--the one Sir Dinadan"
"4447"	"told me, what time I got into trouble with Sir Sagramor and was"
"4448"	"challenged of him on account of it.  I excused myself and dropped"
"4449"	"to the rear of the procession, sad at heart, willing to go hence"
"4450"	"from this troubled life, this vale of tears, this brief day of"
"4451"	"broken rest, of cloud and storm, of weary struggle and monotonous"
"4452"	"defeat; and yet shrinking from the change, as remembering how long"
"4453"	"eternity is, and how many have wended thither who know that anecdote."
"4454"	"Early in the afternoon we overtook another procession of pilgrims;"
"4455"	"but in this one was no merriment, no jokes, no laughter, no playful"
"4456"	"ways, nor any happy giddiness, whether of youth or age.  Yet both"
"4457"	"were here, both age and youth; gray old men and women, strong men"
"4458"	"and women of middle age, young husbands, young wives, little boys"
"4459"	"and girls, and three babies at the breast.  Even the children were"
"4460"	"smileless; there was not a face among all these half a hundred"
"4461"	"people but was cast down, and bore that set expression of hopelessness"
"4462"	"which is bred of long and hard trials and old acquaintance with"
"4463"	"despair.  They were slaves.  Chains led from their fettered feet"
"4464"	"and their manacled hands to a sole-leather belt about their waists;"
"4465"	"and all except the children were also linked together in a file"
"4466"	"six feet apart, by a single chain which led from collar to collar"
"4467"	"all down the line.  They were on foot, and had tramped three"
"4468"	"hundred miles in eighteen days, upon the cheapest odds and ends"
"4469"	"of food, and stingy rations of that.  They had slept in these"
"4470"	"chains every night, bundled together like swine.  They had upon"
"4471"	"their bodies some poor rags, but they could not be said to be"
"4472"	"clothed.  Their irons had chafed the skin from their ankles and"
"4473"	"made sores which were ulcerated and wormy.  Their naked feet were"
"4474"	"torn, and none walked without a limp.  Originally there had been a"
"4475"	"hundred of these unfortunates, but about half had been sold on"
"4476"	"the trip.  The trader in charge of them rode a horse and carried"
"4477"	"a whip with a short handle and a long heavy lash divided into"
"4478"	"several knotted tails at the end.  With this whip he cut the"
"4479"	"shoulders of any that tottered from weariness and pain, and"
"4480"	"straightened them up.  He did not speak; the whip conveyed his"
"4481"	"desire without that.  None of these poor creatures looked up as"
"4482"	"we rode along by; they showed no consciousness of our presence."
"4483"	"And they made no sound but one; that was the dull and awful clank"
"4484"	"of their chains from end to end of the long file, as forty-three"
"4485"	"burdened feet rose and fell in unison.  The file moved in a cloud"
"4486"	"of its own making."
"4487"	"All these faces were gray with a coating of dust.  One has seen"
"4488"	"the like of this coating upon furniture in unoccupied houses, and"
"4489"	"has written his idle thought in it with his finger.  I was reminded"
"4490"	"of this when I noticed the faces of some of those women, young"
"4491"	"mothers carrying babes that were near to death and freedom, how"
"4492"	"a something in their hearts was written in the dust upon their"
"4493"	"faces, plain to see, and lord, how plain to read! for it was the"
"4494"	"track of tears.  One of these young mothers was but a girl, and"
"4495"	"it hurt me to the heart to read that writing, and reflect that it"
"4496"	"was come up out of the breast of such a child, a breast that ought"
"4497"	"not to know trouble yet, but only the gladness of the morning of"
"4498"	"life; and no doubt--"
"4499"	"She reeled just then, giddy with fatigue, and down came the lash"
"4500"	"and flicked a flake of skin from her naked shoulder.  It stung me"
"4501"	"as if I had been hit instead.  The master halted the file and"
"4502"	"jumped from his horse.  He stormed and swore at this girl, and"
"4503"	"said she had made annoyance enough with her laziness, and as this"
"4504"	"was the last chance he should have, he would settle the account now."
"4505"	"She dropped on her knees and put up her hands and began to beg,"
"4506"	"and cry, and implore, in a passion of terror, but the master gave"
"4507"	"no attention.  He snatched the child from her, and then made the"
"4508"	"men-slaves who were chained before and behind her throw her on"
"4509"	"the ground and hold her there and expose her body; and then he"
"4510"	"laid on with his lash like a madman till her back was flayed, she"
"4511"	"shrieking and struggling the while piteously.  One of the men who"
"4512"	"was holding her turned away his face, and for this humanity he was"
"4513"	"reviled and flogged."
"4514"	"All our pilgrims looked on and commented--on the expert way in"
"4515"	"which the whip was handled.  They were too much hardened by lifelong"
"4516"	"everyday familiarity with slavery to notice that there was anything"
"4517"	"else in the exhibition that invited comment.  This was what slavery"
"4518"	"could do, in the way of ossifying what one may call the superior"
"4519"	"lobe of human feeling; for these pilgrims were kind-hearted people,"
"4520"	"and they would not have allowed that man to treat a horse like that."
"4521"	"I wanted to stop the whole thing and set the slaves free, but that"
"4522"	"would not do.  I must not interfere too much and get myself a name"
"4523"	"for riding over the country’s laws and the citizen’s rights"
"4524"	"roughshod.  If I lived and prospered I would be the death of"
"4525"	"slavery, that I was resolved upon; but I would try to fix it so"
"4526"	"that when I became its executioner it should be by command of"
"4527"	"the nation."
"4528"	"Just here was the wayside shop of a smith; and now arrived a landed"
"4529"	"proprietor who had bought this girl a few miles back, deliverable"
"4530"	"here where her irons could be taken off.  They were removed; then"
"4531"	"there was a squabble between the gentleman and the dealer as to"
"4532"	"which should pay the blacksmith.  The moment the girl was delivered"
"4533"	"from her irons, she flung herself, all tears and frantic sobbings,"
"4534"	"into the arms of the slave who had turned away his face when she"
"4535"	"was whipped.  He strained her to his breast, and smothered her"
"4536"	"face and the child’s with kisses, and washed them with the rain"
"4537"	"of his tears.  I suspected.  I inquired.  Yes, I was right; it was"
"4538"	"husband and wife.  They had to be torn apart by force; the girl"
"4539"	"had to be dragged away, and she struggled and fought and shrieked"
"4540"	"like one gone mad till a turn of the road hid her from sight; and"
"4541"	"even after that, we could still make out the fading plaint of those"
"4542"	"receding shrieks.  And the husband and father, with his wife and"
"4543"	"child gone, never to be seen by him again in life?--well, the look"
"4544"	"of him one might not bear at all, and so I turned away; but I knew"
"4545"	"I should never get his picture out of my mind again, and there"
"4546"	"it is to this day, to wring my heartstrings whenever I think of it."
"4547"	"We put up at the inn in a village just at nightfall, and when"
"4548"	"I rose next morning and looked abroad, I was ware where a knight"
"4549"	"came riding in the golden glory of the new day, and recognized him"
"4550"	"for knight of mine--Sir Ozana le Cure Hardy.  He was in the"
"4551"	"gentlemen’s furnishing line, and his missionarying specialty was"
"4552"	"plug hats.  He was clothed all in steel, in the beautifulest armor"
"4553"	"of the time--up to where his helmet ought to have been; but he"
"4554"	"hadn’t any helmet, he wore a shiny stove-pipe hat, and was ridiculous"
"4555"	"a spectacle as one might want to see.  It was another of my"
"4556"	"surreptitious schemes for extinguishing knighthood by making it"
"4557"	"grotesque and absurd.  Sir Ozana’s saddle was hung about with"
"4558"	"leather hat boxes, and every time he overcame a wandering knight"
"4559"	"he swore him into my service and fitted him with a plug and made"
"4560"	"him wear it.  I dressed and ran down to welcome Sir Ozana and"
"4561"	"get his news."
"4562"	"“How is trade?” I asked."
"4563"	"“Ye will note that I have but these four left; yet were they sixteen"
"4564"	"whenas I got me from Camelot.”"
"4565"	"“Why, you have certainly done nobly, Sir Ozana.  Where have you"
"4566"	"been foraging of late?”"
"4567"	"“I am but now come from the Valley of Holiness, please you sir.”"
"4568"	"“I am pointed for that place myself.  Is there anything stirring"
"4569"	"in the monkery, more than common?”"
"4570"	"“By the mass ye may not question it!....  Give him good feed,"
"4571"	"boy, and stint it not, an thou valuest thy crown; so get ye lightly"
"4572"	"to the stable and do even as I bid....  Sir, it is parlous news"
"4573"	"I bring, and--be these pilgrims?  Then ye may not do better, good"
"4574"	"folk, than gather and hear the tale I have to tell, sith it"
"4575"	"concerneth you, forasmuch as ye go to find that ye will not find,"
"4576"	"and seek that ye will seek in vain, my life being hostage for my"
"4577"	"word, and my word and message being these, namely: That a hap"
"4578"	"has happened whereof the like has not been seen no more but once"
"4579"	"this two hundred years, which was the first and last time that"
"4580"	"that said misfortune strake the holy valley in that form by"
"4581"	"commandment of the Most High whereto by reasons just and causes"
"4582"	"thereunto contributing, wherein the matter--”"
"4583"	"“The miraculous fount hath ceased to flow!”  This shout burst from"
"4584"	"twenty pilgrim mouths at once."
"4585"	"“Ye say well, good people.  I was verging to it, even when ye spake.”"
"4586"	"“Has somebody been washing again?”"
"4587"	"“Nay, it is suspected, but none believe it.  It is thought to be"
"4588"	"some other sin, but none wit what.”"
"4589"	"“How are they feeling about the calamity?”"
"4590"	"“None may describe it in words.  The fount is these nine days dry."
"4591"	"The prayers that did begin then, and the lamentations in sackcloth"
"4592"	"and ashes, and the holy processions, none of these have ceased"
"4593"	"nor night nor day; and so the monks and the nuns and the foundlings"
"4594"	"be all exhausted, and do hang up prayers writ upon parchment,"
"4595"	"sith that no strength is left in man to lift up voice.  And at last"
"4596"	"they sent for thee, Sir Boss, to try magic and enchantment; and"
"4597"	"if you could not come, then was the messenger to fetch Merlin,"
"4598"	"and he is there these three days now, and saith he will fetch that"
"4599"	"water though he burst the globe and wreck its kingdoms to accomplish"
"4600"	"it; and right bravely doth he work his magic and call upon his"
"4601"	"hellions to hie them hither and help, but not a whiff of moisture"
"4602"	"hath he started yet, even so much as might qualify as mist upon"
"4603"	"a copper mirror an ye count not the barrel of sweat he sweateth"
"4604"	"betwixt sun and sun over the dire labors of his task; and if ye--”"
"4605"	"Breakfast was ready.  As soon as it was over I showed to Sir Ozana"
"4606"	"these words which I had written on the inside of his hat: “Chemical"
"4607"	"Department, Laboratory extension, Section G. Pxxp.  Send two of"
"4608"	"first size, two of No. 3, and six of No. 4, together with the proper"
"4609"	"complementary details--and two of my trained assistants.”  And I said:"
"4610"	"“Now get you to Camelot as fast as you can fly, brave knight, and"
"4611"	"show the writing to Clarence, and tell him to have these required"
"4612"	"matters in the Valley of Holiness with all possible dispatch.”"
"4613"	"“I will well, Sir Boss,” and he was off."
"4614"	"CHAPTER XXII"
"4615"	"THE HOLY FOUNTAIN"
"4616"	"The pilgrims were human beings.  Otherwise they would have acted"
"4617"	"differently.  They had come a long and difficult journey, and now"
"4618"	"when the journey was nearly finished, and they learned that the main"
"4619"	"thing they had come for had ceased to exist, they didn’t do as"
"4620"	"horses or cats or angle-worms would probably have done--turn back"
"4621"	"and get at something profitable--no, anxious as they had before"
"4622"	"been to see the miraculous fountain, they were as much as forty"
"4623"	"times as anxious now to see the place where it had used to be."
"4624"	"There is no accounting for human beings."
"4625"	"We made good time; and a couple of hours before sunset we stood"
"4626"	"upon the high confines of the Valley of Holiness, and our eyes"
"4627"	"swept it from end to end and noted its features.  That is, its"
"4628"	"large features.  These were the three masses of buildings.  They"
"4629"	"were distant and isolated temporalities shrunken to toy constructions"
"4630"	"in the lonely waste of what seemed a desert--and was.  Such a scene"
"4631"	"is always mournful, it is so impressively still, and looks so"
"4632"	"steeped in death.  But there was a sound here which interrupted"
"4633"	"the stillness only to add to its mournfulness; this was the faint"
"4634"	"far sound of tolling bells which floated fitfully to us on the"
"4635"	"passing breeze, and so faintly, so softly, that we hardly knew"
"4636"	"whether we heard it with our ears or with our spirits."
"4637"	"We reached the monastery before dark, and there the males were"
"4638"	"given lodging, but the women were sent over to the nunnery.  The"
"4639"	"bells were close at hand now, and their solemn booming smote"
"4640"	"upon the ear like a message of doom.  A superstitious despair"
"4641"	"possessed the heart of every monk and published itself in his"
"4642"	"ghastly face.  Everywhere, these black-robed, soft-sandaled,"
"4643"	"tallow-visaged specters appeared, flitted about and disappeared,"
"4644"	"noiseless as the creatures of a troubled dream, and as uncanny."
"4645"	"The old abbot’s joy to see me was pathetic.  Even to tears; but"
"4646"	"he did the shedding himself.  He said:"
"4647"	"“Delay not, son, but get to thy saving work.  An we bring not"
"4648"	"the water back again, and soon, we are ruined, and the good work"
"4649"	"of two hundred years must end.  And see thou do it with enchantments"
"4650"	"that be holy, for the Church will not endure that work in her cause"
"4651"	"be done by devil’s magic.”"
"4652"	"“When I work, Father, be sure there will be no devil’s work"
"4653"	"connected with it.  I shall use no arts that come of the devil,"
"4654"	"and no elements not created by the hand of God.  But is Merlin"
"4655"	"working strictly on pious lines?”"
"4656"	"“Ah, he said he would, my son, he said he would, and took oath"
"4657"	"to make his promise good.”"
"4658"	"“Well, in that case, let him proceed.”"
"4659"	"“But surely you will not sit idle by, but help?”"
"4660"	"“It will not answer to mix methods, Father; neither would it be"
"4661"	"professional courtesy.  Two of a trade must not underbid each"
"4662"	"other.  We might as well cut rates and be done with it; it would"
"4663"	"arrive at that in the end.  Merlin has the contract; no other"
"4664"	"magician can touch it till he throws it up.”"
"4665"	"“But I will take it from him; it is a terrible emergency and the"
"4666"	"act is thereby justified.  And if it were not so, who will give"
"4667"	"law to the Church?  The Church giveth law to all; and what she"
"4668"	"wills to do, that she may do, hurt whom it may.  I will take it"
"4669"	"from him; you shall begin upon the moment.”"
"4670"	"“It may not be, Father.  No doubt, as you say, where power is"
"4671"	"supreme, one can do as one likes and suffer no injury; but we poor"
"4672"	"magicians are not so situated.  Merlin is a very good magician"
"4673"	"in a small way, and has quite a neat provincial reputation.  He"
"4674"	"is struggling along, doing the best he can, and it would not be"
"4675"	"etiquette for me to take his job until he himself abandons it.”"
"4676"	"The abbot’s face lighted."
"4677"	"“Ah, that is simple.  There are ways to persuade him to abandon it.”"
"4678"	"“No-no, Father, it skills not, as these people say.  If he were"
"4679"	"persuaded against his will, he would load that well with a malicious"
"4680"	"enchantment which would balk me until I found out its secret."
"4681"	"It might take a month.  I could set up a little enchantment of"
"4682"	"mine which I call the telephone, and he could not find out its"
"4683"	"secret in a hundred years.  Yes, you perceive, he might block me"
"4684"	"for a month.  Would you like to risk a month in a dry time like this?”"
"4685"	"“A month!  The mere thought of it maketh me to shudder.  Have it"
"4686"	"thy way, my son.  But my heart is heavy with this disappointment."
"4687"	"Leave me, and let me wear my spirit with weariness and waiting,"
"4688"	"even as I have done these ten long days, counterfeiting thus"
"4689"	"the thing that is called rest, the prone body making outward sign"
"4690"	"of repose where inwardly is none.”"
"4691"	"Of course, it would have been best, all round, for Merlin to waive"
"4692"	"etiquette and quit and call it half a day, since he would never be"
"4693"	"able to start that water, for he was a true magician of the time;"
"4694"	"which is to say, the big miracles, the ones that gave him his"
"4695"	"reputation, always had the luck to be performed when nobody but"
"4696"	"Merlin was present; he couldn’t start this well with all this crowd"
"4697"	"around to see; a crowd was as bad for a magician’s miracle in"
"4698"	"that day as it was for a spiritualist’s miracle in mine; there was"
"4699"	"sure to be some skeptic on hand to turn up the gas at the crucial"
"4700"	"moment and spoil everything.  But I did not want Merlin to retire"
"4701"	"from the job until I was ready to take hold of it effectively"
"4702"	"myself; and I could not do that until I got my things from Camelot,"
"4703"	"and that would take two or three days."
"4704"	"My presence gave the monks hope, and cheered them up a good deal;"
"4705"	"insomuch that they ate a square meal that night for the first time"
"4706"	"in ten days.  As soon as their stomachs had been properly reinforced"
"4707"	"with food, their spirits began to rise fast; when the mead began to"
"4708"	"go round they rose faster.  By the time everybody was half-seas over,"
"4709"	"the holy community was in good shape to make a night of it; so we"
"4710"	"stayed by the board and put it through on that line.  Matters got"
"4711"	"to be very jolly.  Good old questionable stories were told that made"
"4712"	"the tears run down and cavernous mouths stand wide and the round"
"4713"	"bellies shake with laughter; and questionable songs were bellowed out"
"4714"	"in a mighty chorus that drowned the boom of the tolling bells."
"4715"	"At last I ventured a story myself; and vast was the success of it."
"4716"	"Not right off, of course, for the native of those islands does"
"4717"	"not, as a rule, dissolve upon the early applications of a humorous"
"4718"	"thing; but the fifth time I told it, they began to crack in places;"
"4719"	"the eight time I told it, they began to crumble; at the twelfth"
"4720"	"repetition they fell apart in chunks; and at the fifteenth they"
"4721"	"disintegrated, and I got a broom and swept them up.  This language"
"4722"	"is figurative.  Those islanders--well, they are slow pay at first,"
"4723"	"in the matter of return for your investment of effort, but in the end"
"4724"	"they make the pay of all other nations poor and small by contrast."
"4725"	"I was at the well next day betimes.  Merlin was there, enchanting"
"4726"	"away like a beaver, but not raising the moisture.  He was not in"
"4727"	"a pleasant humor; and every time I hinted that perhaps this contract"
"4728"	"was a shade too hefty for a novice he unlimbered his tongue and"
"4729"	"cursed like a bishop--French bishop of the Regency days, I mean."
"4730"	"Matters were about as I expected to find them.  The “fountain” was"
"4731"	"an ordinary well, it had been dug in the ordinary way, and stoned up"
"4732"	"in the ordinary way.  There was no miracle about it.  Even the lie"
"4733"	"that had created its reputation was not miraculous; I could have"
"4734"	"told it myself, with one hand tied behind me.  The well was in a"
"4735"	"dark chamber which stood in the center of a cut-stone chapel, whose"
"4736"	"walls were hung with pious pictures of a workmanship that would"
"4737"	"have made a chromo feel good; pictures historically commemorative"
"4738"	"of curative miracles which had been achieved by the waters when"
"4739"	"nobody was looking.  That is, nobody but angels; they are always"
"4740"	"on deck when there is a miracle to the fore--so as to get put in"
"4741"	"the picture, perhaps.  Angels are as fond of that as a fire company;"
"4742"	"look at the old masters."
"4743"	"The well-chamber was dimly lighted by lamps; the water was drawn"
"4744"	"with a windlass and chain by monks, and poured into troughs which"
"4745"	"delivered it into stone reservoirs outside in the chapel--when"
"4746"	"there was water to draw, I mean--and none but monks could enter"
"4747"	"the well-chamber.  I entered it, for I had temporary authority"
"4748"	"to do so, by courtesy of my professional brother and subordinate."
"4749"	"But he hadn’t entered it himself.  He did everything by incantations;"
"4750"	"he never worked his intellect.  If he had stepped in there and used"
"4751"	"his eyes, instead of his disordered mind, he could have cured"
"4752"	"the well by natural means, and then turned it into a miracle in"
"4753"	"the customary way; but no, he was an old numskull, a magician who"
"4754"	"believed in his own magic; and no magician can thrive who is"
"4755"	"handicapped with a superstition like that."
"4756"	"I had an idea that the well had sprung a leak; that some of the"
"4757"	"wall stones near the bottom had fallen and exposed fissures that"
"4758"	"allowed the water to escape.  I measured the chain--98 feet.  Then"
"4759"	"I called in a couple of monks, locked the door, took a candle, and"
"4760"	"made them lower me in the bucket.  When the chain was all paid out,"
"4761"	"the candle confirmed my suspicion; a considerable section of the"
"4762"	"wall was gone, exposing a good big fissure."
"4763"	"I almost regretted that my theory about the well’s trouble was"
"4764"	"correct, because I had another one that had a showy point or two"
"4765"	"about it for a miracle.  I remembered that in America, many"
"4766"	"centuries later, when an oil well ceased to flow, they used to"
"4767"	"blast it out with a dynamite torpedo.  If I should find this well"
"4768"	"dry and no explanation of it, I could astonish these people most"
"4769"	"nobly by having a person of no especial value drop a dynamite"
"4770"	"bomb into it.  It was my idea to appoint Merlin.  However, it was"
"4771"	"plain that there was no occasion for the bomb.  One cannot have"
"4772"	"everything the way he would like it.  A man has no business to"
"4773"	"be depressed by a disappointment, anyway; he ought to make up his"
"4774"	"mind to get even.  That is what I did.  I said to myself, I am in no"
"4775"	"hurry, I can wait; that bomb will come good yet.  And it did, too."
"4776"	"When I was above ground again, I turned out the monks, and let down"
"4777"	"a fish-line; the well was a hundred and fifty feet deep, and there"
"4778"	"was forty-one feet of water in it.  I called in a monk and asked:"
"4779"	"“How deep is the well?”"
"4780"	"“That, sir, I wit not, having never been told.”"
"4781"	"“How does the water usually stand in it?”"
"4782"	"“Near to the top, these two centuries, as the testimony goeth,"
"4783"	"brought down to us through our predecessors.”"
"4784"	"It was true--as to recent times at least--for there was witness"
"4785"	"to it, and better witness than a monk; only about twenty or thirty"
"4786"	"feet of the chain showed wear and use, the rest of it was unworn"
"4787"	"and rusty.  What had happened when the well gave out that other"
"4788"	"time?  Without doubt some practical person had come along and"
"4789"	"mended the leak, and then had come up and told the abbot he had"
"4790"	"discovered by divination that if the sinful bath were destroyed"
"4791"	"the well would flow again.  The leak had befallen again now, and"
"4792"	"these children would have prayed, and processioned, and tolled"
"4793"	"their bells for heavenly succor till they all dried up and blew"
"4794"	"away, and no innocent of them all would ever have thought to drop"
"4795"	"a fish-line into the well or go down in it and find out what was"
"4796"	"really the matter.  Old habit of mind is one of the toughest things"
"4797"	"to get away from in the world.  It transmits itself like physical"
"4798"	"form and feature; and for a man, in those days, to have had an idea"
"4799"	"that his ancestors hadn’t had, would have brought him under suspicion"
"4800"	"of being illegitimate.  I said to the monk:"
"4801"	"“It is a difficult miracle to restore water in a dry well, but we"
"4802"	"will try, if my brother Merlin fails.  Brother Merlin is a very"
"4803"	"passable artist, but only in the parlor-magic line, and he may"
"4804"	"not succeed; in fact, is not likely to succeed.  But that should"
"4805"	"be nothing to his discredit; the man that can do _this_ kind of"
"4806"	"miracle knows enough to keep hotel.”"
"4807"	"“Hotel?  I mind not to have heard--”"
"4808"	"“Of hotel?  It’s what you call hostel.  The man that can do this"
"4809"	"miracle can keep hostel.  I can do this miracle; I shall do this"
"4810"	"miracle; yet I do not try to conceal from you that it is a miracle"
"4811"	"to tax the occult powers to the last strain.”"
"4812"	"“None knoweth that truth better than the brotherhood, indeed; for"
"4813"	"it is of record that aforetime it was parlous difficult and took"
"4814"	"a year.  Natheless, God send you good success, and to that end"
"4815"	"will we pray.”"
"4816"	"As a matter of business it was a good idea to get the notion around"
"4817"	"that the thing was difficult.  Many a small thing has been made"
"4818"	"large by the right kind of advertising.  That monk was filled up"
"4819"	"with the difficulty of this enterprise; he would fill up the others."
"4820"	"In two days the solicitude would be booming."
"4821"	"On my way home at noon, I met Sandy.  She had been sampling the"
"4822"	"hermits.  I said:"
"4823"	"“I would like to do that myself.  This is Wednesday.  Is there"
"4824"	"a matinee?”"
"4825"	"“A which, please you, sir?”"
"4826"	"“Matinee.  Do they keep open afternoons?”"
"4827"	"“Who?”"
"4828"	"“The hermits, of course.”"
"4829"	"“Keep open?”"
"4830"	"“Yes, keep open.  Isn’t that plain enough?  Do they knock off at noon?”"
"4831"	"“Knock off?”"
"4832"	"“Knock off?--yes, knock off.  What is the matter with knock off?"
"4833"	"I never saw such a dunderhead; can’t you understand anything at all?"
"4834"	"In plain terms, do they shut up shop, draw the game, bank the fires--”"
"4835"	"“Shut up shop, draw--”"
"4836"	"“There, never mind, let it go; you make me tired.  You can’t seem"
"4837"	"to understand the simplest thing.”"
"4838"	"“I would I might please thee, sir, and it is to me dole and sorrow"
