"4839"	"that I fail, albeit sith I am but a simple damsel and taught of"
"4840"	"none, being from the cradle unbaptized in those deep waters of"
"4841"	"learning that do anoint with a sovereignty him that partaketh of"
"4842"	"that most noble sacrament, investing him with reverend state to"
"4843"	"the mental eye of the humble mortal who, by bar and lack of that"
"4844"	"great consecration seeth in his own unlearned estate but a symbol"
"4845"	"of that other sort of lack and loss which men do publish to the"
"4846"	"pitying eye with sackcloth trappings whereon the ashes of grief"
"4847"	"do lie bepowdered and bestrewn, and so, when such shall in the"
"4848"	"darkness of his mind encounter these golden phrases of high mystery,"
"4849"	"these shut-up-shops, and draw-the-game, and bank-the-fires, it is"
"4850"	"but by the grace of God that he burst not for envy of the mind that"
"4851"	"can beget, and tongue that can deliver so great and mellow-sounding"
"4852"	"miracles of speech, and if there do ensue confusion in that humbler"
"4853"	"mind, and failure to divine the meanings of these wonders, then"
"4854"	"if so be this miscomprehension is not vain but sooth and true,"
"4855"	"wit ye well it is the very substance of worshipful dear homage and"
"4856"	"may not lightly be misprized, nor had been, an ye had noted this"
"4857"	"complexion of mood and mind and understood that that I would"
"4858"	"I could not, and that I could not I might not, nor yet nor might"
"4859"	"_nor_ could, nor might-not nor could-not, might be by advantage"
"4860"	"turned to the desired _would_, and so I pray you mercy of my fault,"
"4861"	"and that ye will of your kindness and your charity forgive it, good"
"4862"	"my master and most dear lord.”"
"4863"	"I couldn’t make it all out--that is, the details--but I got the"
"4864"	"general idea; and enough of it, too, to be ashamed.  It was not"
"4865"	"fair to spring those nineteenth century technicalities upon the"
"4866"	"untutored infant of the sixth and then rail at her because she"
"4867"	"couldn’t get their drift; and when she was making the honest best"
"4868"	"drive at it she could, too, and no fault of hers that she couldn’t"
"4869"	"fetch the home plate; and so I apologized.  Then we meandered"
"4870"	"pleasantly away toward the hermit holes in sociable converse"
"4871"	"together, and better friends than ever."
"4872"	"I was gradually coming to have a mysterious and shuddery reverence"
"4873"	"for this girl; nowadays whenever she pulled out from the station"
"4874"	"and got her train fairly started on one of those horizonless"
"4875"	"transcontinental sentences of hers, it was borne in upon me that"
"4876"	"I was standing in the awful presence of the Mother of the German"
"4877"	"Language.  I was so impressed with this, that sometimes when she"
"4878"	"began to empty one of these sentences on me I unconsciously took"
"4879"	"the very attitude of reverence, and stood uncovered; and if words"
"4880"	"had been water, I had been drowned, sure.  She had exactly the"
"4881"	"German way; whatever was in her mind to be delivered, whether a"
"4882"	"mere remark, or a sermon, or a cyclopedia, or the history of a war,"
"4883"	"she would get it into a single sentence or die.  Whenever the literary"
"4884"	"German dives into a sentence, that is the last you are going to see"
"4885"	"of him till he emerges on the other side of his Atlantic with his"
"4886"	"verb in his mouth."
"4887"	"We drifted from hermit to hermit all the afternoon.  It was a most"
"4888"	"strange menagerie.  The chief emulation among them seemed to be,"
"4889"	"to see which could manage to be the uncleanest and most prosperous"
"4890"	"with vermin.  Their manner and attitudes were the last expression"
"4891"	"of complacent self-righteousness.  It was one anchorite’s pride"
"4892"	"to lie naked in the mud and let the insects bite him and blister"
"4893"	"him unmolested; it was another’s to lean against a rock, all day"
"4894"	"long, conspicuous to the admiration of the throng of pilgrims"
"4895"	"and pray; it was another’s to go naked and crawl around on all fours;"
"4896"	"it was another’s to drag about with him, year in and year out,"
"4897"	"eighty pounds of iron; it was another’s to never lie down when"
"4898"	"he slept, but to stand among the thorn-bushes and snore when there"
"4899"	"were pilgrims around to look; a woman, who had the white hair of"
"4900"	"age, and no other apparel, was black from crown to heel with"
"4901"	"forty-seven years of holy abstinence from water.  Groups of gazing"
"4902"	"pilgrims stood around all and every of these strange objects, lost"
"4903"	"in reverent wonder, and envious of the fleckless sanctity which"
"4904"	"these pious austerities had won for them from an exacting heaven."
"4905"	"By and by we went to see one of the supremely great ones.  He was"
"4906"	"a mighty celebrity; his fame had penetrated all Christendom; the"
"4907"	"noble and the renowned journeyed from the remotest lands on the globe"
"4908"	"to pay him reverence.  His stand was in the center of the widest part"
"4909"	"of the valley; and it took all that space to hold his crowds."
"4910"	"His stand was a pillar sixty feet high, with a broad platform on"
"4911"	"the top of it.  He was now doing what he had been doing every day"
"4912"	"for twenty years up there--bowing his body ceaselessly and rapidly"
"4913"	"almost to his feet.  It was his way of praying.  I timed him with a"
"4914"	"stop watch, and he made 1,244 revolutions in 24 minutes and"
"4915"	"46 seconds.  It seemed a pity to have all this power going to waste."
"4916"	"It was one of the most useful motions in mechanics, the pedal"
"4917"	"movement; so I made a note in my memorandum book, purposing some"
"4918"	"day to apply a system of elastic cords to him and run a sewing"
"4919"	"machine with it.  I afterward carried out that scheme, and got"
"4920"	"five years’ good service out of him; in which time he turned out"
"4921"	"upward of eighteen thousand first-rate tow-linen shirts, which"
"4922"	"was ten a day.  I worked him Sundays and all; he was going, Sundays,"
"4923"	"the same as week days, and it was no use to waste the power."
"4924"	"These shirts cost me nothing but just the mere trifle for the"
"4925"	"materials--I furnished those myself, it would not have been right"
"4926"	"to make him do that--and they sold like smoke to pilgrims at a"
"4927"	"dollar and a half apiece, which was the price of fifty cows or"
"4928"	"a blooded race horse in Arthurdom.  They were regarded as a perfect"
"4929"	"protection against sin, and advertised as such by my knights"
"4930"	"everywhere, with the paint-pot and stencil-plate; insomuch that"
"4931"	"there was not a cliff or a bowlder or a dead wall in England but"
"4932"	"you could read on it at a mile distance:"
"4933"	"“Buy the only genuine St. Stylite; patronized by the Nobility."
"4934"	"Patent applied for.”"
"4935"	"There was more money in the business than one knew what to do with."
"4936"	"As it extended, I brought out a line of goods suitable for kings,"
"4937"	"and a nobby thing for duchesses and that sort, with ruffles down"
"4938"	"the forehatch and the running-gear clewed up with a featherstitch"
"4939"	"to leeward and then hauled aft with a back-stay and triced up with"
"4940"	"a half-turn in the standing rigging forward of the weather-gaskets."
"4941"	"Yes, it was a daisy."
"4942"	"But about that time I noticed that the motive power had taken to"
"4943"	"standing on one leg, and I found that there was something the matter"
"4944"	"with the other one; so I stocked the business and unloaded, taking"
"4945"	"Sir Bors de Ganis into camp financially along with certain of his"
"4946"	"friends; for the works stopped within a year, and the good saint"
"4947"	"got him to his rest.  But he had earned it.  I can say that for him."
"4948"	"When I saw him that first time--however, his personal condition"
"4949"	"will not quite bear description here.  You can read it in the"
"4950"	"Lives of the Saints.*"
"4951"	"[*All the details concerning the hermits, in this chapter, are from"
"4952"	"Lecky--but greatly modified.  This book not being a history but"
"4953"	"only a tale, the majority of the historian’s frank details were too"
"4954"	"strong for reproduction in it.--_Editor_]"
"4955"	"CHAPTER XXIII"
"4956"	"RESTORATION OF THE FOUNTAIN"
"4957"	"Saturday noon I went to the well and looked on a while.  Merlin"
"4958"	"was still burning smoke-powders, and pawing the air, and muttering"
"4959"	"gibberish as hard as ever, but looking pretty down-hearted, for"
"4960"	"of course he had not started even a perspiration in that well yet."
"4961"	"Finally I said:"
"4962"	"“How does the thing promise by this time, partner?”"
"4963"	"“Behold, I am even now busied with trial of the powerfulest"
"4964"	"enchantment known to the princes of the occult arts in the lands"
"4965"	"of the East; an it fail me, naught can avail.  Peace, until I finish.”"
"4966"	"He raised a smoke this time that darkened all the region, and must"
"4967"	"have made matters uncomfortable for the hermits, for the wind"
"4968"	"was their way, and it rolled down over their dens in a dense and"
"4969"	"billowy fog.  He poured out volumes of speech to match, and contorted"
"4970"	"his body and sawed the air with his hands in a most extraordinary"
"4971"	"way.  At the end of twenty minutes he dropped down panting, and"
"4972"	"about exhausted.  Now arrived the abbot and several hundred monks"
"4973"	"and nuns, and behind them a multitude of pilgrims and a couple of"
"4974"	"acres of foundlings, all drawn by the prodigious smoke, and all"
"4975"	"in a grand state of excitement.  The abbot inquired anxiously for"
"4976"	"results.  Merlin said:"
"4977"	"“If any labor of mortal might break the spell that binds these"
"4978"	"waters, this which I have but just essayed had done it.  It has"
"4979"	"failed; whereby I do now know that that which I had feared is"
"4980"	"a truth established; the sign of this failure is, that the most"
"4981"	"potent spirit known to the magicians of the East, and whose name"
"4982"	"none may utter and live, has laid his spell upon this well.  The"
"4983"	"mortal does not breathe, nor ever will, who can penetrate the secret"
"4984"	"of that spell, and without that secret none can break it.  The"
"4985"	"water will flow no more forever, good Father.  I have done what"
"4986"	"man could.  Suffer me to go.”"
"4987"	"Of course this threw the abbot into a good deal of a consternation."
"4988"	"He turned to me with the signs of it in his face, and said:"
"4989"	"“Ye have heard him. Is it true?”"
"4990"	"“Part of it is.”"
"4991"	"“Not all, then, not all!  What part is true?”"
"4992"	"“That that spirit with the Russian name has put his spell"
"4993"	"upon the well.”"
"4994"	"“God’s wounds, then are we ruined!”"
"4995"	"“Possibly.”"
"4996"	"“But not certainly?  Ye mean, not certainly?”"
"4997"	"“That is it.”"
"4998"	"“Wherefore, ye also mean that when he saith none can break the spell--”"
"4999"	"“Yes, when he says that, he says what isn’t necessarily true."
"5000"	"There are conditions under which an effort to break it may have"
"5001"	"some chance--that is, some small, some trifling chance--of success.”"
"5002"	"“The conditions--”"
"5003"	"“Oh, they are nothing difficult.  Only these: I want the well"
"5004"	"and the surroundings for the space of half a mile, entirely to"
"5005"	"myself from sunset to-day until I remove the ban--and nobody"
"5006"	"allowed to cross the ground but by my authority.”"
"5007"	"“Are these all?”"
"5008"	"“Yes.”"
"5009"	"“And you have no fear to try?”"
"5010"	"“Oh, none.  One may fail, of course; and one may also succeed."
"5011"	"One can try, and I am ready to chance it.  I have my conditions?”"
"5012"	"“These and all others ye may name.  I will issue commandment"
"5013"	"to that effect.”"
"5014"	"“Wait,” said Merlin, with an evil smile.  “Ye wit that he that"
"5015"	"would break this spell must know that spirit’s name?”"
"5016"	"“Yes, I know his name.”"
"5017"	"“And wit you also that to know it skills not of itself, but ye"
"5018"	"must likewise pronounce it?  Ha-ha!  Knew ye that?”"
"5019"	"“Yes, I knew that, too.”"
"5020"	"“You had that knowledge!  Art a fool?  Are ye minded to utter"
"5021"	"that name and die?”"
"5022"	"“Utter it?  Why certainly.  I would utter it if it was Welsh.”"
"5023"	"“Ye are even a dead man, then; and I go to tell Arthur.”"
"5024"	"“That’s all right.  Take your gripsack and get along.  The thing"
"5025"	"for _you_ to do is to go home and work the weather, John W. Merlin.”"
"5026"	"It was a home shot, and it made him wince; for he was the worst"
"5027"	"weather-failure in the kingdom.  Whenever he ordered up the"
"5028"	"danger-signals along the coast there was a week’s dead calm, sure,"
"5029"	"and every time he prophesied fair weather it rained brickbats."
"5030"	"But I kept him in the weather bureau right along, to undermine"
"5031"	"his reputation.  However, that shot raised his bile, and instead"
"5032"	"of starting home to report my death, he said he would remain"
"5033"	"and enjoy it."
"5034"	"My two experts arrived in the evening, and pretty well fagged,"
"5035"	"for they had traveled double tides.  They had pack-mules along,"
"5036"	"and had brought everything I needed--tools, pump, lead pipe,"
"5037"	"Greek fire, sheaves of big rockets, roman candles, colored fire"
"5038"	"sprays, electric apparatus, and a lot of sundries--everything"
"5039"	"necessary for the stateliest kind of a miracle.  They got their"
"5040"	"supper and a nap, and about midnight we sallied out through a"
"5041"	"solitude so wholly vacant and complete that it quite overpassed"
"5042"	"the required conditions.  We took possession of the well and its"
"5043"	"surroundings.  My boys were experts in all sorts of things, from"
"5044"	"the stoning up of a well to the constructing of a mathematical"
"5045"	"instrument.  An hour before sunrise we had that leak mended in"
"5046"	"ship-shape fashion, and the water began to rise.  Then we stowed our"
"5047"	"fireworks in the chapel, locked up the place, and went home to bed."
"5048"	"Before the noon mass was over, we were at the well again; for there"
"5049"	"was a deal to do yet, and I was determined to spring the miracle"
"5050"	"before midnight, for business reasons: for whereas a miracle"
"5051"	"worked for the Church on a week-day is worth a good deal, it is"
"5052"	"worth six times as much if you get it in on a Sunday.  In nine hours"
"5053"	"the water had risen to its customary level--that is to say, it was"
"5054"	"within twenty-three feet of the top.  We put in a little iron pump,"
"5055"	"one of the first turned out by my works near the capital; we bored"
"5056"	"into a stone reservoir which stood against the outer wall of the"
"5057"	"well-chamber and inserted a section of lead pipe that was long"
"5058"	"enough to reach to the door of the chapel and project beyond"
"5059"	"the threshold, where the gushing water would be visible to the"
"5060"	"two hundred and fifty acres of people I was intending should be"
"5061"	"present on the flat plain in front of this little holy hillock at"
"5062"	"the proper time."
"5063"	"We knocked the head out of an empty hogshead and hoisted this"
"5064"	"hogshead to the flat roof of the chapel, where we clamped it down"
"5065"	"fast, poured in gunpowder till it lay loosely an inch deep on the"
"5066"	"bottom, then we stood up rockets in the hogshead as thick as they"
"5067"	"could loosely stand, all the different breeds of rockets there are;"
"5068"	"and they made a portly and imposing sheaf, I can tell you.  We"
"5069"	"grounded the wire of a pocket electrical battery in that powder,"
"5070"	"we placed a whole magazine of Greek fire on each corner of the"
"5071"	"roof--blue on one corner, green on another, red on another, and"
"5072"	"purple on the last--and grounded a wire in each."
"5073"	"About two hundred yards off, in the flat, we built a pen of"
"5074"	"scantlings, about four feet high, and laid planks on it, and so"
"5075"	"made a platform.  We covered it with swell tapestries borrowed"
"5076"	"for the occasion, and topped it off with the abbot’s own throne."
"5077"	"When you are going to do a miracle for an ignorant race, you want"
"5078"	"to get in every detail that will count; you want to make all the"
"5079"	"properties impressive to the public eye; you want to make matters"
"5080"	"comfortable for your head guest; then you can turn yourself loose"
"5081"	"and play your effects for all they are worth.  I know the value of"
"5082"	"these things, for I know human nature.  You can’t throw too much"
"5083"	"style into a miracle.  It costs trouble, and work, and sometimes"
"5084"	"money; but it pays in the end.  Well, we brought the wires to"
"5085"	"the ground at the chapel, and then brought them under the ground"
"5086"	"to the platform, and hid the batteries there.  We put a rope fence"
"5087"	"a hundred feet square around the platform to keep off the common"
"5088"	"multitude, and that finished the work.  My idea was, doors open"
"5089"	"at 10:30, performance to begin at 11:25 sharp.  I wished I could"
"5090"	"charge admission, but of course that wouldn’t answer.  I instructed"
"5091"	"my boys to be in the chapel as early as 10, before anybody was"
"5092"	"around, and be ready to man the pumps at the proper time, and"
"5093"	"make the fur fly.  Then we went home to supper."
"5094"	"The news of the disaster to the well had traveled far by this time;"
"5095"	"and now for two or three days a steady avalanche of people had"
"5096"	"been pouring into the valley.  The lower end of the valley was"
"5097"	"become one huge camp; we should have a good house, no question"
"5098"	"about that.  Criers went the rounds early in the evening and"
"5099"	"announced the coming attempt, which put every pulse up to fever"
"5100"	"heat.  They gave notice that the abbot and his official suite would"
"5101"	"move in state and occupy the platform at 10:30, up to which time"
"5102"	"all the region which was under my ban must be clear; the bells"
"5103"	"would then cease from tolling, and this sign should be permission"
"5104"	"to the multitudes to close in and take their places."
"5105"	"I was at the platform and all ready to do the honors when the"
"5106"	"abbot’s solemn procession hove in sight--which it did not do till"
"5107"	"it was nearly to the rope fence, because it was a starless black"
"5108"	"night and no torches permitted.  With it came Merlin, and took"
"5109"	"a front seat on the platform; he was as good as his word for once."
"5110"	"One could not see the multitudes banked together beyond the ban,"
"5111"	"but they were there, just the same.  The moment the bells stopped,"
"5112"	"those banked masses broke and poured over the line like a vast"
"5113"	"black wave, and for as much as a half hour it continued to flow,"
"5114"	"and then it solidified itself, and you could have walked upon"
"5115"	"a pavement of human heads to--well, miles."
"5116"	"We had a solemn stage-wait, now, for about twenty minutes--a thing"
"5117"	"I had counted on for effect; it is always good to let your audience"
"5118"	"have a chance to work up its expectancy.  At length, out of the"
"5119"	"silence a noble Latin chant--men’s voices--broke and swelled up"
"5120"	"and rolled away into the night, a majestic tide of melody.  I had"
"5121"	"put that up, too, and it was one of the best effects I ever invented."
"5122"	"When it was finished I stood up on the platform and extended my"
"5123"	"hands abroad, for two minutes, with my face uplifted--that always"
"5124"	"produces a dead hush--and then slowly pronounced this ghastly word"
"5125"	"with a kind of awfulness which caused hundreds to tremble, and"
"5126"	"many women to faint:"
"5127"	"“Constantinopolitanischerdudelsackspfeifenmachersgesellschafft!”"
"5128"	"Just as I was moaning out the closing hunks of that word, I touched"
"5129"	"off one of my electric connections and all that murky world of"
"5130"	"people stood revealed in a hideous blue glare!  It was immense"
"5131"	"--that effect!  Lots of people shrieked, women curled up and quit"
"5132"	"in every direction, foundlings collapsed by platoons.  The abbot"
"5133"	"and the monks crossed themselves nimbly and their lips fluttered"
"5134"	"with agitated prayers.  Merlin held his grip, but he was astonished"
"5135"	"clear down to his corns; he had never seen anything to begin"
"5136"	"with that, before.  Now was the time to pile in the effects.  I lifted"
"5137"	"my hands and groaned out this word--as it were in agony:"
"5138"	"“Nihilistendynamittheaterkaestchenssprengungsattentaetsversuchungen!”"
"5139"	"--and turned on the red fire!  You should have heard that Atlantic"
"5140"	"of people moan and howl when that crimson hell joined the blue!"
"5141"	"After sixty seconds I shouted:"
"5142"	"“Transvaaltruppentropentransporttrampelthiertreibertrauungsthraenen-"
"5143"	"tragoedie!”"
"5144"	"--and lit up the green fire!  After waiting only forty seconds this"
"5145"	"time, I spread my arms abroad and thundered out the devastating"
"5146"	"syllables of this word of words:"
"5147"	"“Mekkamuselmannenmassenmenchenmoerdermohrenmuttermarmormonumentenmacher!”"
"5148"	"--and whirled on the purple glare!  There they were, all going"
"5149"	"at once, red, blue, green, purple!--four furious volcanoes pouring"
"5150"	"vast clouds of radiant smoke aloft, and spreading a blinding"
"5151"	"rainbowed noonday to the furthest confines of that valley.  In"
"5152"	"the distance one could see that fellow on the pillar standing rigid"
"5153"	"against the background of sky, his seesaw stopped for the first"
"5154"	"time in twenty years.  I knew the boys were at the pump now and"
"5155"	"ready.  So I said to the abbot:"
"5156"	"“The time is come, Father.  I am about to pronounce the dread name"
"5157"	"and command the spell to dissolve.  You want to brace up, and take"
"5158"	"hold of something.”  Then I shouted to the people: “Behold, in"
"5159"	"another minute the spell will be broken, or no mortal can break it."
"5160"	"If it break, all will know it, for you will see the sacred water"
"5161"	"gush from the chapel door!”"
"5162"	"I stood a few moments, to let the hearers have a chance to spread"
"5163"	"my announcement to those who couldn’t hear, and so convey it"
"5164"	"to the furthest ranks, then I made a grand exhibition of extra"
"5165"	"posturing and gesturing, and shouted:"
"5166"	"“Lo, I command the fell spirit that possesses the holy fountain"
"5167"	"to now disgorge into the skies all the infernal fires that still"
"5168"	"remain in him, and straightway dissolve his spell and flee hence"
"5169"	"to the pit, there to lie bound a thousand years.  By his own dread"
"5170"	"name I command it--BGWJJILLIGKKK!”"
"5171"	"Then I touched off the hogshead of rockets, and a vast fountain of"
"5172"	"dazzling lances of fire vomited itself toward the zenith with a"
"5173"	"hissing rush, and burst in mid-sky into a storm of flashing jewels!"
"5174"	"One mighty groan of terror started up from the massed people"
"5175"	"--then suddenly broke into a wild hosannah of joy--for there, fair"
"5176"	"and plain in the uncanny glare, they saw the freed water leaping"
"5177"	"forth!  The old abbot could not speak a word, for tears and the"
"5178"	"chokings in his throat; without utterance of any sort, he folded me"
"5179"	"in his arms and mashed me.  It was more eloquent than speech."
"5180"	"And harder to get over, too, in a country where there were really"
"5181"	"no doctors that were worth a damaged nickel."
"5182"	"You should have seen those acres of people throw themselves down"
"5183"	"in that water and kiss it; kiss it, and pet it, and fondle it, and"
"5184"	"talk to it as if it were alive, and welcome it back with the dear"
"5185"	"names they gave their darlings, just as if it had been a friend who"
"5186"	"was long gone away and lost, and was come home again.  Yes, it was"
"5187"	"pretty to see, and made me think more of them than I had done before."
"5188"	"I sent Merlin home on a shutter.  He had caved in and gone down"
"5189"	"like a landslide when I pronounced that fearful name, and had"
"5190"	"never come to since.  He never had heard that name before,--neither"
"5191"	"had I--but to him it was the right one.  Any jumble would have"
"5192"	"been the right one.  He admitted, afterward, that that spirit’s own"
"5193"	"mother could not have pronounced that name better than I did."
"5194"	"He never could understand how I survived it, and I didn’t tell"
"5195"	"him.  It is only young magicians that give away a secret like that."
"5196"	"Merlin spent three months working enchantments to try to find out"
"5197"	"the deep trick of how to pronounce that name and outlive it."
"5198"	"But he didn’t arrive."
"5199"	"When I started to the chapel, the populace uncovered and fell back"
"5200"	"reverently to make a wide way for me, as if I had been some kind"
"5201"	"of a superior being--and I was.  I was aware of that.  I took along"
"5202"	"a night shift of monks, and taught them the mystery of the pump,"
"5203"	"and set them to work, for it was plain that a good part of the"
"5204"	"people out there were going to sit up with the water all night,"
"5205"	"consequently it was but right that they should have all they wanted"
"5206"	"of it.  To those monks that pump was a good deal of a miracle"
"5207"	"itself, and they were full of wonder over it; and of admiration,"
"5208"	"too, of the exceeding effectiveness of its performance."
"5209"	"It was a great night, an immense night.  There was reputation in it."
"5210"	"I could hardly get to sleep for glorying over it."
"5211"	"CHAPTER XXIV"
"5212"	"A RIVAL MAGICIAN"
"5213"	"My influence in the Valley of Holiness was something prodigious"
"5214"	"now.  It seemed worth while to try to turn it to some valuable"
"5215"	"account.  The thought came to me the next morning, and was suggested"
"5216"	"by my seeing one of my knights who was in the soap line come"
"5217"	"riding in.  According to history, the monks of this place two"
"5218"	"centuries before had been worldly minded enough to want to wash."
"5219"	"It might be that there was a leaven of this unrighteousness still"
"5220"	"remaining.  So I sounded a Brother:"
"5221"	"“Wouldn’t you like a bath?”"
"5222"	"He shuddered at the thought--the thought of the peril of it to"
"5223"	"the well--but he said with feeling:"
"5224"	"“One needs not to ask that of a poor body who has not known that"
"5225"	"blessed refreshment sith that he was a boy.  Would God I might"
"5226"	"wash me! but it may not be, fair sir, tempt me not; it is forbidden.”"
"5227"	"And then he sighed in such a sorrowful way that I was resolved"
"5228"	"he should have at least one layer of his real estate removed,"
"5229"	"if it sized up my whole influence and bankrupted the pile.  So I"
"5230"	"went to the abbot and asked for a permit for this Brother.  He"
"5231"	"blenched at the idea--I don’t mean that you could see him blench,"
"5232"	"for of course you couldn’t see it without you scraped him, and"
"5233"	"I didn’t care enough about it to scrape him, but I knew the blench"
"5234"	"was there, just the same, and within a book-cover’s thickness of"
"5235"	"the surface, too--blenched, and trembled.  He said:"
"5236"	"“Ah, son, ask aught else thou wilt, and it is thine, and freely"
"5237"	"granted out of a grateful heart--but this, oh, this!  Would you"
"5238"	"drive away the blessed water again?”"
"5239"	"“No, Father, I will not drive it away.  I have mysterious knowledge"
"5240"	"which teaches me that there was an error that other time when"
"5241"	"it was thought the institution of the bath banished the fountain.”"
"5242"	" A large interest began to show up in the old man’s face.  “My"
"5243"	"knowledge informs me that the bath was innocent of that misfortune,"
"5244"	"which was caused by quite another sort of sin.”"
"5245"	"“These are brave words--but--but right welcome, if they be true.”"
"5246"	"“They are true, indeed.  Let me build the bath again, Father."
"5247"	"Let me build it again, and the fountain shall flow forever.”"
"5248"	"“You promise this?--you promise it?  Say the word--say you promise it!”"
"5249"	"“I do promise it.”"
"5250"	"“Then will I have the first bath myself!  Go--get ye to your work."
"5251"	"Tarry not, tarry not, but go.”"
"5252"	"I and my boys were at work, straight off.  The ruins of the old"
"5253"	"bath were there yet in the basement of the monastery, not a stone"
"5254"	"missing.  They had been left just so, all these lifetimes, and"
"5255"	"avoided with a pious fear, as things accursed.  In two days we"
"5256"	"had it all done and the water in--a spacious pool of clear pure"
"5257"	"water that a body could swim in.  It was running water, too."
"5258"	"It came in, and went out, through the ancient pipes.  The old abbot"
"5259"	"kept his word, and was the first to try it.  He went down black"
"5260"	"and shaky, leaving the whole black community above troubled and"
"5261"	"worried and full of bodings; but he came back white and joyful,"
"5262"	"and the game was made! another triumph scored."
"5263"	"It was a good campaign that we made in that Valley of Holiness,"
"5264"	"and I was very well satisfied, and ready to move on now, but"
"5265"	"I struck a disappointment.  I caught a heavy cold, and it started"
"5266"	"up an old lurking rheumatism of mine.  Of course the rheumatism"
"5267"	"hunted up my weakest place and located itself there.  This was"
"5268"	"the place where the abbot put his arms about me and mashed me, what"
"5269"	"time he was moved to testify his gratitude to me with an embrace."
"5270"	"When at last I got out, I was a shadow.  But everybody was full"
"5271"	"of attentions and kindnesses, and these brought cheer back into"
"5272"	"my life, and were the right medicine to help a convalescent swiftly"
"5273"	"up toward health and strength again; so I gained fast."
"5274"	"Sandy was worn out with nursing; so I made up my mind to turn out"
"5275"	"and go a cruise alone, leaving her at the nunnery to rest up."
"5276"	"My idea was to disguise myself as a freeman of peasant degree"
"5277"	"and wander through the country a week or two on foot.  This would"
"5278"	"give me a chance to eat and lodge with the lowliest and poorest"
"5279"	"class of free citizens on equal terms.  There was no other way"
"5280"	"to inform myself perfectly of their everyday life and the operation"
"5281"	"of the laws upon it.  If I went among them as a gentleman, there"
"5282"	"would be restraints and conventionalities which would shut me out"
"5283"	"from their private joys and troubles, and I should get no further"
"5284"	"than the outside shell."
"5285"	"One morning I was out on a long walk to get up muscle for my trip,"
"5286"	"and had climbed the ridge which bordered the northern extremity"
"5287"	"of the valley, when I came upon an artificial opening in the face"
"5288"	"of a low precipice, and recognized it by its location as a hermitage"
"5289"	"which had often been pointed out to me from a distance as the den"
"5290"	"of a hermit of high renown for dirt and austerity.  I knew he had"
"5291"	"lately been offered a situation in the Great Sahara, where lions"
"5292"	"and sandflies made the hermit-life peculiarly attractive and"
"5293"	"difficult, and had gone to Africa to take possession, so I thought"
"5294"	"I would look in and see how the atmosphere of this den agreed"
"5295"	"with its reputation."
"5296"	"My surprise was great: the place was newly swept and scoured."
"5297"	"Then there was another surprise.  Back in the gloom of the cavern"
"5298"	"I heard the clink of a little bell, and then this exclamation:"
"5299"	"“Hello Central!  Is this you, Camelot?--Behold, thou mayst glad"
"5300"	"thy heart an thou hast faith to believe the wonderful when that"
"5301"	"it cometh in unexpected guise and maketh itself manifest in"
"5302"	"impossible places--here standeth in the flesh his mightiness"
"5303"	"The Boss, and with thine own ears shall ye hear him speak!”"
"5304"	"Now what a radical reversal of things this was; what a jumbling"
"5305"	"together of extravagant incongruities; what a fantastic conjunction"
"5306"	"of opposites and irreconcilables--the home of the bogus miracle"
"5307"	"become the home of a real one, the den of a mediaeval hermit turned"
"5308"	"into a telephone office!"
"5309"	"The telephone clerk stepped into the light, and I recognized one"
"5310"	"of my young fellows.  I said:"
"5311"	"“How long has this office been established here, Ulfius?”"
"5312"	"“But since midnight, fair Sir Boss, an it please you.  We saw many"
"5313"	"lights in the valley, and so judged it well to make a station,"
"5314"	"for that where so many lights be needs must they indicate a town"
"5315"	"of goodly size.”"
"5316"	"“Quite right.  It isn’t a town in the customary sense, but it’s"
"5317"	"a good stand, anyway.  Do you know where you are?”"
"5318"	"“Of that I have had no time to make inquiry; for whenas my"
"5319"	"comradeship moved hence upon their labors, leaving me in charge,"
"5320"	"I got me to needed rest, purposing to inquire when I waked, and"
"5321"	"report the place’s name to Camelot for record.”"
"5322"	"“Well, this is the Valley of Holiness.”"
"5323"	"It didn’t take; I mean, he didn’t start at the name, as I had"
"5324"	"supposed he would.  He merely said:"
"5325"	"“I will so report it.”"
"5326"	"“Why, the surrounding regions are filled with the noise of late"
"5327"	"wonders that have happened here!  You didn’t hear of them?”"
"5328"	"“Ah, ye will remember we move by night, and avoid speech with all."
"5329"	"We learn naught but that we get by the telephone from Camelot.”"
"5330"	"“Why _they_ know all about this thing.  Haven’t they told you anything"
"5331"	"about the great miracle of the restoration of a holy fountain?”"
"5332"	"“Oh, _that_?  Indeed yes.  But the name of _this_ valley doth woundily"
"5333"	"differ from the name of _that_ one; indeed to differ wider were not pos--”"
"5334"	"“What was that name, then?”"
"5335"	"“The Valley of Hellishness.”"
"5336"	"“_That_ explains it.  Confound a telephone, anyway.  It is the very"
"5337"	"demon for conveying similarities of sound that are miracles of"
"5338"	"divergence from similarity of sense.  But no matter, you know"
"5339"	"the name of the place now.  Call up Camelot.”"
"5340"	"He did it, and had Clarence sent for.  It was good to hear my boy’s"
"5341"	"voice again.  It was like being home.  After some affectionate"
"5342"	"interchanges, and some account of my late illness, I said:"
"5343"	"“What is new?”"
"5344"	"“The king and queen and many of the court do start even in this"
"5345"	"hour, to go to your valley to pay pious homage to the waters ye"
"5346"	"have restored, and cleanse themselves of sin, and see the place"
"5347"	"where the infernal spirit spouted true hell-flames to the clouds"
"5348"	"--an ye listen sharply ye may hear me wink and hear me likewise"
"5349"	"smile a smile, sith ‘twas I that made selection of those flames"
"5350"	"from out our stock and sent them by your order.”"
"5351"	"“Does the king know the way to this place?”"
"5352"	"“The king?--no, nor to any other in his realms, mayhap; but the lads"
"5353"	"that holp you with your miracle will be his guide and lead the way,"
"5354"	"and appoint the places for rests at noons and sleeps at night.”"
"5355"	"“This will bring them here--when?”"
"5356"	"“Mid-afternoon, or later, the third day.”"
"5357"	"“Anything else in the way of news?”"
"5358"	"“The king hath begun the raising of the standing army ye suggested"
"5359"	"to him; one regiment is complete and officered.”"
"5360"	"“The mischief!  I wanted a main hand in that myself.  There is"
"5361"	"only one body of men in the kingdom that are fitted to officer"
"5362"	"a regular army.”"
"5363"	"“Yes--and now ye will marvel to know there’s not so much as one"
"5364"	"West Pointer in that regiment.”"
"5365"	"“What are you talking about?  Are you in earnest?”"
"5366"	"“It is truly as I have said.”"
"5367"	"“Why, this makes me uneasy.  Who were chosen, and what was the"
"5368"	"method?  Competitive examination?”"
"5369"	"“Indeed, I know naught of the method.  I but know this--these"
"5370"	"officers be all of noble family, and are born--what is it you"
"5371"	"call it?--chuckleheads.”"
"5372"	"“There’s something wrong, Clarence.”"
"5373"	"“Comfort yourself, then; for two candidates for a lieutenancy do"
"5374"	"travel hence with the king--young nobles both--and if you but wait"
"5375"	"where you are you will hear them questioned.”"
"5376"	"“That is news to the purpose.  I will get one West Pointer in,"
"5377"	"anyway.  Mount a man and send him to that school with a message;"
"5378"	"let him kill horses, if necessary, but he must be there before"
"5379"	"sunset to-night and say--”"
"5380"	"“There is no need.  I have laid a ground wire to the school."
"5381"	"Prithee let me connect you with it.”"
"5382"	"It sounded good!  In this atmosphere of telephones and lightning"
"5383"	"communication with distant regions, I was breathing the breath"
"5384"	"of life again after long suffocation.  I realized, then, what a"
"5385"	"creepy, dull, inanimate horror this land had been to me all these"
"5386"	"years, and how I had been in such a stifled condition of mind as"
"5387"	"to have grown used to it almost beyond the power to notice it."
"5388"	"I gave my order to the superintendent of the Academy personally."
"5389"	"I also asked him to bring me some paper and a fountain pen and"
"5390"	"a box or so of safety matches.  I was getting tired of doing"
"5391"	"without these conveniences.  I could have them now, as I wasn’t"
"5392"	"going to wear armor any more at present, and therefore could get"
"5393"	"at my pockets."
"5394"	"When I got back to the monastery, I found a thing of interest"
"5395"	"going on.  The abbot and his monks were assembled in the great"
"5396"	"hall, observing with childish wonder and faith the performances"
"5397"	"of a new magician, a fresh arrival.  His dress was the extreme of"
"5398"	"the fantastic; as showy and foolish as the sort of thing an Indian"
"5399"	"medicine-man wears.  He was mowing, and mumbling, and gesticulating,"
"5400"	"and drawing mystical figures in the air and on the floor,--the"
"5401"	"regular thing, you know.  He was a celebrity from Asia--so he"
"5402"	"said, and that was enough.  That sort of evidence was as good"
"5403"	"as gold, and passed current everywhere."
"5404"	"How easy and cheap it was to be a great magician on this fellow’s"
"5405"	"terms.  His specialty was to tell you what any individual on the"
"5406"	"face of the globe was doing at the moment; and what he had done"
"5407"	"at any time in the past, and what he would do at any time in the"
"5408"	"future.  He asked if any would like to know what the Emperor of"
"5409"	"the East was doing now?  The sparkling eyes and the delighted rubbing"
"5410"	"of hands made eloquent answer--this reverend crowd _would_ like to"
"5411"	"know what that monarch was at, just as this moment.  The fraud"
"5412"	"went through some more mummery, and then made grave announcement:"
"5413"	"“The high and mighty Emperor of the East doth at this moment put"
"5414"	"money in the palm of a holy begging friar--one, two, three pieces,"
"5415"	"and they be all of silver.”"
"5416"	"A buzz of admiring exclamations broke out, all around:"
"5417"	"“It is marvelous!”  “Wonderful!”  “What study, what labor, to have"
"5418"	"acquired a so amazing power as this!”"
"5419"	"Would they like to know what the Supreme Lord of Inde was doing?"
"5420"	"Yes.  He told them what the Supreme Lord of Inde was doing.  Then"
"5421"	"he told them what the Sultan of Egypt was at; also what the King"
"5422"	"of the Remote Seas was about.  And so on and so on; and with each"
"5423"	"new marvel the astonishment at his accuracy rose higher and higher."
"5424"	"They thought he must surely strike an uncertain place some time;"
"5425"	"but no, he never had to hesitate, he always knew, and always with"
"5426"	"unerring precision.  I saw that if this thing went on I should lose"
"5427"	"my supremacy, this fellow would capture my following, I should"
"5428"	"be left out in the cold.  I must put a cog in his wheel, and do it"
"5429"	"right away, too.  I said:"
"5430"	"“If I might ask, I should very greatly like to know what a certain"
"5431"	"person is doing.”"
"5432"	"“Speak, and freely.  I will tell you.”"
"5433"	"“It will be difficult--perhaps impossible.”"
"5434"	"“My art knoweth not that word.  The more difficult it is, the more"
"5435"	"certainly will I reveal it to you.”"
"5436"	"You see, I was working up the interest.  It was getting pretty"
"5437"	"high, too; you could see that by the craning necks all around,"
"5438"	"and the half-suspended breathing.  So now I climaxed it:"
"5439"	"“If you make no mistake--if you tell me truly what I want to"
"5440"	"know--I will give you two hundred silver pennies.”"
"5441"	"“The fortune is mine!  I will tell you what you would know.”"
"5442"	"“Then tell me what I am doing with my right hand.”"
"5443"	"“Ah-h!”  There was a general gasp of surprise.  It had not occurred"
"5444"	"to anybody in the crowd--that simple trick of inquiring about"
"5445"	"somebody who wasn’t ten thousand miles away.  The magician was"
"5446"	"hit hard; it was an emergency that had never happened in his"
"5447"	"experience before, and it corked him; he didn’t know how to meet"
"5448"	"it.  He looked stunned, confused; he couldn’t say a word.  “Come,”"
"5449"	" I said, “what are you waiting for?  Is it possible you can answer up,"
"5450"	"right off, and tell what anybody on the other side of the earth is"
"5451"	"doing, and yet can’t tell what a person is doing who isn’t three"
"5452"	"yards from you?  Persons behind me know what I am doing with my"
"5453"	"right hand--they will indorse you if you tell correctly.”  He was"
"5454"	"still dumb.  “Very well, I’ll tell you why you don’t speak up and"
"5455"	"tell; it is because you don’t know.  _You_ a magician!  Good friends,"
"5456"	"this tramp is a mere fraud and liar.”"
"5457"	"This distressed the monks and terrified them.  They were not used"
"5458"	"to hearing these awful beings called names, and they did not know"
"5459"	"what might be the consequence.  There was a dead silence now;"
"5460"	"superstitious bodings were in every mind.  The magician began to"
"5461"	"pull his wits together, and when he presently smiled an easy,"
"5462"	"nonchalant smile, it spread a mighty relief around; for it indicated"
"5463"	"that his mood was not destructive.  He said:"
"5464"	"“It hath struck me speechless, the frivolity of this person’s"
"5465"	"speech.  Let all know, if perchance there be any who know it not,"
"5466"	"that enchanters of my degree deign not to concern themselves with"
"5467"	"the doings of any but kings, princes, emperors, them that be born"
"5468"	"in the purple and them only.  Had ye asked me what Arthur the great"
"5469"	"king is doing, it were another matter, and I had told ye; but the"
"5470"	"doings of a subject interest me not.”"
"5471"	"“Oh, I misunderstood you.  I thought you said ‘anybody,’ and so"
"5472"	"I supposed ‘anybody’ included--well, anybody; that is, everybody.”"
"5473"	"“It doth--anybody that is of lofty birth; and the better if"
"5474"	"he be royal.”"
"5475"	"“That, it meseemeth, might well be,” said the abbot, who saw his"
"5476"	"opportunity to smooth things and avert disaster, “for it were not"
"5477"	"likely that so wonderful a gift as this would be conferred for"
"5478"	"the revelation of the concerns of lesser beings than such as be"
"5479"	"born near to the summits of greatness.  Our Arthur the king--”"
"5480"	"“Would you know of him?” broke in the enchanter."
"5481"	"“Most gladly, yea, and gratefully.”"
"5482"	"Everybody was full of awe and interest again right away, the"
"5483"	"incorrigible idiots.  They watched the incantations absorbingly,"
"5484"	"and looked at me with a “There, now, what can you say to that?”"
"5485"	" air, when the announcement came:"
"5486"	"“The king is weary with the chase, and lieth in his palace these"
"5487"	"two hours sleeping a dreamless sleep.”"
"5488"	"“God’s benison upon him!” said the abbot, and crossed himself;"
"5489"	"“may that sleep be to the refreshment of his body and his soul.”"
"5490"	"“And so it might be, if he were sleeping,” I said, “but the king"
"5491"	"is not sleeping, the king rides.”"
"5492"	"Here was trouble again--a conflict of authority.  Nobody knew which"
"5493"	"of us to believe; I still had some reputation left.  The magician’s"
"5494"	"scorn was stirred, and he said:"
"5495"	"“Lo, I have seen many wonderful soothsayers and prophets and"
"5496"	"magicians in my life days, but none before that could sit idle and"
"5497"	"see to the heart of things with never an incantation to help.”"
"5498"	"“You have lived in the woods, and lost much by it.  I use incantations"
"5499"	"myself, as this good brotherhood are aware--but only on occasions"
"5500"	"of moment.”"
"5501"	"When it comes to sarcasming, I reckon I know how to keep my end up."
"5502"	"That jab made this fellow squirm.  The abbot inquired after the"
"5503"	"queen and the court, and got this information:"
"5504"	"“They be all on sleep, being overcome by fatigue, like as to the king.”"
"5505"	"I said:"
"5506"	"“That is merely another lie.  Half of them are about their amusements,"
"5507"	"the queen and the other half are not sleeping, they ride.  Now"
"5508"	"perhaps you can spread yourself a little, and tell us where the king"
"5509"	"and queen and all that are this moment riding with them are going?”"
"5510"	"“They sleep now, as I said; but on the morrow they will ride,"
"5511"	"for they go a journey toward the sea.”"
"5512"	"“And where will they be the day after to-morrow at vespers?”"
"5513"	"“Far to the north of Camelot, and half their journey will be done.”"
"5514"	"“That is another lie, by the space of a hundred and fifty miles."
"5515"	"Their journey will not be merely half done, it will be all done,"
"5516"	"and they will be _here_, in this valley.”"
"5517"	"_That_ was a noble shot!  It set the abbot and the monks in a whirl"
"5518"	"of excitement, and it rocked the enchanter to his base.  I followed"
"5519"	"the thing right up:"
"5520"	"“If the king does not arrive, I will have myself ridden on a rail:"
"5521"	"if he does I will ride you on a rail instead.”"
"5522"	"Next day I went up to the telephone office and found that the king"
"5523"	"had passed through two towns that were on the line.  I spotted"
"5524"	"his progress on the succeeding day in the same way.  I kept these"
"5525"	"matters to myself.  The third day’s reports showed that if he"
"5526"	"kept up his gait he would arrive by four in the afternoon.  There"
"5527"	"was still no sign anywhere of interest in his coming; there seemed"
"5528"	"to be no preparations making to receive him in state; a strange"
"5529"	"thing, truly.  Only one thing could explain this: that other"
"5530"	"magician had been cutting under me, sure.  This was true.  I asked"
"5531"	"a friend of mine, a monk, about it, and he said, yes, the magician"
"5532"	"had tried some further enchantments and found out that the court"
"5533"	"had concluded to make no journey at all, but stay at home.  Think"
"5534"	"of that!  Observe how much a reputation was worth in such a country."
"5535"	"These people had seen me do the very showiest bit of magic in"
"5536"	"history, and the only one within their memory that had a positive"
"5537"	"value, and yet here they were, ready to take up with an adventurer"
"5538"	"who could offer no evidence of his powers but his mere unproven word."
"5539"	"However, it was not good politics to let the king come without"
"5540"	"any fuss and feathers at all, so I went down and drummed up a"
"5541"	"procession of pilgrims and smoked out a batch of hermits and"
"5542"	"started them out at two o’clock to meet him.  And that was the"
"5543"	"sort of state he arrived in.  The abbot was helpless with rage"
"5544"	"and humiliation when I brought him out on a balcony and showed"
"5545"	"him the head of the state marching in and never a monk on hand to"
"5546"	"offer him welcome, and no stir of life or clang of joy-bell to glad"
"5547"	"his spirit.  He took one look and then flew to rouse out his forces."
"5548"	"The next minute the bells were dinning furiously, and the various"
"5549"	"buildings were vomiting monks and nuns, who went swarming in a"
"5550"	"rush toward the coming procession; and with them went that magician"
"5551"	"--and he was on a rail, too, by the abbot’s order; and his reputation"
"5552"	"was in the mud, and mine was in the sky again.  Yes, a man can"
"5553"	"keep his trademark current in such a country, but he can’t sit"
"5554"	"around and do it; he has got to be on deck and attending to business"
"5555"	"right along."
"5556"	"CHAPTER XXV"
"5557"	"A COMPETITIVE EXAMINATION"
"5558"	"When the king traveled for change of air, or made a progress, or"
"5559"	"visited a distant noble whom he wished to bankrupt with the cost"
"5560"	"of his keep, part of the administration moved with him.  It was"
"5561"	"a fashion of the time.  The Commission charged with the examination"
"5562"	"of candidates for posts in the army came with the king to the"
"5563"	"Valley, whereas they could have transacted their business just"
"5564"	"as well at home.  And although this expedition was strictly a"
"5565"	"holiday excursion for the king, he kept some of his business"
"5566"	"functions going just the same.  He touched for the evil, as usual;"
"5567"	"he held court in the gate at sunrise and tried cases, for he was"
"5568"	"himself Chief Justice of the King’s Bench."
"5569"	"He shone very well in this latter office.  He was a wise and humane"
"5570"	"judge, and he clearly did his honest best and fairest,--according"
"5571"	"to his lights.  That is a large reservation.  His lights--I mean"
"5572"	"his rearing--often colored his decisions.  Whenever there was a"
"5573"	"dispute between a noble or gentleman and a person of lower degree,"
"5574"	"the king’s leanings and sympathies were for the former class always,"
"5575"	"whether he suspected it or not.  It was impossible that this should"
"5576"	"be otherwise.  The blunting effects of slavery upon the slaveholder’s"
"5577"	"moral perceptions are known and conceded, the world over; and a"
"5578"	"privileged class, an aristocracy, is but a band of slaveholders"
"5579"	"under another name.  This has a harsh sound, and yet should not"
"5580"	"be offensive to any--even to the noble himself--unless the fact"
"5581"	"itself be an offense: for the statement simply formulates a fact."
"5582"	"The repulsive feature of slavery is the _thing_, not its name.  One"
"5583"	"needs but to hear an aristocrat speak of the classes that are below"
"5584"	"him to recognize--and in but indifferently modified measure"
"5585"	"--the very air and tone of the actual slaveholder; and behind these"
"5586"	"are the slaveholder’s spirit, the slaveholder’s blunted feeling."
"5587"	"They are the result of the same cause in both cases: the possessor’s"
"5588"	"old and inbred custom of regarding himself as a superior being."
"5589"	"The king’s judgments wrought frequent injustices, but it was merely"
"5590"	"the fault of his training, his natural and unalterable sympathies."
"5591"	"He was as unfitted for a judgeship as would be the average mother"
"5592"	"for the position of milk-distributor to starving children in"
"5593"	"famine-time; her own children would fare a shade better than the rest."
"5594"	"One very curious case came before the king.  A young girl, an"
"5595"	"orphan, who had a considerable estate, married a fine young fellow"
"5596"	"who had nothing.  The girl’s property was within a seigniory held"
"5597"	"by the Church.  The bishop of the diocese, an arrogant scion of"
"5598"	"the great nobility, claimed the girl’s estate on the ground that"
"5599"	"she had married privately, and thus had cheated the Church out"
"5600"	"of one of its rights as lord of the seigniory--the one heretofore"
"5601"	"referred to as le droit du seigneur.  The penalty of refusal or"
"5602"	"avoidance was confiscation.  The girl’s defense was, that the"
"5603"	"lordship of the seigniory was vested in the bishop, and the"
"5604"	"particular right here involved was not transferable, but must be"
"5605"	"exercised by the lord himself or stand vacated; and that an older"
"5606"	"law, of the Church itself, strictly barred the bishop from exercising"
"5607"	"it.  It was a very odd case, indeed."
"5608"	"It reminded me of something I had read in my youth about the"
"5609"	"ingenious way in which the aldermen of London raised the money"
"5610"	"that built the Mansion House.  A person who had not taken the"
"5611"	"Sacrament according to the Anglican rite could not stand as a"
"5612"	"candidate for sheriff of London.  Thus Dissenters were ineligible;"
"5613"	"they could not run if asked, they could not serve if elected."
"5614"	"The aldermen, who without any question were Yankees in disguise,"
"5615"	"hit upon this neat device: they passed a by-law imposing a fine"
"5616"	"of L400 upon any one who should refuse to be a candidate for"
"5617"	"sheriff, and a fine of L600 upon any person who, after being"
"5618"	"elected sheriff, refused to serve.  Then they went to work and"
"5619"	"elected a lot of Dissenters, one after another, and kept it up"
"5620"	"until they had collected L15,000 in fines; and there stands the"
"5621"	"stately Mansion House to this day, to keep the blushing citizen"
"5622"	"in mind of a long past and lamented day when a band of Yankees"
"5623"	"slipped into London and played games of the sort that has given"
"5624"	"their race a unique and shady reputation among all truly good"
"5625"	"and holy peoples that be in the earth."
"5626"	"The girl’s case seemed strong to me; the bishop’s case was just"
"5627"	"as strong.  I did not see how the king was going to get out of"
"5628"	"this hole.  But he got out.  I append his decision:"
"5629"	"“Truly I find small difficulty here, the matter being even a"
"5630"	"child’s affair for simpleness.  An the young bride had conveyed"
"5631"	"notice, as in duty bound, to her feudal lord and proper master"
"5632"	"and protector the bishop, she had suffered no loss, for the said"
"5633"	"bishop could have got a dispensation making him, for temporary"
"5634"	"conveniency, eligible to the exercise of his said right, and thus"
"5635"	"would she have kept all she had.  Whereas, failing in her first"
"5636"	"duty, she hath by that failure failed in all; for whoso, clinging"
"5637"	"to a rope, severeth it above his hands, must fall; it being no"
"5638"	"defense to claim that the rest of the rope is sound, neither any"
"5639"	"deliverance from his peril, as he shall find.  Pardy, the woman’s"
"5640"	"case is rotten at the source.  It is the decree of the court that"
"5641"	"she forfeit to the said lord bishop all her goods, even to the"
"5642"	"last farthing that she doth possess, and be thereto mulcted in"
"5643"	"the costs.  Next!”"
"5644"	"Here was a tragic end to a beautiful honeymoon not yet three months"
"5645"	"old.  Poor young creatures!  They had lived these three months"
"5646"	"lapped to the lips in worldly comforts.  These clothes and trinkets"
"5647"	"they were wearing were as fine and dainty as the shrewdest stretch"
"5648"	"of the sumptuary laws allowed to people of their degree; and in"
"5649"	"these pretty clothes, she crying on his shoulder, and he trying"
"5650"	"to comfort her with hopeful words set to the music of despair,"
"5651"	"they went from the judgment seat out into the world homeless,"
"5652"	"bedless, breadless; why, the very beggars by the roadsides were"
"5653"	"not so poor as they."
"5654"	"Well, the king was out of the hole; and on terms satisfactory to"
"5655"	"the Church and the rest of the aristocracy, no doubt.  Men write"
"5656"	"many fine and plausible arguments in support of monarchy, but"
"5657"	"the fact remains that where every man in a State has a vote, brutal"
"5658"	"laws are impossible.  Arthur’s people were of course poor material"
"5659"	"for a republic, because they had been debased so long by monarchy;"
"5660"	"and yet even they would have been intelligent enough to make short"
"5661"	"work of that law which the king had just been administering if it"
"5662"	"had been submitted to their full and free vote.  There is a phrase"
"5663"	"which has grown so common in the world’s mouth that it has come"
"5664"	"to seem to have sense and meaning--the sense and meaning implied"
"5665"	"when it is used; that is the phrase which refers to this or that or"
"5666"	"the other nation as possibly being “capable of self-government”;"
"5667"	"and the implied sense of it is, that there has been a nation"
"5668"	"somewhere, some time or other which _wasn’t_ capable of it--wasn’t as"
"5669"	"able to govern itself as some self-appointed specialists were or"
"5670"	"would be to govern it.  The master minds of all nations, in all"
"5671"	"ages, have sprung in affluent multitude from the mass of the nation,"
"5672"	"and from the mass of the nation only--not from its privileged"
"5673"	"classes; and so, no matter what the nation’s intellectual grade"
"5674"	"was; whether high or low, the bulk of its ability was in the long"
"5675"	"ranks of its nameless and its poor, and so it never saw the day"
"5676"	"that it had not the material in abundance whereby to govern itself."
"5677"	"Which is to assert an always self-proven fact: that even the best"
"5678"	"governed and most free and most enlightened monarchy is still"
"5679"	"behind the best condition attainable by its people; and that the"
"5680"	"same is true of kindred governments of lower grades, all the way"
"5681"	"down to the lowest."
"5682"	"King Arthur had hurried up the army business altogether beyond"
"5683"	"my calculations.  I had not supposed he would move in the matter"
"5684"	"while I was away; and so I had not mapped out a scheme for determining"
"5685"	"the merits of officers; I had only remarked that it would be wise"
"5686"	"to submit every candidate to a sharp and searching examination;"
"5687"	"and privately I meant to put together a list of military qualifications"
"5688"	"that nobody could answer to but my West Pointers.  That ought"
"5689"	"to have been attended to before I left; for the king was so taken"
"5690"	"with the idea of a standing army that he couldn’t wait but must"
"5691"	"get about it at once, and get up as good a scheme of examination"
"5692"	"as he could invent out of his own head."
"5693"	"I was impatient to see what this was; and to show, too, how much"
"5694"	"more admirable was the one which I should display to the Examining"
"5695"	"Board.  I intimated this, gently, to the king, and it fired his"
"5696"	"curiosity.  When the Board was assembled, I followed him in; and"
"5697"	"behind us came the candidates.  One of these candidates was a bright"
"5698"	"young West Pointer of mine, and with him were a couple of my"
"5699"	"West Point professors."
"5700"	"When I saw the Board, I did not know whether to cry or to laugh."
"5701"	"The head of it was the officer known to later centuries as Norroy"
"5702"	"King-at-Arms!  The two other members were chiefs of bureaus in"
"5703"	"his department; and all three were priests, of course; all officials"
"5704"	"who had to know how to read and write were priests."
"5705"	"My candidate was called first, out of courtesy to me, and the head"
"5706"	"of the Board opened on him with official solemnity:"
"5707"	"“Name?”"
"5708"	"“Mal-ease.”"
"5709"	"“Son of?”"
"5710"	"“Webster.”"
"5711"	"“Webster--Webster.  H’m--I--my memory faileth to recall the"
"5712"	"name.  Condition?”"
"5713"	"“Weaver.”"
"5714"	"“Weaver!--God keep us!”"
"5715"	"The king was staggered, from his summit to his foundations; one"
"5716"	"clerk fainted, and the others came near it.  The chairman pulled"
"5717"	"himself together, and said indignantly:"
"5718"	"“It is sufficient.  Get you hence.”"
"5719"	"But I appealed to the king.  I begged that my candidate might be"
"5720"	"examined.  The king was willing, but the Board, who were all"
"5721"	"well-born folk, implored the king to spare them the indignity of"
"5722"	"examining the weaver’s son.  I knew they didn’t know enough to"
"5723"	"examine him anyway, so I joined my prayers to theirs and the king"
"5724"	"turned the duty over to my professors.  I had had a blackboard"
"5725"	"prepared, and it was put up now, and the circus began.  It was"
"5726"	"beautiful to hear the lad lay out the science of war, and wallow"
"5727"	"in details of battle and siege, of supply, transportation, mining"
"5728"	"and countermining, grand tactics, big strategy and little strategy,"
"5729"	"signal service, infantry, cavalry, artillery, and all about siege"
"5730"	"guns, field guns, gatling guns, rifled guns, smooth bores, musket"
"5731"	"practice, revolver practice--and not a solitary word of it all"
"5732"	"could these catfish make head or tail of, you understand--and it"
"5733"	"was handsome to see him chalk off mathematical nightmares on the"
"5734"	"blackboard that would stump the angels themselves, and do it like"
"5735"	"nothing, too--all about eclipses, and comets, and solstices, and"
"5736"	"constellations, and mean time, and sidereal time, and dinner time,"
"5737"	"and bedtime, and every other imaginable thing above the clouds or"
"5738"	"under them that you could harry or bullyrag an enemy with and make"
"5739"	"him wish he hadn’t come--and when the boy made his military salute"
"5740"	"and stood aside at last, I was proud enough to hug him, and all"
"5741"	"those other people were so dazed they looked partly petrified,"
"5742"	"partly drunk, and wholly caught out and snowed under.  I judged"
"5743"	"that the cake was ours, and by a large majority."
"5744"	"Education is a great thing.  This was the same youth who had come"
"5745"	"to West Point so ignorant that when I asked him, “If a general"
"5746"	"officer should have a horse shot under him on the field of battle,"
"5747"	"what ought he to do?” answered up naively and said:"
"5748"	"“Get up and brush himself.”"
"5749"	"One of the young nobles was called up now.  I thought I would"
"5750"	"question him a little myself.  I said:"
"5751"	"“Can your lordship read?”"
"5752"	"His face flushed indignantly, and he fired this at me:"
"5753"	"“Takest me for a clerk?  I trow I am not of a blood that--”"
"5754"	"“Answer the question!”"
"5755"	"He crowded his wrath down and made out to answer “No.”"
"5756"	"“Can you write?”"
"5757"	"He wanted to resent this, too, but I said:"
"5758"	"“You will confine yourself to the questions, and make no comments."
"5759"	"You are not here to air your blood or your graces, and nothing"
"5760"	"of the sort will be permitted.  Can you write?”"
"5761"	"“No.”"
"5762"	"“Do you know the multiplication table?”"
"5763"	"“I wit not what ye refer to.”"
"5764"	"“How much is 9 times 6?”"
"5765"	"“It is a mystery that is hidden from me by reason that the emergency"
"5766"	"requiring the fathoming of it hath not in my life-days occurred,"
"5767"	"and so, not having no need to know this thing, I abide barren"
"5768"	"of the knowledge.”"
"5769"	"“If A trade a barrel of onions to B, worth 2 pence the bushel,"
"5770"	"in exchange for a sheep worth 4 pence and a dog worth a penny,"
"5771"	"and C kill the dog before delivery, because bitten by the same,"
"5772"	"who mistook him for D, what sum is still due to A from B, and"
"5773"	"which party pays for the dog, C or D, and who gets the money?"
"5774"	"If A, is the penny sufficient, or may he claim consequential damages"
"5775"	"in the form of additional money to represent the possible profit"
"5776"	"which might have inured from the dog, and classifiable as earned"
"5777"	"increment, that is to say, usufruct?”"
"5778"	"“Verily, in the all-wise and unknowable providence of God, who"
"5779"	"moveth in mysterious ways his wonders to perform, have I never"
"5780"	"heard the fellow to this question for confusion of the mind and"
"5781"	"congestion of the ducts of thought.  Wherefore I beseech you let"
"5782"	"the dog and the onions and these people of the strange and godless"
"5783"	"names work out their several salvations from their piteous and"
"5784"	"wonderful difficulties without help of mine, for indeed their"
"5785"	"trouble is sufficient as it is, whereas an I tried to help I should"
"5786"	"but damage their cause the more and yet mayhap not live myself"
"5787"	"to see the desolation wrought.”"
"5788"	"“What do you know of the laws of attraction and gravitation?”"
"5789"	"“If there be such, mayhap his grace the king did promulgate them"
"5790"	"whilst that I lay sick about the beginning of the year and thereby"
"5791"	"failed to hear his proclamation.”"
"5792"	"“What do you know of the science of optics?”"
"5793"	"“I know of governors of places, and seneschals of castles, and"
"5794"	"sheriffs of counties, and many like small offices and titles of"
"5795"	"honor, but him you call the Science of Optics I have not heard"
"5796"	"of before; peradventure it is a new dignity.”"
"5797"	"“Yes, in this country.”"
"5798"	"Try to conceive of this mollusk gravely applying for an official"
"5799"	"position, of any kind under the sun!  Why, he had all the earmarks"
"5800"	"of a typewriter copyist, if you leave out the disposition to"
"5801"	"contribute uninvited emendations of your grammar and punctuation."
"5802"	"It was unaccountable that he didn’t attempt a little help of that"
"5803"	"sort out of his majestic supply of incapacity for the job.  But that"
"5804"	"didn’t prove that he hadn’t material in him for the disposition,"
"5805"	"it only proved that he wasn’t a typewriter copyist yet.  After"
"5806"	"nagging him a little more, I let the professors loose on him and"
"5807"	"they turned him inside out, on the line of scientific war, and"
"5808"	"found him empty, of course.  He knew somewhat about the warfare"
"5809"	"of the time--bushwhacking around for ogres, and bull-fights in"
"5810"	"the tournament ring, and such things--but otherwise he was empty"
"5811"	"and useless.  Then we took the other young noble in hand, and he"
"5812"	"was the first one’s twin, for ignorance and incapacity.  I delivered"
"5813"	"them into the hands of the chairman of the Board with the comfortable"
"5814"	"consciousness that their cake was dough.  They were examined in"
"5815"	"the previous order of precedence."
"5816"	"“Name, so please you?”"
"5817"	"“Pertipole, son of Sir Pertipole, Baron of Barley Mash.”"
"5818"	"“Grandfather?”"
"5819"	"“Also Sir Pertipole, Baron of Barley Mash.”"
"5820"	"“Great-grandfather?”"
"5821"	"“The same name and title.”"
"5822"	"“Great-great-grandfather?”"
"5823"	"“We had none, worshipful sir, the line failing before it had"
"5824"	"reached so far back.”"
"5825"	"“It mattereth not.  It is a good four generations, and fulfilleth"
"5826"	"the requirements of the rule.”"
"5827"	"“Fulfills what rule?” I asked."
"5828"	"“The rule requiring four generations of nobility or else the"
"5829"	"candidate is not eligible.”"
"5830"	"“A man not eligible for a lieutenancy in the army unless he can"
"5831"	"prove four generations of noble descent?”"
"5832"	"“Even so; neither lieutenant nor any other officer may be commissioned"
"5833"	"without that qualification.”"
"5834"	"“Oh, come, this is an astonishing thing.  What good is such a"
"5835"	"qualification as that?”"
"5836"	"“What good?  It is a hardy question, fair sir and Boss, since it doth"
"5837"	"go far to impugn the wisdom of even our holy Mother Church herself.”"
"5838"	"“As how?”"
"5839"	"“For that she hath established the self-same rule regarding"
"5840"	"saints.  By her law none may be canonized until he hath lain dead"
"5841"	"four generations.”"
"5842"	"“I see, I see--it is the same thing.  It is wonderful.  In the one"
"5843"	"case a man lies dead-alive four generations--mummified in ignorance"
"5844"	"and sloth--and that qualifies him to command live people, and take"
"5845"	"their weal and woe into his impotent hands; and in the other case,"
"5846"	"a man lies bedded with death and worms four generations, and that"
"5847"	"qualifies him for office in the celestial camp.  Does the king’s"
"5848"	"grace approve of this strange law?”"
"5849"	"The king said:"
"5850"	"“Why, truly I see naught about it that is strange.  All places of"
"5851"	"honor and of profit do belong, by natural right, to them that be"
"5852"	"of noble blood, and so these dignities in the army are their"
"5853"	"property and would be so without this or any rule.  The rule is"
"5854"	"but to mark a limit.  Its purpose is to keep out too recent blood,"
"5855"	"which would bring into contempt these offices, and men of lofty"
"5856"	"lineage would turn their backs and scorn to take them.  I were"
"5857"	"to blame an I permitted this calamity.  _You_ can permit it an you"
"5858"	"are minded so to do, for you have the delegated authority, but"
"5859"	"that the king should do it were a most strange madness and not"
"5860"	"comprehensible to any.”"
"5861"	"“I yield.  Proceed, sir Chief of the Herald’s College.”"
"5862"	"The chairman resumed as follows:"
"5863"	"“By what illustrious achievement for the honor of the Throne and"
"5864"	"State did the founder of your great line lift himself to the"
"5865"	"sacred dignity of the British nobility?”"
"5866"	"“He built a brewery.”"
"5867"	"“Sire, the Board finds this candidate perfect in all the requirements"
"5868"	"and qualifications for military command, and doth hold his case"
"5869"	"open for decision after due examination of his competitor.”"
"5870"	"The competitor came forward and proved exactly four generations"
"5871"	"of nobility himself.  So there was a tie in military qualifications"
"5872"	"that far."
"5873"	"He stood aside a moment, and Sir Pertipole was questioned further:"
"5874"	"“Of what condition was the wife of the founder of your line?”"
"5875"	"“She came of the highest landed gentry, yet she was not noble;"
"5876"	"she was gracious and pure and charitable, of a blameless life and"
"5877"	"character, insomuch that in these regards was she peer of the"
"5878"	"best lady in the land.”"
"5879"	"“That will do.  Stand down.”  He called up the competing lordling"
"5880"	"again, and asked: “What was the rank and condition of the"
"5881"	"great-grandmother who conferred British nobility upon your"
"5882"	"great house?”"
"5883"	"“She was a king’s leman and did climb to that splendid eminence"
"5884"	"by her own unholpen merit from the sewer where she was born.”"
"5885"	"“Ah, this, indeed, is true nobility, this is the right and perfect"
"5886"	"intermixture.  The lieutenancy is yours, fair lord.  Hold it not in"
"5887"	"contempt; it is the humble step which will lead to grandeurs more"
"5888"	"worthy of the splendor of an origin like to thine.”"
"5889"	"I was down in the bottomless pit of humiliation.  I had promised"
"5890"	"myself an easy and zenith-scouring triumph, and this was the outcome!"
"5891"	"I was almost ashamed to look my poor disappointed cadet in the"
"5892"	"face.  I told him to go home and be patient, this wasn’t the end."
"5893"	"I had a private audience with the king, and made a proposition."
"5894"	"I said it was quite right to officer that regiment with nobilities,"
"5895"	"and he couldn’t have done a wiser thing.  It would also be a good"
"5896"	"idea to add five hundred officers to it; in fact, add as many"
"5897"	"officers as there were nobles and relatives of nobles in the"
"5898"	"country, even if there should finally be five times as many officers"
"5899"	"as privates in it; and thus make it the crack regiment, the envied"
"5900"	"regiment, the King’s Own regiment, and entitled to fight on its"
"5901"	"own hook and in its own way, and go whither it would and come"
"5902"	"when it pleased, in time of war, and be utterly swell and independent."
"5903"	"This would make that regiment the heart’s desire of all the"
"5904"	"nobility, and they would all be satisfied and happy.  Then we"
"5905"	"would make up the rest of the standing army out of commonplace"
"5906"	"materials, and officer it with nobodies, as was proper--nobodies"
"5907"	"selected on a basis of mere efficiency--and we would make this"
"5908"	"regiment toe the line, allow it no aristocratic freedom from"
"5909"	"restraint, and force it to do all the work and persistent hammering,"
"5910"	"to the end that whenever the King’s Own was tired and wanted to go"
"5911"	"off for a change and rummage around amongst ogres and have a good"
"5912"	"time, it could go without uneasiness, knowing that matters were in"
"5913"	"safe hands behind it, and business going to be continued at the"
"5914"	"old stand, same as usual.  The king was charmed with the idea."
"5915"	"When I noticed that, it gave me a valuable notion.  I thought"
"5916"	"I saw my way out of an old and stubborn difficulty at last.  You"
"5917"	"see, the royalties of the Pendragon stock were a long-lived race"
"5918"	"and very fruitful.  Whenever a child was born to any of these"
"5919"	"--and it was pretty often--there was wild joy in the nation’s mouth,"
"5920"	"and piteous sorrow in the nation’s heart.  The joy was questionable,"
"5921"	"but the grief was honest.  Because the event meant another call"
"5922"	"for a Royal Grant.  Long was the list of these royalties, and"
"5923"	"they were a heavy and steadily increasing burden upon the treasury"
"5924"	"and a menace to the crown.  Yet Arthur could not believe this"
"5925"	"latter fact, and he would not listen to any of my various projects"
"5926"	"for substituting something in the place of the royal grants.  If I"
"5927"	"could have persuaded him to now and then provide a support for"
"5928"	"one of these outlying scions from his own pocket, I could have"
"5929"	"made a grand to-do over it, and it would have had a good effect"
"5930"	"with the nation; but no, he wouldn’t hear of such a thing.  He had"
"5931"	"something like a religious passion for royal grant; he seemed to"
"5932"	"look upon it as a sort of sacred swag, and one could not irritate"
"5933"	"him in any way so quickly and so surely as by an attack upon that"
"5934"	"venerable institution.  If I ventured to cautiously hint that there"
"5935"	"was not another respectable family in England that would humble"
"5936"	"itself to hold out the hat--however, that is as far as I ever got;"
"5937"	"he always cut me short there, and peremptorily, too."
"5938"	"But I believed I saw my chance at last.  I would form this crack"
"5939"	"regiment out of officers alone--not a single private.  Half of it"
"5940"	"should consist of nobles, who should fill all the places up to"
"5941"	"Major-General, and serve gratis and pay their own expenses; and"
"5942"	"they would be glad to do this when they should learn that the rest"
"5943"	"of the regiment would consist exclusively of princes of the blood."
"5944"	"These princes of the blood should range in rank from Lieutenant-General"
"5945"	"up to Field Marshal, and be gorgeously salaried and equipped and"
"5946"	"fed by the state.  Moreover--and this was the master stroke"
"5947"	"--it should be decreed that these princely grandees should be always"
"5948"	"addressed by a stunningly gaudy and awe-compelling title (which"
"5949"	"I would presently invent), and they and they only in all England"
"5950"	"should be so addressed.  Finally, all princes of the blood should"
"5951"	"have free choice; join that regiment, get that great title, and"
"5952"	"renounce the royal grant, or stay out and receive a grant.  Neatest"
"5953"	"touch of all: unborn but imminent princes of the blood could be"
"5954"	"_born_ into the regiment, and start fair, with good wages and a"
"5955"	"permanent situation, upon due notice from the parents."
"5956"	"All the boys would join, I was sure of that; so, all existing"
"5957"	"grants would be relinquished; that the newly born would always"
"5958"	"join was equally certain.  Within sixty days that quaint and"
"5959"	"bizarre anomaly, the Royal Grant, would cease to be a living fact,"
"5960"	"and take its place among the curiosities of the past."
"5961"	"CHAPTER XXVI"
"5962"	"THE FIRST NEWSPAPER"
"5963"	"When I told the king I was going out disguised as a petty freeman"
"5964"	"to scour the country and familiarize myself with the humbler life"
"5965"	"of the people, he was all afire with the novelty of the thing"
"5966"	"in a minute, and was bound to take a chance in the adventure"
"5967"	"himself--nothing should stop him--he would drop everything and"
"5968"	"go along--it was the prettiest idea he had run across for many"
"5969"	"a day.  He wanted to glide out the back way and start at once;"
"5970"	"but I showed him that that wouldn’t answer.  You see, he was billed"
"5971"	"for the king’s-evil--to touch for it, I mean--and it wouldn’t be"
"5972"	"right to disappoint the house and it wouldn’t make a delay worth"
"5973"	"considering, anyway, it was only a one-night stand.  And I thought"
"5974"	"he ought to tell the queen he was going away.  He clouded up at"
"5975"	"that and looked sad.  I was sorry I had spoken, especially when"
"5976"	"he said mournfully:"
"5977"	"“Thou forgettest that Launcelot is here; and where Launcelot is,"
"5978"	"she noteth not the going forth of the king, nor what day he returneth.”"
"5979"	"Of course, I changed the Subject.  Yes, Guenever was beautiful,"
"5980"	"it is true, but take her all around she was pretty slack.  I never"
"5981"	"meddled in these matters, they weren’t my affair, but I did hate"
"5982"	"to see the way things were going on, and I don’t mind saying that"
"5983"	"much.  Many’s the time she had asked me, “Sir Boss, hast seen"
"5984"	"Sir Launcelot about?” but if ever she went fretting around for"
"5985"	"the king I didn’t happen to be around at the time."
"5986"	"There was a very good lay-out for the king’s-evil business--very"
"5987"	"tidy and creditable.  The king sat under a canopy of state; about"
"5988"	"him were clustered a large body of the clergy in full canonicals."
"5989"	"Conspicuous, both for location and personal outfit, stood Marinel,"
"5990"	"a hermit of the quack-doctor species, to introduce the sick.  All"
"5991"	"abroad over the spacious floor, and clear down to the doors,"
"5992"	"in a thick jumble, lay or sat the scrofulous, under a strong light."
"5993"	"It was as good as a tableau; in fact, it had all the look of being"
"5994"	"gotten up for that, though it wasn’t.  There were eight hundred"
"5995"	"sick people present.  The work was slow; it lacked the interest"
"5996"	"of novelty for me, because I had seen the ceremonies before;"
"5997"	"the thing soon became tedious, but the proprieties required me"
"5998"	"to stick it out.  The doctor was there for the reason that in all"
"5999"	"such crowds there were many people who only imagined something"
"6000"	"was the matter with them, and many who were consciously sound"
"6001"	"but wanted the immortal honor of fleshly contact with a king, and"
"6002"	"yet others who pretended to illness in order to get the piece of"
"6003"	"coin that went with the touch.  Up to this time this coin had been"
"6004"	"a wee little gold piece worth about a third of a dollar.  When you"
"6005"	"consider how much that amount of money would buy, in that age"
"6006"	"and country, and how usual it was to be scrofulous, when not dead,"
"6007"	"you would understand that the annual king’s-evil appropriation was"
"6008"	"just the River and Harbor bill of that government for the grip it"
"6009"	"took on the treasury and the chance it afforded for skinning the"
