"8442"	"seem to get over that seven dollars.  Well, it stunned me so, when"
"8443"	"I first found it out, that I couldn’t believe it; it didn’t seem"
"8444"	"natural.  But as soon as my mental sight cleared and I got a right"
"8445"	"focus on it, I saw I was mistaken; it _was_ natural.  For this"
"8446"	"reason: a king is a mere artificiality, and so a king’s feelings,"
"8447"	"like the impulses of an automatic doll, are mere artificialities;"
"8448"	"but as a man, he is a reality, and his feelings, as a man, are"
"8449"	"real, not phantoms.  It shames the average man to be valued below"
"8450"	"his own estimate of his worth, and the king certainly wasn’t"
"8451"	"anything more than an average man, if he was up that high."
"8452"	"Confound him, he wearied me with arguments to show that in anything"
"8453"	"like a fair market he would have fetched twenty-five dollars,"
"8454"	"sure--a thing which was plainly nonsense, and full or the baldest"
"8455"	"conceit; I wasn’t worth it myself.  But it was tender ground for"
"8456"	"me to argue on.  In fact, I had to simply shirk argument and do"
"8457"	"the diplomatic instead.  I had to throw conscience aside, and"
"8458"	"brazenly concede that he ought to have brought twenty-five dollars;"
"8459"	"whereas I was quite well aware that in all the ages, the world had"
"8460"	"never seen a king that was worth half the money, and during the"
"8461"	"next thirteen centuries wouldn’t see one that was worth the fourth"
"8462"	"of it.  Yes, he tired me.  If he began to talk about the crops;"
"8463"	"or about the recent weather; or about the condition of politics;"
"8464"	"or about dogs, or cats, or morals, or theology--no matter what"
"8465"	"--I sighed, for I knew what was coming; he was going to get out of it"
"8466"	"a palliation of that tiresome seven-dollar sale.  Wherever we"
"8467"	"halted where there was a crowd, he would give me a look which"
"8468"	"said plainly: “if that thing could be tried over again now, with"
"8469"	"this kind of folk, you would see a different result.”  Well, when"
"8470"	"he was first sold, it secretly tickled me to see him go for seven"
"8471"	"dollars; but before he was done with his sweating and worrying"
"8472"	"I wished he had fetched a hundred.  The thing never got a chance"
"8473"	"to die, for every day, at one place or another, possible purchasers"
"8474"	"looked us over, and, as often as any other way, their comment on"
"8475"	"the king was something like this:"
"8476"	"“Here’s a two-dollar-and-a-half chump with a thirty-dollar style."
"8477"	"Pity but style was marketable.”"
"8478"	"At last this sort of remark produced an evil result.  Our owner"
"8479"	"was a practical person and he perceived that this defect must be"
"8480"	"mended if he hoped to find a purchaser for the king.  So he went"
"8481"	"to work to take the style out of his sacred majesty.  I could have"
"8482"	"given the man some valuable advice, but I didn’t; you mustn’t"
"8483"	"volunteer advice to a slave-driver unless you want to damage"
"8484"	"the cause you are arguing for.  I had found it a sufficiently"
"8485"	"difficult job to reduce the king’s style to a peasant’s style,"
"8486"	"even when he was a willing and anxious pupil; now then, to undertake"
"8487"	"to reduce the king’s style to a slave’s style--and by force--go to!"
"8488"	"it was a stately contract.  Never mind the details--it will save me"
"8489"	"trouble to let you imagine them.  I will only remark that at the"
"8490"	"end of a week there was plenty of evidence that lash and club"
"8491"	"and fist had done their work well; the king’s body was a sight"
"8492"	"to see--and to weep over; but his spirit?--why, it wasn’t even"
"8493"	"phased.  Even that dull clod of a slave-driver was able to see"
"8494"	"that there can be such a thing as a slave who will remain a man"
"8495"	"till he dies; whose bones you can break, but whose manhood you"
"8496"	"can’t.  This man found that from his first effort down to his"
"8497"	"latest, he couldn’t ever come within reach of the king, but the"
"8498"	"king was ready to plunge for him, and did it.  So he gave up"
"8499"	"at last, and left the king in possession of his style unimpaired."
"8500"	"The fact is, the king was a good deal more than a king, he was"
"8501"	"a man; and when a man is a man, you can’t knock it out of him."
"8502"	"We had a rough time for a month, tramping to and fro in the earth,"
"8503"	"and suffering.  And what Englishman was the most interested in"
"8504"	"the slavery question by that time?  His grace the king!  Yes; from"
"8505"	"being the most indifferent, he was become the most interested."
"8506"	"He was become the bitterest hater of the institution I had ever"
"8507"	"heard talk.  And so I ventured to ask once more a question which"
"8508"	"I had asked years before and had gotten such a sharp answer that"
"8509"	"I had not thought it prudent to meddle in the matter further."
"8510"	"Would he abolish slavery?"
"8511"	"His answer was as sharp as before, but it was music this time;"
"8512"	"I shouldn’t ever wish to hear pleasanter, though the profanity"
"8513"	"was not good, being awkwardly put together, and with the crash-word"
"8514"	"almost in the middle instead of at the end, where, of course, it"
"8515"	"ought to have been."
"8516"	"I was ready and willing to get free now; I hadn’t wanted to get"
"8517"	"free any sooner.  No, I cannot quite say that.  I had wanted to,"
"8518"	"but I had not been willing to take desperate chances, and had"
"8519"	"always dissuaded the king from them.  But now--ah, it was a new"
"8520"	"atmosphere!  Liberty would be worth any cost that might be put"
"8521"	"upon it now.  I set about a plan, and was straightway charmed"
"8522"	"with it.  It would require time, yes, and patience, too, a great"
"8523"	"deal of both.  One could invent quicker ways, and fully as sure"
"8524"	"ones; but none that would be as picturesque as this; none that"
"8525"	"could be made so dramatic.  And so I was not going to give this"
"8526"	"one up.  It might delay us months, but no matter, I would carry"
"8527"	"it out or break something."
"8528"	"Now and then we had an adventure.  One night we were overtaken"
"8529"	"by a snow-storm while still a mile from the village we were making"
"8530"	"for.  Almost instantly we were shut up as in a fog, the driving"
"8531"	"snow was so thick.  You couldn’t see a thing, and we were soon"
"8532"	"lost.  The slave-driver lashed us desperately, for he saw ruin"
"8533"	"before him, but his lashings only made matters worse, for they"
"8534"	"drove us further from the road and from likelihood of succor."
"8535"	"So we had to stop at last and slump down in the snow where we"
"8536"	"were.  The storm continued until toward midnight, then ceased."
"8537"	"By this time two of our feebler men and three of our women were"
"8538"	"dead, and others past moving and threatened with death.  Our"
"8539"	"master was nearly beside himself.  He stirred up the living, and"
"8540"	"made us stand, jump, slap ourselves, to restore our circulation,"
"8541"	"and he helped as well as he could with his whip."
"8542"	"Now came a diversion.  We heard shrieks and yells, and soon a"
"8543"	"woman came running and crying; and seeing our group, she flung"
"8544"	"herself into our midst and begged for protection.  A mob of people"
"8545"	"came tearing after her, some with torches, and they said she was a"
"8546"	"witch who had caused several cows to die by a strange disease,"
"8547"	"and practiced her arts by help of a devil in the form of a black"
"8548"	"cat.  This poor woman had been stoned until she hardly looked"
"8549"	"human, she was so battered and bloody.  The mob wanted to burn her."
"8550"	"Well, now, what do you suppose our master did?  When we closed"
"8551"	"around this poor creature to shelter her, he saw his chance.  He"
"8552"	"said, burn her here, or they shouldn’t have her at all.  Imagine"
"8553"	"that!  They were willing.  They fastened her to a post; they"
"8554"	"brought wood and piled it about her; they applied the torch while"
"8555"	"she shrieked and pleaded and strained her two young daughters"
"8556"	"to her breast; and our brute, with a heart solely for business,"
"8557"	"lashed us into position about the stake and warmed us into life"
"8558"	"and commercial value by the same fire which took away the innocent"
"8559"	"life of that poor harmless mother.  That was the sort of master we"
"8560"	"had.  I took _his_ number.  That snow-storm cost him nine of his"
"8561"	"flock; and he was more brutal to us than ever, after that, for"
"8562"	"many days together, he was so enraged over his loss."
"8563"	"We had adventures all along.  One day we ran into a procession."
"8564"	"And such a procession!  All the riffraff of the kingdom seemed"
"8565"	"to be comprehended in it; and all drunk at that.  In the van was"
"8566"	"a cart with a coffin in it, and on the coffin sat a comely young"
"8567"	"girl of about eighteen suckling a baby, which she squeezed to her"
"8568"	"breast in a passion of love every little while, and every little"
"8569"	"while wiped from its face the tears which her eyes rained down"
"8570"	"upon it; and always the foolish little thing smiled up at her,"
"8571"	"happy and content, kneading her breast with its dimpled fat hand,"
"8572"	"which she patted and fondled right over her breaking heart."
"8573"	"Men and women, boys and girls, trotted along beside or after"
"8574"	"the cart, hooting, shouting profane and ribald remarks, singing"
"8575"	"snatches of foul song, skipping, dancing--a very holiday of"
"8576"	"hellions, a sickening sight.  We had struck a suburb of London,"
"8577"	"outside the walls, and this was a sample of one sort of London"
"8578"	"society.  Our master secured a good place for us near the gallows."
"8579"	"A priest was in attendance, and he helped the girl climb up, and"
"8580"	"said comforting words to her, and made the under-sheriff provide"
"8581"	"a stool for her.  Then he stood there by her on the gallows, and"
"8582"	"for a moment looked down upon the mass of upturned faces at his"
"8583"	"feet, then out over the solid pavement of heads that stretched away"
"8584"	"on every side occupying the vacancies far and near, and then began"
"8585"	"to tell the story of the case.  And there was pity in his voice"
"8586"	"--how seldom a sound that was in that ignorant and savage land!"
"8587"	"I remember every detail of what he said, except the words he said"
"8588"	"it in; and so I change it into my own words:"
"8589"	"“Law is intended to mete out justice.  Sometimes it fails. This"
"8590"	"cannot be helped.  We can only grieve, and be resigned, and pray"
"8591"	"for the soul of him who falls unfairly by the arm of the law, and"
"8592"	"that his fellows may be few.  A law sends this poor young thing"
"8593"	"to death--and it is right.  But another law had placed her where"
"8594"	"she must commit her crime or starve with her child--and before God"
"8595"	"that law is responsible for both her crime and her ignominious death!"
"8596"	"“A little while ago this young thing, this child of eighteen years,"
"8597"	"was as happy a wife and mother as any in England; and her lips"
"8598"	"were blithe with song, which is the native speech of glad and"
"8599"	"innocent hearts.  Her young husband was as happy as she; for he was"
"8600"	"doing his whole duty, he worked early and late at his handicraft,"
"8601"	"his bread was honest bread well and fairly earned, he was prospering,"
"8602"	"he was furnishing shelter and sustenance to his family, he was"
"8603"	"adding his mite to the wealth of the nation.  By consent of a"
"8604"	"treacherous law, instant destruction fell upon this holy home and"
"8605"	"swept it away!  That young husband was waylaid and impressed,"
"8606"	"and sent to sea.  The wife knew nothing of it.  She sought him"
"8607"	"everywhere, she moved the hardest hearts with the supplications"
"8608"	"of her tears, the broken eloquence of her despair.  Weeks dragged"
"8609"	"by, she watching, waiting, hoping, her mind going slowly to wreck"
"8610"	"under the burden of her misery.  Little by little all her small"
"8611"	"possessions went for food.  When she could no longer pay her rent,"
"8612"	"they turned her out of doors.  She begged, while she had strength;"
"8613"	"when she was starving at last, and her milk failing, she stole a"
"8614"	"piece of linen cloth of the value of a fourth part of a cent,"
"8615"	"thinking to sell it and save her child.  But she was seen by the"
"8616"	"owner of the cloth.  She was put in jail and brought to trial."
"8617"	"The man testified to the facts.  A plea was made for her, and her"
"8618"	"sorrowful story was told in her behalf.  She spoke, too, by"
"8619"	"permission, and said she did steal the cloth, but that her mind"
"8620"	"was so disordered of late by trouble that when she was overborne"
"8621"	"with hunger all acts, criminal or other, swam meaningless through"
"8622"	"her brain and she knew nothing rightly, except that she was so"
"8623"	"hungry!  For a moment all were touched, and there was disposition"
"8624"	"to deal mercifully with her, seeing that she was so young and"
"8625"	"friendless, and her case so piteous, and the law that robbed her"
"8626"	"of her support to blame as being the first and only cause of her"
"8627"	"transgression; but the prosecuting officer replied that whereas"
"8628"	"these things were all true, and most pitiful as well, still there"
"8629"	"was much small theft in these days, and mistimed mercy here would"
"8630"	"be a danger to property--oh, my God, is there no property in ruined"
"8631"	"homes, and orphaned babes, and broken hearts that British law"
"8632"	"holds precious!--and so he must require sentence."
"8633"	"“When the judge put on his black cap, the owner of the stolen"
"8634"	"linen rose trembling up, his lip quivering, his face as gray as"
"8635"	"ashes; and when the awful words came, he cried out, ‘Oh, poor"
"8636"	"child, poor child, I did not know it was death!’ and fell as a"
"8637"	"tree falls.  When they lifted him up his reason was gone; before"
"8638"	"the sun was set, he had taken his own life.  A kindly man; a man"
"8639"	"whose heart was right, at bottom; add his murder to this that"
"8640"	"is to be now done here; and charge them both where they belong"
"8641"	"--to the rulers and the bitter laws of Britain.  The time is come, my"
"8642"	"child; let me pray over thee--not _for_ thee, dear abused poor heart"
"8643"	"and innocent, but for them that be guilty of thy ruin and death,"
"8644"	"who need it more.”"
"8645"	"After his prayer they put the noose around the young girl’s neck,"
"8646"	"and they had great trouble to adjust the knot under her ear,"
"8647"	"because she was devouring the baby all the time, wildly kissing it,"
"8648"	"and snatching it to her face and her breast, and drenching it"
"8649"	"with tears, and half moaning, half shrieking all the while, and the"
"8650"	"baby crowing, and laughing, and kicking its feet with delight over"
"8651"	"what it took for romp and play.  Even the hangman couldn’t stand it,"
"8652"	"but turned away.  When all was ready the priest gently pulled and"
"8653"	"tugged and forced the child out of the mother’s arms, and stepped"
"8654"	"quickly out of her reach; but she clasped her hands, and made a"
"8655"	"wild spring toward him, with a shriek; but the rope--and the"
"8656"	"under-sheriff--held her short.  Then she went on her knees and"
"8657"	"stretched out her hands and cried:"
"8658"	"“One more kiss--oh, my God, one more, one more,--it is the dying"
"8659"	"that begs it!”"
"8660"	"She got it; she almost smothered the little thing.  And when they"
"8661"	"got it away again, she cried out:"
"8662"	"“Oh, my child, my darling, it will die!  It has no home, it has"
"8663"	"no father, no friend, no mother--”"
"8664"	"“It has them all!” said that good priest.  “All these will I be"
"8665"	"to it till I die.”"
"8666"	"You should have seen her face then!  Gratitude?  Lord, what do"
"8667"	"you want with words to express that?  Words are only painted fire;"
"8668"	"a look is the fire itself.  She gave that look, and carried it away"
"8669"	"to the treasury of heaven, where all things that are divine belong."
"8670"	"CHAPTER XXXVI"
"8671"	"AN ENCOUNTER IN THE DARK"
"8672"	"London--to a slave--was a sufficiently interesting place.  It was"
"8673"	"merely a great big village; and mainly mud and thatch.  The streets"
"8674"	"were muddy, crooked, unpaved.  The populace was an ever flocking"
"8675"	"and drifting swarm of rags, and splendors, of nodding plumes and"
"8676"	"shining armor.  The king had a palace there; he saw the outside"
"8677"	"of it.  It made him sigh; yes, and swear a little, in a poor"
"8678"	"juvenile sixth century way.  We saw knights and grandees whom"
"8679"	"we knew, but they didn’t know us in our rags and dirt and raw"
"8680"	"welts and bruises, and wouldn’t have recognized us if we had hailed"
"8681"	"them, nor stopped to answer, either, it being unlawful to speak"
"8682"	"with slaves on a chain.  Sandy passed within ten yards of me on"
"8683"	"a mule--hunting for me, I imagined.  But the thing which clean"
"8684"	"broke my heart was something which happened in front of our old"
"8685"	"barrack in a square, while we were enduring the spectacle of a man"
"8686"	"being boiled to death in oil for counterfeiting pennies.  It was"
"8687"	"the sight of a newsboy--and I couldn’t get at him!  Still, I had"
"8688"	"one comfort--here was proof that Clarence was still alive and"
"8689"	"banging away.  I meant to be with him before long; the thought was"
"8690"	"full of cheer."
"8691"	"I had one little glimpse of another thing, one day, which gave me"
"8692"	"a great uplift.  It was a wire stretching from housetop to housetop."
"8693"	"Telegraph or telephone, sure.  I did very much wish I had a little"
"8694"	"piece of it.  It was just what I needed, in order to carry out my"
"8695"	"project of escape.  My idea was to get loose some night, along with"
"8696"	"the king, then gag and bind our master, change clothes with him,"
"8697"	"batter him into the aspect of a stranger, hitch him to the slave-chain,"
"8698"	"assume possession of the property, march to Camelot, and--"
"8699"	"But you get my idea; you see what a stunning dramatic surprise"
"8700"	"I would wind up with at the palace.  It was all feasible, if"
"8701"	"I could only get hold of a slender piece of iron which I could"
"8702"	"shape into a lock-pick.  I could then undo the lumbering padlocks"
"8703"	"with which our chains were fastened, whenever I might choose."
"8704"	"But I never had any luck; no such thing ever happened to fall"
"8705"	"in my way.  However, my chance came at last.  A gentleman who"
"8706"	"had come twice before to dicker for me, without result, or indeed"
"8707"	"any approach to a result, came again.  I was far from expecting"
"8708"	"ever to belong to him, for the price asked for me from the time"
"8709"	"I was first enslaved was exorbitant, and always provoked either"
"8710"	"anger or derision, yet my master stuck stubbornly to it--twenty-two"
"8711"	"dollars.  He wouldn’t bate a cent.  The king was greatly admired,"
"8712"	"because of his grand physique, but his kingly style was against"
"8713"	"him, and he wasn’t salable; nobody wanted that kind of a slave."
"8714"	"I considered myself safe from parting from him because of my"
"8715"	"extravagant price.  No, I was not expecting to ever belong to"
"8716"	"this gentleman whom I have spoken of, but he had something which"
"8717"	"I expected would belong to me eventually, if he would but visit"
"8718"	"us often enough.  It was a steel thing with a long pin to it, with"
"8719"	"which his long cloth outside garment was fastened together in"
"8720"	"front.  There were three of them. He had disappointed me twice,"
"8721"	"because he did not come quite close enough to me to make my project"
"8722"	"entirely safe; but this time I succeeded; I captured the lower"
"8723"	"clasp of the three, and when he missed it he thought he had lost"
"8724"	"it on the way."
"8725"	"I had a chance to be glad about a minute, then straightway a chance"
"8726"	"to be sad again.  For when the purchase was about to fail, as usual,"
"8727"	"the master suddenly spoke up and said what would be worded thus"
"8728"	"--in modern English:"
"8729"	"“I’ll tell you what I’ll do.  I’m tired supporting these two for"
"8730"	"no good.  Give me twenty-two dollars for this one, and I’ll throw"
"8731"	"the other one in.”"
"8732"	"The king couldn’t get his breath, he was in such a fury.  He began"
"8733"	"to choke and gag, and meantime the master and the gentleman moved"
"8734"	"away discussing."
"8735"	"“An ye will keep the offer open--”"
"8736"	"“‘Tis open till the morrow at this hour.”"
"8737"	"“Then I will answer you at that time,” said the gentleman, and"
"8738"	"disappeared, the master following him."
"8739"	"I had a time of it to cool the king down, but I managed it."
"8740"	"I whispered in his ear, to this effect:"
"8741"	"“Your grace _will_ go for nothing, but after another fashion.  And"
"8742"	"so shall I.  To-night we shall both be free.”"
"8743"	"“Ah!  How is that?”"
"8744"	"“With this thing which I have stolen, I will unlock these locks"
"8745"	"and cast off these chains to-night.  When he comes about nine-thirty"
"8746"	"to inspect us for the night, we will seize him, gag him, batter"
"8747"	"him, and early in the morning we will march out of this town,"
"8748"	"proprietors of this caravan of slaves.”"
"8749"	"That was as far as I went, but the king was charmed and satisfied."
"8750"	"That evening we waited patiently for our fellow-slaves to get"
"8751"	"to sleep and signify it by the usual sign, for you must not take"
"8752"	"many chances on those poor fellows if you can avoid it.  It is"
"8753"	"best to keep your own secrets.  No doubt they fidgeted only about"
"8754"	"as usual, but it didn’t seem so to me.  It seemed to me that they"
"8755"	"were going to be forever getting down to their regular snoring."
"8756"	"As the time dragged on I got nervously afraid we shouldn’t have"
"8757"	"enough of it left for our needs; so I made several premature"
"8758"	"attempts, and merely delayed things by it; for I couldn’t seem"
"8759"	"to touch a padlock, there in the dark, without starting a rattle"
"8760"	"out of it which interrupted somebody’s sleep and made him turn"
"8761"	"over and wake some more of the gang."
"8762"	"But finally I did get my last iron off, and was a free man once"
"8763"	"more.  I took a good breath of relief, and reached for the king’s"
"8764"	"irons.  Too late! in comes the master, with a light in one hand"
"8765"	"and his heavy walking-staff in the other.  I snuggled close among"
"8766"	"the wallow of snorers, to conceal as nearly as possible that I was"
"8767"	"naked of irons; and I kept a sharp lookout and prepared to spring"
"8768"	"for my man the moment he should bend over me."
"8769"	"But he didn’t approach.  He stopped, gazed absently toward our"
"8770"	"dusky mass a minute, evidently thinking about something else;"
"8771"	"then set down his light, moved musingly toward the door, and before"
"8772"	"a body could imagine what he was going to do, he was out of the"
"8773"	"door and had closed it behind him."
"8774"	"“Quick!” said the king.  “Fetch him back!”"
"8775"	"Of course, it was the thing to do, and I was up and out in a"
"8776"	"moment.  But, dear me, there were no lamps in those days, and"
"8777"	"it was a dark night.  But I glimpsed a dim figure a few steps"
"8778"	"away.  I darted for it, threw myself upon it, and then there was"
"8779"	"a state of things and lively!  We fought and scuffled and struggled,"
"8780"	"and drew a crowd in no time.  They took an immense interest in"
"8781"	"the fight and encouraged us all they could, and, in fact, couldn’t"
"8782"	"have been pleasanter or more cordial if it had been their own"
"8783"	"fight.  Then a tremendous row broke out behind us, and as much"
"8784"	"as half of our audience left us, with a rush, to invest some"
"8785"	"sympathy in that.  Lanterns began to swing in all directions;"
"8786"	"it was the watch gathering from far and near.  Presently a halberd"
"8787"	"fell across my back, as a reminder, and I knew what it meant."
"8788"	"I was in custody.  So was my adversary.  We were marched off toward"
"8789"	"prison, one on each side of the watchman.  Here was disaster,"
"8790"	"here was a fine scheme gone to sudden destruction!  I tried to"
"8791"	"imagine what would happen when the master should discover that"
"8792"	"it was I who had been fighting him; and what would happen if they"
"8793"	"jailed us together in the general apartment for brawlers and petty"
"8794"	"law-breakers, as was the custom; and what might--"
"8795"	"Just then my antagonist turned his face around in my direction,"
"8796"	"the freckled light from the watchman’s tin lantern fell on it,"
"8797"	"and, by George, he was the wrong man!"
"8798"	"CHAPTER XXXVII"
"8799"	"AN AWFUL PREDICAMENT"
"8800"	"Sleep?  It was impossible.  It would naturally have been impossible"
"8801"	"in that noisome cavern of a jail, with its mangy crowd of drunken,"
"8802"	"quarrelsome, and song-singing rapscallions.  But the thing that"
"8803"	"made sleep all the more a thing not to be dreamed of, was my"
"8804"	"racking impatience to get out of this place and find out the whole"
"8805"	"size of what might have happened yonder in the slave-quarters"
"8806"	"in consequence of that intolerable miscarriage of mine."
"8807"	"It was a long night, but the morning got around at last.  I made"
"8808"	"a full and frank explanation to the court.  I said I was a slave,"
"8809"	"the property of the great Earl Grip, who had arrived just after"
"8810"	"dark at the Tabard inn in the village on the other side of the"
"8811"	"water, and had stopped there over night, by compulsion, he being"
"8812"	"taken deadly sick with a strange and sudden disorder.  I had been"
"8813"	"ordered to cross to the city in all haste and bring the best"
"8814"	"physician; I was doing my best; naturally I was running with all"
"8815"	"my might; the night was dark, I ran against this common person"
"8816"	"here, who seized me by the throat and began to pummel me, although"
"8817"	"I told him my errand, and implored him, for the sake of the great"
"8818"	"earl my master’s mortal peril--"
"8819"	"The common person interrupted and said it was a lie; and was going"
"8820"	"to explain how I rushed upon him and attacked him without a word--"
"8821"	"“Silence, sirrah!” from the court.  “Take him hence and give him"
"8822"	"a few stripes whereby to teach him how to treat the servant of"
"8823"	"a nobleman after a different fashion another time.  Go!”"
"8824"	"Then the court begged my pardon, and hoped I would not fail"
"8825"	"to tell his lordship it was in no wise the court’s fault that this"
"8826"	"high-handed thing had happened.  I said I would make it all right,"
"8827"	"and so took my leave.  Took it just in time, too; he was starting"
"8828"	"to ask me why I didn’t fetch out these facts the moment I was"
"8829"	"arrested.  I said I would if I had thought of it--which was true"
"8830"	"--but that I was so battered by that man that all my wit was knocked"
"8831"	"out of me--and so forth and so on, and got myself away, still"
"8832"	"mumbling.  I didn’t wait for breakfast.  No grass grew under my"
"8833"	"feet.  I was soon at the slave quarters.  Empty--everybody gone!"
"8834"	"That is, everybody except one body--the slave-master’s.  It lay"
"8835"	"there all battered to pulp; and all about were the evidences of"
"8836"	"a terrific fight.  There was a rude board coffin on a cart at"
"8837"	"the door, and workmen, assisted by the police, were thinning a"
"8838"	"road through the gaping crowd in order that they might bring it in."
"8839"	"I picked out a man humble enough in life to condescend to talk"
"8840"	"with one so shabby as I, and got his account of the matter."
"8841"	"“There were sixteen slaves here.  They rose against their master"
"8842"	"in the night, and thou seest how it ended.”"
"8843"	"“Yes.  How did it begin?”"
"8844"	"“There was no witness but the slaves.  They said the slave that"
"8845"	"was most valuable got free of his bonds and escaped in some strange"
"8846"	"way--by magic arts ‘twas thought, by reason that he had no key,"
"8847"	"and the locks were neither broke nor in any wise injured.  When"
"8848"	"the master discovered his loss, he was mad with despair, and threw"
"8849"	"himself upon his people with his heavy stick, who resisted and"
"8850"	"brake his back and in other and divers ways did give him hurts"
"8851"	"that brought him swiftly to his end.”"
"8852"	"“This is dreadful.  It will go hard with the slaves, no doubt,"
"8853"	"upon the trial.”"
"8854"	"“Marry, the trial is over.”"
"8855"	"“Over!”"
"8856"	"“Would they be a week, think you--and the matter so simple?  They"
"8857"	"were not the half of a quarter of an hour at it.”"
"8858"	"“Why, I don’t see how they could determine which were the guilty"
"8859"	"ones in so short a time.”"
"8860"	"“_Which_ ones?  Indeed, they considered not particulars like to that."
"8861"	"They condemned them in a body.  Wit ye not the law?--which men"
"8862"	"say the Romans left behind them here when they went--that if one"
"8863"	"slave killeth his master all the slaves of that man must die for it.”"
"8864"	"“True.  I had forgotten.  And when will these die?”"
"8865"	"“Belike within a four and twenty hours; albeit some say they will"
"8866"	"wait a pair of days more, if peradventure they may find the missing"
"8867"	"one meantime.”"
"8868"	"The missing one!  It made me feel uncomfortable."
"8869"	"“Is it likely they will find him?”"
"8870"	"“Before the day is spent--yes.  They seek him everywhere.  They"
"8871"	"stand at the gates of the town, with certain of the slaves who"
"8872"	"will discover him to them if he cometh, and none can pass out"
"8873"	"but he will be first examined.”"
"8874"	"“Might one see the place where the rest are confined?”"
"8875"	"“The outside of it--yes.  The inside of it--but ye will not want"
"8876"	"to see that.”"
"8877"	"I took the address of that prison for future reference and then"
"8878"	"sauntered off.  At the first second-hand clothing shop I came to,"
"8879"	"up a back street, I got a rough rig suitable for a common seaman"
"8880"	"who might be going on a cold voyage, and bound up my face with"
"8881"	"a liberal bandage, saying I had a toothache.  This concealed my"
"8882"	"worst bruises.  It was a transformation.  I no longer resembled my"
"8883"	"former self.  Then I struck out for that wire, found it and"
"8884"	"followed it to its den.  It was a little room over a butcher’s"
"8885"	"shop--which meant that business wasn’t very brisk in the telegraphic"
"8886"	"line.  The young chap in charge was drowsing at his table.  I locked"
"8887"	"the door and put the vast key in my bosom.  This alarmed the young"
"8888"	"fellow, and he was going to make a noise; but I said:"
"8889"	"“Save your wind; if you open your mouth you are dead, sure.  Tackle"
"8890"	"your instrument.  Lively, now!  Call Camelot.”"
"8891"	"“This doth amaze me!  How should such as you know aught of such"
"8892"	"matters as--”"
"8893"	"“Call Camelot!  I am a desperate man.  Call Camelot, or get away"
"8894"	"from the instrument and I will do it myself.”"
"8895"	"“What--you?”"
"8896"	"“Yes--certainly.  Stop gabbling.  Call the palace.”"
"8897"	"He made the call."
"8898"	"“Now, then, call Clarence.”"
"8899"	"“Clarence _who_?”"
"8900"	"“Never mind Clarence who.  Say you want Clarence; you’ll get"
"8901"	"an answer.”"
"8902"	"He did so.  We waited five nerve-straining minutes--ten minutes"
"8903"	"--how long it did seem!--and then came a click that was as familiar"
"8904"	"to me as a human voice; for Clarence had been my own pupil."
"8905"	"“Now, my lad, vacate!  They would have known _my_ touch, maybe,"
"8906"	"and so your call was surest; but I’m all right now.”"
"8907"	"He vacated the place and cocked his ear to listen--but it didn’t"
"8908"	"win.  I used a cipher.  I didn’t waste any time in sociabilities"
"8909"	"with Clarence, but squared away for business, straight-off--thus:"
"8910"	"“The king is here and in danger.  We were captured and brought"
"8911"	"here as slaves.  We should not be able to prove our identity"
"8912"	"--and the fact is, I am not in a position to try.  Send a telegram"
"8913"	"for the palace here which will carry conviction with it.”"
"8914"	"His answer came straight back:"
"8915"	"“They don’t know anything about the telegraph; they haven’t had"
"8916"	"any experience yet, the line to London is so new.  Better not"
"8917"	"venture that.  They might hang you.  Think up something else.”"
"8918"	"Might hang us!  Little he knew how closely he was crowding the"
"8919"	"facts.  I couldn’t think up anything for the moment.  Then an idea"
"8920"	"struck me, and I started it along:"
"8921"	"“Send five hundred picked knights with Launcelot in the lead; and"
"8922"	"send them on the jump.  Let them enter by the southwest gate, and"
"8923"	"look out for the man with a white cloth around his right arm.”"
"8924"	"The answer was prompt:"
"8925"	"“They shall start in half an hour.”"
"8926"	"“All right, Clarence; now tell this lad here that I’m a friend"
"8927"	"of yours and a dead-head; and that he must be discreet and say"
"8928"	"nothing about this visit of mine.”"
"8929"	"The instrument began to talk to the youth and I hurried away."
"8930"	"I fell to ciphering.  In half an hour it would be nine o’clock."
"8931"	"Knights and horses in heavy armor couldn’t travel very fast."
"8932"	"These would make the best time they could, and now that the ground"
"8933"	"was in good condition, and no snow or mud, they would probably"
"8934"	"make a seven-mile gait; they would have to change horses a couple"
"8935"	"of times; they would arrive about six, or a little after; it would"
"8936"	"still be plenty light enough; they would see the white cloth which"
"8937"	"I should tie around my right arm, and I would take command.  We"
"8938"	"would surround that prison and have the king out in no time."
"8939"	"It would be showy and picturesque enough, all things considered,"
"8940"	"though I would have preferred noonday, on account of the more"
"8941"	"theatrical aspect the thing would have."
"8942"	"Now, then, in order to increase the strings to my bow, I thought"
"8943"	"I would look up some of those people whom I had formerly recognized,"
"8944"	"and make myself known.  That would help us out of our scrape,"
"8945"	"without the knights.  But I must proceed cautiously, for it was"
"8946"	"a risky business.  I must get into sumptuous raiment, and it"
"8947"	"wouldn’t do to run and jump into it.  No, I must work up to it"
"8948"	"by degrees, buying suit after suit of clothes, in shops wide apart,"
"8949"	"and getting a little finer article with each change, until I should"
"8950"	"finally reach silk and velvet, and be ready for my project.  So"
"8951"	"I started."
"8952"	"But the scheme fell through like scat!  The first corner I turned,"
"8953"	"I came plump upon one of our slaves, snooping around with a watchman."
"8954"	"I coughed at the moment, and he gave me a sudden look that bit right"
"8955"	"into my marrow.  I judge he thought he had heard that cough before."
"8956"	"I turned immediately into a shop and worked along down the counter,"
"8957"	"pricing things and watching out of the corner of my eye.  Those"
"8958"	"people had stopped, and were talking together and looking in at"
"8959"	"the door.  I made up my mind to get out the back way, if there"
"8960"	"was a back way, and I asked the shopwoman if I could step out"
"8961"	"there and look for the escaped slave, who was believed to be in"
"8962"	"hiding back there somewhere, and said I was an officer in disguise,"
"8963"	"and my pard was yonder at the door with one of the murderers in"
"8964"	"charge, and would she be good enough to step there and tell him"
"8965"	"he needn’t wait, but had better go at once to the further end of"
"8966"	"the back alley and be ready to head him off when I rousted him out."
"8967"	"She was blazing with eagerness to see one of those already celebrated"
"8968"	"murderers, and she started on the errand at once.  I slipped out"
"8969"	"the back way, locked the door behind me, put the key in my pocket"
"8970"	"and started off, chuckling to myself and comfortable."
"8971"	"Well, I had gone and spoiled it again, made another mistake."
"8972"	"A double one, in fact.  There were plenty of ways to get rid of"
"8973"	"that officer by some simple and plausible device, but no, I must"
"8974"	"pick out a picturesque one; it is the crying defect of my character."
"8975"	"And then, I had ordered my procedure upon what the officer, being"
"8976"	"human, would _naturally_ do; whereas when you are least expecting it,"
"8977"	"a man will now and then go and do the very thing which it’s _not_"
"8978"	"natural for him to do.  The natural thing for the officer to do,"
"8979"	"in this case, was to follow straight on my heels; he would find"
"8980"	"a stout oaken door, securely locked, between him and me; before"
"8981"	"he could break it down, I should be far away and engaged in slipping"
"8982"	"into a succession of baffling disguises which would soon get me"
"8983"	"into a sort of raiment which was a surer protection from meddling"
"8984"	"law-dogs in Britain than any amount of mere innocence and purity"
"8985"	"of character.  But instead of doing the natural thing, the officer"
"8986"	"took me at my word, and followed my instructions.  And so, as I"
"8987"	"came trotting out of that cul de sac, full of satisfaction with my"
"8988"	"own cleverness, he turned the corner and I walked right into his"
"8989"	"handcuffs.  If I had known it was a cul de sac--however, there"
"8990"	"isn’t any excusing a blunder like that, let it go.  Charge it up"
"8991"	"to profit and loss."
"8992"	"Of course, I was indignant, and swore I had just come ashore from"
"8993"	"a long voyage, and all that sort of thing--just to see, you know,"
"8994"	"if it would deceive that slave.  But it didn’t.  He knew me.  Then"
"8995"	"I reproached him for betraying me.  He was more surprised than"
"8996"	"hurt.  He stretched his eyes wide, and said:"
"8997"	"“What, wouldst have me let thee, of all men, escape and not hang"
"8998"	"with us, when thou’rt the very _cause_ of our hanging?  Go to!”"
"8999"	"“Go to” was their way of saying “I should smile!” or “I like that!”"
"9000"	" Queer talkers, those people."
"9001"	"Well, there was a sort of bastard justice in his view of the case,"
"9002"	"and so I dropped the matter.  When you can’t cure a disaster by"
"9003"	"argument, what is the use to argue?  It isn’t my way.  So I only said:"
"9004"	"“You’re not going to be hanged.  None of us are.”"
"9005"	"Both men laughed, and the slave said:"
"9006"	"“Ye have not ranked as a fool--before.  You might better keep"
"9007"	"your reputation, seeing the strain would not be for long.”"
"9008"	"“It will stand it, I reckon.  Before to-morrow we shall be out"
"9009"	"of prison, and free to go where we will, besides.”"
"9010"	"The witty officer lifted at his left ear with his thumb, made"
"9011"	"a rasping noise in his throat, and said:"
"9012"	"“Out of prison--yes--ye say true.  And free likewise to go where"
"9013"	"ye will, so ye wander not out of his grace the Devil’s sultry realm.”"
"9014"	"I kept my temper, and said, indifferently:"
"9015"	"“Now I suppose you really think we are going to hang within"
"9016"	"a day or two.”"
"9017"	"“I thought it not many minutes ago, for so the thing was decided"
"9018"	"and proclaimed.”"
"9019"	"“Ah, then you’ve changed your mind, is that it?”"
"9020"	"“Even that.  I only _thought_, then; I _know_, now.”"
"9021"	"I felt sarcastical, so I said:"
"9022"	"“Oh, sapient servant of the law, condescend to tell us, then,"
"9023"	"what you _know_.”"
"9024"	"“That ye will all be hanged _to-day_, at mid-afternoon!  Oho! that"
"9025"	"shot hit home!  Lean upon me.”"
"9026"	"The fact is I did need to lean upon somebody.  My knights couldn’t"
"9027"	"arrive in time.  They would be as much as three hours too late."
"9028"	"Nothing in the world could save the King of England; nor me, which"
"9029"	"was more important.  More important, not merely to me, but to"
"9030"	"the nation--the only nation on earth standing ready to blossom"
"9031"	"into civilization.  I was sick.  I said no more, there wasn’t"
"9032"	"anything to say.  I knew what the man meant; that if the missing"
"9033"	"slave was found, the postponement would be revoked, the execution"
"9034"	"take place to-day.  Well, the missing slave was found."
"9035"	"CHAPTER XXXVIII"
"9036"	"SIR LAUNCELOT AND KNIGHTS TO THE RESCUE"
"9037"	"Nearing four in the afternoon.  The scene was just outside the"
"9038"	"walls of London.  A cool, comfortable, superb day, with a brilliant"
"9039"	"sun; the kind of day to make one want to live, not die.  The"
"9040"	"multitude was prodigious and far-reaching; and yet we fifteen"
"9041"	"poor devils hadn’t a friend in it.  There was something painful"
"9042"	"in that thought, look at it how you might.  There we sat, on our"
"9043"	"tall scaffold, the butt of the hate and mockery of all those"
"9044"	"enemies.  We were being made a holiday spectacle.  They had built"
"9045"	"a sort of grand stand for the nobility and gentry, and these were"
"9046"	"there in full force, with their ladies.  We recognized a good"
"9047"	"many of them."
"9048"	"The crowd got a brief and unexpected dash of diversion out of"
"9049"	"the king.  The moment we were freed of our bonds he sprang up,"
"9050"	"in his fantastic rags, with face bruised out of all recognition, and"
"9051"	"proclaimed himself Arthur, King of Britain, and denounced the"
"9052"	"awful penalties of treason upon every soul there present if hair"
"9053"	"of his sacred head were touched.  It startled and surprised him"
"9054"	"to hear them break into a vast roar of laughter.  It wounded his"
"9055"	"dignity, and he locked himself up in silence.  Then, although"
"9056"	"the crowd begged him to go on, and tried to provoke him to it"
"9057"	"by catcalls, jeers, and shouts of:"
"9058"	"“Let him speak!  The king!  The king! his humble subjects hunger"
"9059"	"and thirst for words of wisdom out of the mouth of their master"
"9060"	"his Serene and Sacred Raggedness!”"
"9061"	"But it went for nothing.  He put on all his majesty and sat under"
"9062"	"this rain of contempt and insult unmoved.  He certainly was great"
"9063"	"in his way.  Absently, I had taken off my white bandage and wound"
"9064"	"it about my right arm.  When the crowd noticed this, they began"
"9065"	"upon me.  They said:"
"9066"	"“Doubtless this sailor-man is his minister--observe his costly"
"9067"	"badge of office!”"
"9068"	"I let them go on until they got tired, and then I said:"
"9069"	"“Yes, I am his minister, The Boss; and to-morrow you will hear"
"9070"	"that from Camelot which--”"
"9071"	"I got no further.  They drowned me out with joyous derision.  But"
"9072"	"presently there was silence; for the sheriffs of London, in their"
"9073"	"official robes, with their subordinates, began to make a stir which"
"9074"	"indicated that business was about to begin.  In the hush which"
"9075"	"followed, our crime was recited, the death warrant read, then"
"9076"	"everybody uncovered while a priest uttered a prayer."
"9077"	"Then a slave was blindfolded; the hangman unslung his rope.  There"
"9078"	"lay the smooth road below us, we upon one side of it, the banked"
"9079"	"multitude wailing its other side--a good clear road, and kept free"
"9080"	"by the police--how good it would be to see my five hundred horsemen"
"9081"	"come tearing down it!  But no, it was out of the possibilities."
"9082"	"I followed its receding thread out into the distance--not a horseman"
"9083"	"on it, or sign of one."
"9084"	"There was a jerk, and the slave hung dangling; dangling and hideously"
"9085"	"squirming, for his limbs were not tied."
"9086"	"A second rope was unslung, in a moment another slave was dangling."
"9087"	"In a minute a third slave was struggling in the air.  It was"
"9088"	"dreadful.  I turned away my head a moment, and when I turned back"
"9089"	"I missed the king!  They were blindfolding him!  I was paralyzed;"
"9090"	"I couldn’t move, I was choking, my tongue was petrified.  They"
"9091"	"finished blindfolding him, they led him under the rope.  I couldn’t"
"9092"	"shake off that clinging impotence.  But when I saw them put the"
"9093"	"noose around his neck, then everything let go in me and I made"
"9094"	"a spring to the rescue--and as I made it I shot one more glance"
"9095"	"abroad--by George! here they came, a-tilting!--five hundred mailed"
"9096"	"and belted knights on bicycles!"
"9097"	"The grandest sight that ever was seen.  Lord, how the plumes"
"9098"	"streamed, how the sun flamed and flashed from the endless procession"
"9099"	"of webby wheels!"
"9100"	"I waved my right arm as Launcelot swept in--he recognized my rag"
"9101"	"--I tore away noose and bandage, and shouted:"
"9102"	"“On your knees, every rascal of you, and salute the king!  Who"
"9103"	"fails shall sup in hell to-night!”"
"9104"	"I always use that high style when I’m climaxing an effect.  Well,"
"9105"	"it was noble to see Launcelot and the boys swarm up onto that"
"9106"	"scaffold and heave sheriffs and such overboard.  And it was fine"
"9107"	"to see that astonished multitude go down on their knees and beg"
"9108"	"their lives of the king they had just been deriding and insulting."
"9109"	"And as he stood apart there, receiving this homage in rags,"
"9110"	"I thought to myself, well, really there is something peculiarly"
"9111"	"grand about the gait and bearing of a king, after all."
"9112"	"I was immensely satisfied.  Take the whole situation all around,"
"9113"	"it was one of the gaudiest effects I ever instigated."
"9114"	"And presently up comes Clarence, his own self! and winks, and"
"9115"	"says, very modernly:"
"9116"	"“Good deal of a surprise, wasn’t it?  I knew you’d like it.  I’ve"
"9117"	"had the boys practicing this long time, privately; and just hungry"
"9118"	"for a chance to show off.”"
"9119"	"CHAPTER XXXIX"
"9120"	"THE YANKEE’S FIGHT WITH THE KNIGHTS"
"9121"	"Home again, at Camelot.  A morning or two later I found the paper,"
"9122"	"damp from the press, by my plate at the breakfast table.  I turned"
"9123"	"to the advertising columns, knowing I should find something of"
"9124"	"personal interest to me there.  It was this:"
"9125"	"             DE PAR LE ROI."
"9126"	"   Know that the great lord and illus-"
"9127"	"   trious Kni8ht, SIR SAGRAMOR LE"
"9128"	"   DESIROUS having condescended to"
"9129"	"   meet the King’s Minister, Hank Mor-"
"9130"	"    gan, the which is surnamed The Boss,"
"9131"	"   for satisfgction of offence anciently given,"
"9132"	"   these wilL engage in the lists by"
"9133"	"   Camelot about the fourth hour of the"
"9134"	"   morning of the sixteenth day of this"
"9135"	"   next succeeding month. The battle"
"9136"	"   will be a l outrance, sith the said offence"
"9137"	"   was of a deadly sort, admitting of no"
"9138"	"   comPosition."
"9139"	"             DE PAR LE ROI"
"9140"	"Clarence’s editorial reference to this affair was to this effect:"
"9141"	"   It will be observed, by a gl7nce at our"
"9142"	"   advertising columns, that the commu-"
"9143"	"   nity is to be favored with a treat of un-"
"9144"	"   usual interest in the tournament line."
"9145"	"   The names of the artists are warrant of"
"9146"	"   good enterrainment. The box-office"
"9147"	"   will be open at noon of the 13th; ad-"
"9148"	"   mission 3 cents, reserved seatsh 5; pro-"
"9149"	"   ceeds to go to the hospital fund  The"
"9150"	"   royal pair and all the Court will be pres-"
"9151"	"   ent. With these exceptions, and the"
"9152"	"   press and the clergy, the free list is strict-"
"9153"	"   ly susPended. Parties are hereby warn-"
"9154"	"   ed against buying tickets of speculators;"
"9155"	"   they will not be good at the door."
"9156"	"   Everybody knows and likes The Boss,"
"9157"	"   everybody knows and likes Sir Sag.;"
"9158"	"   come, let us give the lads a good send-"
"9159"	"   off. ReMember, the proceeds go to a"
"9160"	"   great and free charity, and one whose"
"9161"	"   broad begevolence stretches out its help-"
"9162"	"   ing hand, warm with the blood of a lov-"
"9163"	"   ing heart, to all that suffer, regardless of"
"9164"	"   race, creed, condition or color--the"
"9165"	"   only charity yet established in the earth"
"9166"	"   which has no politico-religious stop-"
"9167"	"   cock on its compassion, but says Here"
"9168"	"   flows the stream, let ALL come and"
"9169"	"   drink! Turn out, all hands! fetch along"
"9170"	"   your dou3hnuts and your gum-drops"
"9171"	"   and have a good time. Pie for sale on"
"9172"	"   the grounds, and rocks to crack it with;"
"9173"	"   and ciRcus-lemonade--three drops of"
"9174"	"   lime juice to a barrel of water."
"9175"	"   N.B. This is the first tournament"
"9176"	"   under the new law, whidh allow each"
"9177"	"   combatant to use any weapon he may pre-"
"9178"	"   fer. You may want to make a note of that."
"9179"	"Up to the day set, there was no talk in all Britain of anything"
"9180"	"but this combat.  All other topics sank into insignificance and"
"9181"	"passed out of men’s thoughts and interest.  It was not because"
"9182"	"a tournament was a great matter, it was not because Sir Sagramor"
"9183"	"had found the Holy Grail, for he had not, but had failed; it was"
"9184"	"not because the second (official) personage in the kingdom was"
"9185"	"one of the duellists; no, all these features were commonplace."
"9186"	"Yet there was abundant reason for the extraordinary interest which"
"9187"	"this coming fight was creating.  It was born of the fact that all"
"9188"	"the nation knew that this was not to be a duel between mere men,"
"9189"	"so to speak, but a duel between two mighty magicians; a duel not"
"9190"	"of muscle but of mind, not of human skill but of superhuman art"
"9191"	"and craft; a final struggle for supremacy between the two master"
"9192"	"enchanters of the age.  It was realized that the most prodigious"
"9193"	"achievements of the most renowned knights could not be worthy"
"9194"	"of comparison with a spectacle like this; they could be but child’s"
"9195"	"play, contrasted with this mysterious and awful battle of the gods."
"9196"	"Yes, all the world knew it was going to be in reality a duel"
"9197"	"between Merlin and me, a measuring of his magic powers against"
"9198"	"mine.  It was known that Merlin had been busy whole days and nights"
"9199"	"together, imbuing Sir Sagramor’s arms and armor with supernal"
"9200"	"powers of offense and defense, and that he had procured for him"
"9201"	"from the spirits of the air a fleecy veil which would render the"
"9202"	"wearer invisible to his antagonist while still visible to other"
"9203"	"men.  Against Sir Sagramor, so weaponed and protected, a thousand"
"9204"	"knights could accomplish nothing; against him no known enchantments"
"9205"	"could prevail.  These facts were sure; regarding them there was"
"9206"	"no doubt, no reason for doubt.  There was but one question: might"
"9207"	"there be still other enchantments, _unknown_ to Merlin, which could"
"9208"	"render Sir Sagramor’s veil transparent to me, and make his enchanted"
"9209"	"mail vulnerable to my weapons?  This was the one thing to be"
"9210"	"decided in the lists.  Until then the world must remain in suspense."
"9211"	"So the world thought there was a vast matter at stake here, and"
"9212"	"the world was right, but it was not the one they had in their"
"9213"	"minds.  No, a far vaster one was upon the cast of this die:"
"9214"	"_the life of knight-errantry_.  I was a champion, it was true, but"
"9215"	"not the champion of the frivolous black arts, I was the champion"
"9216"	"of hard unsentimental common-sense and reason.  I was entering"
"9217"	"the lists to either destroy knight-errantry or be its victim."
"9218"	"Vast as the show-grounds were, there were no vacant spaces in them"
"9219"	"outside of the lists, at ten o’clock on the morning of the 16th."
"9220"	"The mammoth grand-stand was clothed in flags, streamers, and rich"
"9221"	"tapestries, and packed with several acres of small-fry tributary"
"9222"	"kings, their suites, and the British aristocracy; with our own"
"9223"	"royal gang in the chief place, and each and every individual"
"9224"	"a flashing prism of gaudy silks and velvets--well, I never saw"
"9225"	"anything to begin with it but a fight between an Upper Mississippi"
"9226"	"sunset and the aurora borealis.  The huge camp of beflagged and"
"9227"	"gay-colored tents at one end of the lists, with a stiff-standing"
"9228"	"sentinel at every door and a shining shield hanging by him for"
"9229"	"challenge, was another fine sight.  You see, every knight was"
"9230"	"there who had any ambition or any caste feeling; for my feeling"
"9231"	"toward their order was not much of a secret, and so here was their"
"9232"	"chance.  If I won my fight with Sir Sagramor, others would have"
"9233"	"the right to call me out as long as I might be willing to respond."
"9234"	"Down at our end there were but two tents; one for me, and another"
"9235"	"for my servants.  At the appointed hour the king made a sign, and"
"9236"	"the heralds, in their tabards, appeared and made proclamation,"
"9237"	"naming the combatants and stating the cause of quarrel.  There"
"9238"	"was a pause, then a ringing bugle-blast, which was the signal for"
"9239"	"us to come forth.  All the multitude caught their breath, and"
"9240"	"an eager curiosity flashed into every face."
"9241"	"Out from his tent rode great Sir Sagramor, an imposing tower"
"9242"	"of iron, stately and rigid, his huge spear standing upright in its"
"9243"	"socket and grasped in his strong hand, his grand horse’s face and"
"9244"	"breast cased in steel, his body clothed in rich trappings that"
"9245"	"almost dragged the ground--oh, a most noble picture.  A great"
"9246"	"shout went up, of welcome and admiration."
"9247"	"And then out I came.  But I didn’t get any shout.  There was"
"9248"	"a wondering and eloquent silence for a moment, then a great wave"
"9249"	"of laughter began to sweep along that human sea, but a warning"
"9250"	"bugle-blast cut its career short.  I was in the simplest and"
"9251"	"comfortablest of gymnast costumes--flesh-colored tights from neck"
"9252"	"to heel, with blue silk puffings about my loins, and bareheaded."
"9253"	"My horse was not above medium size, but he was alert, slender-limbed,"
"9254"	"muscled with watchsprings, and just a greyhound to go.  He was"
"9255"	"a beauty, glossy as silk, and naked as he was when he was born,"
"9256"	"except for bridle and ranger-saddle."
"9257"	"The iron tower and the gorgeous bedquilt came cumbrously but"
"9258"	"gracefully pirouetting down the lists, and we tripped lightly up"
"9259"	"to meet them.  We halted; the tower saluted, I responded; then"
"9260"	"we wheeled and rode side by side to the grand-stand and faced"
"9261"	"our king and queen, to whom we made obeisance.  The queen exclaimed:"
"9262"	"“Alack, Sir Boss, wilt fight naked, and without lance or sword or--”"
"9263"	"But the king checked her and made her understand, with a polite"
"9264"	"phrase or two, that this was none of her business.  The bugles"
"9265"	"rang again; and we separated and rode to the ends of the lists,"
"9266"	"and took position.  Now old Merlin stepped into view and cast"
"9267"	"a dainty web of gossamer threads over Sir Sagramor which turned"
"9268"	"him into Hamlet’s ghost; the king made a sign, the bugles blew,"
"9269"	"Sir Sagramor laid his great lance in rest, and the next moment here"
"9270"	"he came thundering down the course with his veil flying out behind,"
"9271"	"and I went whistling through the air like an arrow to meet him"
"9272"	"--cocking my ear the while, as if noting the invisible knight’s"
"9273"	"position and progress by hearing, not sight.  A chorus of encouraging"
"9274"	"shouts burst out for him, and one brave voice flung out a heartening"
"9275"	"word for me--said:"
"9276"	"“Go it, slim Jim!”"
"9277"	"It was an even bet that Clarence had procured that favor for me"
"9278"	"--and furnished the language, too.  When that formidable lance-point"
"9279"	"was within a yard and a half of my breast I twitched my horse aside"
"9280"	"without an effort, and the big knight swept by, scoring a blank."
"9281"	"I got plenty of applause that time.  We turned, braced up, and"
"9282"	"down we came again.  Another blank for the knight, a roar of"
"9283"	"applause for me.  This same thing was repeated once more; and"
"9284"	"it fetched such a whirlwind of applause that Sir Sagramor lost his"
"9285"	"temper, and at once changed his tactics and set himself the task"
"9286"	"of chasing me down.  Why, he hadn’t any show in the world at that;"
"9287"	"it was a game of tag, with all the advantage on my side; I whirled"
"9288"	"out of his path with ease whenever I chose, and once I slapped him"
"9289"	"on the back as I went to the rear.  Finally I took the chase into"
"9290"	"my own hands; and after that, turn, or twist, or do what he would,"
"9291"	"he was never able to get behind me again; he found himself always"
"9292"	"in front at the end of his maneuver.  So he gave up that business"
"9293"	"and retired to his end of the lists.  His temper was clear gone now,"
"9294"	"and he forgot himself and flung an insult at me which disposed"
"9295"	"of mine.  I slipped my lasso from the horn of my saddle, and"
"9296"	"grasped the coil in my right hand.  This time you should have seen"
"9297"	"him come!--it was a business trip, sure; by his gait there was"
"9298"	"blood in his eye.  I was sitting my horse at ease, and swinging"
"9299"	"the great loop of my lasso in wide circles about my head; the"
"9300"	"moment he was under way, I started for him; when the space between"
"9301"	"us had narrowed to forty feet, I sent the snaky spirals of the rope"
"9302"	"a-cleaving through the air, then darted aside and faced about and"
"9303"	"brought my trained animal to a halt with all his feet braced under"
"9304"	"him for a surge.  The next moment the rope sprang taut and yanked"
"9305"	"Sir Sagramor out of the saddle!  Great Scott, but there was"
"9306"	"a sensation!"
"9307"	"Unquestionably, the popular thing in this world is novelty.  These"
"9308"	"people had never seen anything of that cowboy business before,"
"9309"	"and it carried them clear off their feet with delight.  From all"
"9310"	"around and everywhere, the shout went up:"
"9311"	"“Encore! encore!”"
"9312"	"I wondered where they got the word, but there was no time to cipher"
"9313"	"on philological matters, because the whole knight-errantry hive"
"9314"	"was just humming now, and my prospect for trade couldn’t have"
"9315"	"been better.  The moment my lasso was released and Sir Sagramor"
"9316"	"had been assisted to his tent, I hauled in the slack, took my"
"9317"	"station and began to swing my loop around my head again.  I was"
"9318"	"sure to have use for it as soon as they could elect a successor"
"9319"	"for Sir Sagramor, and that couldn’t take long where there were"
"9320"	"so many hungry candidates.  Indeed, they elected one straight off"
"9321"	"--Sir Hervis de Revel."
"9322"	"_Bzz_!  Here he came, like a house afire; I dodged: he passed like"
"9323"	"a flash, with my horse-hair coils settling around his neck;"
"9324"	"a second or so later, _fst_! his saddle was empty."
"9325"	"I got another encore; and another, and another, and still another."
"9326"	"When I had snaked five men out, things began to look serious to"
"9327"	"the ironclads, and they stopped and consulted together.  As a"
"9328"	"result, they decided that it was time to waive etiquette and send"
"9329"	"their greatest and best against me.  To the astonishment of that"
"9330"	"little world, I lassoed Sir Lamorak de Galis, and after him"
"9331"	"Sir Galahad.  So you see there was simply nothing to be done now,"
"9332"	"but play their right bower--bring out the superbest of the superb,"
"9333"	"the mightiest of the mighty, the great Sir Launcelot himself!"
"9334"	"A proud moment for me?  I should think so.  Yonder was Arthur,"
"9335"	"King of Britain; yonder was Guenever; yes, and whole tribes of"
"9336"	"little provincial kings and kinglets; and in the tented camp yonder,"
"9337"	"renowned knights from many lands; and likewise the selectest body"
"9338"	"known to chivalry, the Knights of the Table Round, the most"
"9339"	"illustrious in Christendom; and biggest fact of all, the very sun"
"9340"	"of their shining system was yonder couching his lance, the focal"
"9341"	"point of forty thousand adoring eyes; and all by myself, here was"
"9342"	"I laying for him.  Across my mind flitted the dear image of a"
"9343"	"certain hello-girl of West Hartford, and I wished she could see"
"9344"	"me now.  In that moment, down came the Invincible, with the rush"
"9345"	"of a whirlwind--the courtly world rose to its feet and bent forward"
"9346"	"--the fateful coils went circling through the air, and before you"
"9347"	"could wink I was towing Sir Launcelot across the field on his"
"9348"	"back, and kissing my hand to the storm of waving kerchiefs and"
"9349"	"the thunder-crash of applause that greeted me!"
"9350"	"Said I to myself, as I coiled my lariat and hung it on my saddle-horn,"
"9351"	"and sat there drunk with glory, “The victory is perfect--no other"
"9352"	"will venture against me--knight-errantry is dead.”  Now imagine my"
"9353"	"astonishment--and everybody else’s, too--to hear the peculiar"
"9354"	"bugle-call which announces that another competitor is about to"
"9355"	"enter the lists!  There was a mystery here; I couldn’t account for"
"9356"	"this thing.  Next, I noticed Merlin gliding away from me; and then"
"9357"	"I noticed that my lasso was gone!  The old sleight-of-hand expert"
"9358"	"had stolen it, sure, and slipped it under his robe."
"9359"	"The bugle blew again.  I looked, and down came Sagramor riding"
"9360"	"again, with his dust brushed off and his veil nicely re-arranged."
"9361"	"I trotted up to meet him, and pretended to find him by the sound"
"9362"	"of his horse’s hoofs.  He said:"
"9363"	"“Thou’rt quick of ear, but it will not save thee from this!” and"
"9364"	"he touched the hilt of his great sword.  “An ye are not able to see"
"9365"	"it, because of the influence of the veil, know that it is no cumbrous"
"9366"	"lance, but a sword--and I ween ye will not be able to avoid it.”"
"9367"	"His visor was up; there was death in his smile.  I should never"
"9368"	"be able to dodge his sword, that was plain.  Somebody was going"
"9369"	"to die this time.  If he got the drop on me, I could name the"
"9370"	"corpse.  We rode forward together, and saluted the royalties."
"9371"	"This time the king was disturbed.  He said:"
"9372"	"“Where is thy strange weapon?”"
"9373"	"“It is stolen, sire.”"
"9374"	"“Hast another at hand?”"
"9375"	"“No, sire, I brought only the one.”"
"9376"	"Then Merlin mixed in:"
"9377"	"“He brought but the one because there was but the one to bring."
"9378"	"There exists none other but that one.  It belongeth to the king"
"9379"	"of the Demons of the Sea.  This man is a pretender, and ignorant,"
"9380"	"else he had known that that weapon can be used in but eight bouts"
"9381"	"only, and then it vanisheth away to its home under the sea.”"
"9382"	"“Then is he weaponless,” said the king.  “Sir Sagramore, ye will"
"9383"	"grant him leave to borrow.”"
"9384"	"“And I will lend!” said Sir Launcelot, limping up.  “He is as"
"9385"	"brave a knight of his hands as any that be on live, and he shall"
"9386"	"have mine.”"
"9387"	"He put his hand on his sword to draw it, but Sir Sagramor said:"
"9388"	"“Stay, it may not be.  He shall fight with his own weapons; it"
"9389"	"was his privilege to choose them and bring them.  If he has erred,"
"9390"	"on his head be it.”"
"9391"	"“Knight!” said the king.  “Thou’rt overwrought with passion; it"
"9392"	"disorders thy mind.  Wouldst kill a naked man?”"
"9393"	"“An he do it, he shall answer it to me,” said Sir Launcelot."
"9394"	"“I will answer it to any he that desireth!” retorted Sir Sagramor hotly."
"9395"	"Merlin broke in, rubbing his hands and smiling his lowdownest"
"9396"	"smile of malicious gratification:"
"9397"	"“‘Tis well said, right well said!  And ‘tis enough of parleying,"
"9398"	"let my lord the king deliver the battle signal.”"
"9399"	"The king had to yield.  The bugle made proclamation, and we turned"
"9400"	"apart and rode to our stations.  There we stood, a hundred yards"
"9401"	"apart, facing each other, rigid and motionless, like horsed statues."
"9402"	"And so we remained, in a soundless hush, as much as a full minute,"
"9403"	"everybody gazing, nobody stirring.  It seemed as if the king could"
"9404"	"not take heart to give the signal.  But at last he lifted his hand,"
"9405"	"the clear note of the bugle followed, Sir Sagramor’s long blade"
"9406"	"described a flashing curve in the air, and it was superb to see him"
"9407"	"come.  I sat still.  On he came.  I did not move.  People got so"
"9408"	"excited that they shouted to me:"
"9409"	"“Fly, fly!  Save thyself!  This is murther!”"
"9410"	"I never budged so much as an inch till that thundering apparition"
"9411"	"had got within fifteen paces of me; then I snatched a dragoon"
"9412"	"revolver out of my holster, there was a flash and a roar, and"
"9413"	"the revolver was back in the holster before anybody could tell"
"9414"	"what had happened."
"9415"	"Here was a riderless horse plunging by, and yonder lay Sir Sagramor,"
"9416"	"stone dead."
"9417"	"The people that ran to him were stricken dumb to find that the life"
"9418"	"was actually gone out of the man and no reason for it visible,"
"9419"	"no hurt upon his body, nothing like a wound.  There was a hole"
"9420"	"through the breast of his chain-mail, but they attached no importance"
"9421"	"to a little thing like that; and as a bullet wound there produces"
"9422"	"but little blood, none came in sight because of the clothing and"
"9423"	"swaddlings under the armor.  The body was dragged over to let"
"9424"	"the king and the swells look down upon it.  They were stupefied"
"9425"	"with astonishment naturally.  I was requested to come and explain"
"9426"	"the miracle.  But I remained in my tracks, like a statue, and said:"
"9427"	"“If it is a command, I will come, but my lord the king knows that"
"9428"	"I am where the laws of combat require me to remain while any desire"
"9429"	"to come against me.”"
"9430"	"I waited.  Nobody challenged.  Then I said:"
"9431"	"“If there are any who doubt that this field is well and fairly won,"
"9432"	"I do not wait for them to challenge me, I challenge them.”"
"9433"	"“It is a gallant offer,” said the king, “and well beseems you."
"9434"	"Whom will you name first?”"
"9435"	"“I name none, I challenge all!  Here I stand, and dare the chivalry"
"9436"	"of England to come against me--not by individuals, but in mass!”"
"9437"	"“What!” shouted a score of knights."
"9438"	"“You have heard the challenge.  Take it, or I proclaim you recreant"
"9439"	"knights and vanquished, every one!”"
"9440"	"It was a “bluff” you know.  At such a time it is sound judgment"
"9441"	"to put on a bold face and play your hand for a hundred times what"
"9442"	"it is worth; forty-nine times out of fifty nobody dares to “call,”"
"9443"	" and you rake in the chips.  But just this once--well, things looked"
"9444"	"squally!  In just no time, five hundred knights were scrambling"
"9445"	"into their saddles, and before you could wink a widely scattering"
"9446"	"drove were under way and clattering down upon me.  I snatched"
"9447"	"both revolvers from the holsters and began to measure distances"
"9448"	"and calculate chances."
"9449"	"Bang!  One saddle empty.  Bang! another one.  Bang--bang, and"
"9450"	"I bagged two.  Well, it was nip and tuck with us, and I knew it."
"9451"	"If I spent the eleventh shot without convincing these people,"
"9452"	"the twelfth man would kill me, sure.  And so I never did feel"
"9453"	"so happy as I did when my ninth downed its man and I detected"
"9454"	"the wavering in the crowd which is premonitory of panic.  An instant"
"9455"	"lost now could knock out my last chance.  But I didn’t lose it."
"9456"	"I raised both revolvers and pointed them--the halted host stood"
"9457"	"their ground just about one good square moment, then broke and fled."
"9458"	"The day was mine.  Knight-errantry was a doomed institution.  The"
"9459"	"march of civilization was begun.  How did I feel?  Ah, you never"
"9460"	"could imagine it."
"9461"	"And Brer Merlin?  His stock was flat again.  Somehow, every time"
"9462"	"the magic of fol-de-rol tried conclusions with the magic of science,"
"9463"	"the magic of fol-de-rol got left."
"9464"	"CHAPTER XL"
"9465"	"THREE YEARS LATER"
"9466"	"When I broke the back of knight-errantry that time, I no longer"
"9467"	"felt obliged to work in secret.  So, the very next day I exposed"
"9468"	"my hidden schools, my mines, and my vast system of clandestine"
"9469"	"factories and workshops to an astonished world.  That is to say,"
"9470"	"I exposed the nineteenth century to the inspection of the sixth."
"9471"	"Well, it is always a good plan to follow up an advantage promptly."
"9472"	"The knights were temporarily down, but if I would keep them so"
"9473"	"I must just simply paralyze them--nothing short of that would"
"9474"	"answer.  You see, I was “bluffing” that last time in the field;"
"9475"	"it would be natural for them to work around to that conclusion,"
"9476"	"if I gave them a chance.  So I must not give them time; and I didn’t."
"9477"	"I renewed my challenge, engraved it on brass, posted it up where"
"9478"	"any priest could read it to them, and also kept it standing in"
"9479"	"the advertising columns of the paper."
"9480"	"I not only renewed it, but added to its proportions.  I said,"
"9481"	"name the day, and I would take fifty assistants and stand up"
"9482"	"_against the massed chivalry of the whole earth and destroy it_."
"9483"	"I was not bluffing this time.  I meant what I said; I could do"
"9484"	"what I promised.  There wasn’t any way to misunderstand the language"
"9485"	"of that challenge.  Even the dullest of the chivalry perceived"
"9486"	"that this was a plain case of “put up, or shut up.”  They were"
"9487"	"wise and did the latter.  In all the next three years they gave"
"9488"	"me no trouble worth mentioning."
"9489"	"Consider the three years sped.  Now look around on England.  A happy"
"9490"	"and prosperous country, and strangely altered.  Schools everywhere,"
"9491"	"and several colleges; a number of pretty good newspapers.  Even"
"9492"	"authorship was taking a start; Sir Dinadan the Humorist was first"
"9493"	"in the field, with a volume of gray-headed jokes which I had been"
"9494"	"familiar with during thirteen centuries.  If he had left out that"
"9495"	"old rancid one about the lecturer I wouldn’t have said anything;"
"9496"	"but I couldn’t stand that one.  I suppressed the book and hanged"
"9497"	"the author."
"9498"	"Slavery was dead and gone; all men were equal before the law;"
"9499"	"taxation had been equalized.  The telegraph, the telephone, the"
"9500"	"phonograph, the typewriter, the sewing-machine, and all the thousand"
"9501"	"willing and handy servants of steam and electricity were working"
"9502"	"their way into favor.  We had a steamboat or two on the Thames,"
"9503"	"we had steam warships, and the beginnings of a steam commercial"
"9504"	"marine; I was getting ready to send out an expedition to discover"
"9505"	"America."
"9506"	"We were building several lines of railway, and our line from"
"9507"	"Camelot to London was already finished and in operation.  I was"
"9508"	"shrewd enough to make all offices connected with the passenger"
"9509"	"service places of high and distinguished honor.  My idea was"
"9510"	"to attract the chivalry and nobility, and make them useful and keep"
"9511"	"them out of mischief.  The plan worked very well, the competition"
"9512"	"for the places was hot.  The conductor of the 4.33 express was"
"9513"	"a duke; there wasn’t a passenger conductor on the line below"
"9514"	"the degree of earl.  They were good men, every one, but they had"
"9515"	"two defects which I couldn’t cure, and so had to wink at: they"
"9516"	"wouldn’t lay aside their armor, and they would “knock down” fare"
"9517"	"--I mean rob the company."
"9518"	"There was hardly a knight in all the land who wasn’t in some useful"
"9519"	"employment.  They were going from end to end of the country in all"
"9520"	"manner of useful missionary capacities; their penchant for wandering,"
"9521"	"and their experience in it, made them altogether the most effective"
"9522"	"spreaders of civilization we had.  They went clothed in steel and"
"9523"	"equipped with sword and lance and battle-axe, and if they couldn’t"
"9524"	"persuade a person to try a sewing-machine on the installment plan,"
"9525"	"or a melodeon, or a barbed-wire fence, or a prohibition journal,"
"9526"	"or any of the other thousand and one things they canvassed for,"
"9527"	"they removed him and passed on."
"9528"	"I was very happy.  Things were working steadily toward a secretly"
"9529"	"longed-for point.  You see, I had two schemes in my head which"
"9530"	"were the vastest of all my projects.  The one was to overthrow the"
"9531"	"Catholic Church and set up the Protestant faith on its ruins"
"9532"	"--not as an Established Church, but a go-as-you-please one; and"
"9533"	"the other project was to get a decree issued by and by, commanding"
"9534"	"that upon Arthur’s death unlimited suffrage should be introduced,"
"9535"	"and given to men and women alike--at any rate to all men, wise"
"9536"	"or unwise, and to all mothers who at middle age should be found"
"9537"	"to know nearly as much as their sons at twenty-one.  Arthur was"
"9538"	"good for thirty years yet, he being about my own age--that is"
"9539"	"to say, forty--and I believed that in that time I could easily"
"9540"	"have the active part of the population of that day ready and eager"
"9541"	"for an event which should be the first of its kind in the history"
"9542"	"of the world--a rounded and complete governmental revolution"
"9543"	"without bloodshed.  The result to be a republic.  Well, I may"
"9544"	"as well confess, though I do feel ashamed when I think of it:"
"9545"	"I was beginning to have a base hankering to be its first president"
"9546"	"myself.  Yes, there was more or less human nature in me; I found"
"9547"	"that out."
"9548"	"Clarence was with me as concerned the revolution, but in a modified"
"9549"	"way.  His idea was a republic, without privileged orders, but with"
"9550"	"a hereditary royal family at the head of it instead of an elective"
"9551"	"chief magistrate.  He believed that no nation that had ever known"
"9552"	"the joy of worshiping a royal family could ever be robbed of it"
"9553"	"and not fade away and die of melancholy.  I urged that kings were"
"9554"	"dangerous.  He said, then have cats.  He was sure that a royal"
"9555"	"family of cats would answer every purpose.  They would be as useful"
"9556"	"as any other royal family, they would know as much, they would"
"9557"	"have the same virtues and the same treacheries, the same disposition"
"9558"	"to get up shindies with other royal cats, they would be laughably"
"9559"	"vain and absurd and never know it, they would be wholly inexpensive;"
"9560"	"finally, they would have as sound a divine right as any other"
"9561"	"royal house, and “Tom VII, or Tom XI, or Tom XIV by the grace"
"9562"	"of God King,” would sound as well as it would when applied to"
"9563"	"the ordinary royal tomcat with tights on.  “And as a rule,” said"
"9564"	"he, in his neat modern English, “the character of these cats would"
"9565"	"be considerably above the character of the average king, and this"
"9566"	"would be an immense moral advantage to the nation, for the reason"
"9567"	"that a nation always models its morals after its monarch’s.  The"
"9568"	"worship of royalty being founded in unreason, these graceful and"
"9569"	"harmless cats would easily become as sacred as any other royalties,"
"9570"	"and indeed more so, because it would presently be noticed that"
"9571"	"they hanged nobody, beheaded nobody, imprisoned nobody, inflicted"
"9572"	"no cruelties or injustices of any sort, and so must be worthy of"
"9573"	"a deeper love and reverence than the customary human king, and"
"9574"	"would certainly get it.  The eyes of the whole harried world would"
"9575"	"soon be fixed upon this humane and gentle system, and royal butchers"
"9576"	"would presently begin to disappear; their subjects would fill"
"9577"	"the vacancies with catlings from our own royal house; we should"
"9578"	"become a factory; we should supply the thrones of the world; within"
"9579"	"forty years all Europe would be governed by cats, and we should"
"9580"	"furnish the cats.  The reign of universal peace would begin then,"
"9581"	"to end no more forever....  Me-e-e-yow-ow-ow-ow--fzt!--wow!”"
"9582"	"Hang him, I supposed he was in earnest, and was beginning to be"
"9583"	"persuaded by him, until he exploded that cat-howl and startled me"
"9584"	"almost out of my clothes.  But he never could be in earnest.  He"
"9585"	"didn’t know what it was.  He had pictured a distinct and perfectly"
"9586"	"rational and feasible improvement upon constitutional monarchy,"
"9587"	"but he was too feather-headed to know it, or care anything about"
"9588"	"it, either.  I was going to give him a scolding, but Sandy came"
"9589"	"flying in at that moment, wild with terror, and so choked with sobs"
"9590"	"that for a minute she could not get her voice.  I ran and took her"
"9591"	"in my arms, and lavished caresses upon her and said, beseechingly:"
"9592"	"“Speak, darling, speak!  What is it?”"
"9593"	"Her head fell limp upon my bosom, and she gasped, almost inaudibly:"
"9594"	"“HELLO-CENTRAL!”"
"9595"	"“Quick!” I shouted to Clarence; “telephone the king’s homeopath"
"9596"	"to come!”"
"9597"	"In two minutes I was kneeling by the child’s crib, and Sandy was"
"9598"	"dispatching servants here, there, and everywhere, all over the"
"9599"	"palace.  I took in the situation almost at a glance--membranous"
"9600"	"croup!  I bent down and whispered:"
"9601"	"“Wake up, sweetheart!  Hello-Central.”"
"9602"	"She opened her soft eyes languidly, and made out to say:"
"9603"	"“Papa.”"
"9604"	"That was a comfort.  She was far from dead yet.  I sent for"
"9605"	"preparations of sulphur, I rousted out the croup-kettle myself;"
"9606"	"for I don’t sit down and wait for doctors when Sandy or the child"
"9607"	"is sick.  I knew how to nurse both of them, and had had experience."
"9608"	"This little chap had lived in my arms a good part of its small life,"
"9609"	"and often I could soothe away its troubles and get it to laugh"
"9610"	"through the tear-dews on its eye-lashes when even its mother couldn’t."
"9611"	"Sir Launcelot, in his richest armor, came striding along the great"
"9612"	"hall now on his way to the stock-board; he was president of the"
"9613"	"stock-board, and occupied the Siege Perilous, which he had bought"
"9614"	"of Sir Galahad; for the stock-board consisted of the Knights of"
"9615"	"the Round Table, and they used the Round Table for business purposes"
"9616"	"now.  Seats at it were worth--well, you would never believe the"
