"9617"	"figure, so it is no use to state it.  Sir Launcelot was a bear, and"
"9618"	"he had put up a corner in one of the new lines, and was just getting"
"9619"	"ready to squeeze the shorts to-day; but what of that?  He was"
"9620"	"the same old Launcelot, and when he glanced in as he was passing"
"9621"	"the door and found out that his pet was sick, that was enough"
"9622"	"for him; bulls and bears might fight it out their own way for all"
"9623"	"him, he would come right in here and stand by little Hello-Central"
"9624"	"for all he was worth.  And that was what he did.  He shied his"
"9625"	"helmet into the corner, and in half a minute he had a new wick"
"9626"	"in the alcohol lamp and was firing up on the croup-kettle.  By this"
"9627"	"time Sandy had built a blanket canopy over the crib, and everything"
"9628"	"was ready."
"9629"	"Sir Launcelot got up steam, he and I loaded up the kettle with"
"9630"	"unslaked lime and carbolic acid, with a touch of lactic acid added"
"9631"	"thereto, then filled the thing up with water and inserted the"
"9632"	"steam-spout under the canopy.  Everything was ship-shape now,"
"9633"	"and we sat down on either side of the crib to stand our watch."
"9634"	"Sandy was so grateful and so comforted that she charged a couple"
"9635"	"of church-wardens with willow-bark and sumach-tobacco for us,"
"9636"	"and told us to smoke as much as we pleased, it couldn’t get under"
"9637"	"the canopy, and she was used to smoke, being the first lady in the"
"9638"	"land who had ever seen a cloud blown.  Well, there couldn’t be"
"9639"	"a more contented or comfortable sight than Sir Launcelot in his"
"9640"	"noble armor sitting in gracious serenity at the end of a yard"
"9641"	"of snowy church-warden.  He was a beautiful man, a lovely man,"
"9642"	"and was just intended to make a wife and children happy.  But, of"
"9643"	"course Guenever--however, it’s no use to cry over what’s done and"
"9644"	"can’t be helped."
"9645"	"Well, he stood watch-and-watch with me, right straight through,"
"9646"	"for three days and nights, till the child was out of danger; then"
"9647"	"he took her up in his great arms and kissed her, with his plumes"
"9648"	"falling about her golden head, then laid her softly in Sandy’s"
"9649"	"lap again and took his stately way down the vast hall, between"
"9650"	"the ranks of admiring men-at-arms and menials, and so disappeared."
"9651"	"And no instinct warned me that I should never look upon him again"
"9652"	"in this world!  Lord, what a world of heart-break it is."
"9653"	"The doctors said we must take the child away, if we would coax"
"9654"	"her back to health and strength again.  And she must have sea-air."
"9655"	"So we took a man-of-war, and a suite of two hundred and sixty"
"9656"	"persons, and went cruising about, and after a fortnight of this we"
"9657"	"stepped ashore on the French coast, and the doctors thought it"
"9658"	"would be a good idea to make something of a stay there.  The little"
"9659"	"king of that region offered us his hospitalities, and we were glad"
"9660"	"to accept.  If he had had as many conveniences as he lacked, we"
"9661"	"should have been plenty comfortable enough; even as it was, we"
"9662"	"made out very well, in his queer old castle, by the help of comforts"
"9663"	"and luxuries from the ship."
"9664"	"At the end of a month I sent the vessel home for fresh supplies,"
"9665"	"and for news.  We expected her back in three or four days.  She"
"9666"	"would bring me, along with other news, the result of a certain"
"9667"	"experiment which I had been starting.  It was a project of mine"
"9668"	"to replace the tournament with something which might furnish an"
"9669"	"escape for the extra steam of the chivalry, keep those bucks"
"9670"	"entertained and out of mischief, and at the same time preserve"
"9671"	"the best thing in them, which was their hardy spirit of emulation."
"9672"	"I had had a choice band of them in private training for some time,"
"9673"	"and the date was now arriving for their first public effort."
"9674"	"This experiment was baseball.  In order to give the thing vogue"
"9675"	"from the start, and place it out of the reach of criticism, I chose"
"9676"	"my nines by rank, not capacity.  There wasn’t a knight in either"
"9677"	"team who wasn’t a sceptered sovereign.  As for material of this"
"9678"	"sort, there was a glut of it always around Arthur.  You couldn’t"
"9679"	"throw a brick in any direction and not cripple a king.  Of course,"
"9680"	"I couldn’t get these people to leave off their armor; they wouldn’t"
"9681"	"do that when they bathed.  They consented to differentiate the"
"9682"	"armor so that a body could tell one team from the other, but that"
"9683"	"was the most they would do.  So, one of the teams wore chain-mail"
"9684"	"ulsters, and the other wore plate-armor made of my new Bessemer"
"9685"	"steel.  Their practice in the field was the most fantastic thing I"
"9686"	"ever saw.  Being ball-proof, they never skipped out of the way,"
"9687"	"but stood still and took the result; when a Bessemer was at the bat"
"9688"	"and a ball hit him, it would bound a hundred and fifty yards"
"9689"	"sometimes.  And when a man was running, and threw himself on his"
"9690"	"stomach to slide to his base, it was like an iron-clad coming into"
"9691"	"port.  At first I appointed men of no rank to act as umpires, but"
"9692"	"I had to discontinue that.  These people were no easier to please"
"9693"	"than other nines.  The umpire’s first decision was usually his"
"9694"	"last; they broke him in two with a bat, and his friends toted him"
"9695"	"home on a shutter.  When it was noticed that no umpire ever survived"
"9696"	"a game, umpiring got to be unpopular.  So I was obliged to appoint"
"9697"	"somebody whose rank and lofty position under the government would"
"9698"	"protect him."
"9699"	"Here are the names of the nines:"
"9700"	"     BESSEMERS                   ULSTERS"
"9701"	"   KING ARTHUR.                EMPEROR LUCIUS."
"9702"	"   KING LOT OF LOTHIAN.        KING LOGRIS."
"9703"	"   KING OF NORTHGALIS.         KING MARHALT OF IRELAND."
"9704"	"   KING MARSIL.                KING MORGANORE."
"9705"	"   KING OF LITTLE BRITAIN.     KING MARK OF CORNWALL."
"9706"	"   KING LABOR.                 KING NENTRES OF GARLOT."
"9707"	"   KING PELLAM OF LISTENGESE.  KING MELIODAS OF LIONES."
"9708"	"   KING BAGDEMAGUS.            KING OF THE LAKE."
"9709"	"   KING TOLLEME LA FEINTES.    THE SOWDAN OF SYRIA."
"9710"	"                  Umpire--CLARENCE."
"9711"	"The first public game would certainly draw fifty thousand people;"
"9712"	"and for solid fun would be worth going around the world to see."
"9713"	"Everything would be favorable; it was balmy and beautiful spring"
"9714"	"weather now, and Nature was all tailored out in her new clothes."
"9715"	"CHAPTER XLI"
"9716"	"THE INTERDICT"
"9717"	"However, my attention was suddenly snatched from such matters;"
"9718"	"our child began to lose ground again, and we had to go to sitting"
"9719"	"up with her, her case became so serious.  We couldn’t bear to allow"
"9720"	"anybody to help in this service, so we two stood watch-and-watch,"
"9721"	"day in and day out.  Ah, Sandy, what a right heart she had, how"
"9722"	"simple, and genuine, and good she was!  She was a flawless wife"
"9723"	"and mother; and yet I had married her for no other particular"
"9724"	"reasons, except that by the customs of chivalry she was my property"
"9725"	"until some knight should win her from me in the field.  She had"
"9726"	"hunted Britain over for me; had found me at the hanging-bout"
"9727"	"outside of London, and had straightway resumed her old place at"
"9728"	"my side in the placidest way and as of right.  I was a New Englander,"
"9729"	"and in my opinion this sort of partnership would compromise her,"
"9730"	"sooner or later.  She couldn’t see how, but I cut argument short"
"9731"	"and we had a wedding."
"9732"	"Now I didn’t know I was drawing a prize, yet that was what I did"
"9733"	"draw.  Within the twelvemonth I became her worshiper; and ours"
"9734"	"was the dearest and perfectest comradeship that ever was.  People"
"9735"	"talk about beautiful friendships between two persons of the same"
"9736"	"sex.  What is the best of that sort, as compared with the friendship"
"9737"	"of man and wife, where the best impulses and highest ideals of"
"9738"	"both are the same?  There is no place for comparison between"
"9739"	"the two friendships; the one is earthly, the other divine."
"9740"	"In my dreams, along at first, I still wandered thirteen centuries"
"9741"	"away, and my unsatisfied spirit went calling and harking all up"
"9742"	"and down the unreplying vacancies of a vanished world.  Many a"
"9743"	"time Sandy heard that imploring cry come from my lips in my sleep."
"9744"	"With a grand magnanimity she saddled that cry of mine upon our"
"9745"	"child, conceiving it to be the name of some lost darling of mine."
"9746"	"It touched me to tears, and it also nearly knocked me off my feet,"
"9747"	"too, when she smiled up in my face for an earned reward, and played"
"9748"	"her quaint and pretty surprise upon me:"
"9749"	"“The name of one who was dear to thee is here preserved, here made"
"9750"	"holy, and the music of it will abide alway in our ears.  Now"
"9751"	"thou’lt kiss me, as knowing the name I have given the child.”"
"9752"	"But I didn’t know it, all the same.  I hadn’t an idea in the"
"9753"	"world; but it would have been cruel to confess it and spoil her"
"9754"	"pretty game; so I never let on, but said:"
"9755"	"“Yes, I know, sweetheart--how dear and good it is of you, too!"
"9756"	"But I want to hear these lips of yours, which are also mine, utter"
"9757"	"it first--then its music will be perfect.”"
"9758"	"Pleased to the marrow, she murmured:"
"9759"	"“HELLO-CENTRAL!”"
"9760"	"I didn’t laugh--I am always thankful for that--but the strain"
"9761"	"ruptured every cartilage in me, and for weeks afterward I could"
"9762"	"hear my bones clack when I walked.  She never found out her mistake."
"9763"	"The first time she heard that form of salute used at the telephone"
"9764"	"she was surprised, and not pleased; but I told her I had given"
"9765"	"order for it: that henceforth and forever the telephone must"
"9766"	"always be invoked with that reverent formality, in perpetual honor"
"9767"	"and remembrance of my lost friend and her small namesake.  This"
"9768"	"was not true.  But it answered."
"9769"	"Well, during two weeks and a half we watched by the crib, and in"
"9770"	"our deep solicitude we were unconscious of any world outside of"
"9771"	"that sick-room.  Then our reward came: the center of the universe"
"9772"	"turned the corner and began to mend.  Grateful?  It isn’t the term."
"9773"	"There _isn’t_ any term for it.  You know that yourself, if you’ve"
"9774"	"watched your child through the Valley of the Shadow and seen it"
"9775"	"come back to life and sweep night out of the earth with one"
"9776"	"all-illuminating smile that you could cover with your hand."
"9777"	"Why, we were back in this world in one instant!  Then we looked"
"9778"	"the same startled thought into each other’s eyes at the same"
"9779"	"moment; more than two weeks gone, and that ship not back yet!"
"9780"	"In another minute I appeared in the presence of my train.  They"
"9781"	"had been steeped in troubled bodings all this time--their faces"
"9782"	"showed it.  I called an escort and we galloped five miles to a"
"9783"	"hilltop overlooking the sea.  Where was my great commerce that"
"9784"	"so lately had made these glistening expanses populous and beautiful"
"9785"	"with its white-winged flocks?  Vanished, every one!  Not a sail,"
"9786"	"from verge to verge, not a smoke-bank--just a dead and empty"
"9787"	"solitude, in place of all that brisk and breezy life."
"9788"	"I went swiftly back, saying not a word to anybody.  I told Sandy"
"9789"	"this ghastly news.  We could imagine no explanation that would"
"9790"	"begin to explain.  Had there been an invasion? an earthquake?"
"9791"	"a pestilence?  Had the nation been swept out of existence?  But"
"9792"	"guessing was profitless.  I must go--at once.  I borrowed the king’s"
"9793"	"navy--a “ship” no bigger than a steam launch--and was soon ready."
"9794"	"The parting--ah, yes, that was hard.  As I was devouring the child"
"9795"	"with last kisses, it brisked up and jabbered out its vocabulary!"
"9796"	"--the first time in more than two weeks, and it made fools of us"
"9797"	"for joy.  The darling mispronunciations of childhood!--dear me,"
"9798"	"there’s no music that can touch it; and how one grieves when it"
"9799"	"wastes away and dissolves into correctness, knowing it will never"
"9800"	"visit his bereaved ear again.  Well, how good it was to be able"
"9801"	"to carry that gracious memory away with me!"
"9802"	"I approached England the next morning, with the wide highway of"
"9803"	"salt water all to myself.  There were ships in the harbor, at"
"9804"	"Dover, but they were naked as to sails, and there was no sign"
"9805"	"of life about them.  It was Sunday; yet at Canterbury the streets"
"9806"	"were empty; strangest of all, there was not even a priest in sight,"
"9807"	"and no stroke of a bell fell upon my ear.  The mournfulness of"
"9808"	"death was everywhere.  I couldn’t understand it.  At last, in"
"9809"	"the further edge of that town I saw a small funeral procession"
"9810"	"--just a family and a few friends following a coffin--no priest;"
"9811"	"a funeral without bell, book, or candle; there was a church there"
"9812"	"close at hand, but they passed it by weeping, and did not enter it;"
"9813"	"I glanced up at the belfry, and there hung the bell, shrouded in"
"9814"	"black, and its tongue tied back.  Now I knew!  Now I understood"
"9815"	"the stupendous calamity that had overtaken England.  Invasion?"
"9816"	"Invasion is a triviality to it.  It was the INTERDICT!"
"9817"	"I asked no questions; I didn’t need to ask any.  The Church had"
"9818"	"struck; the thing for me to do was to get into a disguise, and"
"9819"	"go warily.  One of my servants gave me a suit of clothes, and"
"9820"	"when we were safe beyond the town I put them on, and from that time"
"9821"	"I traveled alone; I could not risk the embarrassment of company."
"9822"	"A miserable journey.  A desolate silence everywhere.  Even in"
"9823"	"London itself.  Traffic had ceased; men did not talk or laugh, or"
"9824"	"go in groups, or even in couples; they moved aimlessly about, each"
"9825"	"man by himself, with his head down, and woe and terror at his heart."
"9826"	"The Tower showed recent war-scars.  Verily, much had been happening."
"9827"	"Of course, I meant to take the train for Camelot.  Train!  Why,"
"9828"	"the station was as vacant as a cavern.  I moved on.  The journey"
"9829"	"to Camelot was a repetition of what I had already seen.  The Monday"
"9830"	"and the Tuesday differed in no way from the Sunday.  I arrived"
"9831"	"far in the night.  From being the best electric-lighted town in"
"9832"	"the kingdom and the most like a recumbent sun of anything you ever"
"9833"	"saw, it was become simply a blot--a blot upon darkness--that is"
"9834"	"to say, it was darker and solider than the rest of the darkness,"
"9835"	"and so you could see it a little better; it made me feel as if"
"9836"	"maybe it was symbolical--a sort of sign that the Church was going to"
"9837"	"_keep_ the upper hand now, and snuff out all my beautiful civilization"
"9838"	"just like that.  I found no life stirring in the somber streets."
"9839"	"I groped my way with a heavy heart.  The vast castle loomed black"
"9840"	"upon the hilltop, not a spark visible about it.  The drawbridge"
"9841"	"was down, the great gate stood wide, I entered without challenge,"
"9842"	"my own heels making the only sound I heard--and it was sepulchral"
"9843"	"enough, in those huge vacant courts."
"9844"	"CHAPTER XLII"
"9845"	"WAR!"
"9846"	"I found Clarence alone in his quarters, drowned in melancholy;"
"9847"	"and in place of the electric light, he had reinstituted the ancient"
"9848"	"rag-lamp, and sat there in a grisly twilight with all curtains"
"9849"	"drawn tight.  He sprang up and rushed for me eagerly, saying:"
"9850"	"“Oh, it’s worth a billion milrays to look upon a live person again!”"
"9851"	"He knew me as easily as if I hadn’t been disguised at all.  Which"
"9852"	"frightened me; one may easily believe that."
"9853"	"“Quick, now, tell me the meaning of this fearful disaster,” I said."
"9854"	"“How did it come about?”"
"9855"	"“Well, if there hadn’t been any Queen Guenever, it wouldn’t have"
"9856"	"come so early; but it would have come, anyway.  It would have"
"9857"	"come on your own account by and by; by luck, it happened to come"
"9858"	"on the queen’s.”"
"9859"	"“_And_ Sir Launcelot’s?”"
"9860"	"“Just so.”"
"9861"	"“Give me the details.”"
"9862"	"“I reckon you will grant that during some years there has been"
"9863"	"only one pair of eyes in these kingdoms that has not been looking"
"9864"	"steadily askance at the queen and Sir Launcelot--”"
"9865"	"“Yes, King Arthur’s.”"
"9866"	"“--and only one heart that was without suspicion--”"
"9867"	"“Yes--the king’s; a heart that isn’t capable of thinking evil"
"9868"	"of a friend.”"
"9869"	"“Well, the king might have gone on, still happy and unsuspecting,"
"9870"	"to the end of his days, but for one of your modern improvements"

"9874"	"everybody knew it.  The stock was for sale at a give-away.  What"
"9875"	"does Sir Launcelot do, but--”"
"9876"	"“Yes, I know; he quietly picked up nearly all of it for a song;"
"9877"	"then he bought about twice as much more, deliverable upon call;"

"9884"	"they rested-up that side by shifting the laugh to the other side."
"9885"	"That was when they compromised with the Invincible at 283!”"
"9886"	"“Good land!”"
"9887"	"“He skinned them alive, and they deserved it--anyway, the whole"

"9906"	"“Yes--that was the way of it.  The king sent the queen to the"

"9949"	"you should return--”"
"9950"	"“Ah--a king’s customary wisdom!”"

"9973"	"Then the king--however, we have started something fresh since"

"9975"	"“No?  What is that?”"

"9977"	"“Why, that’s good.”"

"9982"	"   ‘Then the king looked about him, and then was he"

"10111"	"plant when I was projecting a miracle.”"
"10112"	"“Just so.  And as that miracle hadn’t become necessary then,"
"10113"	"I thought it might be a good idea to utilize the plant now.  I’ve"
"10114"	"provisioned the cave for a siege--”"
"10115"	"“A good idea, a first-rate idea.”"
"10116"	"“I think so.  I placed four of my boys there as a guard--inside,"
"10117"	"and out of sight.  Nobody was to be hurt--while outside; but any"
"10118"	"attempt to enter--well, we said just let anybody try it!  Then"
"10119"	"I went out into the hills and uncovered and cut the secret wires"
"10120"	"which connected your bedroom with the wires that go to the dynamite"
"10121"	"deposits under all our vast factories, mills, workshops, magazines,"
"10122"	"etc., and about midnight I and my boys turned out and connected"
"10123"	"that wire with the cave, and nobody but you and I suspects where"
"10124"	"the other end of it goes to.  We laid it under ground, of course, and"
"10125"	"it was all finished in a couple of hours or so.  We sha’n’t have"
"10126"	"to leave our fortress now when we want to blow up our civilization.”"
"10127"	"“It was the right move--and the natural one; military necessity,"
"10128"	"in the changed condition of things.  Well, what changes _have_ come!"
"10129"	"We expected to be besieged in the palace some time or other, but"
"10130"	"--however, go on.”"
"10131"	"“Next, we built a wire fence.”"
"10132"	"“Wire fence?”"
"10133"	"“Yes.  You dropped the hint of it yourself, two or three years ago.”"
"10134"	"“Oh, I remember--the time the Church tried her strength against"
"10135"	"us the first time, and presently thought it wise to wait for a"
"10136"	"hopefuler season.  Well, how have you arranged the fence?”"
"10137"	"“I start twelve immensely strong wires--naked, not insulated"
"10138"	"--from a big dynamo in the cave--dynamo with no brushes except"
"10139"	"a positive and a negative one--”"
"10140"	"“Yes, that’s right.”"
"10141"	"“The wires go out from the cave and fence in a circle of level"
"10142"	"ground a hundred yards in diameter; they make twelve independent"
"10143"	"fences, ten feet apart--that is to say, twelve circles within"
"10144"	"circles--and their ends come into the cave again.”"
"10145"	"“Right; go on.”"
"10146"	"“The fences are fastened to heavy oaken posts only three feet apart,"
"10147"	"and these posts are sunk five feet in the ground.”"
"10148"	"“That is good and strong.”"
"10149"	"“Yes.  The wires have no ground-connection outside of the cave."
"10150"	"They go out from the positive brush of the dynamo; there is a"
"10151"	"ground-connection through the negative brush; the other ends of"
"10152"	"the wire return to the cave, and each is grounded independently.”"
"10153"	"“No, no, that won’t do!”"
"10154"	"“Why?”"
"10155"	"“It’s too expensive--uses up force for nothing.  You don’t want"
"10156"	"any ground-connection except the one through the negative brush."
"10157"	"The other end of every wire must be brought back into the cave"
"10158"	"and fastened independently, and _without_ any ground-connection."
"10159"	"Now, then, observe the economy of it.  A cavalry charge hurls"
"10160"	"itself against the fence; you are using no power, you are spending"
"10161"	"no money, for there is only one ground-connection till those horses"
"10162"	"come against the wire; the moment they touch it they form a"
"10163"	"connection with the negative brush _through the ground_, and drop"
"10164"	"dead.  Don’t you see?--you are using no energy until it is needed;"
"10165"	"your lightning is there, and ready, like the load in a gun; but"
"10166"	"it isn’t costing you a cent till you touch it off.  Oh, yes, the"
"10167"	"single ground-connection--”"
"10168"	"“Of course!  I don’t know how I overlooked that.  It’s not only"
"10169"	"cheaper, but it’s more effectual than the other way, for if wires"
"10170"	"break or get tangled, no harm is done.”"
"10171"	"“No, especially if we have a tell-tale in the cave and disconnect"
"10172"	"the broken wire.  Well, go on.  The gatlings?”"
"10173"	"“Yes--that’s arranged.  In the center of the inner circle, on a"
"10174"	"spacious platform six feet high, I’ve grouped a battery of thirteen"
"10175"	"gatling guns, and provided plenty of ammunition.”"
"10176"	"“That’s it.  They command every approach, and when the Church’s"
"10177"	"knights arrive, there’s going to be music.  The brow of the"
"10178"	"precipice over the cave--”"
"10179"	"“I’ve got a wire fence there, and a gatling.  They won’t drop any"
"10180"	"rocks down on us.”"
"10181"	"“Well, and the glass-cylinder dynamite torpedoes?”"
"10182"	"“That’s attended to.  It’s the prettiest garden that was ever"
"10183"	"planted.  It’s a belt forty feet wide, and goes around the outer"
"10184"	"fence--distance between it and the fence one hundred yards--kind of"
"10185"	"neutral ground that space is.  There isn’t a single square yard"
"10186"	"of that whole belt but is equipped with a torpedo.  We laid them"
"10187"	"on the surface of the ground, and sprinkled a layer of sand over"
"10188"	"them.  It’s an innocent looking garden, but you let a man start"
"10189"	"in to hoe it once, and you’ll see.”"
"10190"	"“You tested the torpedoes?”"
"10191"	"“Well, I was going to, but--”"
"10192"	"“But what?  Why, it’s an immense oversight not to apply a--”"
"10193"	"“Test?  Yes, I know; but they’re all right; I laid a few in the"
"10194"	"public road beyond our lines and they’ve been tested.”"
"10195"	"“Oh, that alters the case.  Who did it?”"
"10196"	"“A Church committee.”"
"10197"	"“How kind!”"
"10198"	"“Yes.  They came to command us to make submission.  You see they"
"10199"	"didn’t really come to test the torpedoes; that was merely an incident.”"
"10200"	"“Did the committee make a report?”"
"10201"	"“Yes, they made one.  You could have heard it a mile.”"
"10202"	"“Unanimous?”"
"10203"	"“That was the nature of it.  After that I put up some signs, for the"
"10204"	"protection of future committees, and we have had no intruders since.”"
"10205"	"“Clarence, you’ve done a world of work, and done it perfectly.”"
"10206"	"“We had plenty of time for it; there wasn’t any occasion for hurry.”"
"10207"	"We sat silent awhile, thinking.  Then my mind was made up, and"
"10208"	"I said:"
"10209"	"“Yes, everything is ready; everything is shipshape, no detail is"
"10210"	"wanting.  I know what to do now.”"
"10211"	"“So do I; sit down and wait.”"
"10212"	"“No, _sir_! rise up and _strike_!”"
"10213"	"“Do you mean it?”"
"10214"	"“Yes, indeed!  The _de_fensive isn’t in my line, and the _of_fensive"
"10215"	"is.  That is, when I hold a fair hand--two-thirds as good a hand"
"10216"	"as the enemy.  Oh, yes, we’ll rise up and strike; that’s our game.”"
"10217"	"“A hundred to one you are right.  When does the performance begin?”"
"10218"	"“_Now!_  We’ll proclaim the Republic.”"
"10219"	"“Well, that _will_ precipitate things, sure enough!”"
"10220"	"“It will make them buzz, I tell you!  England will be a hornets’"
"10221"	"nest before noon to-morrow, if the Church’s hand hasn’t lost its"
"10222"	"cunning--and we know it hasn’t.  Now you write and I’ll dictate thus:"
"10223"	"                      “PROCLAMATION"
"10224"	"                           ---"
"10225"	"   “BE IT KNOWN UNTO ALL.  Whereas the king having died"
"10226"	"   and left no heir, it becomes my duty to continue the"
"10227"	"   executive authority vested in me, until a government"
"10228"	"   shall have been created and set in motion.  The"
"10229"	"   monarchy has lapsed, it no longer exists.  By"
"10230"	"   consequence, all political power has reverted to its"
"10231"	"   original source, the people of the nation.  With the"
"10232"	"   monarchy, its several adjuncts died also; wherefore"
"10233"	"   there is no longer a nobility, no longer a privileged"
"10234"	"   class, no longer an Established Church; all men are"
"10235"	"   become exactly equal; they are upon one common"
"10236"	"   level, and religion is free.  _A Republic is hereby"
"10237"	"   proclaimed_, as being the natural estate of a nation"
"10238"	"   when other authority has ceased.  It is the duty of"
"10239"	"   the British people to meet together immediately,"
"10240"	"   and by their votes elect representatives and deliver"
"10241"	"   into their hands the government.”"
"10242"	"I signed it “The Boss,” and dated it from Merlin’s Cave."
"10243"	"Clarence said--"
"10244"	"“Why, that tells where we are, and invites them to call right away.”"
"10245"	"“That is the idea.  We _strike_--by the Proclamation--then it’s"
"10246"	"their innings.  Now have the thing set up and printed and posted,"
"10247"	"right off; that is, give the order; then, if you’ve got a couple"
"10248"	"of bicycles handy at the foot of the hill, ho for Merlin’s Cave!”"
"10249"	"“I shall be ready in ten minutes.  What a cyclone there is going"
"10250"	"to be to-morrow when this piece of paper gets to work!...  It’s a"
"10251"	"pleasant old palace, this is; I wonder if we shall ever again"
"10252"	"--but never mind about that.”"
"10253"	"CHAPTER XLIII"
"10254"	"THE BATTLE OF THE SAND BELT"
"10255"	"In Merlin’s Cave--Clarence and I and fifty-two fresh, bright,"
"10256"	"well-educated, clean-minded young British boys.  At dawn I sent"
"10257"	"an order to the factories and to all our great works to stop"
"10258"	"operations and remove all life to a safe distance, as everything"
"10259"	"was going to be blown up by secret mines, “_and no telling at what"
"10260"	"moment--therefore, vacate at once_.”  These people knew me, and"
"10261"	"had confidence in my word.  They would clear out without waiting"
"10262"	"to part their hair, and I could take my own time about dating the"
"10263"	"explosion.  You couldn’t hire one of them to go back during the"
"10264"	"century, if the explosion was still impending."
"10265"	"We had a week of waiting.  It was not dull for me, because I was"
"10266"	"writing all the time.  During the first three days, I finished"
"10267"	"turning my old diary into this narrative form; it only required"
"10268"	"a chapter or so to bring it down to date.  The rest of the week"
"10269"	"I took up in writing letters to my wife.  It was always my habit"
"10270"	"to write to Sandy every day, whenever we were separate, and now"
"10271"	"I kept up the habit for love of it, and of her, though I couldn’t"
"10272"	"do anything with the letters, of course, after I had written them."
"10273"	"But it put in the time, you see, and was almost like talking;"
"10274"	"it was almost as if I was saying, “Sandy, if you and Hello-Central"
"10275"	"were here in the cave, instead of only your photographs, what"
"10276"	"good times we could have!”  And then, you know, I could imagine"
"10277"	"the baby goo-gooing something out in reply, with its fists in its"
"10278"	"mouth and itself stretched across its mother’s lap on its back,"
"10279"	"and she a-laughing and admiring and worshipping, and now and then"
"10280"	"tickling under the baby’s chin to set it cackling, and then maybe"
"10281"	"throwing in a word of answer to me herself--and so on and so on"
"10282"	"--well, don’t you know, I could sit there in the cave with my pen,"
"10283"	"and keep it up, that way, by the hour with them.  Why, it was"
"10284"	"almost like having us all together again."
"10285"	"I had spies out every night, of course, to get news.  Every report"
"10286"	"made things look more and more impressive.  The hosts were gathering,"
"10287"	"gathering; down all the roads and paths of England the knights were"
"10288"	"riding, and priests rode with them, to hearten these original"
"10289"	"Crusaders, this being the Church’s war.  All the nobilities, big"
"10290"	"and little, were on their way, and all the gentry.  This was all"
"10291"	"as was expected.  We should thin out this sort of folk to such"
"10292"	"a degree that the people would have nothing to do but just step"
"10293"	"to the front with their republic and--"
"10294"	"Ah, what a donkey I was!  Toward the end of the week I began to get"
"10295"	"this large and disenchanting fact through my head: that the mass"
"10296"	"of the nation had swung their caps and shouted for the republic for"
"10297"	"about one day, and there an end!  The Church, the nobles, and"
"10298"	"the gentry then turned one grand, all-disapproving frown upon them"
"10299"	"and shriveled them into sheep!  From that moment the sheep had"
"10300"	"begun to gather to the fold--that is to say, the camps--and offer"
"10301"	"their valueless lives and their valuable wool to the “righteous"
"10302"	"cause.”  Why, even the very men who had lately been slaves were"
"10303"	"in the “righteous cause,” and glorifying it, praying for it,"
"10304"	"sentimentally slabbering over it, just like all the other commoners."
"10305"	"Imagine such human muck as this; conceive of this folly!"
"10306"	"Yes, it was now “Death to the Republic!” everywhere--not a dissenting"
"10307"	"voice.  All England was marching against us!  Truly, this was more"
"10308"	"than I had bargained for."
"10309"	"I watched my fifty-two boys narrowly; watched their faces, their"
"10310"	"walk, their unconscious attitudes: for all these are a language"
"10311"	"--a language given us purposely that it may betray us in times of"
"10312"	"emergency, when we have secrets which we want to keep.  I knew"
"10313"	"that that thought would keep saying itself over and over again"
"10314"	"in their minds and hearts, _All England is marching against us!_"
"10315"	"and ever more strenuously imploring attention with each repetition,"
"10316"	"ever more sharply realizing itself to their imaginations, until"
"10317"	"even in their sleep they would find no rest from it, but hear"
"10318"	"the vague and flitting creatures of the dreams say, _All England_"
"10319"	"--ALL ENGLAND!--_is marching against you_!  I knew all this would"
"10320"	"happen; I knew that ultimately the pressure would become so great"
"10321"	"that it would compel utterance; therefore, I must be ready with an"
"10322"	"answer at that time--an answer well chosen and tranquilizing."
"10323"	"I was right.  The time came.  They HAD to speak.  Poor lads, it"
"10324"	"was pitiful to see, they were so pale, so worn, so troubled.  At"
"10325"	"first their spokesman could hardly find voice or words; but he"
"10326"	"presently got both.  This is what he said--and he put it in the"
"10327"	"neat modern English taught him in my schools:"
"10328"	"“We have tried to forget what we are--English boys!  We have tried"
"10329"	"to put reason before sentiment, duty before love; our minds"
"10330"	"approve, but our hearts reproach us.  While apparently it was"
"10331"	"only the nobility, only the gentry, only the twenty-five or thirty"
"10332"	"thousand knights left alive out of the late wars, we were of one"
"10333"	"mind, and undisturbed by any troubling doubt; each and every one"
"10334"	"of these fifty-two lads who stand here before you, said, ‘They"
"10335"	"have chosen--it is their affair.’  But think!--the matter is"
"10336"	"altered--_All England is marching against us_!  Oh, sir, consider!"
"10337"	"--reflect!--these people are our people, they are bone of our bone,"
"10338"	"flesh of our flesh, we love them--do not ask us to destroy our nation!”"
"10339"	"Well, it shows the value of looking ahead, and being ready for"
"10340"	"a thing when it happens.  If I hadn’t foreseen this thing and been"
"10341"	"fixed, that boy would have had me!--I couldn’t have said a word."
"10342"	"But I was fixed.  I said:"
"10343"	"“My boys, your hearts are in the right place, you have thought the"
"10344"	"worthy thought, you have done the worthy thing.  You are English"
"10345"	"boys, you will remain English boys, and you will keep that name"
"10346"	"unsmirched.  Give yourselves no further concern, let your minds be"
"10347"	"at peace.  Consider this: while all England is marching against"
"10348"	"us, who is in the van?  Who, by the commonest rules of war, will"
"10349"	"march in the front?  Answer me.”"
"10350"	"“The mounted host of mailed knights.”"
"10351"	"“True.  They are thirty thousand strong.  Acres deep they will march."
"10352"	"Now, observe: none but _they_ will ever strike the sand-belt!  Then"
"10353"	"there will be an episode!  Immediately after, the civilian multitude"
"10354"	"in the rear will retire, to meet business engagements elsewhere."
"10355"	"None but nobles and gentry are knights, and _none but these_ will"
"10356"	"remain to dance to our music after that episode.  It is absolutely"
"10357"	"true that we shall have to fight nobody but these thirty thousand"
"10358"	"knights.  Now speak, and it shall be as you decide.  Shall we"
"10359"	"avoid the battle, retire from the field?”"
"10360"	"“NO!!!”"
"10361"	"The shout was unanimous and hearty."
"10362"	"“Are you--are you--well, afraid of these thirty thousand knights?”"
"10363"	"That joke brought out a good laugh, the boys’ troubles vanished"
"10364"	"away, and they went gaily to their posts.  Ah, they were a darling"
"10365"	"fifty-two!  As pretty as girls, too."
"10366"	"I was ready for the enemy now.  Let the approaching big day come"
"10367"	"along--it would find us on deck."
"10368"	"The big day arrived on time.  At dawn the sentry on watch in the"
"10369"	"corral came into the cave and reported a moving black mass under"
"10370"	"the horizon, and a faint sound which he thought to be military"
"10371"	"music.  Breakfast was just ready; we sat down and ate it."
"10372"	"This over, I made the boys a little speech, and then sent out"
"10373"	"a detail to man the battery, with Clarence in command of it."
"10374"	"The sun rose presently and sent its unobstructed splendors over"
"10375"	"the land, and we saw a prodigious host moving slowly toward us,"
"10376"	"with the steady drift and aligned front of a wave of the sea."
"10377"	"Nearer and nearer it came, and more and more sublimely imposing"
"10378"	"became its aspect; yes, all England was there, apparently.  Soon"
"10379"	"we could see the innumerable banners fluttering, and then the sun"
"10380"	"struck the sea of armor and set it all aflash.  Yes, it was a fine"
"10381"	"sight; I hadn’t ever seen anything to beat it."
"10382"	"At last we could make out details.  All the front ranks, no telling"
"10383"	"how many acres deep, were horsemen--plumed knights in armor."
"10384"	"Suddenly we heard the blare of trumpets; the slow walk burst into"
"10385"	"a gallop, and then--well, it was wonderful to see!  Down swept"
"10386"	"that vast horse-shoe wave--it approached the sand-belt--my breath"
"10387"	"stood still; nearer, nearer--the strip of green turf beyond the"
"10388"	"yellow belt grew narrow--narrower still--became a mere ribbon in"
"10389"	"front of the horses--then disappeared under their hoofs.  Great"
"10390"	"Scott!  Why, the whole front of that host shot into the sky with"
"10391"	"a thunder-crash, and became a whirling tempest of rags and fragments;"
"10392"	"and along the ground lay a thick wall of smoke that hid what was"
"10393"	"left of the multitude from our sight."
"10394"	"Time for the second step in the plan of campaign!  I touched"
"10395"	"a button, and shook the bones of England loose from her spine!"
"10396"	"In that explosion all our noble civilization-factories went up in"
"10397"	"the air and disappeared from the earth.  It was a pity, but it"
"10398"	"was necessary.  We could not afford to let the enemy turn our own"
"10399"	"weapons against us."
"10400"	"Now ensued one of the dullest quarter-hours I had ever endured."
"10401"	"We waited in a silent solitude enclosed by our circles of wire,"
"10402"	"and by a circle of heavy smoke outside of these.  We couldn’t"
"10403"	"see over the wall of smoke, and we couldn’t see through it.  But"
"10404"	"at last it began to shred away lazily, and by the end of another"
"10405"	"quarter-hour the land was clear and our curiosity was enabled"
"10406"	"to satisfy itself.  No living creature was in sight!  We now"
"10407"	"perceived that additions had been made to our defenses.  The"
"10408"	"dynamite had dug a ditch more than a hundred feet wide, all around"
"10409"	"us, and cast up an embankment some twenty-five feet high on both"
"10410"	"borders of it.  As to destruction of life, it was amazing.  Moreover,"
"10411"	"it was beyond estimate.  Of course, we could not _count_ the dead,"
"10412"	"because they did not exist as individuals, but merely as homogeneous"
"10413"	"protoplasm, with alloys of iron and buttons."
"10414"	"No life was in sight, but necessarily there must have been some"
"10415"	"wounded in the rear ranks, who were carried off the field under"
"10416"	"cover of the wall of smoke; there would be sickness among the"
"10417"	"others--there always is, after an episode like that.  But there"
"10418"	"would be no reinforcements; this was the last stand of the chivalry"
"10419"	"of England; it was all that was left of the order, after the recent"
"10420"	"annihilating wars.  So I felt quite safe in believing that the"
"10421"	"utmost force that could for the future be brought against us"
"10422"	"would be but small; that is, of knights.  I therefore issued a"
"10423"	"congratulatory proclamation to my army in these words:"
"10424"	"   SOLDIERS, CHAMPIONS OF HUMAN LIBERTY AND EQUALITY:"
"10425"	"   Your General congratulates you!  In the pride of his"
"10426"	"   strength and the vanity of his renown, an arrogant"
"10427"	"   enemy came against you.  You were ready.  The conflict"
"10428"	"   was brief; on your side, glorious.  This mighty"
"10429"	"   victory, having been achieved utterly without loss,"
"10430"	"   stands without example in history.  So long as the"
"10431"	"   planets shall continue to move in their orbits, the"
"10432"	"   BATTLE OF THE SAND-BELT will not perish out of the"
"10433"	"   memories of men."
"10434"	"                                THE BOSS."
"10435"	"I read it well, and the applause I got was very gratifying to me."
"10436"	"I then wound up with these remarks:"
"10437"	"“The war with the English nation, as a nation, is at an end."
"10438"	"The nation has retired from the field and the war.  Before it can"
"10439"	"be persuaded to return, war will have ceased.  This campaign is"
"10440"	"the only one that is going to be fought.  It will be brief"
"10441"	"--the briefest in history.  Also the most destructive to life,"
"10442"	"considered from the standpoint of proportion of casualties to"
"10443"	"numbers engaged.  We are done with the nation; henceforth we deal"
"10444"	"only with the knights.  English knights can be killed, but they"
"10445"	"cannot be conquered.  We know what is before us.  While one of"
"10446"	"these men remains alive, our task is not finished, the war is not"
"10447"	"ended.  We will kill them all.”  [Loud and long continued applause.]"
"10448"	"I picketed the great embankments thrown up around our lines by"
"10449"	"the dynamite explosion--merely a lookout of a couple of boys"
"10450"	"to announce the enemy when he should appear again."
"10451"	"Next, I sent an engineer and forty men to a point just beyond"
"10452"	"our lines on the south, to turn a mountain brook that was there,"
"10453"	"and bring it within our lines and under our command, arranging"
"10454"	"it in such a way that I could make instant use of it in an emergency."
"10455"	"The forty men were divided into two shifts of twenty each, and"
"10456"	"were to relieve each other every two hours.  In ten hours the"
"10457"	"work was accomplished."
"10458"	"It was nightfall now, and I withdrew my pickets.  The one who"
"10459"	"had had the northern outlook reported a camp in sight, but visible"
"10460"	"with the glass only.  He also reported that a few knights had been"
"10461"	"feeling their way toward us, and had driven some cattle across our"
"10462"	"lines, but that the knights themselves had not come very near."
"10463"	"That was what I had been expecting.  They were feeling us, you"
"10464"	"see; they wanted to know if we were going to play that red terror"
"10465"	"on them again.  They would grow bolder in the night, perhaps."
"10466"	"I believed I knew what project they would attempt, because it was"
"10467"	"plainly the thing I would attempt myself if I were in their places"
"10468"	"and as ignorant as they were.  I mentioned it to Clarence."
"10469"	"“I think you are right,” said he; “it is the obvious thing for"
"10470"	"them to try.”"
"10471"	"“Well, then,” I said, “if they do it they are doomed.”"
"10472"	"“Certainly.”"
"10473"	"“They won’t have the slightest show in the world.”"
"10474"	"“Of course they won’t.”"
"10475"	"“It’s dreadful, Clarence.  It seems an awful pity.”"
"10476"	"The thing disturbed me so that I couldn’t get any peace of mind"
"10477"	"for thinking of it and worrying over it.  So, at last, to quiet"
"10478"	"my conscience, I framed this message to the knights:"
"10479"	"   TO THE HONORABLE THE COMMANDER OF THE INSURGENT"
"10480"	"   CHIVALRY OF ENGLAND: YOU fight in vain.  We know"
"10481"	"   your strength--if one may call it by that name."
"10482"	"   We know that at the utmost you cannot bring"
"10483"	"   against us above five and twenty thousand knights."
"10484"	"   Therefore, you have no chance--none whatever."
"10485"	"   Reflect: we are well equipped, well fortified, we"
"10486"	"   number 54.  Fifty-four what?  Men?  No, MINDS--the"
"10487"	"   capablest in the world; a force against which"
"10488"	"   mere animal might may no more hope to prevail than"
"10489"	"   may the idle waves of the sea hope to prevail"
"10490"	"   against the granite barriers of England.  Be advised."
"10491"	"   We offer you your lives; for the sake of your"
"10492"	"   families, do not reject the gift.  We offer you"
"10493"	"   this chance, and it is the last: throw down your"
"10494"	"   arms; surrender unconditionally to the Republic,"
"10495"	"   and all will be forgiven."
"10496"	"                          (Signed) THE BOSS."
"10497"	"I read it to Clarence, and said I proposed to send it by a flag"
"10498"	"of truce.  He laughed the sarcastic laugh he was born with, and said:"
"10499"	"“Somehow it seems impossible for you to ever fully realize what"
"10500"	"these nobilities are.  Now let us save a little time and trouble."
"10501"	"Consider me the commander of the knights yonder.  Now, then,"
"10502"	"you are the flag of truce; approach and deliver me your message,"
"10503"	"and I will give you your answer.”"
"10504"	"I humored the idea.  I came forward under an imaginary guard of"
"10505"	"the enemy’s soldiers, produced my paper, and read it through."
"10506"	"For answer, Clarence struck the paper out of my hand, pursed up"
"10507"	"a scornful lip and said with lofty disdain:"
"10508"	"“Dismember me this animal, and return him in a basket to the"
"10509"	"base-born knave who sent him; other answer have I none!”"
"10510"	"How empty is theory in presence of fact!  And this was just fact,"
"10511"	"and nothing else.  It was the thing that would have happened,"
"10512"	"there was no getting around that.  I tore up the paper and granted"
"10513"	"my mistimed sentimentalities a permanent rest."
"10514"	"Then, to business.  I tested the electric signals from the gatling"
"10515"	"platform to the cave, and made sure that they were all right;"
"10516"	"I tested and retested those which commanded the fences--these"
"10517"	"were signals whereby I could break and renew the electric current"
"10518"	"in each fence independently of the others at will.  I placed the"
"10519"	"brook-connection under the guard and authority of three of my"
"10520"	"best boys, who would alternate in two-hour watches all night and"
"10521"	"promptly obey my signal, if I should have occasion to give it"
"10522"	"--three revolver-shots in quick succession.  Sentry-duty was discarded"
"10523"	"for the night, and the corral left empty of life; I ordered that"
"10524"	"quiet be maintained in the cave, and the electric lights turned"
"10525"	"down to a glimmer."
"10526"	"As soon as it was good and dark, I shut off the current from all"
"10527"	"the fences, and then groped my way out to the embankment bordering"
"10528"	"our side of the great dynamite ditch.  I crept to the top of it"
"10529"	"and lay there on the slant of the muck to watch.  But it was"
"10530"	"too dark to see anything.  As for sounds, there were none.  The"
"10531"	"stillness was deathlike.  True, there were the usual night-sounds"
"10532"	"of the country--the whir of night-birds, the buzzing of insects,"
"10533"	"the barking of distant dogs, the mellow lowing of far-off kine"
"10534"	"--but these didn’t seem to break the stillness, they only intensified"
"10535"	"it, and added a grewsome melancholy to it into the bargain."
"10536"	"I presently gave up looking, the night shut down so black, but"
"10537"	"I kept my ears strained to catch the least suspicious sound, for"
"10538"	"I judged I had only to wait, and I shouldn’t be disappointed."
"10539"	"However, I had to wait a long time.  At last I caught what you"
"10540"	"may call in distinct glimpses of sound dulled metallic sound."
"10541"	"I pricked up my ears, then, and held my breath, for this was the"
"10542"	"sort of thing I had been waiting for.  This sound thickened, and"
"10543"	"approached--from toward the north.  Presently, I heard it at my"
"10544"	"own level--the ridge-top of the opposite embankment, a hundred"
"10545"	"feet or more away.  Then I seemed to see a row of black dots appear"
"10546"	"along that ridge--human heads?  I couldn’t tell; it mightn’t be"
"10547"	"anything at all; you can’t depend on your eyes when your imagination"
"10548"	"is out of focus.  However, the question was soon settled.  I heard"
"10549"	"that metallic noise descending into the great ditch.  It augmented"
"10550"	"fast, it spread all along, and it unmistakably furnished me this"
"10551"	"fact: an armed host was taking up its quarters in the ditch.  Yes,"
"10552"	"these people were arranging a little surprise party for us.  We"
"10553"	"could expect entertainment about dawn, possibly earlier."
"10554"	"I groped my way back to the corral now; I had seen enough.  I went"
"10555"	"to the platform and signaled to turn the current on to the two"
"10556"	"inner fences.  Then I went into the cave, and found everything"
"10557"	"satisfactory there--nobody awake but the working-watch.  I woke"
"10558"	"Clarence and told him the great ditch was filling up with men,"
"10559"	"and that I believed all the knights were coming for us in a body."
"10560"	"It was my notion that as soon as dawn approached we could expect"
"10561"	"the ditch’s ambuscaded thousands to swarm up over the embankment"
"10562"	"and make an assault, and be followed immediately by the rest"
"10563"	"of their army."
"10564"	"Clarence said:"
"10565"	"“They will be wanting to send a scout or two in the dark to make"
"10566"	"preliminary observations.  Why not take the lightning off the"
"10567"	"outer fences, and give them a chance?”"
"10568"	"“I’ve already done it, Clarence.  Did you ever know me to be"
"10569"	"inhospitable?”"
"10570"	"“No, you are a good heart.  I want to go and--”"
"10571"	"“Be a reception committee?  I will go, too.”"
"10572"	"We crossed the corral and lay down together between the two inside"
"10573"	"fences.  Even the dim light of the cave had disordered our eyesight"
"10574"	"somewhat, but the focus straightway began to regulate itself and"
"10575"	"soon it was adjusted for present circumstances.  We had had to feel"
"10576"	"our way before, but we could make out to see the fence posts now."
"10577"	"We started a whispered conversation, but suddenly Clarence broke"
"10578"	"off and said:"
"10579"	"“What is that?”"
"10580"	"“What is what?”"
"10581"	"“That thing yonder.”"
"10582"	"“What thing--where?”"
"10583"	"“There beyond you a little piece--dark something--a dull shape"
"10584"	"of some kind--against the second fence.”"
"10585"	"I gazed and he gazed.  I said:"
"10586"	"“Could it be a man, Clarence?”"
"10587"	"“No, I think not.  If you notice, it looks a lit--why, it _is_"
"10588"	"a man!--leaning on the fence.”"
"10589"	"“I certainly believe it is; let us go and see.”"
"10590"	"We crept along on our hands and knees until we were pretty close,"
"10591"	"and then looked up.  Yes, it was a man--a dim great figure in armor,"
"10592"	"standing erect, with both hands on the upper wire--and, of course,"
"10593"	"there was a smell of burning flesh.  Poor fellow, dead as a"
"10594"	"door-nail, and never knew what hurt him.  He stood there like a"
"10595"	"statue--no motion about him, except that his plumes swished about"
"10596"	"a little in the night wind.  We rose up and looked in through"
"10597"	"the bars of his visor, but couldn’t make out whether we knew him"
"10598"	"or not--features too dim and shadowed."
"10599"	"We heard muffled sounds approaching, and we sank down to the ground"
"10600"	"where we were.  We made out another knight vaguely; he was coming"
"10601"	"very stealthily, and feeling his way.  He was near enough now for"
"10602"	"us to see him put out a hand, find an upper wire, then bend and"
"10603"	"step under it and over the lower one.  Now he arrived at the"
"10604"	"first knight--and started slightly when he discovered him.  He"
"10605"	"stood a moment--no doubt wondering why the other one didn’t move"
"10606"	"on; then he said, in a low voice, “Why dreamest thou here, good"
"10607"	"Sir Mar--” then he laid his hand on the corpse’s shoulder--and just"
"10608"	"uttered a little soft moan and sunk down dead.  Killed by a dead"
"10609"	"man, you see--killed by a dead friend, in fact.  There was something"
"10610"	"awful about it."
"10611"	"These early birds came scattering along after each other, about"
"10612"	"one every five minutes in our vicinity, during half an hour."
"10613"	"They brought no armor of offense but their swords; as a rule,"
"10614"	"they carried the sword ready in the hand, and put it forward and"
"10615"	"found the wires with it.  We would now and then see a blue spark"
"10616"	"when the knight that caused it was so far away as to be invisible"
"10617"	"to us; but we knew what had happened, all the same; poor fellow,"
"10618"	"he had touched a charged wire with his sword and been electrocuted."
"10619"	"We had brief intervals of grim stillness, interrupted with piteous"
"10620"	"regularity by the clash made by the falling of an iron-clad; and"
"10621"	"this sort of thing was going on, right along, and was very creepy"
"10622"	"there in the dark and lonesomeness."
"10623"	"We concluded to make a tour between the inner fences.  We elected"
"10624"	"to walk upright, for convenience’s sake; we argued that if discerned,"
"10625"	"we should be taken for friends rather than enemies, and in any case"
"10626"	"we should be out of reach of swords, and these gentry did not seem"
"10627"	"to have any spears along.  Well, it was a curious trip.  Everywhere"
"10628"	"dead men were lying outside the second fence--not plainly visible,"
"10629"	"but still visible; and we counted fifteen of those pathetic"
"10630"	"statues--dead knights standing with their hands on the upper wire."
"10631"	"One thing seemed to be sufficiently demonstrated: our current"
"10632"	"was so tremendous that it killed before the victim could cry out."
"10633"	"Pretty soon we detected a muffled and heavy sound, and next moment"
"10634"	"we guessed what it was.  It was a surprise in force coming! I whispered"
"10635"	"Clarence to go and wake the army, and notify it to wait in silence"
"10636"	"in the cave for further orders.  He was soon back, and we stood"
"10637"	"by the inner fence and watched the silent lightning do its awful"
"10638"	"work upon that swarming host.  One could make out but little of"
"10639"	"detail; but he could note that a black mass was piling itself up"
"10640"	"beyond the second fence.  That swelling bulk was dead men!  Our"
"10641"	"camp was enclosed with a solid wall of the dead--a bulwark,"
"10642"	"a breastwork, of corpses, you may say.  One terrible thing about"
"10643"	"this thing was the absence of human voices; there were no cheers,"
"10644"	"no war cries; being intent upon a surprise, these men moved as"
"10645"	"noiselessly as they could; and always when the front rank was near"
"10646"	"enough to their goal to make it proper for them to begin to get"
"10647"	"a shout ready, of course they struck the fatal line and went down"
"10648"	"without testifying."
"10649"	"I sent a current through the third fence now; and almost immediately"
"10650"	"through the fourth and fifth, so quickly were the gaps filled up."
"10651"	"I believed the time was come now for my climax; I believed that"
"10652"	"that whole army was in our trap.  Anyway, it was high time to find"
"10653"	"out.  So I touched a button and set fifty electric suns aflame"
"10654"	"on the top of our precipice."
"10655"	"Land, what a sight!  We were enclosed in three walls of dead men!"
"10656"	"All the other fences were pretty nearly filled with the living,"
"10657"	"who were stealthily working their way forward through the wires."
"10658"	"The sudden glare paralyzed this host, petrified them, you may say,"
"10659"	"with astonishment; there was just one instant for me to utilize"
"10660"	"their immobility in, and I didn’t lose the chance.  You see, in"
"10661"	"another instant they would have recovered their faculties, then"
"10662"	"they’d have burst into a cheer and made a rush, and my wires"
"10663"	"would have gone down before it; but that lost instant lost them"
"10664"	"their opportunity forever; while even that slight fragment of time"
"10665"	"was still unspent, I shot the current through all the fences and"
"10666"	"struck the whole host dead in their tracks!  _There_ was a groan"
"10667"	"you could _hear_!  It voiced the death-pang of eleven thousand men."
"10668"	"It swelled out on the night with awful pathos."
"10669"	"A glance showed that the rest of the enemy--perhaps ten thousand"
"10670"	"strong--were between us and the encircling ditch, and pressing"
"10671"	"forward to the assault.  Consequently we had them _all!_ and had"
"10672"	"them past help.  Time for the last act of the tragedy.  I fired"
"10673"	"the three appointed revolver shots--which meant:"
"10674"	"“Turn on the water!”"
"10675"	"There was a sudden rush and roar, and in a minute the mountain"
"10676"	"brook was raging through the big ditch and creating a river a"
"10677"	"hundred feet wide and twenty-five deep."
"10678"	"“Stand to your guns, men!  Open fire!”"
"10679"	"The thirteen gatlings began to vomit death into the fated ten"
"10680"	"thousand.  They halted, they stood their ground a moment against"
"10681"	"that withering deluge of fire, then they broke, faced about and"
"10682"	"swept toward the ditch like chaff before a gale.  A full fourth"
"10683"	"part of their force never reached the top of the lofty embankment;"
"10684"	"the three-fourths reached it and plunged over--to death by drowning."
"10685"	"Within ten short minutes after we had opened fire, armed resistance"
"10686"	"was totally annihilated, the campaign was ended, we fifty-four were"
"10687"	"masters of England.  Twenty-five thousand men lay dead around us."
"10688"	"But how treacherous is fortune!  In a little while--say an hour"
"10689"	"--happened a thing, by my own fault, which--but I have no heart"
"10690"	"to write that.  Let the record end here."
"10691"	"CHAPTER XLIV"
"10692"	"A POSTSCRIPT BY CLARENCE"
"10693"	"I, Clarence, must write it for him.  He proposed that we two"
"10694"	"go out and see if any help could be accorded the wounded.  I was"
"10695"	"strenuous against the project.  I said that if there were many,"
"10696"	"we could do but little for them; and it would not be wise for us to"
"10697"	"trust ourselves among them, anyway.  But he could seldom be turned"
"10698"	"from a purpose once formed; so we shut off the electric current"
"10699"	"from the fences, took an escort along, climbed over the enclosing"
"10700"	"ramparts of dead knights, and moved out upon the field.  The first"
"10701"	"wounded mall who appealed for help was sitting with his back"
"10702"	"against a dead comrade.  When The Boss bent over him and spoke"
"10703"	"to him, the man recognized him and stabbed him.  That knight was"
"10704"	"Sir Meliagraunce, as I found out by tearing off his helmet.  He"
"10705"	"will not ask for help any more."
"10706"	"We carried The Boss to the cave and gave his wound, which was"
"10707"	"not very serious, the best care we could.  In this service we had"
"10708"	"the help of Merlin, though we did not know it.  He was disguised"
"10709"	"as a woman, and appeared to be a simple old peasant goodwife."
"10710"	"In this disguise, with brown-stained face and smooth shaven, he"
"10711"	"had appeared a few days after The Boss was hurt and offered to cook"
"10712"	"for us, saying her people had gone off to join certain new camps"
"10713"	"which the enemy were forming, and that she was starving.  The Boss"
"10714"	"had been getting along very well, and had amused himself with"
"10715"	"finishing up his record."
"10716"	"We were glad to have this woman, for we were short handed.  We"
"10717"	"were in a trap, you see--a trap of our own making.  If we stayed"
"10718"	"where we were, our dead would kill us; if we moved out of our"
"10719"	"defenses, we should no longer be invincible.  We had conquered;"
"10720"	"in turn we were conquered.  The Boss recognized this; we all"
"10721"	"recognized it.  If we could go to one of those new camps and"
"10722"	"patch up some kind of terms with the enemy--yes, but The Boss"
"10723"	"could not go, and neither could I, for I was among the first that"
"10724"	"were made sick by the poisonous air bred by those dead thousands."
"10725"	"Others were taken down, and still others.  To-morrow--"
"10726"	"_To-morrow._  It is here.  And with it the end.  About midnight"
"10727"	"I awoke, and saw that hag making curious passes in the air about"
"10728"	"The Boss’s head and face, and wondered what it meant.  Everybody"
"10729"	"but the dynamo-watch lay steeped in sleep; there was no sound."
"10730"	"The woman ceased from her mysterious foolery, and started tip-toeing"
"10731"	"toward the door.  I called out:"
"10732"	"“Stop!  What have you been doing?”"
"10733"	"She halted, and said with an accent of malicious satisfaction:"
"10734"	"“Ye were conquerors; ye are conquered!  These others are perishing"
"10735"	"--you also.  Ye shall all die in this place--every one--except _him_."
"10736"	"He sleepeth now--and shall sleep thirteen centuries.  I am Merlin!”"
"10737"	"Then such a delirium of silly laughter overtook him that he reeled"
"10738"	"about like a drunken man, and presently fetched up against one"
"10739"	"of our wires.  His mouth is spread open yet; apparently he is still"
"10740"	"laughing.  I suppose the face will retain that petrified laugh until"
"10741"	"the corpse turns to dust."
"10742"	"The Boss has never stirred--sleeps like a stone.  If he does not"
"10743"	"wake to-day we shall understand what kind of a sleep it is, and"
"10744"	"his body will then be borne to a place in one of the remote recesses"
"10745"	"of the cave where none will ever find it to desecrate it.  As for"
"10746"	"the rest of us--well, it is agreed that if any one of us ever"
"10747"	"escapes alive from this place, he will write the fact here, and"
"10748"	"loyally hide this Manuscript with The Boss, our dear good chief,"
"10749"	"whose property it is, be he alive or dead."
"10750"	"THE END OF THE MANUSCRIPT"
"10751"	"FINAL P.S. BY M.T."
"10752"	"The dawn was come when I laid the Manuscript aside.  The rain"
"10753"	"had almost ceased, the world was gray and sad, the exhausted storm"
"10754"	"was sighing and sobbing itself to rest.  I went to the stranger’s"
"10755"	"room, and listened at his door, which was slightly ajar.  I could"
"10756"	"hear his voice, and so I knocked.  There was no answer, but I still"
"10757"	"heard the voice.  I peeped in.  The man lay on his back in bed,"
"10758"	"talking brokenly but with spirit, and punctuating with his arms,"
"10759"	"which he thrashed about, restlessly, as sick people do in delirium."
"10760"	"I slipped in softly and bent over him.  His mutterings and"
"10761"	"ejaculations went on.  I spoke--merely a word, to call his attention."
"10762"	"His glassy eyes and his ashy face were alight in an instant with"
"10763"	"pleasure, gratitude, gladness, welcome:"
"10764"	"“Oh, Sandy, you are come at last--how I have longed for you!  Sit"
"10765"	"by me--do not leave me--never leave me again, Sandy, never again."
"10766"	"Where is your hand?--give it me, dear, let me hold it--there"
"10767"	"--now all is well, all is peace, and I am happy again--_we_ are happy"
"10768"	"again, isn’t it so, Sandy?  You are so dim, so vague, you are but"
"10769"	"a mist, a cloud, but you are _here_, and that is blessedness sufficient;"
"10770"	"and I have your hand; don’t take it away--it is for only a little"
"10771"	"while, I shall not require it long....  Was that the child?..."
"10772"	"Hello-Central!... she doesn’t answer.  Asleep, perhaps?  Bring her"
"10773"	"when she wakes, and let me touch her hands, her face, her hair,"
"10774"	"and tell her good-bye....  Sandy!  Yes, you are there.  I lost"
"10775"	"myself a moment, and I thought you were gone....  Have I been"
"10776"	"sick long?  It must be so; it seems months to me.  And such dreams!"
"10777"	"such strange and awful dreams, Sandy!  Dreams that were as real"
"10778"	"as reality--delirium, of course, but _so_ real!  Why, I thought"
"10779"	"the king was dead, I thought you were in Gaul and couldn’t get"
"10780"	"home, I thought there was a revolution; in the fantastic frenzy"
"10781"	"of these dreams, I thought that Clarence and I and a handful of"
"10782"	"my cadets fought and exterminated the whole chivalry of England!"
"10783"	"But even that was not the strangest.  I seemed to be a creature"
"10784"	"out of a remote unborn age, centuries hence, and even _that_ was"
"10785"	"as real as the rest!  Yes, I seemed to have flown back out of that"
"10786"	"age into this of ours, and then forward to it again, and was set"
"10787"	"down, a stranger and forlorn in that strange England, with an"
"10788"	"abyss of thirteen centuries yawning between me and you! between"
"10789"	"me and my home and my friends! between me and all that is dear"
"10790"	"to me, all that could make life worth the living!  It was awful"
"10791"	"--awfuler than you can ever imagine, Sandy.  Ah, watch by me, Sandy"
"10792"	"--stay by me every moment--_don’t_ let me go out of my mind again;"
"10793"	"death is nothing, let it come, but not with those dreams, not with"
"10794"	"the torture of those hideous dreams--I cannot endure _that_ again...."
"10795"	"Sandy?...”"
"10796"	"He lay muttering incoherently some little time; then for a time he"
"10797"	"lay silent, and apparently sinking away toward death.  Presently"
"10798"	"his fingers began to pick busily at the coverlet, and by that sign"
"10799"	"I knew that his end was at hand with the first suggestion of the"
"10800"	"death-rattle in his throat he started up slightly, and seemed"
"10801"	"to listen: then he said:"
"10802"	"“A bugle?...  It is the king!  The drawbridge, there!  Man the"
"10803"	"battlements!--turn out the--”"
"10804"	"He was getting up his last “effect”; but he never finished it."

"10806"	"Court, Complete, by Mark Twain (Samuel Clemens)"
